# Overview

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

- [debian/changelog](debian/changelog)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document provides a high-level introduction to `tt-tools-common`, a shared Python library that provides common functionality for Tenstorrent hardware management tools. This page covers the library's architecture, core components, consumer applications, and runtime requirements. 

For installation instructions, see [Installation and Setup](#1.1). For detailed documentation of specific subsystems, refer to [Hardware Reset System](#2), [System Utilities](#3), [User Interface Components](#4), and [Build and Distribution](#5).

## What is tt-tools-common?

`tt-tools-common` is a helper library that consolidates shared functionality across multiple Tenstorrent command-line and TUI applications. It is **not a standalone tool** but rather a foundation that other tools build upon. The library serves three primary purposes:

1. **Hardware Management**: Provides chip reset capabilities, driver interaction, and hardware detection for Blackhole, Wormhole, and Grayskull architectures
2. **User Interface Framework**: Offers reusable Textual-based widgets, themes, and styling for building consistent terminal user interfaces
3. **System Utilities**: Implements common operations like version checking, host information gathering, and configuration management

**Sources**: [README.md:1-46](), [pyproject.toml:1-84]()

## Architecture Overview

The library is organized into three distinct layers that can be consumed independently or in combination:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "tt-tools-common Library Structure"
        subgraph "Hardware Interface Layer"
            ResetCommon["reset_common/<br/>ChipReset, BHChipReset, WHChipReset, GSTensixReset"]
            ResetConfig["reset_common/reset_utils.py<br/>parse_reset_input, generate_reset_logs"]
        end
        
        subgraph "System Utilities Layer"
            SystemUtils["utils_common/system_utils.py<br/>check_driver_version, get_host_info"]
            ToolsUtils["utils_common/tools_utils.py<br/>detect_chips_with_callback, hex_to_semver_*"]
        end
        
        subgraph "UI Framework Layer"
            Widgets["ui_common/tt_widget.py<br/>TTHeader, TTFooter, TTDataTable, TTMenu"]
            Modals["ui_common/modal_screens.py<br/>TTConfirmBox, TTHelperMenuBox"]
            Styles["ui_common/common_style.css<br/>Themes and color variables"]
        end
        
        subgraph "Data and Configuration"
            ChipData["data/chip_data/<br/>fw_defines.yaml"]
            ResetData["data/reset_data/<br/>reset configs"]
        end
    end
    
    subgraph "External Dependencies"
        PyLuwen["pyluwen ~=0.8.0<br/>PciChip hardware abstraction"]
        Textual["textual >=0.59.0<br/>TUI framework"]
        Pydantic["pydantic >=1.2<br/>Data validation"]
    end
    
    ResetCommon --> PyLuwen
    SystemUtils --> PyLuwen
    ToolsUtils --> PyLuwen
    ToolsUtils --> ChipData
    
    Widgets --> Textual
    Widgets --> Styles
    Modals --> Textual
    
    ResetConfig --> Pydantic
    ResetConfig --> ResetData
```

**Figure 1**: Component architecture showing module organization and dependencies

**Sources**: [pyproject.toml:23-34](), Architecture diagram from context

## Core Components

### Hardware Interface Layer

The hardware interface layer provides the most critical functionality in `tt-tools-common`: chip reset operations and hardware communication.

| Module | Primary Classes/Functions | Purpose |
|--------|--------------------------|---------|
| `reset_common/` | `ChipReset`, `BHChipReset`, `WHChipReset`, `GSTensixReset` | Chip-specific reset implementations for all supported architectures |
| `reset_common/reset_utils.py` | `parse_reset_input()`, `generate_reset_logs()` | Configuration parsing and structured logging |
| `reset_common/host_reset_log.py` | `HostResetLog`, `PciResetDeviceInfo` | Pydantic models for reset logging |

The reset system implements a **delegation pattern** where chip-specific classes route to the unified `ChipReset` implementation when driver version >= 2.4.1. This architecture enables backward compatibility while migrating to modern reset sequences. For comprehensive documentation, see [Hardware Reset System](#2).

**Sources**: Architecture diagrams from context, [pyproject.toml:23-34]()

### System Utilities Layer

The utilities layer provides system-level operations required by all Tenstorrent tools:

| Module | Primary Functions | Purpose |
|--------|------------------|---------|
| `utils_common/system_utils.py` | `check_driver_version()`, `get_host_info()`, `is_driver_version_at_least()` | Driver validation and host information collection |
| `utils_common/tools_utils.py` | `detect_chips_with_callback()`, `hex_to_semver_*()`, `get_board_type_from_upi()` | Chip detection, version conversions, firmware utilities |

These utilities abstract platform-specific details and provide consistent APIs for driver interaction, hardware detection, and version management. See [System Utilities](#3) for detailed documentation.

**Sources**: Architecture diagrams from context

### UI Framework Layer

The UI framework provides pre-built Textual widgets and styling for building consistent terminal interfaces:

| Module | Components | Purpose |
|--------|-----------|---------|
| `ui_common/tt_widget.py` | `TTHeader`, `TTFooter`, `TTDataTable`, `TTMenu`, `TTCompatibilityMenu` | Core reusable widgets |
| `ui_common/modal_screens.py` | `TTConfirmBox`, `TTHelperMenuBox`, `TTSettingsMenu` | Modal dialog screens |
| `ui_common/common_style.css` | CSS variables and rules | Global theming and styling |

The framework enables developers to build TUI applications with consistent appearance and behavior without reimplementing common UI patterns. See [User Interface Components](#4) for widget reference and usage examples.

**Sources**: Architecture diagrams from context, [pyproject.toml:59-63]()

## Consumer Applications

`tt-tools-common` is consumed by multiple Tenstorrent tools, each importing different subsets of functionality:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Consumer Applications"
        TTSMI["tt-smi<br/>System Management Interface"]
        TTFlash["tt-flash<br/>Firmware Update Tool"]
        TTOther["Other TT Tools"]
    end
    
    subgraph "tt-tools-common API Surface"
        ResetAPI["Reset API<br/>ChipReset.full_lds_reset<br/>parse_reset_input"]
        UtilsAPI["Utilities API<br/>detect_chips_with_callback<br/>check_driver_version<br/>get_host_info"]
        UIAPI["UI API<br/>TTHeader, TTFooter<br/>TTDataTable, TTMenu<br/>common_style.css"]
    end
    
    TTSMI --> ResetAPI
    TTSMI --> UtilsAPI
    TTSMI --> UIAPI
    
    TTFlash --> UtilsAPI
    
    TTOther --> ResetAPI
    TTOther --> UtilsAPI
    TTOther --> UIAPI
```

**Figure 2**: Consumer applications and their API usage patterns

Consumer tools typically:
- Import `reset_common` for chip reset operations
- Import `utils_common` for system detection and validation
- Import `ui_common` for building terminal user interfaces
- Bundle `data/` files for chip-specific configuration

**Sources**: Architecture diagrams from context

## Dependencies and Requirements

### Runtime Dependencies

The library requires Python >= 3.10 and the following core dependencies:

| Dependency | Version Constraint | Purpose |
|-----------|-------------------|---------|
| `pyluwen` | `~=0.8.0` | Hardware abstraction layer for PCI device communication |
| `textual` | `>=0.59.0` | TUI framework for building terminal applications |
| `pydantic` | `>=1.2` | Data validation and serialization |
| `pyyaml` | `>=6.0.1` | YAML configuration parsing |
| `psutil` | `>=5.9.6` | System and process utilities |
| `distro` | `>=1.8.0` | Linux distribution detection |
| `elasticsearch` | `>=8.11.0` | Optional structured logging backend |
| `rich` | `>=13.7.0` | Terminal text formatting |
| `requests` | `>=2.32.3` | HTTP client for remote operations |
| `tqdm` | `>=4.66.3` | Progress bar displays |
| `tomli` | (no constraint) | TOML file parsing |

**Sources**: [pyproject.toml:23-34]()

### Development Dependencies

For developers contributing to `tt-tools-common`:

```python
# pyproject.toml [project.optional-dependencies]
dev = [
    'black>=23.11.0',      # Code formatting
    'pre-commit>=3.5.0',   # Git hook framework
    'pyluwen~=0.8.0',      # Hardware testing
    'pytest>=7.0.0',       # Test framework
    'pytest-asyncio>=0.21.0',  # Async test support
]
```

**Sources**: [pyproject.toml:36-43]()

### System Requirements

- **Operating System**: Ubuntu 22.04, 24.04, or latest
- **Python Version**: 3.10, 3.11, or 3.12
- **Driver**: Tenstorrent kernel driver (`tt-kmd`) >= 1.26.0 for hardware operations
- **Architecture**: x86_64 (ARM has restrictions for certain reset operations)

For detailed installation procedures, see [Installation and Setup](#1.1).

**Sources**: [pyproject.toml:3](), [pyproject.toml:14-22](), Architecture diagrams from context

## Package Distribution

`tt-tools-common` is distributed through two channels:

### PyPI (Python Package Index)

```bash
pip install tt-tools-common
```

Python wheel packages are published to PyPI for installation via pip. The build process uses `setuptools` with version information extracted from Git tags. See [Python Package Build](#5.2) for build details.

### Debian Repository

```bash
apt install tt-tools-common
```

Debian packages are built for multiple Ubuntu distributions and published to GitHub Releases. The packaging includes proper dependency resolution and system integration. See [Debian Package Build System](#5.1) for packaging details.

**Sources**: [pyproject.toml:45-48](), [debian/changelog:1-236](), Architecture diagrams from context

**Sources**: [pyproject.toml:1-48](), [README.md:44-45]()

## Data Assets

The library includes chip-specific data files packaged with the installation:

```
data/
├── chip_data/
│   └── fw_defines.yaml          # Firmware definitions and addresses
└── reset_data/
    └── *.json                   # Reset configuration templates
```

These files are automatically included in distributions via `setuptools` configuration and are accessible to consumer applications at runtime. The `tools_utils` module provides functions to load and parse these data files.

**Sources**: [pyproject.toml:58-63]()

## Version History and Changelog

The package uses semantic versioning (MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH) with the current version defined in [pyproject.toml:4](). Release history and detailed changelogs are maintained in [debian/changelog:1-236]() and GitHub Releases. Recent significant changes include:

- **1.6.0**: Latest stable release
- **1.5.1**: Added secondary bus reset option, enhanced docstrings
- **1.5.0**: Updated pyluwen dependency to 0.8.0
- **1.4.32**: Xen HVM integration with xenstore coordination
- **1.4.28**: Redesigned reset sequence support with driver version checking

For the complete release workflow and versioning strategy, see [Automated Release Workflow](#5.3).

**Sources**: [pyproject.toml:4](), [debian/changelog:1-42]()

# Installation and Setup

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml](.github/workflows/build-debian.yml)
- [debian/control](debian/control)
- [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml)
- [setup.py](setup.py)

</details>



This document provides complete instructions for installing and configuring `tt-tools-common` on your system. It covers both production installation via pip/PyPI and Debian packages, as well as development environment setup. For details on the CI/CD build and release process, see [Automated Release Workflow](#5.3) and [Python Package Build](#5.2). For setting up a development environment with all dev dependencies, see [Development Environment Setup](#6.4).

## System Requirements

### Python Version Compatibility

`tt-tools-common` requires Python 3.10 or higher. The package is tested against the following Python versions in CI:

| Python Version | Support Status | Testing Coverage |
|---------------|----------------|------------------|
| 3.10          | ✅ Supported    | Full test suite  |
| 3.11          | ✅ Supported    | Full test suite  |
| 3.12          | ✅ Supported    | Full test suite  |
| < 3.10        | ❌ Unsupported  | Not tested       |

The minimum version constraint is enforced in [pyproject.toml:3]() through the `requires-python = ">=3.10"` field.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:3]()

### Operating System Support

The package supports the following Ubuntu distributions with dedicated Debian package builds:

| Distribution    | Package Support | Build Matrix |
|----------------|-----------------|--------------|
| Ubuntu 22.04   | ✅ Full support  | [build-debian.yml:32]() |
| Ubuntu 24.04   | ✅ Full support  | [build-debian.yml:33]() |
| Ubuntu Latest  | ✅ Full support  | [build-debian.yml:34]() |
| Other Linux    | ⚠️ Via pip only | Not tested   |

**Platform Restrictions:** ARM architecture support is limited for certain reset operations. See [Platform Support and Virtualization](#2.7) for details on architecture-specific constraints.

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:31-34]()

### Hardware Requirements

While `tt-tools-common` can be installed on any compatible system, hardware interaction features require:

- **Tenstorrent Hardware**: Blackhole (BH), Wormhole (WH), or Grayskull (GS) accelerators
- **Kernel Driver**: tt-kmd version >= 1.26.0 (see [Driver Version Management](#3.1))
- **PCIe Interface**: Hardware must be accessible via `/dev/tenstorrent/*` device nodes

**Sources:** System architecture diagrams

## Installation Methods

```mermaid
graph TB
    User["User/Consumer Application"]
    
    subgraph "Installation Methods"
        PipInstall["pip install<br/>tt-tools-common"]
        DebInstall["apt install<br/>python3-tt-tools-common"]
        DevInstall["pip install -e .<br/>(editable mode)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Package Sources"
        PyPI["PyPI Repository<br/>pypi.org/project/tt-tools-common"]
        DebRepo["Debian Repository<br/>(GPG-signed .deb)"]
        LocalSource["Local Git Clone<br/>github.com/tenstorrent/tt-tools-common"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Dependency Resolution"
        CoreDeps["Core Dependencies<br/>textual, pydantic, pyyaml, etc."]
        PyLuwen["pyluwen ~=0.8.0<br/>(hardware abstraction)"]
        DevDeps["Dev Dependencies<br/>pytest, black, pre-commit"]
    end
    
    PipInstall --> PyPI
    DebInstall --> DebRepo
    DevInstall --> LocalSource
    
    PyPI --> CoreDeps
    DebRepo --> CoreDeps
    DebRepo --> PyLuwen
    LocalSource --> CoreDeps
    LocalSource --> DevDeps
    
    CoreDeps --> User
    PyLuwen --> User
```

**Diagram: Installation Flow and Package Sources**

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:23-43](), [debian/control:22-25]()

### Method 1: Install from PyPI (Recommended)

Install the latest stable release from PyPI using pip:

```bash
pip install tt-tools-common
```

For a specific version:

```bash
pip install tt-tools-common==1.6.0
```

To include hardware interaction capabilities, `pyluwen` must be installed separately:

```bash
pip install tt-tools-common pyluwen~=0.8.0
```

**Important:** The PyPI package does **not** include `pyluwen` as a core dependency ([pyproject.toml:23-34]()), but it is required in [dev dependencies:40](). Consumer applications requiring hardware reset or chip detection features must install `pyluwen` explicitly.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:1-43]()

### Method 2: Install Debian Package

For Ubuntu systems, install the pre-built Debian package:

```bash
# Add Tenstorrent package repository (if not already configured)
# Repository setup instructions provided by Tenstorrent

# Install the package
sudo apt update
sudo apt install python3-tt-tools-common
```

The Debian package automatically includes `python3-pyluwen` as a dependency ([debian/control:25]()), ensuring all hardware interaction features work out-of-the-box.

**Package Details:**
- **Package Name**: `python3-tt-tools-common`
- **Architecture**: `all` (architecture-independent Python code)
- **Maintainer**: Sam Bansal <sbansal@tenstorrent.com>
- **Build System**: Uses `gbp` (git-buildpackage) with GPG signing

**Sources:** [debian/control:19-35](), [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:129-133]()

### Method 3: Development Installation

For development or contributing to `tt-tools-common`, clone the repository and install in editable mode:

```bash
git clone https://github.com/tenstorrent/tt-tools-common.git
cd tt-tools-common
pip install -e ".[dev]"
```

This installs the package with all development dependencies including:
- `black>=23.11.0` - Code formatting
- `pre-commit>=3.5.0` - Git hooks for code quality
- `pyluwen~=0.8.0` - Hardware abstraction layer
- `pytest>=7.0.0` - Testing framework
- `pytest-asyncio>=0.21.0` - Async test support

See [Development Environment Setup](#6.4) for comprehensive development setup instructions.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:36-43]()

## Core Dependencies

The following table details all runtime dependencies managed by the package:

| Dependency | Minimum Version | Purpose | Optional |
|-----------|----------------|---------|----------|
| `distro` | 1.8.0 | OS distribution detection | No |
| `elasticsearch` | 8.11.0 | Structured logging backend | Yes* |
| `psutil` | 5.9.6 | System metrics and process info | No |
| `pyyaml` | 6.0.1 | Configuration file parsing | No |
| `rich` | 13.7.0 | Terminal text formatting | No |
| `textual` | 0.59.0 | TUI framework | No |
| `requests` | 2.32.3 | HTTP client operations | No |
| `tqdm` | 4.66.3 | Progress bar rendering | No |
| `pydantic` | 1.2+ | Data validation and models | No |
| `tomli` | (any) | TOML parsing for pyproject.toml | No |
| `pyluwen` | ~=0.8.0 | Hardware abstraction (pip: manual, deb: auto) | No** |

\* Elasticsearch is technically required but logging features gracefully degrade without it  
\** Required for hardware operations; manual install needed for pip, automatic for Debian

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:23-34](), [pyproject.toml:37-43]()

The [setup.py:11-12]() script uses `tomli` to dynamically read version and metadata from [pyproject.toml:1-84](). During installation, setuptools includes package data specified in [pyproject.toml:58-63](), ensuring CSS themes and YAML chip data files are bundled with the package.

**Sources:** [setup.py:1-21](), [pyproject.toml:55-63]()

## Installation Verification

After installation, verify the package is correctly installed and importable:

```bash
# Check package version
python -c "import importlib.metadata; print(importlib.metadata.version('tt-tools-common'))"

# Verify core modules are importable
python -c "from tt_tools_common.reset_common import ChipReset"
python -c "from tt_tools_common.ui_common.widgets import TTHeader"
python -c "from tt_tools_common.utils_common import system_utils"

# Check if pyluwen is available (for hardware features)
python -c "import pyluwen; print('pyluwen available')" 2>/dev/null || echo "pyluwen not installed"
```

### Testing Hardware Interaction

If `pyluwen` is installed and Tenstorrent hardware is available:

```bash
# Attempt to detect chips (requires hardware)
python -c "from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import detect_chips_with_callback; \
           detect_chips_with_callback(lambda x: print(x))"
```

This command will fail gracefully if no hardware is present or if the kernel driver is not installed.

**Sources:** API expectations from system architecture diagrams

## Platform-Specific Considerations

### Debian Package Build Matrix

The Debian build workflow creates separate packages for multiple Ubuntu versions:

| Build Target | Matrix Entry | Package Name Pattern |
|-------------|--------------|---------------------|
| Ubuntu 22.04 | [build-debian.yml:32]() | `*_all-ubuntu-22.04.deb` |
| Ubuntu 24.04 | [build-debian.yml:33]() | `*_all-ubuntu-24.04.deb` |
| Ubuntu Latest | [build-debian.yml:34]() | `*_all-ubuntu-latest.deb` |

Each build produces:
- `.deb` package file
- `.changes` file with package metadata
- `debian/changelog` with version history

The workflow uses `fail-fast: false` ([build-debian.yml:29]()) to ensure all builds complete even if one target fails.

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:26-35]()

### Package Signing

All Debian packages are cryptographically signed using GPG:

1. GPG private key imported from GitHub secrets ([build-debian.yml:68-71]())
2. Key fingerprint extracted and passed to `gbp buildpackage` ([build-debian.yml:133]())
3. `DEBSIGN_KEYID` environment variable configures signing

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:67-133]()

### Virtualization Support

`tt-tools-common` includes special handling for Xen HVM environments. When running under Xen, the reset system coordinates with xenstore for PCIe device management. No special installation steps are required; the library auto-detects virtualization at runtime.

See [Platform Support and Virtualization](#2.7) for implementation details.

**Sources:** System architecture diagram (Diagram 2)

## Troubleshooting Common Installation Issues

### Issue: Python Version Too Old

**Symptom:** Installation fails with "Python 3.10 or higher is required"

**Solution:** Upgrade Python or use a virtual environment with Python 3.10+:
```bash
python3.10 -m venv venv
source venv/bin/activate
pip install tt-tools-common
```

### Issue: Missing pyluwen for Hardware Operations

**Symptom:** `ImportError: No module named 'pyluwen'` when attempting chip reset

**Solution:** Install pyluwen explicitly (PyPI installations only):
```bash
pip install pyluwen~=0.8.0
```

Debian package installations include this automatically.

### Issue: Package Data Files Not Found

**Symptom:** `FileNotFoundError` when loading CSS or YAML files

**Solution:** Verify package data was installed correctly:
```bash
python -c "import tt_tools_common; print(tt_tools_common.__file__)"
# Check if ui_common/*.css files exist in the printed directory
```

If files are missing, reinstall the package:
```bash
pip install --force-reinstall tt-tools-common
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:55-70]()

1. **For Tool Users**: Refer to consumer tool documentation (tt-smi, tt-flash) that depend on `tt-tools-common`

4. **For System Utilities**: See [System Utilities](#3) for driver and chip detection functions
5. **For Development**: See [Development Guide](#6) for contributing to the library

**Sources:** Table of contents structure

# Hardware Reset System

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

The Hardware Reset System is the core functionality of tt-tools-common, providing chip-level reset capabilities for Tenstorrent hardware. This system performs PCIe link resets and ASIC resets on Blackhole (BH), Wormhole (WH), and Grayskull (GS) chips, enabling recovery from hung states and facilitating firmware upgrades.

This document covers the overall architecture, implementation hierarchy, driver requirements, and reset workflows. For detailed implementation specifics of each chip type, see:
- Blackhole reset details: [Blackhole Reset Implementation](#2.3)
- Wormhole reset details: [Wormhole Reset Implementation](#2.4)
- Grayskull reset details: [Grayskull Tensix Reset](#2.5)
- Reset configuration and logging: [Reset Configuration and Logging](#2.6)
- Virtualization support: [Platform Support and Virtualization](#2.7)

**Sources:** [CHANGELOG.md:1-143](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:1-289](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:1-224](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:1-181]()

---

## Reset System Architecture

The reset system implements a **delegation pattern** that enables gradual migration from legacy chip-specific implementations to a modern unified implementation. The architecture consists of three chip-specific reset classes (`BHChipReset`, `WHChipReset`, `GSTensixReset`) and one unified modern implementation (`ChipReset`).

### High-Level Reset Architecture

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Reset Entry Points"
        UserApp["User Application<br/>(tt-smi, tt-flash)"]
        ParseInput["parse_reset_input()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Chip-Specific Reset Classes"
        BHChipReset["BHChipReset<br/>bh_reset.py"]
        WHChipReset["WHChipReset<br/>wh_reset.py"]
        GSTensixReset["GSTensixReset<br/>gs_tensix_reset.py"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Modern Unified Implementation"
        ChipReset["ChipReset<br/>chip_reset.py"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Driver Interface"
        IOCTL["IOCTL Interface<br/>/dev/tenstorrent/{id}"]
        DriverCheck["check_driver_version()<br/>is_driver_version_at_least()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Hardware Communication"
        PyLuwen["pyluwen.PciChip"]
        Kernel["tt-kmd Driver"]
        Hardware["Tenstorrent ASICs"]
    end
    
    UserApp --> ParseInput
    ParseInput --> BHChipReset
    ParseInput --> WHChipReset
    ParseInput --> GSTensixReset
    
    BHChipReset -->|"Driver >= 2.4.1<br/>or Xen HVM"| ChipReset
    WHChipReset -->|"Driver >= 2.4.1<br/>or Xen HVM"| ChipReset
    BHChipReset -->|"Legacy Path"| IOCTL
    WHChipReset -->|"Legacy Path"| IOCTL
    GSTensixReset --> PyLuwen
    
    ChipReset --> DriverCheck
    ChipReset --> IOCTL
    
    DriverCheck --> Kernel
    IOCTL --> Kernel
    PyLuwen --> Kernel
    Kernel --> Hardware
```

The delegation logic in `BHChipReset` and `WHChipReset` conditionally routes to `ChipReset` based on driver version or virtualization environment, maintaining backward compatibility while enabling adoption of the modern implementation.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:92-99](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:89-90](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-134]()

---

## Implementation Class Hierarchy

### Reset Class Structure

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class ChipReset {
        +full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces, reset_m3, silent, m3_delay, secondary_bus_reset)
        +reset_device_ioctl(interface_id, flags)
        +wait_for_device_to_reappear(bdf, timeout)
        -TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC: 0xFA
        -TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_RESET_DEVICE: 0xFA06
    }
    
    class BHChipReset {
        +full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces, reset_m3, silent, m3_delay, secondary_bus_reset)
        +reset_device_ioctl(interface_id, flags)
        -MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET: 0x56
        -MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3: 0xA3
        -POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME: 2
    }
    
    class WHChipReset {
        +full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces, reset_m3, silent, secondary_bus_reset)
        +reset_device_ioctl(interface_id, flags)
        -MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET: 0x56
        -MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3: 0xA3
        -A3_STATE_PROP_TIME: 0.03
    }
    
    class GSTensixReset {
        +full_tensix_reset(pci_interfaces, harvested_rows, silent)
        +get_tlb_config(chip)
        +tensix_reset(chip, harvested_coord)
    }
    
    class IoctlResetFlags {
        <<enumeration>>
        RESTORE_STATE: 0
        RESET_PCIE_LINK: 1
        CONFIG_WRITE: 2
        USER_RESET: 3
        ASIC_RESET: 4
        ASIC_DMC_RESET: 5
        POST_RESET: 6
    }
    
    BHChipReset ..> ChipReset : delegates to
    WHChipReset ..> ChipReset : delegates to
    ChipReset ..> IoctlResetFlags : uses
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:25-33](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:53-289](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:27-224](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:28-181]()

### Key Class Responsibilities

| Class | File | Primary Responsibility | Hardware Target |
|-------|------|----------------------|-----------------|
| `ChipReset` | `chip_reset.py` | Modern unified reset using driver v2.4.1+ IOCTL interface | Blackhole, Wormhole |
| `BHChipReset` | `bh_reset.py` | Blackhole reset with legacy and modern paths | Blackhole |
| `WHChipReset` | `wh_reset.py` | Wormhole reset with legacy and modern paths | Wormhole |
| `GSTensixReset` | (not shown) | Tensix core reset via NOC operations | Grayskull |
| `IoctlResetFlags` | `chip_reset.py` | Enumeration of IOCTL reset operation types | All |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:53-54](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:27-28](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:28-29]()

---

## Driver and Platform Requirements

### Driver Version Requirements

The reset system has specific minimum driver version requirements that determine which reset implementation path is used:

| Operation | Minimum Driver Version | Validation Function |
|-----------|----------------------|---------------------|
| Basic reset (legacy WH/BH) | 1.26.0 | `check_driver_version()` |
| Modern unified reset (ChipReset) | 2.4.1 | `is_driver_version_at_least()` |
| Xen HVM reset | 2.4.1 | `check_xen_hvm()` + version check |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:137](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:92](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:89](), [CHANGELOG.md:103]()

### Platform Restrictions

```mermaid
graph TD
    StartReset["full_lds_reset() called"]
    CheckDriver["Check driver version<br/>check_driver_version()"]
    CheckPlatform["Check platform<br/>get_host_info()['Platform']"]
    IsArm{"Platform starts with<br/>'arm' or 'aarch'?"}
    ExitError["Print error message<br/>sys.exit(1)"]
    ProceedReset["Proceed with reset"]
    
    StartReset --> CheckDriver
    CheckDriver --> CheckPlatform
    CheckPlatform --> IsArm
    IsArm -->|Yes| ExitError
    IsArm -->|No| ProceedReset
```

**ARM Platform Restriction:** The reset system does not support ARM/AArch64 platforms due to how these systems handle PCIe device rescans. When an ARM platform is detected, the reset operations exit with an error message directing users to reboot the system instead.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:139-148](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:109-118](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:103-112]()

---

## Reset Workflow and Sequence

### Modern Reset Workflow (ChipReset)

The `ChipReset.full_lds_reset()` method implements a multi-stage reset sequence:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant App as "User Application"
    participant CR as "ChipReset"
    participant DV as "Driver Version Check"
    participant PC as "Platform Check"
    participant XS as "Xenstore (Xen HVM)"
    participant IOCTL as "IOCTL Interface"
    participant KD as "Kernel Driver (tt-kmd)"
    participant HW as "Hardware"
    
    App->>CR: full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces)
    CR->>DV: check_driver_version(minimum="2.4.1")
    DV-->>CR: Version validated
    CR->>PC: Check if ARM platform
    PC-->>CR: Platform OK (not ARM)
    
    alt Xen HVM Detected
        CR->>XS: Write "1" to xenstore<br/>(notify host reset starting)
    end
    
    opt Secondary Bus Reset
        loop For each interface
            CR->>IOCTL: reset_device_ioctl(id, RESET_PCIE_LINK)
            IOCTL->>KD: IOCTL call
            KD->>HW: Secondary bus reset
        end
    end
    
    loop For each interface
        CR->>IOCTL: reset_device_ioctl(id, ASIC_RESET or ASIC_DMC_RESET)
        IOCTL->>KD: IOCTL call
        KD->>HW: ASIC/DMC reset
    end
    
    alt Xen HVM Detected
        CR->>XS: Poll for xenstore file removal<br/>(wait for host to complete hot-plug)
        XS-->>CR: File removed (hot-plug complete)
    end
    
    CR->>CR: Sleep(post_reset_wait)
    
    loop For each interface
        CR->>CR: wait_for_device_to_reappear(bdf)
        CR->>IOCTL: reset_device_ioctl(new_id, POST_RESET)
        IOCTL->>KD: Post-reset cleanup
    end
    
    CR-->>App: List[PciChip]
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-288](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:167-256]()

### Reset Stages Detail

**Stage 1: Pre-flight Validation**
- Driver version check via `check_driver_version()` [chip_reset.py:137]()
- Platform architecture check via `get_host_info()` [chip_reset.py:141]()
- PCI interface deduplication [chip_reset.py:151]()
- Collection of BDF (Bus:Device.Function) addresses [chip_reset.py:159-162]()

**Stage 2: Xen HVM Coordination (if applicable)**
- Detect Xen HVM environment using `check_xen_hvm()` [chip_reset.py:169]()
- Write "1" to xenstore files to notify host [chip_reset.py:176-193]()
- Format: `pci_hard_reset/{bus}_{device}-{function}` [chip_reset.py:179]()

**Stage 3: Secondary Bus Reset (optional)**
- Issue IOCTL with `RESET_PCIE_LINK` flag [chip_reset.py:198]()
- Performed before ASIC reset if `secondary_bus_reset=True` [chip_reset.py:196]()

**Stage 4: ASIC Reset**
- Issue IOCTL with `ASIC_RESET` or `ASIC_DMC_RESET` flag [chip_reset.py:206-212]()
- `ASIC_DMC_RESET` includes M3/DMC reset when `reset_m3=True` [chip_reset.py:208]()

**Stage 5: Xen Hot-plug Wait (if applicable)**
- Poll xenstore files for removal by host [chip_reset.py:228-256]()
- Timeout: 300 seconds (5 minutes) [chip_reset.py:216]()
- Uses parallel threads for multiple devices [chip_reset.py:250-256]()

**Stage 6: Post-reset Recovery**
- Wait for potential hot-plug removal [chip_reset.py:259-265]()
- Wait time: `m3_delay` if M3 reset, else `max(2, 0.4 * num_devices)` seconds [chip_reset.py:259]()
- Poll for device reappearance on PCI bus [chip_reset.py:87-111]()
- Issue `POST_RESET` IOCTL for driver cleanup [chip_reset.py:270]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-288]()

---

## Communication Mechanisms

### IOCTL Interface

The reset system communicates with the kernel driver through IOCTL calls to device nodes at `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}`.

**IOCTL Structure:**
```
Input struct:  "II" (output_size_bytes, flags)
Output struct: "II" (output_size_bytes, result)
IOCTL number:  0xFA06 (TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC << 8 | 6)
```

**IOCTL Reset Flags:**

| Flag Value | Enum Name | Operation | Used In |
|------------|-----------|-----------|---------|
| 0 | `RESTORE_STATE` | Restore PCI config space (legacy) | Legacy WH/BH reset |
| 1 | `RESET_PCIE_LINK` | Secondary bus reset | Modern and legacy |
| 2 | `CONFIG_WRITE` | Config space write reset (legacy BH) | Legacy BH reset |
| 3 | `USER_RESET` | User-initiated reset | Modern reset |
| 4 | `ASIC_RESET` | ASIC-only reset | Modern reset |
| 5 | `ASIC_DMC_RESET` | ASIC + M3/DMC reset | Modern reset |
| 6 | `POST_RESET` | Post-reset cleanup | Modern reset |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:25-32](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:56-58](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-85]()

### IOCTL Call Implementation

```mermaid
graph LR
    App["Application Code"]
    ResetFunc["reset_device_ioctl(interface_id, flags)"]
    OpenDev["Open /dev/tenstorrent/{id}"]
    PackStruct["Pack struct: output_size, flags"]
    IoctlCall["fcntl.ioctl(fd, 0xFA06, buf)"]
    UnpackResult["Unpack result from buffer"]
    CloseDev["Close file descriptor"]
    
    App --> ResetFunc
    ResetFunc --> OpenDev
    OpenDev --> PackStruct
    PackStruct --> IoctlCall
    IoctlCall --> UnpackResult
    UnpackResult --> CloseDev
```

The `reset_device_ioctl()` method:
1. Opens device node with `O_RDWR | O_CLOEXEC` flags [chip_reset.py:62-64]()
2. Packs input structure with output buffer size and flags [chip_reset.py:68-75]()
3. Calls `fcntl.ioctl()` with buffer [chip_reset.py:76-78]()
4. Unpacks result from output buffer [chip_reset.py:80-81]()
5. Returns `True` if result is 0 (success) [chip_reset.py:83]()
6. Always closes file descriptor in `finally` block [chip_reset.py:84-85]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-85](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:42-66](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:42-66]()

---

## Legacy vs Modern Implementation Migration

### Delegation Pattern Logic

Both `BHChipReset` and `WHChipReset` implement conditional delegation to `ChipReset` based on runtime conditions:

**Blackhole Delegation Logic:**
```
if is_driver_version_at_least("2.4.1") or check_xen_hvm():
    return ChipReset().full_lds_reset(...)
else:
    # Execute legacy BH reset implementation
```

**Wormhole Delegation Logic:**
```
if is_driver_version_at_least("2.4.1") or check_xen_hvm():
    return ChipReset().full_lds_reset(...)
else:
    # Execute legacy WH reset implementation
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:92-99](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:89-90]()

### Migration Status by Chip Type

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Blackhole (BH)"
        BH_Entry["BHChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
        BH_Check{"Driver >= 2.4.1<br/>or Xen HVM?"}
        BH_Modern["ChipReset<br/>(Modern Path)"]
        BH_Legacy["Legacy BH Implementation<br/>CONFIG_WRITE + polling"]
        
        BH_Entry --> BH_Check
        BH_Check -->|Yes| BH_Modern
        BH_Check -->|No| BH_Legacy
    end
    
    subgraph "Wormhole (WH)"
        WH_Entry["WHChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
        WH_Check{"Driver >= 2.4.1<br/>or Xen HVM?"}
        WH_Modern["ChipReset<br/>(Modern Path)"]
        WH_Legacy["Legacy WH Implementation<br/>ARC messages + refclk check"]
        
        WH_Entry --> WH_Check
        WH_Check -->|Yes| WH_Modern
        WH_Check -->|No| WH_Legacy
    end
    
    subgraph "Grayskull (GS)"
        GS_Entry["GSTensixReset.full_tensix_reset()"]
        GS_Impl["NOC-based Tensix reset<br/>(No migration planned)"]
        
        GS_Entry --> GS_Impl
    end
```

**Migration Notes:**
- **Blackhole**: Added in v1.4.6 [CHANGELOG.md:64](), M3 reset option added in v1.4.7 [CHANGELOG.md:55]()
- **Wormhole**: Legacy implementation includes refclk validation [wh_reset.py:157-164]()
- **Grayskull**: Uses separate Tensix-specific reset, no migration to ChipReset [CHANGELOG.md:111]()

**Deprecation Warning:** Legacy implementations print a yellow warning message when used, advising upgrade to driver v2.4.1+.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:101-107](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:92-98](), [CHANGELOG.md:55-65]()

### Key Differences: Legacy vs Modern

| Aspect | Legacy Implementation | Modern Implementation |
|--------|----------------------|----------------------|
| **Driver Requirement** | >= 1.26.0 | >= 2.4.1 |
| **IOCTL Flags** | `RESET_PCIE_LINK`, `RESTORE_STATE`, `CONFIG_WRITE` | `ASIC_RESET`, `ASIC_DMC_RESET`, `POST_RESET` |
| **Reset Validation** | Polling config space memory byte [bh_reset.py:173-179]() | IOCTL return values + device reappearance |
| **M3/DMC Reset** | ARC message 0x56 with arg0=3 [bh_reset.py:140]() | IOCTL with `ASIC_DMC_RESET` flag [chip_reset.py:208]() |
| **Xen HVM Support** | Not supported | Full xenstore coordination [chip_reset.py:167-256]() |
| **Device Re-enumeration** | Manual PCIe rescan | Handled by kernel driver |
| **Refclk Validation** | Manual check (WH only) [wh_reset.py:157-164]() | Not required (driver ensures reset) |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:68-224](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:68-181](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-288]()

---

## Error Handling and Exit Codes

The reset system uses explicit exit codes for fatal errors:

**Fatal Error Conditions:**
1. **ARM Platform Detected**: `sys.exit(1)` [chip_reset.py:148](), [bh_reset.py:118](), [wh_reset.py:112]()
2. **Device Timeout**: `sys.exit(1)` [chip_reset.py:109]()
3. **Post-reset Failure**: `sys.exit(1)` [chip_reset.py:278]()
4. **Config Space Reset Failed** (BH legacy): `sys.exit(failures)` [bh_reset.py:213]()
5. **Refclk Validation Failed** (WH legacy): `sys.exit(1)` [wh_reset.py:172]()
6. **Xen Timeout**: `sys.exit(1)` [chip_reset.py:248]()

**Warning Messages:**
- Legacy implementation usage warning (yellow) [bh_reset.py:102-107](), [wh_reset.py:93-98]()
- Secondary bus reset failure warning (yellow, non-fatal) [chip_reset.py:199-203]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:109](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:148](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:248](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:278](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:213](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:172]()
1a:T60a4,
# Reset Architecture and Design Patterns

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document explains the architectural design and key patterns used in the chip reset subsystem of tt-tools-common. It covers the delegation pattern that enables gradual migration from legacy to modern reset implementations, driver version requirements that trigger different code paths, pre-flight validation systems, and platform-specific considerations.

For implementation details of specific chip types, see [Blackhole Reset Implementation](#2.3), [Wormhole Reset Implementation](#2.4), [Grayskull Tensix Reset](#2.5), and [ChipReset: Modern Unified Reset](#2.2). For configuration and logging, see [Reset Configuration and Logging](#2.6). For virtualization details, see [Platform Support and Virtualization](#2.7).

---

## Overall Reset System Architecture

The reset system consists of four primary classes organized in a hierarchical delegation structure:

```mermaid
graph TD
    User["User Application<br/>(tt-smi, tt-flash)"]
    
    BHChipReset["BHChipReset<br/>tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py"]
    WHChipReset["WHChipReset<br/>tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py"]
    GSTensixReset["GSTensixReset<br/>tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_reset.py"]
    ChipReset["ChipReset<br/>tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py"]
    
    DriverCheck["is_driver_version_at_least()<br/>check_driver_version()"]
    XenCheck["check_xen_hvm()"]
    PlatformCheck["get_host_info()['Platform']"]
    
    PyLuwen["pyluwen.PciChip"]
    IOCTLInterface["IOCTL Interface<br/>/dev/tenstorrent/{id}"]
    
    User --> BHChipReset
    User --> WHChipReset
    User --> GSTensixReset
    
    BHChipReset -->|"driver >= 2.4.1 OR Xen HVM"| ChipReset
    BHChipReset -->|"driver < 2.4.1"| BHLegacy["Legacy BH Reset<br/>CONFIG_WRITE IOCTL"]
    
    WHChipReset -->|"driver >= 2.4.1 OR Xen HVM"| ChipReset
    WHChipReset -->|"driver < 2.4.1"| WHLegacy["Legacy WH Reset<br/>ARC Messages"]
    
    ChipReset --> DriverCheck
    ChipReset --> XenCheck
    ChipReset --> PlatformCheck
    
    ChipReset --> IOCTLInterface
    BHLegacy --> IOCTLInterface
    WHLegacy --> PyLuwen
    GSTensixReset --> PyLuwen
    
    IOCTLInterface --> Kernel["tt-kmd Driver"]
    PyLuwen --> IOCTLInterface
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:1-289](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:1-224](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:1-181]()

### Key Architectural Components

| Component | File Location | Primary Responsibility |
|-----------|--------------|----------------------|
| `ChipReset` | `reset_common/chip_reset.py` | Modern unified reset for BH and WH using new driver IOCTLs |
| `BHChipReset` | `reset_common/bh_reset.py` | Blackhole-specific reset with delegation logic |
| `WHChipReset` | `reset_common/wh_reset.py` | Wormhole-specific reset with delegation logic |
| `GSTensixReset` | `reset_common/gs_reset.py` | Grayskull Tensix core reset (no delegation) |
| `IoctlResetFlags` | `reset_common/chip_reset.py` | Enum defining reset operation types |
| `check_xen_hvm()` | `reset_common/chip_reset.py` | Detects Xen HVM virtualization environment |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:1-289](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:27-28](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:28-29]()

---

## Delegation Pattern for Legacy-to-Modern Migration

The reset system implements a **conditional delegation pattern** that allows gradual migration from legacy reset sequences to the modern unified implementation. This pattern appears in both `BHChipReset` and `WHChipReset`.

### Delegation Decision Logic

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["full_lds_reset() called"]
    CheckDriver{"is_driver_version_at_least()<br/>version >= 2.4.1?"}
    CheckXen{"check_xen_hvm()<br/>Running in Xen HVM?"}
    DelegateModern["Delegate to ChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
    LegacyPath["Execute Legacy Reset Sequence"]
    
    Start --> CheckDriver
    CheckDriver -->|Yes| DelegateModern
    CheckDriver -->|No| CheckXen
    CheckXen -->|Yes| DelegateModern
    CheckXen -->|No| LegacyPath
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:68-99](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:68-90]()

### Blackhole Delegation Implementation

The delegation logic in `BHChipReset.full_lds_reset()` evaluates two conditions before choosing a code path:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:90-99]()

```python
# Use new reset for driver version >= 2.4.1
# or perform reset using ChipReset class which handles Xen HVM case
if is_driver_version_at_least(get_driver_version(), "2.4.1") or check_xen_hvm():
    return ChipReset().full_lds_reset(
        pci_interfaces,
        reset_m3=reset_m3,
        silent=silent,
        m3_delay=m3_delay,
        secondary_bus_reset=secondary_bus_reset
    )
```

When neither condition is met, the legacy path executes with a deprecation warning:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:101-107]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:68-224]()

### Wormhole Delegation Implementation

`WHChipReset` follows an identical delegation pattern:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:88-90]()

```python
# Use new reset for driver version >= 2.4.1 or if in Xen HVM mode
if is_driver_version_at_least(get_driver_version(), "2.4.1") or check_xen_hvm():
    return ChipReset().full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces, reset_m3=reset_m3, silent=silent, secondary_bus_reset=secondary_bus_reset)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:68-90]()

### Migration Timeline

The delegation pattern enables the following migration strategy:

| Phase | Driver Version | Code Path | Status |
|-------|----------------|-----------|--------|
| Legacy Only | < 1.26.0 | Not supported | Deprecated |
| Legacy Supported | 1.26.0 - 2.4.0 | Legacy reset sequences | Maintained |
| Transition | 2.4.1+ | Modern `ChipReset` | Current |
| Modern Only | Future release | Legacy code removed | Planned |

**Sources:** [CHANGELOG.md:103-107](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:137]()

---

## Driver Version Requirements

The reset system has strict driver version dependencies that determine which reset implementations can be used.

### Version Check Architecture

```mermaid
graph TD
    ResetEntry["Reset Entry Point"]
    
    GetVersion["get_driver_version()<br/>Read /sys/module/tenstorrent/version"]
    
    CheckMinimum["check_driver_version()<br/>minimum: 1.26.0"]
    CheckModern["is_driver_version_at_least()<br/>check: 2.4.1"]
    
    ParseVersion["Parse Semantic Version<br/>Handle extraversion field<br/>(e.g. 1.28-bh)"]
    
    ResetEntry --> GetVersion
    GetVersion --> ParseVersion
    ParseVersion --> CheckMinimum
    ParseVersion --> CheckModern
    
    CheckMinimum -->|"< 1.26.0"| Fail["Exit with error"]
    CheckMinimum -->|">= 1.26.0"| Allow["Allow Legacy Reset"]
    
    CheckModern -->|"< 2.4.1"| Legacy["Use Legacy Path"]
    CheckModern -->|">= 2.4.1"| Modern["Use ChipReset"]
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:137]()

### Version Checking Functions

| Function | Purpose | Location |
|----------|---------|----------|
| `get_driver_version()` | Reads driver version from sysfs | `utils_common/system_utils.py` |
| `check_driver_version()` | Validates minimum version requirement | `utils_common/system_utils.py` |
| `is_driver_version_at_least()` | Compares against target version | `utils_common/system_utils.py` |

### Minimum Version Enforcement

The modern `ChipReset` class enforces driver version 2.4.1 as an absolute requirement:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:136-137]()

```python
# Check the driver version and bail if reset cannot be supported
check_driver_version(operation="reset", minimum_required_version_str="2.4.1")
```

Legacy implementations enforce driver version 1.26.0:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:100-101]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:136-137](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:100-101](), [CHANGELOG.md:103-107]()

### Extraversion Field Support

The version parsing system handles non-standard version strings with extraversion fields (e.g., `1.28-bh`):

[CHANGELOG.md:57-60]()

This enhancement was added to prevent crashes during version detection when the driver uses extraversion suffixes.

**Sources:** [CHANGELOG.md:57-60]()

---

## IOCTL Reset Flags Enumeration

The modern reset system uses a standardized set of IOCTL operation codes defined in the `IoctlResetFlags` enum:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:25-32]()

```python
class IoctlResetFlags(IntEnum):
    RESTORE_STATE = 0
    RESET_PCIE_LINK = 1
    CONFIG_WRITE = 2
    USER_RESET = 3
    ASIC_RESET = 4
    ASIC_DMC_RESET = 5
    POST_RESET = 6
```

### Reset Flag Usage

```mermaid
graph LR
    SBR["Secondary Bus Reset"]
    AsicReset["ASIC Reset"]
    AsicDmcReset["ASIC + DMC Reset"]
    PostReset["Post-Reset Validation"]
    
    SBR -->|"IoctlResetFlags.RESET_PCIE_LINK"| IOCTL1["reset_device_ioctl()"]
    AsicReset -->|"IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_RESET"| IOCTL2["reset_device_ioctl()"]
    AsicDmcReset -->|"IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_DMC_RESET"| IOCTL3["reset_device_ioctl()"]
    PostReset -->|"IoctlResetFlags.POST_RESET"| IOCTL4["reset_device_ioctl()"]
```

| Flag | Value | Purpose | When Used |
|------|-------|---------|-----------|
| `RESTORE_STATE` | 0 | Legacy state restoration | Legacy BH/WH only |
| `RESET_PCIE_LINK` | 1 | Secondary bus reset (SBR) | Optional pre-reset phase |
| `CONFIG_WRITE` | 2 | Legacy config space reset | Legacy BH only |
| `USER_RESET` | 3 | Reserved for future use | Not currently used |
| `ASIC_RESET` | 4 | ASIC-only reset | Default reset operation |
| `ASIC_DMC_RESET` | 5 | ASIC + M3/DMC reset | When `reset_m3=True` |
| `POST_RESET` | 6 | Post-reset state restoration | Always after device reappears |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:25-32](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:196-213]()

### IOCTL Implementation

All reset operations use the same IOCTL interface but with different flag values:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-85]()

The IOCTL magic numbers are consistent across implementations:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:56-58]()

```python
TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC = 0xFA
TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_RESET_DEVICE = (TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC << 8) | 6
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:56-85]()

---

## Pre-flight Validation System

Before executing any reset operation, the system performs multiple validation checks to ensure the reset can succeed. These checks follow a fail-fast pattern where any validation failure terminates the operation immediately.

### Validation Sequence

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["full_lds_reset() Entry"]
    
    CheckDriver["check_driver_version()<br/>Minimum: 2.4.1"]
    CheckPlatform["get_host_info()['Platform']<br/>Check for ARM/AARCH"]
    CheckXen["check_xen_hvm()<br/>Detect Xen HVM guest"]
    RemoveDups["Remove Duplicate PCI Interfaces<br/>list(set(pci_interfaces))"]
    
    DriverFail["Print error message<br/>Exit with code 1"]
    PlatformFail["Print ARM restriction message<br/>Exit with code 1"]
    
    ProceedReset["Proceed with Reset Sequence"]
    
    Start --> CheckDriver
    CheckDriver -->|"< 2.4.1"| DriverFail
    CheckDriver -->|">= 2.4.1"| CheckPlatform
    
    CheckPlatform -->|"ARM detected"| PlatformFail
    CheckPlatform -->|"x86"| RemoveDups
    
    RemoveDups --> CheckXen
    CheckXen --> ProceedReset
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:136-155]()

### Validation Checks

#### 1. Driver Version Check

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:136-137]()

Ensures the kernel driver supports the modern reset IOCTLs. Minimum version 2.4.1 is required for `ChipReset`.

#### 2. Platform Architecture Check

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:139-148]()

ARM-based systems cannot properly handle PCIe device rescans after reset. The validation exits if ARM is detected:

```python
platform = get_host_info()["Platform"]
if platform.startswith("arm") or platform.startswith("aarch"):
    print(
        CMD_LINE_COLOR.RED,
        "Cannot perform board reset on Arm systems, please reboot the system to reset the boards. Exiting...",
        CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC,
    )
    sys.exit(1)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:139-148](), [CHANGELOG.md:82-85]()

#### 3. Xen HVM Detection

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:34-51]()

The `check_xen_hvm()` function reads sysfs to determine if the system is a Xen HVM guest:

```python
def check_xen_hvm() -> bool:
    """Check if the system is a Xen HVM guest"""
    is_xen_hvm = False
    try:
        with open("/sys/hypervisor/type", "r") as f:
            hypervisor_type = f.read().strip()
        with open("/sys/hypervisor/guest_type", "r") as f:
            guest_type = f.read().strip()
        if hypervisor_type == "xen" and guest_type == "HVM":
            is_xen_hvm = True
    except FileNotFoundError:
        pass
    except OSError:
        pass
    return is_xen_hvm
```

When Xen HVM is detected, the reset sequence includes xenstore coordination (see [Platform Support and Virtualization](#2.7)).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:34-51](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:167-193]()

#### 4. Duplicate Removal

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:150-151]()

Ensures each PCI interface is reset only once:

```python
# Remove duplicates from the input list of PCI interfaces
pci_interfaces = list(set(pci_interfaces))
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:150-151]()

---

## Three-Phase Reset Sequence

The modern reset implementation follows a three-phase execution model with distinct pre-reset, reset, and post-reset stages.

### Phase Overview

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant App as Application
    participant CR as ChipReset
    participant IOCTL as IOCTL Interface
    participant Driver as tt-kmd Driver
    participant HW as Hardware
    
    Note over App,HW: Phase 1: Pre-Reset
    App->>CR: full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces)
    CR->>CR: Validation checks
    CR->>CR: Collect PCI BDF addresses
    CR->>CR: Check Xen HVM
    
    alt Xen HVM Detected
        CR->>Driver: xenstore-write (notify host)
    end
    
    alt secondary_bus_reset=True
        CR->>IOCTL: RESET_PCIE_LINK
        IOCTL->>Driver: Secondary Bus Reset
        Driver->>HW: SBR on PCIe bridge
    end
    
    Note over App,HW: Phase 2: Reset
    CR->>IOCTL: ASIC_RESET or ASIC_DMC_RESET
    IOCTL->>Driver: Trigger device reset
    Driver->>HW: Reset sequence
    HW-->>Driver: Device goes offline
    
    alt Xen HVM
        CR->>Driver: xenstore-read (poll for removal)
        Driver->>CR: Host removed xenstore entry
    end
    
    CR->>CR: sleep(post_reset_wait)
    HW-->>Driver: Device reappears
    
    Note over App,HW: Phase 3: Post-Reset
    CR->>CR: wait_for_device_to_reappear()
    CR->>IOCTL: POST_RESET
    IOCTL->>Driver: Restore device state
    Driver-->>CR: Success
    CR-->>App: List[PciChip]
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-288]()

### Phase 1: Pre-Reset Setup

Pre-reset activities prepare the system for the reset operation:

1. **BDF Collection**: Store Bus:Device.Function addresses for each PCI interface ([tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:159-165]())
2. **File Descriptor Cleanup**: Force garbage collection to close pyluwen handles ([tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:163-165]())
3. **Xenstore Notification**: If Xen HVM, write `1` to xenstore path ([tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:167-193]())
4. **Secondary Bus Reset**: Optionally perform SBR to reset PCIe link ([tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:195-203]())

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:159-203]()

### Phase 2: Reset Execution

The actual reset is triggered via IOCTL with one of two flags:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:206-212]()

```python
for pci_interface in pci_interfaces:
    if reset_m3:
        reset_flag = IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_DMC_RESET
    else:
        reset_flag = IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_RESET
    
    self.reset_device_ioctl(pci_interface, reset_flag)
```

For Xen HVM systems, the process waits for the host to remove xenstore entries, indicating PCIe hot-unplug completion ([tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:214-256]()).

After issuing resets, the system waits for devices to become available:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:259-265]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:206-265]()

### Phase 3: Post-Reset Validation

After the wait period, the system validates that devices have returned:

1. **Device Reappearance**: Poll sysfs for device node ([tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:87-111]())
2. **Post-Reset IOCTL**: Restore device state ([tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:270-278]())
3. **Success Verification**: Check IOCTL return value

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:267-278]()

If post-reset operations fail, the system exits with a non-zero status ([tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:275-278]()).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:87-111](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:267-288]()

---

## Communication Mechanisms

The reset system uses three distinct hardware communication methods depending on the chip type and code path.

### Communication Method Selection

```mermaid
graph TD
    ResetOp["Reset Operation"]
    
    Modern["Modern ChipReset"]
    LegacyBH["Legacy BHChipReset"]
    LegacyWH["Legacy WHChipReset"]
    GSReset["GSTensixReset"]
    
    IOCTL["IOCTL Calls<br/>fcntl.ioctl()"]
    ARC["ARC Messages<br/>chip.arc_msg()"]
    NOC["NOC Operations<br/>noc_read32/write32"]
    
    ResetOp --> Modern
    ResetOp --> LegacyBH
    ResetOp --> LegacyWH
    ResetOp --> GSReset
    
    Modern --> IOCTL
    LegacyBH --> IOCTL
    LegacyWH --> ARC
    GSReset --> NOC
    
    IOCTL --> Driver["/dev/tenstorrent/{id}"]
    ARC --> PyLuwen["pyluwen.PciChip"]
    NOC --> PyLuwen
    
    Driver --> Kernel["tt-kmd Kernel Driver"]
    PyLuwen --> Kernel
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-85](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:142-144](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:143-149]()

### IOCTL Communication

The primary mechanism for modern and legacy BH resets. Direct system calls to the kernel driver:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-85]()

**IOCTL Structure:**
- Input: `output_size_bytes, flags` (8 bytes)
- Output: `output_size_bytes, result` (8 bytes)
- Device path: `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}`
- IOCTL command: `0xFA06` (magic: 0xFA, number: 6)

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:56-85]()

### ARC Message Communication

Legacy Wormhole resets use ARC (Autonomic Reset Controller) messages sent through pyluwen:

[tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:143-149]()

**ARC Message Types:**

| Message Type | Value | Purpose |
|-------------|-------|---------|
| `MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3` | 0xA3 | Enter safe state (no pending regulator requests) |
| `MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET` | 0x56 | Trigger reset sequence |
| `MSG_TRIGGER_SPI_COPY_LtoR` | 0x50 | SPI flash copy (not used in reset) |

The legacy WH sequence sends messages in order:
1. `MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3` with `wait_for_done=True`
2. Sleep for `A3_STATE_PROP_TIME` (0.03s)
3. `MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET` with `wait_for_done=False`

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:36-40](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:143-149]()

### NOC Communication

Grayskull Tensix reset uses Network-on-Chip read/write operations directly through pyluwen's NOC interface. This is documented in detail in [Grayskull Tensix Reset](#2.5).

**Sources:** Referenced in architecture diagrams, detailed implementation in `gs_reset.py`

---

## Legacy vs Modern Implementation Comparison

### Architectural Differences

| Aspect | Legacy (BH/WH) | Modern (ChipReset) |
|--------|---------------|-------------------|
| **Driver Version** | 1.26.0 - 2.4.0 | 2.4.1+ |
| **Reset Mechanism** | CONFIG_WRITE (BH), ARC messages (WH) | ASIC_RESET / ASIC_DMC_RESET |
| **Config Space Polling** | Manual byte-by-byte polling | Handled by driver |
| **Device Reappearance** | Immediate (no hotplug) | Explicit wait with BDF matching |
| **Xen Support** | None | Xenstore coordination |
| **Error Handling** | Reset bit polling with timeout | IOCTL return codes |
| **State Restoration** | `RESTORE_STATE` flag | `POST_RESET` flag |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:142-213](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:121-172](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-288]()

### Legacy Blackhole Reset Sequence

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant App
    participant BH as BHChipReset
    participant Kernel as Driver
    participant Sysfs
    
    App->>BH: full_lds_reset()
    BH->>BH: Collect PCI BDF
    
    alt reset_m3=True
        BH->>Kernel: chip.arc_msg(MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET, arg0=3)
    else
        BH->>Kernel: IOCTL CONFIG_WRITE
    end
    
    loop Poll for up to POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME
        BH->>Sysfs: Read config space byte 4
        Sysfs-->>BH: Reset bit value
        alt Reset bit == 0
            BH->>BH: Mark complete
        end
    end
    
    BH->>Kernel: IOCTL RESTORE_STATE
    BH-->>App: List[PciChip]
```

The legacy BH implementation polls the PCIe configuration space to detect reset completion ([tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:152-205]()):

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:130-223]()

### Legacy Wormhole Reset Sequence

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant App
    participant WH as WHChipReset
    participant PyLuwen
    participant Driver
    
    App->>WH: full_lds_reset()
    WH->>Driver: IOCTL RESET_PCIE_LINK
    WH->>WH: Create PciChip objects
    
    loop For each chip
        WH->>PyLuwen: read_refclk_counter()
        PyLuwen-->>WH: Pre-reset refclk value
        WH->>PyLuwen: arc_msg(MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3)
        WH->>WH: sleep(A3_STATE_PROP_TIME)
        WH->>PyLuwen: arc_msg(MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET)
    end
    
    WH->>WH: sleep(POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME)
    
    loop For each chip
        WH->>Driver: IOCTL RESTORE_STATE
        WH->>PyLuwen: read_refclk_counter()
        PyLuwen-->>WH: Post-reset refclk value
        alt refclk not decreased
            WH->>WH: Mark as failed
        end
    end
    
    WH-->>App: List[PciChip] or exit(1)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:114-180]()

### Migration Benefits

The modern `ChipReset` implementation addresses several limitations of the legacy approach:

1. **Unified Code Path**: Single implementation for both BH and WH
2. **Kernel-Managed Hotplug**: Driver handles PCIe device removal/reappearance
3. **Proper Xen Support**: Xenstore-based coordination for virtualized environments
4. **Cleaner Error Handling**: IOCTL return codes instead of timeout-based polling
5. **Secondary Bus Reset**: Optional PCIe link reset before ASIC reset

**Sources:** [CHANGELOG.md:63-65](), [CHANGELOG.md:82-85]()

---

## Summary of Design Patterns

### 1. Conditional Delegation Pattern

Chip-specific classes delegate to the modern implementation when conditions are met, enabling gradual migration without breaking existing tools.

### 2. Fail-Fast Validation Pattern

Pre-flight checks (driver version, platform, Xen detection) fail immediately with clear error messages, preventing partial reset attempts.

### 3. Three-Phase Reset Pattern

Separation of pre-reset setup, reset execution, and post-reset validation provides clear structure and error isolation.

### 4. Communication Abstraction Pattern

Different hardware communication methods (IOCTL, ARC, NOC) are encapsulated within reset classes, hiding complexity from callers.

### 5. Version-Gated Migration Pattern

Driver version checks gate access to new features while maintaining backward compatibility through legacy code paths.

**Sources:** All files referenced throughout this document
1b:T560e,
# ChipReset: Modern Unified Reset

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document describes the `ChipReset` class, the modern unified reset implementation for Blackhole and Wormhole chips introduced in driver version 2.4.1. `ChipReset` provides a standardized interface for performing chip-level resets using improved IOCTL commands and supports advanced features including secondary bus reset (SBR), M3/DMC reset, and Xen HVM virtualization coordination.

For chip-specific reset logic that delegates to `ChipReset`, see [Blackhole Reset Implementation](#2.3) and [Wormhole Reset Implementation](#2.4). For the overall reset architecture and migration strategy from legacy implementations, see [Reset Architecture and Design Patterns](#2.1). For Grayskull reset procedures, which use a different approach, see [Grayskull Tensix Reset](#2.5).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:1-289]()

---

## Class Overview

The `ChipReset` class is located in [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:53-288]() and serves as the modern unified implementation for chip-level resets on both Blackhole and Wormhole PCIe boards. It is invoked by chip-specific reset classes when driver version >= 2.4.1 or when running in Xen HVM mode.

```mermaid
graph TD
    BHChipReset["BHChipReset.full_lds_reset"]
    WHChipReset["WHChipReset.full_lds_reset"]
    VersionCheck{"Driver >= 2.4.1<br/>or Xen HVM?"}
    ChipReset["ChipReset.full_lds_reset"]
    LegacyBH["Legacy BH IOCTL"]
    LegacyWH["Legacy WH ARC"]
    
    BHChipReset --> VersionCheck
    WHChipReset --> VersionCheck
    VersionCheck -->|Yes| ChipReset
    VersionCheck -->|No| LegacyBH
    VersionCheck -->|No| LegacyWH
```

**Delegation Pattern**: Chip-specific classes (`BHChipReset`, `WHChipReset`) conditionally delegate to `ChipReset` based on driver version and platform capabilities. This enables gradual migration from legacy implementations while maintaining backward compatibility.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:53-54](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:90-99]()

---

## IOCTL Interface

The `ChipReset` class communicates with the kernel driver via IOCTL commands to the `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}` device file. The IOCTL interface is defined by magic numbers and structured flags.

### IOCTL Constants

| Constant | Value | Description |
|----------|-------|-------------|
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC` | `0xFA` | Magic number identifying Tenstorrent IOCTL operations |
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_RESET_DEVICE` | `0xFA06` | IOCTL command for device reset operations |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:57-58]()

### IoctlResetFlags Enumeration

The `IoctlResetFlags` enum [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:25-32]() defines the operation flags passed to the reset IOCTL:

| Flag | Value | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| `RESTORE_STATE` | 0 | Restore PCIe configuration state after reset |
| `RESET_PCIE_LINK` | 1 | Perform secondary bus reset (SBR) |
| `CONFIG_WRITE` | 2 | Legacy config space write reset |
| `USER_RESET` | 3 | User-initiated reset |
| `ASIC_RESET` | 4 | Reset ASIC only |
| `ASIC_DMC_RESET` | 5 | Reset ASIC including M3/DMC |
| `POST_RESET` | 6 | Post-reset cleanup and validation |

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant App as "ChipReset"
    participant Dev as "/dev/tenstorrent/{id}"
    participant KMD as "tt-kmd Driver"
    participant HW as "Hardware"
    
    App->>Dev: open(O_RDWR | O_CLOEXEC)
    App->>Dev: fcntl.ioctl(RESET_DEVICE, flags)
    Dev->>KMD: Process IOCTL
    KMD->>HW: Execute reset operation
    HW-->>KMD: Operation result
    KMD-->>Dev: Return status
    Dev-->>App: Result (0=success)
    App->>Dev: close()
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:25-32](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-85]()

### reset_device_ioctl Method

The `reset_device_ioctl` method [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-85]() is the low-level interface for sending IOCTL commands:

**Method Signature:**
```python
def reset_device_ioctl(self, interface_id: int, flags: int) -> bool
```

**Parameters:**
- `interface_id`: PCI interface number (e.g., 0, 1, 2)
- `flags`: `IoctlResetFlags` value specifying the operation

**Returns:** `True` if successful (result == 0), `False` otherwise

**Structure Format:** The method uses a structured binary format for IOCTL communication:
- Input: `II` (2 unsigned integers: output_size_bytes, flags)
- Output: `II` (2 unsigned integers: unused, result)

**Error Handling:** The method propagates exceptions from file operations (`FileNotFoundError`) and IOCTL calls (`OSError`). The file descriptor is guaranteed to close via the `finally` block.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-85]()

---

## Secondary Bus Reset

Secondary Bus Reset (SBR) is a PCIe-level reset mechanism that resets all devices on a bus segment. `ChipReset` performs SBR as the first step in the reset sequence when `secondary_bus_reset=True`.

```mermaid
graph LR
    Start["Start Reset"]
    SBR{"secondary_bus_reset?"}
    DoSBR["Issue SBR IOCTL<br/>RESET_PCIE_LINK"]
    CheckSBR{"SBR Success?"}
    WarnSBR["Print Warning<br/>Continue Anyway"]
    ASICReset["ASIC Reset"]
    
    Start --> SBR
    SBR -->|True| DoSBR
    SBR -->|False| ASICReset
    DoSBR --> CheckSBR
    CheckSBR -->|False| WarnSBR
    CheckSBR -->|True| ASICReset
    WarnSBR --> ASICReset
```

**Implementation:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:195-203]()

The SBR step iterates through all PCI interfaces and calls `reset_device_ioctl` with `IoctlResetFlags.RESET_PCIE_LINK`. If SBR fails for a device, a warning is printed but the reset sequence continues. This non-fatal behavior ensures that ASIC reset can proceed even if SBR is not supported or fails on the platform.

**Why SBR First:** Performing SBR before ASIC reset helps clean up any PCIe link state issues and provides a more thorough reset of the PCIe hierarchy.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:195-203]()

---

## ASIC Reset Sequence

After optional secondary bus reset, `ChipReset` performs the ASIC-level reset using either `ASIC_RESET` or `ASIC_DMC_RESET` flags.

### Reset Flag Selection

The reset flag is selected based on the `reset_m3` parameter [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:206-212]():

| Condition | Flag | Behavior |
|-----------|------|----------|
| `reset_m3=True` | `ASIC_DMC_RESET` | Resets ASIC including M3 management processor and DMC |
| `reset_m3=False` | `ASIC_RESET` | Resets ASIC only, preserving M3 state |

**M3 Reset Timing:** When `reset_m3=True`, the post-reset wait time is set to the `m3_delay` parameter (default 20 seconds) to allow time for M3 firmware to reinitialize. During board management firmware (BMFW) upgrades, the M3 reset can take 60 seconds or more [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:138-140]().

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["Issue ASIC Reset IOCTL"]
    M3Check{"reset_m3?"}
    DMCReset["Flag: ASIC_DMC_RESET<br/>Wait: m3_delay"]
    ASICReset["Flag: ASIC_RESET<br/>Wait: 0.4 * len(pci_interfaces)"]
    Hotplug["Wait for Hotplug<br/>Removal/Reappearance"]
    PostReset["POST_RESET IOCTL"]
    Done["Reset Complete"]
    
    Start --> M3Check
    M3Check -->|True| DMCReset
    M3Check -->|False| ASICReset
    DMCReset --> Hotplug
    ASICReset --> Hotplug
    Hotplug --> PostReset
    PostReset --> Done
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:206-212](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:259-265]()

---

## Xen HVM Support

`ChipReset` includes special handling for Xen Hardware Virtual Machine (HVM) environments to coordinate PCIe device removal and reappearance with the hypervisor host.

### Xen HVM Detection

The `check_xen_hvm` function [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:34-51]() determines if the system is running as a Xen HVM guest:

```python
def check_xen_hvm() -> bool:
    """Check if the system is a Xen HVM guest"""
```

**Detection Logic:**
1. Read `/sys/hypervisor/type` → must be `"xen"`
2. Read `/sys/hypervisor/guest_type` → must be `"HVM"`
3. Return `True` if both conditions met, `False` otherwise

**Error Handling:** `FileNotFoundError` and `OSError` are caught and treated as "not Xen HVM". Other exceptions propagate.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:34-51]()

### Xenstore Coordination Protocol

When running in Xen HVM mode, `ChipReset` uses xenstore to coordinate with the host during PCIe hotplug operations:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Guest as "VM Guest (ChipReset)"
    participant XS as "Xenstore"
    participant Host as "Xen Host/Dom0"
    participant PCIe as "PCIe Bus"
    
    Guest->>Guest: Detect Xen HVM mode
    Guest->>Guest: Request sudo credentials
    Guest->>XS: xenstore-write {filename} "1"
    Note over XS: Signal reset start
    Guest->>PCIe: Issue ASIC reset IOCTL
    PCIe->>Host: Hotplug removal event
    Host->>XS: Remove {filename}
    Note over XS: Signal hotplug complete
    loop Every 1 second, max 5 minutes
        Guest->>XS: xenstore-read {filename}
        XS-->>Guest: File exists/not found
    end
    Guest->>Guest: Continue when file removed
    Guest->>PCIe: wait_for_device_to_reappear
```

**Xenstore Filename Format:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:178-180]()
```
pci_hard_reset/{bus}_{device}-{function}
```
Example: `pci_hard_reset/01_00-0` for BDF `0000:01:00.0`

**Parallel Thread Waiting:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:228-256]()

For multiple devices, `ChipReset` spawns parallel threads to wait for each xenstore file removal simultaneously. This prevents sequential timeout delays when resetting multiple devices.

**Timeout:** 5 minutes (300 seconds) per device. If the xenstore file is not removed within this time, the reset exits with an error [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:216]().

**Sudo Requirement:** Xenstore operations require sudo privileges. The user is prompted once at the start [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:170-174]() and credentials are revalidated before waiting [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:223-227]().

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:167-256]()

---

## Device Reappearance

After ASIC reset, devices may be temporarily removed from the PCIe bus (hotplug removal) and then reappear with potentially new interface IDs. The `wait_for_device_to_reappear` method handles this scenario.

### wait_for_device_to_reappear Method

**Method Signature:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:87-111]()
```python
def wait_for_device_to_reappear(self, bdf: str, timeout: int = 10) -> int
```

**Parameters:**
- `bdf`: PCIe Bus:Device.Function identifier (e.g., `"0000:01:00.0"`)
- `timeout`: Maximum seconds to wait (default: 10)

**Returns:** New PCI interface ID for the reappeared device

**Algorithm:**
1. Poll `/sys/bus/pci/devices/{bdf}/tenstorrent/tenstorrent!*` for device node
2. Extract interface ID from filename (e.g., `tenstorrent!0` → `0`)
3. Verify `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}` exists
4. Return interface ID when device is accessible
5. Exit with error if timeout expires

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["wait_for_device_to_reappear(bdf)"]
    Poll["Poll sysfs path:<br/>/sys/bus/pci/devices/{bdf}/tenstorrent/*"]
    Found{"Match found?"}
    Extract["Extract interface_id<br/>from filename"]
    CheckDev{"/dev/tenstorrent/{id}<br/>exists?"}
    Return["Return interface_id"]
    Timeout{"Time < deadline?"}
    Error["Exit with error"]
    
    Start --> Poll
    Poll --> Found
    Found -->|No| Timeout
    Found -->|Yes| Extract
    Extract --> CheckDev
    CheckDev -->|Yes| Return
    CheckDev -->|No| Timeout
    Timeout -->|Yes| Poll
    Timeout -->|No| Error
```

**Why Interface IDs Change:** During hotplug removal and reappearance, the kernel driver may assign a different interface ID to the device. The original interface ID cannot be used after the device reappears.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:87-111]()

---

## Full LDS Reset Method

The `full_lds_reset` method [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-288]() is the main entry point for performing a complete chip reset sequence.

### Method Signature

```python
def full_lds_reset(
    self,
    pci_interfaces: List[int],
    reset_m3: bool = False,
    silent: bool = False,
    m3_delay: int = 20,
    secondary_bus_reset: bool = True,
) -> List[PciChip]:
```

### Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `pci_interfaces` | `List[int]` | Required | List of PCI interface numbers to reset |
| `reset_m3` | `bool` | `False` | Whether to reset M3/DMC (management processor) |
| `silent` | `bool` | `False` | Suppress informational print statements |
| `m3_delay` | `int` | `20` | Seconds to wait after M3 reset |
| `secondary_bus_reset` | `bool` | `True` | Perform secondary bus reset before ASIC reset |

### Return Value

Returns a `List[PciChip]` containing pyluwen `PciChip` objects for all successfully reset devices.

### Complete Reset Flow

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces, ...)"]
    Validate["Validate:<br/>- Driver >= 2.4.1<br/>- Not ARM platform<br/>- Deduplicate interfaces"]
    BDF["Collect PCI BDF for each device"]
    XenCheck{"Xen HVM?"}
    XenWrite["Write '1' to xenstore files<br/>(parallel for all devices)"]
    SBRCheck{"secondary_bus_reset?"}
    SBR["Issue SBR IOCTL<br/>RESET_PCIE_LINK"]
    M3Check{"reset_m3?"}
    ASICDMCReset["IOCTL: ASIC_DMC_RESET"]
    ASICReset["IOCTL: ASIC_RESET"]
    XenWait["Wait for xenstore files removed<br/>(parallel threads, 5min timeout)"]
    Sleep["Sleep: post_reset_wait seconds"]
    Reappear["wait_for_device_to_reappear<br/>for each device"]
    PostReset["IOCTL: POST_RESET"]
    Success["Return List[PciChip]"]
    
    Start --> Validate
    Validate --> BDF
    BDF --> XenCheck
    XenCheck -->|Yes| XenWrite
    XenCheck -->|No| SBRCheck
    XenWrite --> SBRCheck
    SBRCheck -->|True| SBR
```
