```mermaid
    SBRCheck -->|False| M3Check
    SBR --> M3Check
    M3Check -->|True| ASICDMCReset
    M3Check -->|False| ASICReset
    ASICDMCReset --> XenWait
    ASICReset --> XenWait
    XenWait --> Sleep
    Sleep --> Reappear
    Reappear --> PostReset
    PostReset --> Success
```

### Pre-Flight Validation

Before executing the reset, the method performs three critical checks [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:136-148]():

1. **Driver Version:** Calls `check_driver_version(operation="reset", minimum_required_version_str="2.4.1")` to ensure driver >= 2.4.1
2. **Platform Check:** Rejects ARM platforms (`arm` or `aarch` prefix) as they don't support PCIe device rescans
3. **Deduplication:** Removes duplicate PCI interfaces from the input list using `list(set(pci_interfaces))`

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-288]()

### BDF Collection and Cleanup

The method collects PCIe Bus:Device.Function (BDF) strings for all devices and explicitly deletes chip objects to close file descriptors [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:157-165]():

```python
for pci_interface in pci_interfaces:
    chip = PciChip(pci_interface=pci_interface)
    bdf = chip.get_pci_bdf()
    bdf_list.append(bdf)
    # Force garbage collection of the chip object to close any open file descriptors
    # This is necessary for dockerized containers
    del chip
```

This cleanup is critical in containerized environments where file descriptor limits may be restrictive.

### Post-Reset Wait Calculation

The sleep duration after ASIC reset depends on the reset type [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:259]():

- **M3 Reset:** `post_reset_wait = m3_delay` (default 20 seconds)
- **Standard Reset:** `post_reset_wait = max(2, 0.4 * len(pci_interfaces))` (scales with device count)

This scaled timing accounts for staggered hotplug removal when multiple devices are reset.

---

## Platform and Driver Requirements

### Minimum Driver Version

`ChipReset` requires tt-kmd driver version **2.4.1 or higher**. This requirement is enforced at the start of `full_lds_reset` via [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:137]():

```python
check_driver_version(operation="reset", minimum_required_version_str="2.4.1")
```

If the driver version is insufficient, the method raises an exception and exits. For details on driver version checking, see [Driver Version Management](#3.1).

### Platform Restrictions

**ARM Platform Limitation:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:139-148]()

`ChipReset` does not support ARM or aarch64 platforms due to PCIe device rescan limitations on those architectures. If the platform is detected as ARM-based, the method prints an error and exits:

```
Cannot perform board reset on Arm systems, please reboot the system to reset the boards. Exiting...
```

**Platform Detection:** Uses `get_host_info()["Platform"]` to retrieve platform string and checks for `"arm"` or `"aarch"` prefix.

**Workaround:** On ARM systems, users must perform a full system reboot to reset Tenstorrent chips.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:137-148]()

---

## Error Handling and Exit Codes

### IOCTL Failures

The `reset_device_ioctl` method can raise exceptions:
- **`FileNotFoundError`:** Device file `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}` does not exist
- **`OSError`:** IOCTL operation failed in kernel driver

These exceptions propagate to the caller and typically result in program termination.

### Secondary Bus Reset Warnings

SBR failures are non-fatal [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:199-203]():
```python
if not self.reset_device_ioctl(pci_interface, IoctlResetFlags.RESET_PCIE_LINK):
    print(CMD_LINE_COLOR.YELLOW,
          f"Warning: Secondary bus reset not completed for device at PCI index {pci_interface}. Continuing with reset.",
          CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC)
```

The reset sequence continues even if SBR fails, as ASIC reset may still succeed.

### Device Reappearance Timeout

If a device fails to reappear within 10 seconds, the method exits [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:103-109]():
```python
if not device_reappeared:
    print(CMD_LINE_COLOR.RED,
          f"Timeout waiting for device at PCI index {interface_id} to reappear.",
          CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC)
    sys.exit(1)
```

### Xen Xenstore Timeout

In Xen HVM mode, if a xenstore file is not removed by the host within 5 minutes, the method exits [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:245-248]():
```python
print(CMD_LINE_COLOR.RED,
      f"Timeout waiting for xenstore file {xenstore_filename} to be removed. Exiting...",
      CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC)
sys.exit(1)
```

### Post-Reset IOCTL Failure

If the `POST_RESET` IOCTL fails, the method prints an error and exits [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:275-278]():
```python
else:
    print(CMD_LINE_COLOR.RED,
          f"Post-reset actions did not complete successfully for device at PCI index {pci_interface}.",
          CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC)
    sys.exit(1)
```

**Exit Code Strategy:** The method uses `sys.exit(1)` for fatal errors, ensuring that calling scripts can detect failures via non-zero exit codes.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-288]()

---

## Integration with Chip-Specific Reset Classes

The `ChipReset` class is not typically invoked directly by end users. Instead, chip-specific reset classes delegate to it when appropriate conditions are met.

### BHChipReset Delegation

From [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:92-99]():

```python
# Use new reset for driver version >= 2.4.1
# or perform reset using ChipReset class which handles Xen HVM case
if is_driver_version_at_least(get_driver_version(), "2.4.1") or check_xen_hvm():
    return ChipReset().full_lds_reset(
        pci_interfaces,
        reset_m3=reset_m3,
        silent=silent,
        m3_delay=m3_delay,
        secondary_bus_reset=secondary_bus_reset
    )
```

**Delegation Conditions:**
1. Driver version >= 2.4.1, OR
2. Running in Xen HVM mode (regardless of driver version)

If neither condition is met, `BHChipReset` uses its legacy implementation with config space polling.

### WHChipReset Delegation

Wormhole reset follows the same delegation pattern, checking driver version and Xen HVM status before deciding between `ChipReset` and legacy ARC message-based reset. For details, see [Wormhole Reset Implementation](#2.4).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:92-99]()

---

## Summary

The `ChipReset` class provides a modern, unified reset implementation with the following key features:

| Feature | Description |
|---------|-------------|
| **IOCTL Interface** | Structured binary protocol with `IoctlResetFlags` for various reset operations |
| **Secondary Bus Reset** | Optional PCIe-level reset before ASIC reset |
| **M3/DMC Reset** | Support for management processor reset with configurable delays |
| **Xen HVM Support** | Xenstore coordination with parallel thread waiting for multi-device scenarios |
| **Device Hotplug** | Automatic detection of device reappearance with new interface IDs |
| **Platform Validation** | Driver version and architecture checks prevent unsupported operations |
| **Delegation Pattern** | Chip-specific classes transparently upgrade to `ChipReset` when available |

**Migration Path:** The architecture allows gradual adoption as users upgrade to driver version 2.4.1+, with legacy implementations maintained for backward compatibility.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:1-289](), [CHANGELOG.md:97-119]()
1c:T38bd,
# Blackhole Reset Implementation

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document details the Blackhole-specific chip reset implementation provided by the `BHChipReset` class. It covers the legacy IOCTL-based reset sequence, the M3 reset option, and the delegation pattern that routes to the modern unified reset system when available. 

For the modern unified reset implementation used by both Blackhole and Wormhole when driver version >= 2.4.1, see [ChipReset: Modern Unified Reset](#2.2). For reset architecture patterns and driver version requirements, see [Reset Architecture and Design Patterns](#2.1). For reset configuration and logging, see [Reset Configuration and Logging](#2.6).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:1-224](), [CHANGELOG.md:55-65]()

---

## Architecture Overview

The Blackhole reset system implements a **delegation pattern** that conditionally routes to different implementations based on driver version and virtualization environment. This enables gradual migration from the legacy IOCTL-based reset to the modern unified reset system while maintaining backward compatibility.

### Reset Implementation Selection Flow

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["BHChipReset.full_lds_reset()"] --> CheckDriver{"Driver >= 2.4.1<br/>OR<br/>Xen HVM?"}
    
    CheckDriver -->|Yes| Modern["ChipReset().full_lds_reset()"]
    CheckDriver -->|No| Warning["Print Legacy Warning"]
    
    Warning --> CheckPlatform{"Platform == ARM?"}
    CheckPlatform -->|Yes| ExitArm["Exit with Error:<br/>Cannot reset on ARM"]
    CheckPlatform -->|No| Legacy["Legacy IOCTL Reset"]
    
    Legacy --> CheckM3{"reset_m3 == True?"}
    CheckM3 -->|Yes| M3Reset["Send ARC Message<br/>MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET"]
    CheckM3 -->|No| ConfigWrite["IOCTL with<br/>CONFIG_WRITE flag"]
    
    M3Reset --> Monitor["Monitor Config Space<br/>Reset Bit"]
    ConfigWrite --> Monitor
    
    Monitor --> WaitComplete["Wait for Reset Complete<br/>(up to POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME)"]
    WaitComplete --> Restore["IOCTL with<br/>RESTORE_STATE flag"]
    
    Restore --> Return["Return List[PciChip]"]
    Modern --> Return
    
    style Modern fill:#e1f5e1
    style Legacy fill:#ffe1e1
    style ExitArm fill:#ff9999
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:68-99](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:109-118]()

### Version Requirements

| Reset Implementation | Minimum Driver Version | Platform Restrictions |
|---------------------|------------------------|----------------------|
| Modern Unified (`ChipReset`) | 2.4.1 | No ARM support |
| Legacy IOCTL | 1.26.0 | No ARM support |
| Xen HVM Mode | 2.4.1 (uses `ChipReset`) | x86_64 only |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:90-99](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:109-118]()

---

## BHChipReset Class

The `BHChipReset` class is defined in [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:27-224](). It provides the entry point for all Blackhole reset operations and implements the legacy reset sequence for older drivers.

### Class Constants

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "IOCTL Constants"
        MAGIC["TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC<br/>0xFA"]
        CMD["TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_RESET_DEVICE<br/>(0xFA << 8) | 6"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Reset Flags"
        FLAG0["RESTORE_STATE = 0"]
        FLAG1["RESET_PCIE_LINK = 1"]
        FLAG2["CONFIG_WRITE = 2"]
    end
    
    subgraph "ARC Messages"
        ARC1["MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET<br/>0x56"]
        ARC2["MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3<br/>0xA3"]
        ARC3["MSG_TRIGGER_SPI_COPY_LtoR<br/>0x50"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Timing Constants"
        TIME1["A3_STATE_PROP_TIME<br/>0.03s"]
        TIME2["POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME<br/>2s"]
    end
    
    MAGIC --> CMD
    CMD --> FLAG0
    CMD --> FLAG1
    CMD --> FLAG2
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:30-40]()

### Key Methods

| Method | Purpose | Parameters | Returns |
|--------|---------|------------|---------|
| `reset_device_ioctl()` | Execute IOCTL command on device | `interface_id: int`, `flags: int` | `bool` (success) |
| `full_lds_reset()` | Orchestrate complete reset sequence | `pci_interfaces: List[int]`, `reset_m3: bool`, `silent: bool`, `m3_delay: int`, `secondary_bus_reset: bool` | `List[PciChip]` |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:42-66](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:68-223]()

---

## Legacy IOCTL Reset Implementation

The legacy reset implementation directly communicates with the kernel driver via IOCTL commands. This path is used when driver version < 2.4.1 and not running under Xen HVM.

### IOCTL Interface

The `reset_device_ioctl()` method constructs a binary buffer matching the kernel driver's expected structure:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Python as "BHChipReset"
    participant Device as "/dev/tenstorrent/{id}"
    participant Kernel as "tt-kmd Driver"
    
    Python->>Device: open(O_RDWR | O_CLOEXEC)
    Device-->>Python: file descriptor
    
    Python->>Python: pack struct "IIII"<br/>(output_size, flags, 0, 0)
    
    Python->>Kernel: fcntl.ioctl(fd, 0xFA06, buffer)
    Kernel->>Kernel: Execute Reset Command
    Kernel-->>Python: result in buffer
    
    Python->>Python: unpack output_buf<br/>check result == 0
    
    Python->>Device: close(fd)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:42-66]()

### Config Space Reset Sequence

The legacy reset monitors the PCIe config space to verify reset completion:

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["Iterate pci_interfaces"] --> Open["Open PciChip(pci_interface)"]
    Open --> GetBDF["Get PCI BDF:<br/>chip.get_pci_bdf()"]
    GetBDF --> CheckM3{"reset_m3?"}
    
    CheckM3 -->|Yes| SendARC["chip.arc_msg()<br/>MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET<br/>arg0=3"]
    CheckM3 -->|No| SendIOCTL["reset_device_ioctl()<br/>CONFIG_WRITE flag"]
    
    SendARC --> OpenConfig["Open /sys/bus/pci/devices/<br/>{bdf}/config"]
    SendIOCTL --> OpenConfig
    
    OpenConfig --> PollLoop["Poll Loop:<br/>elapsed < POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME"]
    
    PollLoop --> ReadByte["os.pread(fd, 1, offset=4)<br/>Read command.memory byte"]
    ReadByte --> ExtractBit["Extract bit 1:<br/>(byte >> 1) & 1"]
    ExtractBit --> CheckBit{"reset_bit == 0?"}
    
    CheckBit -->|No| Sleep["time.sleep(0.001)"]
    Sleep --> PollLoop
    
    CheckBit -->|Yes & can_early_exit| Complete["Mark Reset Complete"]
    PollLoop -->|Timeout| Complete
    
    Complete --> RestoreState["reset_device_ioctl()<br/>RESTORE_STATE flag"]
    RestoreState --> CheckFailures{"failures > 0?"}
    
    CheckFailures -->|Yes| ExitFail["sys.exit(failures)"]
    CheckFailures -->|No| CreateChips["Create PciChip objects<br/>Return list"]
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:127-223]()

### Config Space Monitoring Details

The reset completion is detected by monitoring the **command.memory** register in PCIe config space:

| File Path | Offset | Bit | Meaning |
|-----------|--------|-----|---------|
| `/sys/bus/pci/devices/{bdf}/config` | 4 bytes | bit 1 | 0 = reset complete, 1 = reset in progress |

The implementation uses `os.pread()` to read the byte at offset 4 without seeking, enabling efficient polling:

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:152-192]()

---

## M3 Reset Option

The M3 reset option was added in version 1.4.7 to enable resetting the M3 processor and DMC (DDR Memory Controller) along with the ASIC. This is useful for firmware upgrade scenarios or recovering from M3-related issues.

### M3 Reset Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Caller
    participant BHChipReset
    participant PciChip
    participant ARC as "ARC Firmware"
    participant M3 as "M3 Processor"
    
    Caller->>BHChipReset: full_lds_reset(reset_m3=True)
    BHChipReset->>PciChip: PciChip(pci_interface)
    BHChipReset->>PciChip: arc_msg(MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET)
    Note over BHChipReset,PciChip: arg0=3 for M3 reset<br/>wait_for_done=False
    
    PciChip->>ARC: Send ARC Message
    ARC->>M3: Trigger M3 Reset
    M3->>M3: Perform Self-Reset<br/>May include BMFW upgrade
    
    Note over BHChipReset: post_reset_wait = max(60, m3_delay)<br/>BMFW upgrade can take 60+ seconds
    
    BHChipReset->>BHChipReset: Monitor config space<br/>Wait for reset_bit == 0
    
    Note over BHChipReset: can_early_exit logic:<br/>Only exit early after seeing<br/>reset_bit transition to 1
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:137-144](), [CHANGELOG.md:55-60]()

### M3 Reset Timing Considerations

When `reset_m3=True`, the implementation adjusts timing parameters:

| Parameter | Standard Reset | M3 Reset | Reason |
|-----------|---------------|----------|--------|
| `post_reset_wait` | 2 seconds | `max(60, m3_delay)` | BMFW may self-upgrade during M3 reset |
| Early exit | Enabled after bit transition | Requires bit transition to 1 first | M3 reset has delayed effect |

The `can_early_exit` flag prevents premature completion detection when the ASIC takes time to enter reset state during M3 firmware operations.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:129-192](), [CHANGELOG.md:48-51]()

---

## Migration to Modern Reset

Starting with driver version 2.4.1, the `BHChipReset` class delegates to the modern `ChipReset` implementation. This provides several advantages:

### Delegation Logic

```mermaid
graph TB
    Entry["BHChipReset.full_lds_reset()"] --> Check1["is_driver_version_at_least()<br/>driver, '2.4.1'"]
    Entry --> Check2["check_xen_hvm()"]
    
    Check1 -->|True| Delegate["ChipReset().full_lds_reset()"]
    Check2 -->|True| Delegate
    
    Check1 -->|False| Check2Continue{" "}
    Check2 -->|False| Check2Continue
    Check2Continue --> Legacy["Execute Legacy Path"]
    
    Delegate --> PassParams["Pass all parameters:<br/>- pci_interfaces<br/>- reset_m3<br/>- silent<br/>- m3_delay<br/>- secondary_bus_reset"]
    
    PassParams --> ReturnResult["Return List[PciChip]"]
    Legacy --> ReturnResult
    
    style Delegate fill:#e1f5e1
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:90-99]()

### Modern Reset Advantages

When using `ChipReset`, Blackhole devices benefit from:

1. **Secondary Bus Reset (SBR)**: Optional PCIe link-level reset before ASIC reset
2. **Xen HVM Integration**: Xenstore coordination for host-guest PCIe hot-plug
3. **Unified IOCTL Interface**: New `IoctlResetFlags` enum with more reset types
4. **Improved Device Detection**: Waits for device to reappear on PCIe bus after hot-plug
5. **Post-Reset Validation**: `POST_RESET` IOCTL flag for final validation

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-288]()

### Parameter Forwarding

All `full_lds_reset()` parameters are forwarded to `ChipReset`:

| Parameter | Type | Description | Default |
|-----------|------|-------------|---------|
| `pci_interfaces` | `List[int]` | PCI interface IDs to reset | Required |
| `reset_m3` | `bool` | Enable M3/DMC reset | `False` |
| `silent` | `bool` | Suppress console output | `False` |
| `m3_delay` | `int` | Seconds to wait after M3 reset | `20` |
| `secondary_bus_reset` | `bool` | Enable SBR before ASIC reset | `True` |

When `reset_m3=True`, the modern implementation uses `IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_DMC_RESET` instead of `IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_RESET`.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:68-99](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:206-212]()

---

## Platform Restrictions

Both legacy and modern implementations enforce platform restrictions:

### ARM Platform Detection

```mermaid
graph LR
    Start["get_host_info()"] --> Extract["platform = info['Platform']"]
    Extract --> Check{"platform.startswith('arm')<br/>OR<br/>platform.startswith('aarch')"}
    
    Check -->|True| Error["Print Error:<br/>'Cannot perform board reset<br/>on Arm systems'"]
    Check -->|False| Continue["Continue Reset"]
    
    Error --> Exit["sys.exit(1)"]
```

ARM systems do not support PCIe device rescans after reset, making device recovery impossible. The implementation checks this early and exits with a clear error message directing users to reboot the system instead.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:109-118](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:139-148]()

---

## Usage Examples

### Basic Blackhole Reset

```python
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.bh_reset import BHChipReset

reset_handler = BHChipReset()
chips = reset_handler.full_lds_reset(
    pci_interfaces=[0, 1],
    silent=False
)
# Returns list of PciChip objects after successful reset
```

### M3 Reset with Custom Delay

```python
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.bh_reset import BHChipReset

reset_handler = BHChipReset()
chips = reset_handler.full_lds_reset(
    pci_interfaces=[0],
    reset_m3=True,
    m3_delay=30,  # Wait 30 seconds for M3 operations
    silent=False
)
```

### Integration with ChipReset (Modern)

```python
# With driver >= 2.4.1, BHChipReset automatically delegates:
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.bh_reset import BHChipReset

reset_handler = BHChipReset()
chips = reset_handler.full_lds_reset(
    pci_interfaces=[0, 1],
    reset_m3=False,
    secondary_bus_reset=True  # Only used in modern path
)
# Internally routes to ChipReset().full_lds_reset()
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:68-99]()

---

## Error Handling

The implementation handles several error conditions:

| Error Condition | Detection | Handling |
|----------------|-----------|----------|
| ARM platform | `platform.startswith()` check | Exit with error message |
| Driver too old (< 1.26) | Implicit in ChipReset delegation | Falls back to legacy if < 2.4.1 |
| Device not found | `PciChip()` constructor failure | Exception propagated to caller |
| IOCTL failure | `fcntl.ioctl()` exception | OSError propagated to caller |
| Reset timeout | Config space polling loop | Marks device as failed, exits with count |
| Config space read error | `os.pread()` failure | Exception propagated to caller |

When reset completion fails, the implementation counts failures and exits with the failure count as the exit code:

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:150-213]()
1d:T3fae,
# Wormhole Reset Implementation

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document details the Wormhole-specific reset implementation in `tt-tools-common`. It covers the `WHChipReset` class, which orchestrates PCIe link resets and ARC message sequences for Wormhole chips. This page focuses on the legacy implementation path and delegation logic specific to Wormhole.

For the modern unified reset implementation that supersedes the legacy path, see [ChipReset: Modern Unified Reset](#2.2). For architecture and design patterns common to all chip types, see [Reset Architecture and Design Patterns](#2.1).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:1-181]()

---

## Architecture Overview

The Wormhole reset system implements a conditional delegation pattern where the `WHChipReset` class routes to either the modern `ChipReset` implementation or a legacy reset sequence based on driver version and virtualization context.

### Reset Path Selection Logic

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Entry["WHChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
    CheckDriver{"Driver version >= 2.4.1<br/>OR<br/>Xen HVM detected?"}
    ModernPath["ChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
    LegacyNotice["Print legacy path warning"]
    DriverCheck["check_driver_version()<br/>Minimum: 1.26.0"]
    PlatformCheck{"Platform == ARM<br/>or AARCH?"}
    ArmExit["Exit with error:<br/>ARM not supported"]
    LegacyReset["Execute legacy reset sequence"]
    
    Entry --> CheckDriver
    CheckDriver -->|Yes| ModernPath
    CheckDriver -->|No| LegacyNotice
    LegacyNotice --> DriverCheck
    DriverCheck --> PlatformCheck
    PlatformCheck -->|Yes| ArmExit
    PlatformCheck -->|No| LegacyReset
    
    ModernPath --> Return["Return List[PciChip]"]
    LegacyReset --> Return
```

**Diagram: Wormhole Reset Delegation Logic**

The decision to use modern or legacy reset is determined at [wh_reset.py:89-90](), where driver version is checked using `is_driver_version_at_least()` or Xen HVM detection via `check_xen_hvm()`. The legacy path requires minimum driver 1.26.0 (checked at [wh_reset.py:101]()) and explicitly blocks ARM platforms (checked at [wh_reset.py:105-112]()).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:68-112]()

---

## WHChipReset Class

The `WHChipReset` class provides the public interface for Wormhole chip resets. It is defined at [wh_reset.py:28-29]() and contains constants, IOCTL wrappers, and the main reset orchestration logic.

### Class Constants

| Constant | Value | Purpose |
|----------|-------|---------|
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC` | `0xFA` | Magic number for ioctl commands |
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_RESET_DEVICE` | `(0xFA << 8) \| 6` | IOCTL command code for device reset |
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESTORE_STATE` | `0` | Flag to restore PCIe state after reset |
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESET_PCIE_LINK` | `1` | Flag to reset PCIe link |
| `A3_STATE_PROP_TIME` | `0.03` | Wait time (seconds) for A3 state propagation |
| `POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME` | `2` | Wait time (seconds) after reset messages |
| `MSG_TRIGGER_SPI_COPY_LtoR` | `0x50` | ARC message: trigger SPI copy left to right |
| `MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3` | `0xA3` | ARC message: enter A3 safe state |
| `MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET` | `0x56` | ARC message: trigger reset sequence |

These constants are defined at [wh_reset.py:31-40]() and specify the low-level protocol for communicating with the kernel driver and ARC firmware.

### Primary Method

The `full_lds_reset()` method is the main entry point:

```python
def full_lds_reset(
    self,
    pci_interfaces: List[int],
    reset_m3: bool = False,
    silent: bool = False,
    secondary_bus_reset: bool = True,
) -> List[PciChip]
```

**Parameters:**
- `pci_interfaces`: List of PCI interface IDs to reset
- `reset_m3`: Whether to perform M3 board-level reset (default: `False`)
- `silent`: Whether to suppress console output (default: `False`)
- `secondary_bus_reset`: Reserved for compatibility with `ChipReset` interface (not used in legacy path)

**Returns:** List of `PciChip` objects representing the reset devices

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:28-86]()

---

## Legacy Reset Sequence

When the legacy path is taken (driver < 2.4.1 and not in Xen HVM), the reset sequence follows a three-phase protocol involving PCIe link manipulation and ARC firmware commands.

### Reset Sequence Phases

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant User as Caller
    participant WH as WHChipReset
    participant IOCTL as Kernel Driver
    participant Chip as PciChip
    participant ARC as ARC Firmware
    
    User->>WH: full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces)
    WH->>WH: Deduplicate interface list
    
    Note over WH,IOCTL: Phase 1: Reset PCIe Link
    loop For each interface
        WH->>IOCTL: reset_device_ioctl(id, RESET_PCIE_LINK)
        IOCTL-->>WH: Success
    end
    
    WH->>WH: Create PciChip objects
    
    Note over WH,ARC: Phase 2: ARC Reset Messages
    loop For each chip
        WH->>Chip: read_refclk_counter()
        Chip-->>WH: refclk_before
        WH->>ARC: arc_msg(MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3)
        Note over ARC: Enter A3 safe state
        ARC-->>WH: Done
        WH->>WH: sleep(A3_STATE_PROP_TIME)
        WH->>ARC: arc_msg(MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET, arg0=3 if reset_m3)
        Note over ARC: Trigger reset
    end
    
    WH->>WH: sleep(POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME)
    
    Note over WH,IOCTL: Phase 3: Restore PCIe State
    loop For each interface
        WH->>IOCTL: reset_device_ioctl(id, RESTORE_STATE)
        IOCTL-->>WH: Success
        WH->>Chip: read_refclk_counter()
        Chip-->>WH: refclk_after
        WH->>WH: Validate refclk_before < refclk_after
    end
    
    WH-->>User: List[PciChip]
```

**Diagram: Legacy Wormhole Reset Sequence**

**Phase 1 (PCIe Link Reset):** Calls `reset_device_ioctl()` with flag `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESET_PCIE_LINK` for each interface ([wh_reset.py:122-124]()). This puts the PCIe link into reset state through the kernel driver.

**Phase 2 (ARC Firmware Reset):** For each chip, the sequence:
1. Reads the reference clock counter before reset ([wh_reset.py:131-132]())
2. Sends `MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3` (0xA3) to enter A3 safe state ([wh_reset.py:143]())
3. Waits 0.03 seconds for state propagation ([wh_reset.py:144]())
4. Sends `MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET` (0x56) with optional `arg0=3` for M3 reset ([wh_reset.py:146-149]())

**Phase 3 (PCIe Restore):** Calls `reset_device_ioctl()` with flag `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESTORE_STATE` for each interface ([wh_reset.py:154-156]()) and validates the reset by checking that reference clock counter decreased ([wh_reset.py:157-164]()).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:121-180]()

---

## IOCTL Interface

The `reset_device_ioctl()` method provides a Python wrapper around the kernel driver's reset ioctl interface.

### IOCTL Structure

```mermaid
graph LR
    Method["reset_device_ioctl(interface_id, flags)"]
    DevPath["/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}"]
    FD["File descriptor"]
    Struct["Packed struct:<br/>input: size_bytes, flags<br/>output: size_bytes, result"]
    IOCTL["fcntl.ioctl(fd, cmd, buf)"]
    Result{"result == 0?"}
    Success["Return True"]
    Failure["Return False"]
    
    Method --> DevPath
    DevPath --> FD
    FD --> Struct
    Struct --> IOCTL
    IOCTL --> Result
    Result -->|Yes| Success
    Result -->|No| Failure
```

**Diagram: IOCTL Communication Flow**

The implementation at [wh_reset.py:42-66]() follows this protocol:

1. **Open device file:** Opens `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}` with flags `O_RDWR | O_CLOEXEC` ([wh_reset.py:43-46]())
2. **Pack input structure:** Creates a buffer with format `"IIII"` containing output size, flags, and two zero fields ([wh_reset.py:48-56]())
3. **Execute ioctl:** Calls `fcntl.ioctl()` with command `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_RESET_DEVICE` ([wh_reset.py:57-59]())
4. **Unpack output:** Extracts the result code from the output portion of the buffer ([wh_reset.py:61-62]())
5. **Return status:** Returns `True` if result is 0, `False` otherwise ([wh_reset.py:64]())

The file descriptor is guaranteed to be closed via a `finally` block ([wh_reset.py:65-66]()).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:42-66]()

---

## ARC Message Sequence

The ARC (Accelerated RISC Core) firmware running on the Wormhole chip must be instructed to perform reset operations through a specific message protocol.

### A3 State and Reset Messages

The reset sequence uses two critical ARC messages:

#### MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3 (0xA3)

This message instructs the ARC firmware to enter A3 safe state, where no pending regulator requests exist. The call is synchronous:

```python
chip.arc_msg(self.MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3, wait_for_done=True)
```

After sending, the implementation waits `A3_STATE_PROP_TIME` (0.03 seconds) for the state to propagate ([wh_reset.py:143-144]()). This ensures the chip is in a stable state before triggering the actual reset.

#### MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET (0x56)

This message triggers the reset sequence. The call is asynchronous (`wait_for_done=False`) because the chip will be resetting and cannot acknowledge:

```python
# Standard reset
chip.arc_msg(self.MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET, wait_for_done=False)

# M3 board-level reset
chip.arc_msg(self.MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET, wait_for_done=False, arg0=3)
```

When `reset_m3=True`, the implementation passes `arg0=3` to request an M3 board-level reset rather than just a chip reset ([wh_reset.py:146-149]()).

After all chips have been sent reset messages, the implementation waits `POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME` (2 seconds) for the reset operations to complete ([wh_reset.py:151]()).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:143-151]()

---

## Reference Clock Validation

The Wormhole reset implementation validates that a reset actually occurred by comparing the ARC reference clock counter values before and after the reset sequence.

### Validation Logic

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Before["Read refclk_counter before reset"]
    Store["Store in refclk_list"]
    Reset["Execute reset sequence"]
    After["Read refclk_counter after reset"]
    Compare{"refclk_list[i] < current_refclk?"}
    Fail["Print error message<br/>Set fail flag"]
    Success["Reset confirmed"]
    CheckFail{"fail flag set?"}
    Exit["sys.exit(1)"]
    Return["Return pci_chips"]
    
    Before --> Store
    Store --> Reset
    Reset --> After
    After --> Compare
    Compare -->|No - ERROR| Fail
    Compare -->|Yes - OK| Success
    Fail --> CheckFail
    Success --> CheckFail
    CheckFail -->|Yes| Exit
    CheckFail -->|No| Return
```

**Diagram: Reference Clock Reset Validation**

The validation process:

1. **Pre-reset capture:** Before sending ARC messages, read and store each chip's reference clock counter using `read_refclk_counter(chip)` ([wh_reset.py:131-132]())
2. **Post-reset read:** After PCIe state restoration, read the current reference clock value ([wh_reset.py:157]())
3. **Comparison:** Verify that `refclk_list[i] < current_refclk` - if the clock did NOT decrease, the reset failed ([wh_reset.py:158-164]())
4. **Error handling:** If any chip fails validation, print an error and set the `fail` flag ([wh_reset.py:159-164]())
5. **Exit on failure:** If `fail` is set, exit with status code 1 ([wh_reset.py:166-172]())

The reference clock counter is expected to be **smaller** after a successful reset because the counter resets to zero and begins counting from the start. If the counter is larger or equal, it indicates the reset did not occur.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:131-180](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py]() (for `read_refclk_counter`)

---

## Platform Restrictions

The legacy Wormhole reset implementation has specific platform restrictions that prevent operation on certain architectures.

### ARM Platform Block

ARM and AArch64 platforms handle PCIe device rescans differently than x86, causing Wormhole device resets to fail. The implementation explicitly checks for ARM platforms and exits:

```python
platform = get_host_info()["Platform"]
if platform.startswith("arm") or platform.startswith("aarch"):
    print(
        CMD_LINE_COLOR.RED,
        "Cannot perform WH board reset on Arm systems, please reboot the system to reset the boards. Exiting...",
        CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC,
    )
    sys.exit(1)
```

This check occurs at [wh_reset.py:105-112](), immediately after driver version validation. The restriction applies **only to the legacy path**; the modern `ChipReset` implementation may handle ARM differently (see [ChipReset: Modern Unified Reset](#2.2)).

### Driver Version Requirements

The legacy reset requires kernel driver version >= 1.26.0, enforced by calling `check_driver_version(operation="board reset")` at [wh_reset.py:101](). This minimum version is required to support the IOCTL commands for PCIe link reset and state restoration.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:101-112](), [CHANGELOG.md:102-106]()

---

## Migration to ChipReset

The Wormhole reset implementation migrates to the modern `ChipReset` implementation when driver version >= 2.4.1 or when running in Xen HVM mode.

### Delegation Implementation

The delegation occurs at the start of `full_lds_reset()`:

```python
# Use new reset for driver version >= 2.4.1 or if in Xen HVM mode. Xen mode also requires newer driver.
if is_driver_version_at_least(get_driver_version(), "2.4.1") or check_xen_hvm():
    return ChipReset().full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces, reset_m3=reset_m3, silent=silent, secondary_bus_reset=secondary_bus_reset)
```

This check at [wh_reset.py:89-90]() immediately delegates to `ChipReset` if conditions are met, bypassing all legacy logic.

### Migration Timeline

| Version | Change | Reference |
|---------|--------|-----------|
| 1.4.3 (May 2024) | Added ARM platform check and Xen HVM detection | [CHANGELOG.md:80-85]() |
| 1.4.2 (April 2024) | Added `silent` flag for versatility in other tools | [CHANGELOG.md:87-90]() |
| 1.4.0 (March 2024) | Updated minimum driver version to 1.26 for LDS reset | [CHANGELOG.md:97-106]() |
| 1.1.0 (February 2024) | Added refclk check to WH link reset | [CHANGELOG.md:126-131]() |

The migration strategy allows gradual adoption of the modern reset implementation while maintaining backward compatibility for systems with older kernel drivers. When the legacy path is used, a warning is printed encouraging users to upgrade ([wh_reset.py:92-98]()).

### Implications for Consumers

Tools consuming `WHChipReset` should:
- **Update drivers:** Upgrade to tt-kmd >= 2.4.1 to use the modern implementation
- **Handle warnings:** The legacy path warning is informational, not fatal
- **Test both paths:** If supporting multiple driver versions, test both legacy and modern reset behavior
- **Plan for deprecation:** The legacy implementation will be removed in a future version

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:89-98](), [CHANGELOG.md:8-142]()

---

## Error Handling

The Wormhole reset implementation includes several failure modes and error handling strategies.

### Fatal Errors

| Error Condition | Location | Action |
|----------------|----------|--------|
| ARM platform detected | [wh_reset.py:107-112]() | Print error, `sys.exit(1)` |
| Driver version < 1.26.0 | `check_driver_version()` call | Print error, `sys.exit(1)` |
| Cannot read refclk before reset | [wh_reset.py:131-141]() | Print "failed to recover" message, `sys.exit(1)` |
| Refclk validation failed | [wh_reset.py:166-172]() | Print "reset failed" warning, `sys.exit(1)` |

### Non-Fatal Warnings

- **Legacy path usage:** Prints yellow warning when driver < 2.4.1 ([wh_reset.py:92-98]())
- **Individual chip failures:** Prints red error for each chip with failed refclk validation ([wh_reset.py:159-164]())

The implementation treats refclk validation failures as fatal, exiting with code 1 if any chip fails validation. This ensures that consumers do not proceed with partially-reset hardware.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:107-172]()
1e:T5b9e,
# Grayskull Tensix Reset

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document describes the Grayskull-specific Tensix core reset implementation provided by the `GSTensixReset` class. Unlike Blackhole and Wormhole chips which use driver-based reset mechanisms (see [Blackhole Reset Implementation](#2.3) and [Wormhole Reset Implementation](#2.4)), Grayskull requires a software-controlled reset sequence that directly manipulates Tensix cores and Network-on-Chip (NOC) routers through register writes and ARC firmware messages.

The Grayskull reset procedure handles:
- Detection of harvested (disabled) Tensix rows via efuse reading
- Safe clock frequency management during reset operations
- NOC router configuration including broadcast disables for harvested cores
- Sequential hard and soft reset assertion/deassertion of RISC-V processors
- Differential handling of harvested vs. non-harvested cores

For the unified reset interface that routes to chip-specific implementations, see [Reset Architecture and Design Patterns](#2.1). For reset configuration and logging, see [Reset Configuration and Logging](#2.6).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:1-403](), [CHANGELOG.md:108-118]()

---

## Grid Architecture and Coordinate Systems

The Grayskull chip contains a 13×12 grid of nodes, including Tensix cores, DRAM controllers, ARC processor, and PCIe interface. The grid uses two coordinate systems that must be mapped between:

### Physical and Routing Coordinates

**Physical coordinates** represent the actual hardware layout, while **routing coordinates** represent NOC addressing. The conversion uses a mirroring algorithm where even physical coordinates map to the lower half and odd coordinates map to the mirrored upper half of routing space.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Coordinate System Mapping"
        PhysCoord["Physical Coordinates<br/>(x, y)"]
        RoutCoord["Routing Coordinates<br/>(rout_x, rout_y)"]
        
        PhysCoord -->|"_physical_to_routing()"| RoutCoord
        RoutCoord -->|"ROUTING_TO_PHYSICAL_TABLE"| PhysCoord
    end
    
    subgraph "Grid Layout (13×12)"
        GridDef["GRID_SIZE_X = 13<br/>GRID_SIZE_Y = 12"]
        TensixArea["Tensix Area:<br/>12×10 cores<br/>(excluding row 0, row 6)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Special Locations (NOC0 Coordinates)"
        DRAM["DRAM Controllers<br/>(1,6), (4,6), (7,6), (10,6)<br/>(1,0), (4,0), (7,0), (10,0)"]
        ARC["ARC Processor<br/>(0,2)"]
        PCI["PCIe Interface<br/>(0,4)"]
    end
    
    GridDef --> TensixArea
    GridDef --> DRAM
    GridDef --> ARC
    GridDef --> PCI
```

**Diagram: Grayskull Grid Architecture and Special Component Locations**

The conversion function `_physical_to_routing()` implements the mirroring:

```
if (phys % 2) == 0:
    rout = phys // 2
else:
    rout = limit - 1 - (phys // 2)
```

During initialization, the `ROUTING_TO_PHYSICAL_TABLE` dictionary is populated for bidirectional lookups between coordinate systems.

| Component | Grid Region | Count | Purpose |
|-----------|-------------|-------|---------|
| Tensix Cores | Columns 1-12, Rows 1-5,7-11 | Up to 120 | Compute cores with RISC-V processors |
| DRAM Controllers | Rows 0,6 at columns 1,4,7,10 | 8 | Memory interface |
| ARC Processor | (0,2) | 1 | Chip management firmware |
| PCIe Interface | (0,4) | 1 | Host communication |
| NOC Routers | Row 0, Column 0, Row 6 | Variable | Routing fabric nodes |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:28-56](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:64-69]()

---

## Harvesting Detection and Core List Generation

Grayskull chips may have rows of Tensix cores disabled during manufacturing due to defects. These "harvested" rows are identified through efuse values read via ARC firmware message.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["get_harvested_rows()"] --> EnvCheck{"T6PY_HARVESTING_OVERRIDE<br/>environment variable set?"}
    
    EnvCheck -->|Yes| ParseEnv["Parse override value<br/>from environment"]
    EnvCheck -->|No| ARCMsg["Send ARC message:<br/>MSG_TYPE_ARC_GET_HARVESTING"]
    
    ARCMsg --> CheckExit{"exit_code == 0?"}
    CheckExit -->|No| Error["Assert: FW too old,<br/>update firmware"]
    CheckExit -->|Yes| ExtractBits["Extract harvesting bits"]
    
    ParseEnv --> ExtractBits
    ExtractBits --> CalcBadMem["bad_mem_bits =<br/>harvesting_fuses & 0x3FF"]
    CalcBadMem --> CalcBadLogic["bad_logic_bits =<br/>(harvesting_fuses >> 10) & 0x3FF"]
    CalcBadLogic --> CombineBits["bad_row_bits =<br/>(bad_mem_bits | bad_logic_bits) << 1"]
    CombineBits --> PhysToNOC["Map physical rows<br/>to NOC0 Y coordinates"]
    PhysToNOC --> ReturnSet["Return frozenset of<br/>disabled NOC0 rows"]
    
    ReturnSet --> CoreList["get_core_list()"]
    CoreList --> FilterRows["Filter out harvested rows<br/>from [1,2,3,4,5,7,8,9,10,11]"]
    FilterRows --> GenCores["Generate all (x,y) combinations<br/>x: 1 to 12, y: good_rows"]
    GenCores --> ReturnDict["Return dict of valid cores<br/>(deterministic order)"]
```

**Diagram: Harvesting Detection and Core List Generation Process**

The harvesting efuse contains two 10-bit fields:
- **Bits [9:0]**: Memory defect rows
- **Bits [19:10]**: Logic defect rows

These are OR'd together and shifted left by 1 to produce a bitmap of bad physical rows. The physical row indices are then mapped to NOC0 Y coordinates using `PHYS_Y_TO_NOC_0_Y` lookup table, which implements the physical-to-routing transformation specific to the Y axis.

The resulting `self.harvested_rows` frozenset is used throughout the reset process to differentiate handling of harvested vs. active cores.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:71-97](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:99-115]()

---

## Safe Clock Management

Before manipulating Tensix reset signals, the ARC firmware must lower clock frequencies to safe levels. This prevents timing violations during reset transitions.

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant User as "tensix_reset()"
    participant SafeClk as "set_safe_clks()"
    participant ARC as "ARC Firmware"
    participant Clocks as "Clock Tree"
    
    User->>SafeClk: set_safe_clks(enter=True)
    SafeClk->>ARC: arc_msg(MSG_TYPE_RESET_SAFE_CLKS,<br/>arg0=1, arg1=0)
    ARC->>Clocks: Lower frequencies to safe levels
    ARC-->>SafeClk: wait_for_done=True
    SafeClk-->>User: Return
    
    Note over User: Perform reset sequence
    
    User->>SafeClk: set_safe_clks(enter=False)
    SafeClk->>ARC: arc_msg(MSG_TYPE_RESET_SAFE_CLKS,<br/>arg0=0, arg1=0)
    ARC->>Clocks: Restore original frequencies
    ARC-->>SafeClk: wait_for_done=True
    SafeClk-->>User: Return
```

**Diagram: Safe Clock Entry and Exit Sequence**

The `set_safe_clks()` method sends the `MSG_TYPE_RESET_SAFE_CLKS` ARC message with `arg0=1` to enter safe mode and `arg0=0` to exit. The main reset sequence uses a try/finally block to ensure clocks are always restored, even if the reset sequence encounters an error:

```python
self.set_safe_clks(True)
try:
    # Reset operations
finally:
    self.set_safe_clks(False)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:143-162](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:376-402]()

---

## NOC Router Configuration

The Network-on-Chip routers must be configured to handle broadcast operations correctly, accounting for harvested rows and special components. This configuration involves setting broadcast disable masks and enabling clock gating.

### NOC Router Register Layout

| Register | Offset | Purpose |
|----------|--------|---------|
| `NIU_CFG_0` | 0x100 | Bit 0: CG enable, Bit 12: Tile clock disable |
| `ROUTER_CFG_0` | 0x104 | Bit 0: CG enable, Bits [11:8]: Max backoff exp |
| `ROUTER_CFG_1` | 0x108 | Column broadcast disable mask |
| `ROUTER_CFG_3` | 0x110 | Row broadcast disable mask |

### Broadcast Disable Calculation

```mermaid
graph TB
    Start["get_noc_router_cfg()"] --> InitList["broadcast_disabled_rows =<br/>[0, 6] + harvested_rows"]
    
    InitList --> NOC0Col["NOC0 Column Disable:<br/>noc0_router_cfg_1 = 1 << 0<br/>(disable column 0)"]
    InitList --> NOC1Col["NOC1 Column Disable:<br/>noc1_router_cfg_1 = 1 << 12<br/>(disable column 12, remapped)"]
    
    InitList --> NOC0Row["NOC0 Row Disable:<br/>OR all bits for disabled rows<br/>noc0_router_cfg_3"]
    InitList --> NOC1Row["NOC1 Row Disable:<br/>Map rows: GRID_SIZE_Y - y - 1<br/>OR all bits<br/>noc1_router_cfg_3"]
    
    NOC0Col --> Return["Return tuple:<br/>(noc0_cfg_1, noc1_cfg_1,<br/>noc0_cfg_3, noc1_cfg_3)"]
    NOC1Col --> Return
    NOC0Row --> Return
    NOC1Row --> Return
```

**Diagram: NOC Router Broadcast Disable Computation**

The broadcast disable masks ensure that:
1. **Column 0** (NOC0) and **Column 12** (NOC1) are always disabled as they contain special components
2. **Row 0** and **Row 6** are always disabled as they contain DRAM controllers
3. **Harvested rows** are disabled to prevent routing to non-functional cores
4. **NOC1 uses mirrored coordinates**, requiring row remapping: `GRID_SIZE_Y - y - 1`

### NOC Setup Procedure

The `setup_noc()` method iterates through all grid locations and configures each node based on its type:

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["setup_noc()"] --> ResetDDR["Reset DDR controllers:<br/>ARC_RESET.DDR_RESET = 0x3"]
    ResetDDR --> GetCfg["Get broadcast disable configs:<br/>get_noc_router_cfg()"]
    GetCfg --> IterateGrid["Iterate all (x,y) in 13×12 grid"]
    
    IterateGrid --> CheckType{"Node Type?"}
    
    CheckType -->|"DRAM_LOCATIONS"| SetupDRAM["setup_noc_by_xy(x, y,<br/>[0xFFFF4000, 0xFFFF5000])"]
    CheckType -->|"ARC_LOCATIONS"| SetupARC["setup_noc_by_address(<br/>[0x1FF50000, 0x1FF58000])"]
    CheckType -->|"PCI_LOCATIONS"| SetupPCI["setup_noc_by_address(<br/>[0x1FD00000, 0x1FD08000])"]
    CheckType -->|"Row 0,6 or Col 0"| SetupRouter["setup_noc_by_xy(x, y,<br/>[0xFFB20000, 0xFFB30000])"]
    CheckType -->|"Tensix Core"| SetupTensix["setup_noc_by_xy(x, y,<br/>[0xFFB20000, 0xFFB30000])"]
    
    SetupTensix --> CheckHarvest{"is_tensix_core_loc(x, y)?"}
    CheckHarvest -->|"Non-harvested"| SetTileClock0["Set NIU_CFG_0 bit 12 = 0<br/>(enable tile clock)"]
    CheckHarvest -->|"Harvested"| SetTileClock1["Set NIU_CFG_0 bit 12 = 1<br/>(disable tile clock)"]
    
    SetupDRAM --> IterateGrid
    SetupARC --> IterateGrid
    SetupPCI --> IterateGrid
    SetupRouter --> IterateGrid
    SetTileClock0 --> IterateGrid
    SetTileClock1 --> IterateGrid
    
    IterateGrid --> Done["NOC Configuration Complete"]
```

**Diagram: NOC Setup Flow for All Grid Nodes**

For each node, the configuration writes:
- **ROUTER_CFG_1**: Column broadcast disable mask
- **ROUTER_CFG_3**: Row broadcast disable mask
- **NIU_CFG_0 bit 0**: Clock gating enable
- **ROUTER_CFG_0 bit 0**: Clock gating enable
- **ROUTER_CFG_0 bits [11:8]**: Maximum exponential backoff (`NOC_MAX_BACKOFF_EXP = 0xF`)

For Tensix cores specifically, **NIU_CFG_0 bit 12** controls tile clock enable/disable based on harvesting status. Harvested cores have their tile clocks disabled to save power.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:117-141](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:188-318]()

---

## Reset Sequence

The complete Tensix reset sequence involves five distinct phases, executed while in safe clock mode:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Main as "tensix_reset()"
    participant SafeClk as "set_safe_clks()"
    participant HardReset as "all_riscs_assert_hard_reset()"
    participant Toggle as "tensix_toggle_reset()"
    participant NOCSetup as "setup_noc()"
    participant SoftReset as "assert_all_riscv_soft_reset()"
    participant Deassert as "all_riscs_deassert_hard_reset()"
    participant Regs as "AXI Registers"
    
    Main->>SafeClk: Enter safe clock mode
    SafeClk-->>Main: Clocks lowered
    
    Main->>HardReset: Phase 1: Assert hard reset
    loop 8 RISCV_RESET registers
        HardReset->>Regs: write32(RISCV_RESET[i], 0x0)
    end
    HardReset-->>Main: All RISCs in hard reset
    
    Main->>Toggle: Phase 2: Toggle Tensix reset
    loop 8 TENSIX_RESET registers
        Toggle->>Regs: write32(TENSIX_RESET[i], 0x0)
    end
    loop 8 TENSIX_RESET registers
        Toggle->>Regs: write32(TENSIX_RESET[i], 0xFFFFFFFF)
    end
    Toggle-->>Main: Tensix cores reset
    
    Main->>NOCSetup: Phase 3: Configure NOC
    NOCSetup->>NOCSetup: Reset DDR controllers
    NOCSetup->>NOCSetup: Configure all node routers
    NOCSetup->>NOCSetup: Set tile clock disable for harvested
    NOCSetup-->>Main: NOC ready
    
    Main->>SoftReset: Phase 4: Assert soft reset
    SoftReset->>Regs: noc_broadcast32(0, 0xFFB121B0,<br/>BRISC | TRISC | NCRISC bits)
    SoftReset-->>Main: All active cores in soft reset
    
    Main->>Deassert: Phase 5: Deassert hard reset
    loop For each non-harvested core
        Deassert->>Regs: write32(RISCV_RESET[i], mask)
    end
    Deassert-->>Main: Active cores out of hard reset
    
    Main->>SafeClk: Exit safe clock mode
    SafeClk-->>Main: Clocks restored
```

**Diagram: Complete Tensix Reset Sequence**

### Phase 1: Assert Hard Reset on All RISCs

The `all_riscs_assert_hard_reset()` method writes 0x0 to all 8 `ARC_RESET.RISCV_RESET[i]` registers, placing every RISC-V processor (across all Tensix cores, harvested or not) into hard reset state.

### Phase 2: Toggle Tensix Core Reset

The `tensix_toggle_reset()` method:
1. Writes 0x0 to all 8 `ARC_RESET.TENSIX_RESET[i]` registers (assert reset)
2. Writes 0xFFFFFFFF to all 8 `ARC_RESET.TENSIX_RESET[i]` registers (deassert reset)

This resets the entire Tensix core fabric, including NOC routers, regardless of harvesting status. All cores' NOC routers must be functional for the network to operate correctly.

### Phase 3: Setup NOC Routers

The `setup_noc()` method configures all NOC nodes as described in the previous section, including broadcast disables, clock gating, and tile clock management.

### Phase 4: Assert Soft Reset via NOC Broadcast

The `assert_all_riscv_soft_reset()` method uses NOC broadcast to write soft reset bits to all **non-harvested** Tensix cores in a single operation:

```
BRISC_SOFT_RESET = 1 << 11
TRISC_SOFT_RESETS = (1 << 12) | (1 << 13) | (1 << 14)
NCRISC_SOFT_RESET = 1 << 18
noc_broadcast32(0, 0xFFB121B0, combined_bits)
```

This targets address 0xFFB121B0 on NOC0, which reaches only active cores due to the broadcast disable configuration set in Phase 3.

### Phase 5: Deassert Hard Reset on Active Cores

The `all_riscs_deassert_hard_reset()` method uses the reset mask computed by `all_tensix_reset_mask()` to selectively deassert hard reset only for non-harvested cores:

```mermaid
graph LR
    GetMask["all_tensix_reset_mask()"] --> Iterate["For each core in core_list"]
    Iterate --> CalcBit["noc_loc_to_reset_mask(x, y):<br/>1. Map NOC to physical coords<br/>2. Calculate blue_x, blue_y<br/>3. Compute bit index and mask"]
    CalcBit --> BuildMask["Accumulate bit masks<br/>into 8-element array"]
    BuildMask --> WriteRegs["For i in 0..7:<br/>write32(RISCV_RESET[i], mask[i])"]
```

**Diagram: Selective Hard Reset Deassertion for Active Cores**

The bit position calculation converts NOC coordinates to "blue coordinates" (Tensix indexing) using the `ROUTING_TO_PHYSICAL_TABLE`:

```
phys_x, phys_y = ROUTING_TO_PHYSICAL_TABLE[(noc_x, noc_y)]
blue_x, blue_y = phys_x - 1, phys_y - 1
reset_bit_index = blue_x * NUM_TENSIX_X + blue_y
reset_reg_index = reset_bit_index // 32
reset_bit_mask = 1 << (reset_bit_index % 32)
```

After Phase 5, active Tensix cores are:
- **Out of hard reset** (RISCs can execute)
- **In soft reset** (RISCs held at reset vector, awaiting firmware load)

Harvested cores remain in hard reset permanently.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:164-181](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:320-331](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:333-365](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:366-402]()

---

## GSTensixReset Class Implementation

### Class Structure and Dependencies

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class GSTensixReset {
        +device: PciChip
        +axi_registers: RegisterObject
        +fw_defines: dict
        +harvested_rows: frozenset
        +core_list: dict
        +ROUTING_TO_PHYSICAL_TABLE: dict
        
        +__init__(device: PciChip)
        +get_harvested_rows() frozenset
        +get_core_list() dict
        +get_noc_router_cfg() tuple
        +set_safe_clks(enter_safe_clks: bool)
        +all_riscs_assert_hard_reset()
        +tensix_toggle_reset()
        +is_tensix_core_loc(x: int, y: int) bool
        +setup_noc()
        +assert_all_riscv_soft_reset()
        +noc_loc_to_reset_mask(noc_x: int, noc_y: int) tuple
        +all_tensix_reset_mask() list
        +all_riscs_deassert_hard_reset()
        +tensix_reset(silent: bool)
    }
    
    class PciChip {
        <<pyluwen>>
        +arc_msg()
        +as_gs()
        +noc_read32()
        +noc_write32()
        +noc_broadcast32()
    }
    
    class RegisterObject {
        <<utils_common>>
        +write32()
        +write_fields()
    }
    
    GSTensixReset --> PciChip : uses
    GSTensixReset --> RegisterObject : uses
```

**Diagram: GSTensixReset Class Structure and Dependencies**

### Initialization Process

```python
def __init__(self, device: PciChip):
    # Build coordinate mapping table
    self.ROUTING_TO_PHYSICAL_TABLE = dict()
    for phys_y in range(self.GRID_SIZE_Y):
        for phys_x in range(self.GRID_SIZE_X):
            rout_x = self._physical_to_routing(self.GRID_SIZE_X, phys_x)
            rout_y = self._physical_to_routing(self.GRID_SIZE_Y, phys_y)
            self.ROUTING_TO_PHYSICAL_TABLE[(rout_x, rout_y)] = (phys_x, phys_y)
    
    self.device = device
    self.axi_registers = get_register_object(device)
    self.fw_defines = init_fw_defines("grayskull", "tt_tools_common.data")
    self.harvested_rows = self.get_harvested_rows()
    self.core_list = self.get_core_list()
```

The constructor performs five initialization steps:
1. **Populate coordinate mapping table** for bidirectional NOC↔physical conversion
2. **Store device reference** for hardware communication
3. **Initialize register abstraction** via `get_register_object()` for AXI writes
4. **Load firmware definitions** from `fw_defines.yaml` for ARC message types
5. **Detect harvesting** and build list of active cores

### Public API: tensix_reset()

The primary entry point is `tensix_reset(silent=False)`, which orchestrates the complete reset sequence:

```python
def tensix_reset(self, silent=False) -> None:
    if not silent:
        print(CMD_LINE_COLOR.YELLOW, "Lowering clks to safe value...", CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC)
    self.set_safe_clks(True)
    try:
        if not silent:
            print(CMD_LINE_COLOR.YELLOW, "Beginning reset sequence...", CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC)
        self.all_riscs_assert_hard_reset()
        self.tensix_toggle_reset()
        self.setup_noc()
        self.assert_all_riscv_soft_reset()
        self.all_riscs_deassert_hard_reset()
        if not silent:
            print(CMD_LINE_COLOR.YELLOW, "Finishing reset sequence...", CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC)
    finally:
        if not silent:
            print(CMD_LINE_COLOR.YELLOW, "Returning clks to original values...", CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC)
        self.set_safe_clks(False)
```

The `silent` parameter suppresses console output for use in automated tools. The try/finally ensures safe clock restoration even on error.

### Register Constants

The class defines NOC register offsets as class constants:

| Constant | Value | Description |
|----------|-------|-------------|
| `NIU_CFG_0` | 0x100 | Network Interface Unit config: CG enable, tile clock disable |
| `ROUTER_CFG_0` | 0x104 | Router config: CG enable, backoff exponent |
| `ROUTER_CFG_1` | 0x108 | Column broadcast disable mask |
| `ROUTER_CFG_3` | 0x110 | Row broadcast disable mask |
| `NOC_MAX_BACKOFF_EXP` | 0xF | Maximum exponential backoff value |

### Grid Layout Constants

| Constant | Value | Description |
|----------|-------|-------------|
| `GRID_SIZE_X` | 13 | Total columns in grid |
| `GRID_SIZE_Y` | 12 | Total rows in grid |
| `NUM_TENSIX_X` | 12 | Tensix columns (excluding column 0) |
| `NUM_TENSIX_Y` | 10 | Tensix rows (excluding rows 0, 6) |
| `PHYS_Y_TO_NOC_0_Y` | `[0,11,1,10,2,9,3,8,4,7,5,6]` | Physical Y to NOC0 Y mapping |
| `DRAM_LOCATIONS` | 8 coordinates | DRAM controller positions |
| `ARC_LOCATIONS` | `[(0, 2)]` | ARC processor position |
| `PCI_LOCATIONS` | `[(0, 4)]` | PCIe interface position |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:17-61](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:366-402]()

---

## Usage Example

The following code demonstrates typical usage of `GSTensixReset`:

```python
from pyluwen import PciChip
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.gs_tensix_reset import GSTensixReset

# Open chip connection
device = PciChip(pci_interface=0)

# Create reset instance (automatically detects harvesting)
reset = GSTensixReset(device)

# Examine harvested rows
print(f"Harvested rows (NOC0 Y): {reset.harvested_rows}")
print(f"Active Tensix cores: {len(reset.core_list)}")

# Perform reset
reset.tensix_reset(silent=False)

# For silent operation in automated scripts
reset.tensix_reset(silent=True)
```

The reset leaves all active Tensix cores in soft reset state, ready for firmware loading via subsequent operations (typically performed by higher-level tools like tt-smi or tt-flash).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:1-403]()

---

## Integration with Reset System

`GSTensixReset` is integrated into the broader reset system through the `parse_reset_input()` function and chip detection logic. The class is instantiated and used for Grayskull devices when a reset is requested:

```python
# Typical integration pattern (simplified)
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import detect_chips_with_callback
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.gs_tensix_reset import GSTensixReset

# Detect Grayskull chips
chips = detect_chips_with_callback(pci_interface_ids=[...])
for chip in chips:
    if chip.architecture == "grayskull":
        reset = GSTensixReset(chip)
        reset.tensix_reset()
```

Unlike Blackhole and Wormhole which route through `ChipReset` based on driver version (see [Reset Architecture and Design Patterns](#2.1)), Grayskull always uses this direct implementation as it predates the unified reset interface.

**Sources:** [CHANGELOG.md:108-118]()

---

## Migration History

The Grayskull Tensix reset implementation was migrated from tt-smi to tt-tools-common in version 1.3.0 (released 2024-03-06) along with related data files. This migration made the reset functionality available to all Tenstorrent tools, promoting code reuse and consistent behavior across the ecosystem.

The implementation includes a `silent` flag (added in version 1.4.2) to make it more versatile for integration into tools that prefer to manage their own output formatting.

**Sources:** [CHANGELOG.md:108-118](), [CHANGELOG.md:87-91]()

# Reset Configuration and Logging

## Purpose and Scope

This document covers the reset configuration system and logging infrastructure in tt-tools-common. It explains how reset operations are specified (via command-line arguments, device IDs, or JSON configuration files), how reset configurations are parsed and validated, and how reset logs are generated in an Elasticsearch-compatible format for centralized monitoring.

For the actual reset execution logic for specific chip architectures, see [Blackhole Reset Implementation](#2.3), [Wormhole Reset Implementation](#2.4), and [Grayskull Tensix Reset](#2.5). For the overall reset architecture and design patterns, see [Reset Architecture and Design Patterns](#2.1).

---

## Reset Input Types and Parsing

The reset system accepts three distinct input types for specifying which devices to reset, represented by the `ResetType` enumeration:

| Reset Type | Description | Example Input |
|------------|-------------|---------------|
| `ALL` | Reset all detected devices | `"all"` or no arguments |
| `ID_LIST` | Reset specific devices by PCI index | `"0,1,2"` or `0 1 2` |
| `CONFIG_JSON` | Reset according to JSON configuration file | `"path/to/reset_config.json"` |

The `ResetInput` dataclass encapsulates the parsed input:

```python
@dataclass
class ResetInput:
    type: ResetType
    value: Union[Dict, int, None]
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:23-31]()

### Input Parsing Flow

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["parse_reset_input(value: list)"]
    CheckEmpty{"value == [] or<br/>value == ['all']?"}
    CheckSingle{"len(value) == 1?"}
    TryJSON["Attempt to open<br/>and parse as JSON"]
    JSONSuccess["Return ResetInput<br/>type=CONFIG_JSON<br/>value=json_data"]
    JSONFail{"JSON parse<br/>failed?"}
    TryCommaList["Parse as comma-separated<br/>integers: split(',')"]
    CommaSuccess["Return ResetInput<br/>type=ID_LIST<br/>value=list_input"]
    CommaFail["Print error: invalid format<br/>sys.exit(1)"]
    TrySpaceList["Parse as space-separated<br/>integers"]
    SpaceSuccess["Return ResetInput<br/>type=ID_LIST<br/>value=list_input"]
    SpaceFail["Print error: invalid format<br/>sys.exit(1)"]
    ReturnAll["Return ResetInput<br/>type=ALL<br/>value=None"]
    
    Start --> CheckEmpty
    CheckEmpty -->|Yes| ReturnAll
    CheckEmpty -->|No| CheckSingle
    CheckSingle -->|Yes| TryJSON
    TryJSON --> JSONFail
    JSONFail -->|FileNotFoundError| TryCommaList
    JSONFail -->|JSONDecodeError| CommaFail
    JSONFail -->|Success| JSONSuccess
    TryCommaList -->|Success| CommaSuccess
    TryCommaList -->|ValueError| CommaFail
    CheckSingle -->|No| TrySpaceList
    TrySpaceList -->|Success| SpaceSuccess
    TrySpaceList -->|ValueError| SpaceFail
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:33-87]()

### Parsing Logic Details

The `parse_reset_input` function implements a cascading parsing strategy:

1. **Empty/All Check**: If input is empty or `["all"]`, return `ResetType.ALL` with no value
2. **Single Argument Path**: 
   - First, attempt to open as a file and parse JSON
   - If file not found, try parsing as comma-separated integers (e.g., `"0,1,2"`)
   - Return error if both fail
3. **Multiple Arguments Path**: Parse as space-separated integers (e.g., `["0", "1", "2"]`)

The function deduplicates and sorts integer lists using `list(sorted(set(list_input)))` at [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:66]() and [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:79]().

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:33-87]()

---

## Reset Configuration File Format

Reset configuration files use JSON format with a structured schema defined by the `HostResetLog` Pydantic model. These files specify which devices to reset, the reset methods to use, and logging preferences.

### Configuration File Structure

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class HostResetLog {
        +datetime time
        +str host_name
        +PciResetDeviceInfo gs_tensix_reset
        +PciResetDeviceInfo wh_link_reset
        +bool re_init_devices
        +List~MoboReset~ wh_mobo_reset
        +bool disable_serial_report
        +bool disable_sw_version_report
        +save_as_json(fname)
    }
    
    class PciResetDeviceInfo {
        +List~int~ pci_index
    }
    
    class MoboReset {
        +Union~List~int~, None~ nb_host_pci_idx
        +str mobo
        +List~str~ credo
        +List~str~ disabled_ports
    }
    
    HostResetLog --> PciResetDeviceInfo : gs_tensix_reset
    HostResetLog --> PciResetDeviceInfo : wh_link_reset
    HostResetLog --> MoboReset : wh_mobo_reset (list)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:149-185]()

### Configuration Fields

| Field | Type | Purpose | Optional |
|-------|------|---------|----------|
| `time` | `datetime` | Timestamp of configuration generation | Yes |
| `host_name` | `str` | Hostname where reset is executed | Yes |
| `gs_tensix_reset` | `PciResetDeviceInfo` | Grayskull devices to reset | Yes |
| `wh_link_reset` | `PciResetDeviceInfo` | Wormhole devices to reset via link reset | Yes |
| `re_init_devices` | `bool` | Whether to reinitialize devices after reset | Yes |
| `wh_mobo_reset` | `List[MoboReset]` | Galaxy motherboard reset configurations | Yes |
| `disable_serial_report` | `bool` | Flag to disable serial number reporting | Yes |
| `disable_sw_version_report` | `bool` | Flag to disable software version reporting | Yes |

All fields are marked optional via the `@optional` decorator at [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:167](), allowing partial configurations.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:167-179](), [CHANGELOG.md:18-21]()

### Example Configuration

A generated configuration file contains:

```json
{
    "time": "2024-03-15T10:30:00",
    "host_name": "tt-host-01",
    "gs_tensix_reset": {
        "pci_index": []
    },
    "wh_link_reset": {
        "pci_index": [0, 1]
    },
    "re_init_devices": true,
    "disable_serial_report": false,
    "disable_sw_version_report": false,
    "wh_mobo_reset": [
        {
            "nb_host_pci_idx": [0, 1],
            "mobo": "<MOBO NAME>",
            "credo": ["<group id>:<credo id>", "<group id>:<credo id>"],
            "disabled_ports": ["<group id>:<credo id>", "<group id>:<credo id>"]
        }
    ]
}
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:102-124]()

## Configuration File Generation

The `generate_reset_logs` function creates a reset configuration file based on detected devices.

### Generation Process

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    Input["generate_reset_logs(<br/>devices,<br/>result_filename)"]
    GetTime["Get current<br/>datetime.datetime.now()"]
    Separate["Separate devices by type:<br/>gs_pci_idx = []<br/>wh_pci_idx = []"]
    IterDevs["For each device:<br/>if dev.as_wh() and<br/>not dev.is_remote():<br/>add to wh_pci_idx"]
    CreateLog["Create HostResetLog<br/>with PciResetDeviceInfo<br/>and sample MoboReset"]
    CheckFilename{"result_filename<br/>provided?"}
    CreateDirs["Create parent directories<br/>Path(dir_path).mkdir()"]
    UseDefault["Use default path:<br/>~/.config/tenstorrent/<br/>reset_config.json"]
    InitLogging["Init logging if<br/>LOG_FOLDER missing"]
    SaveJSON["reset_log.save_as_json(<br/>log_filename)"]
    Return["Return log_filename"]
    
    Input --> GetTime --> Separate --> IterDevs --> CreateLog
    CreateLog --> CheckFilename
    CheckFilename -->|Yes| CreateDirs --> SaveJSON
    CheckFilename -->|No| UseDefault --> InitLogging --> SaveJSON
    SaveJSON --> Return
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:89-134]()

### Default Configuration Path

The default configuration directory is `~/.config/tenstorrent/` defined by the `LOG_FOLDER` constant at [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:21](). If this directory doesn't exist, it is created via `init_logging(LOG_FOLDER)` at [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:132]().

### Sample Motherboard Reset Configuration

The generated configuration includes a sample `wh_mobo_reset` entry with placeholder values:

- `nb_host_pci_idx`: List of Wormhole PCI indices that are nearest-neighbor hosts
- `mobo`: Motherboard model name (placeholder: `"<MOBO NAME>"`)
- `credo`: List of Credo retimer identifiers in format `"<group id>:<credo id>"`
- `disabled_ports`: List of disabled port identifiers in same format

This sample configuration serves as a template for users to fill in actual Galaxy reset topology information.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:110-123]()

## Elasticsearch-Compatible Logging

The logging infrastructure uses Pydantic models that generate Elasticsearch-compatible type mappings, enabling structured log ingestion into Elasticsearch clusters for centralized monitoring and analysis.

### ElasticModel Base Class

All logging models inherit from `ElasticModel`, which extends Pydantic's `BaseModel` with Elasticsearch mapping generation capabilities.

```mermaid
flowchart TB
    subgraph "Type Mapping System"
        PydanticField["Pydantic Field"]
        FieldToMapping["field_to_mapping(info: Field)"]
        TypeToMapping["type_to_mapping(type: Any)"]
        ESMapping["Elasticsearch Mapping<br/>{type: '...', properties: {...}}"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Python to ES Type Translation"
        PyFloat["float"] --> ESFloat["{'type': 'float'}"]
        PyBool["bool"] --> ESBool["{'type': 'boolean'}"]
        PyInt["int"] --> ESInt["{'type': 'integer'}"]
        PyLong["Long"] --> ESLong["{'type': 'long'}"]
        PyStr["str"] --> ESText["{'type': 'text',<br/>'fields': {'keyword': {...}}}"]
        PyDate["datetime.date"] --> ESDate["{'type': 'date',<br/>'format': '...'}"]
        PyBytes["bytes"] --> ESBinary["{'type': 'binary'}"]
        ElasticModelClass["ElasticModel"] --> ESObject["{'type': 'object',<br/>'properties': {...}}"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Special Types"
        Keyword["Keyword(str)"] --> ESKeyword["{'type': 'keyword'}"]
        Text["Text(str)"] --> ESTextOnly["{'type': 'text'}"]
        Nested["Nested[T]"] --> ESNested["{'type': 'nested',<br/>'properties': {...}}"]
    end
    
    PydanticField --> FieldToMapping
    FieldToMapping --> TypeToMapping
    TypeToMapping --> ESMapping
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:68-116](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:127-136]()

### Mapping Generation Process

The `ElasticModel.get_mapping()` class method generates Elasticsearch index mappings:

1. Iterate over all Pydantic `__fields__` in the model
2. For each field, call `field_to_mapping(info)` to determine ES type
3. `field_to_mapping` delegates to `type_to_mapping(type)` for basic types
4. Nested `ElasticModel` instances recursively generate object properties
5. Return complete mapping dictionary

This enables automatic index creation with proper field types for efficient querying and aggregation.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:127-136]()

### Special Elasticsearch Types

The module defines custom type aliases for precise Elasticsearch mapping control:

- `Long(int)`: Maps to `long` type for 64-bit integers
- `Keyword(str)`: Maps to `keyword` type for exact matching (not analyzed)
- `Text(str)`: Maps to `text` type for full-text search
- `Date(datetime.datetime)`: Maps to `date` type with configurable format
- `Nested[T]`: Maps to `nested` type for array of objects

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:28-46](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:146]()

### Pydantic Version Compatibility

The module maintains compatibility with both Pydantic v1 and v2:

```python
try:
    # Try the newer v2 pydantic and use that first
    from pydantic.v1 import BaseModel
    from pydantic.v1.fields import Field
except:
    # Assume we are on v1 and give that a go
    from pydantic import BaseModel
    from pydantic.fields import Field
```

This fallback import strategy allows tt-tools-common to work in environments with either Pydantic major version, addressing compatibility issues noted in [CHANGELOG.md:78]().

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:15-22](), [CHANGELOG.md:74-78]()

## Pydantic Data Models

### PciResetDeviceInfo Model

Represents devices to be reset, identified by their PCI interface indices.

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class PciResetDeviceInfo {
        <<Pydantic Model>>
        +List~int~ pci_index
    }
    
    note for PciResetDeviceInfo "All fields optional via @optional decorator"
```

This model is used for both `gs_tensix_reset` and `wh_link_reset` fields in `HostResetLog`, containing the list of PCI indices for devices of that type.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:149-154]()

### MoboReset Model

Represents a Galaxy motherboard reset configuration with topology information.

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class MoboReset {
        <<Pydantic Model>>
        +Union~List~int~, None~ nb_host_pci_idx
        +str mobo
        +List~str~ credo
        +List~str~ disabled_ports
    }
    
    note for MoboReset "Used for wh_mobo_reset list<br/>All fields optional"
```

**Field Descriptions:**

- `nb_host_pci_idx`: PCI indices of nearest-neighbor host devices (nullable)
- `mobo`: Motherboard model identifier string
- `credo`: Credo retimer identifiers in format `"<group id>:<credo id>"`
- `disabled_ports`: Port identifiers to exclude from reset operations

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:156-165]()

### HostResetLog Model

The top-level model encapsulating complete reset configuration and metadata.

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    subgraph "HostResetLog Methods"
        SaveJSON["save_as_json(fname)"]
        GetMapping["get_mapping()<br/>(inherited)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Serialization Process"
        PydanticJSON["self.json(exclude_none=False)"]
        ReloadJSON["json.loads(raw_json)"]
        WriteFile["json.dump(reloaded_json, f, indent=4)"]
    end
    
    SaveJSON --> PydanticJSON
    PydanticJSON --> ReloadJSON
    ReloadJSON --> WriteFile
```

The `save_as_json` method serializes the model with proper formatting:

1. Call Pydantic's `json()` method with `exclude_none=False` to include all fields
2. Reload the JSON string to a Python dict for proper formatting
3. Write to file with 4-space indentation for readability

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:180-185]()

### Optional Fields Decorator

All data models use the `@optional` decorator to make fields optional:

```python
@optional
class PciResetDeviceInfo(ElasticModel):
    pci_index: List[int]
```

This decorator modifies the Pydantic model class to set `required = False` and `default = None` for specified fields, enabling partial configuration files where users only specify relevant fields.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:47-66]()

## Integration with Reset System

The configuration and logging system integrates with the broader reset infrastructure:

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    UserInput["User invokes reset:<br/>tt-smi -r all<br/>tt-smi -r 0,1<br/>tt-smi -r config.json"]
    ParseInput["parse_reset_input(args)"]
    ResetInput["ResetInput object<br/>type + value"]
    
    subgraph "Reset Execution Path"
        ResetAll["Reset all devices"]
        ResetIDs["Reset specified PCI IDs"]
        LoadConfig["Load JSON config"]
        ParseConfig["Parse HostResetLog"]
        ResetFromConfig["Reset per config"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Logging"
        GenerateLogs["generate_reset_logs(devices)"]
        SaveConfig["save_as_json(filename)"]
        ESIndex["Optional: Index to<br/>Elasticsearch"]
    end
    
    UserInput --> ParseInput
    ParseInput --> ResetInput
    ResetInput -->|ALL| ResetAll
    ResetInput -->|ID_LIST| ResetIDs
    ResetInput -->|CONFIG_JSON| LoadConfig
    LoadConfig --> ParseConfig
    ParseConfig --> ResetFromConfig
    
    ResetAll -.generates.-> GenerateLogs
    ResetIDs -.generates.-> GenerateLogs
    ResetFromConfig -.generates.-> GenerateLogs
    
    GenerateLogs --> SaveConfig
    SaveConfig -.optional.-> ESIndex
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:33-134](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:180-185]()

The configuration system serves dual purposes:
1. **Input specification**: Define which devices to reset and how
2. **Output logging**: Record reset operations for monitoring and debugging

This design enables both interactive reset operations (via command-line arguments) and automated reset workflows (via configuration files), while maintaining structured logging for operational visibility.
