# Platform Support and Virtualization

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document covers the platform-specific requirements and virtualization support for the tt-tools-common hardware reset system. It explains supported CPU architectures, ARM platform restrictions, Xen HVM hypervisor integration, and PCI device hotplug handling during reset operations.

For information about the overall reset architecture and chip-specific implementations, see [Reset Architecture and Design Patterns](#2.1), [ChipReset: Modern Unified Reset](#2.2), [Blackhole Reset Implementation](#2.3), and [Wormhole Reset Implementation](#2.4).

---

## Supported Platforms and Architecture Restrictions

The reset system has **strict platform compatibility requirements** due to PCIe device management differences across CPU architectures.

### x86_64 Platform Support

The reset system is **fully supported** on x86_64 (Intel/AMD) platforms. All reset operations, including:
- Secondary bus reset (SBR)
- ASIC reset
- M3/DMC reset
- PCI device hotplug/rescan

work correctly on x86_64 systems running Linux with the tt-kmd kernel driver version >= 2.4.1.

### ARM Platform Restrictions

**ARM platforms (ARM and AArch64) are NOT supported** for chip reset operations. The system explicitly checks the platform architecture and exits with an error if ARM is detected.

**Technical Reason**: ARM-based systems handle PCIe device rescans differently than x86_64. After issuing a PCIe reset, the PCI subsystem may not properly re-enumerate devices, leaving chips in an inaccessible state. The only reliable way to reset chips on ARM platforms is to **reboot the entire system**.

The platform check is performed in `get_host_info()["Platform"]` and compared against prefixes `"arm"` and `"aarch"`.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:139-148](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:109-118](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:103-112]()

---

## Platform Detection Implementation

```mermaid
graph TB
    ResetEntry["Reset Entry Point<br/>full_lds_reset()"]
    GetHostInfo["get_host_info()<br/>from system_utils"]
    PlatformCheck{"Platform starts with<br/>'arm' or 'aarch'?"}
    X86Path["Continue with<br/>reset sequence"]
    ARMExit["Print error:<br/>'Cannot perform board reset<br/>on Arm systems'<br/>sys.exit(1)"]
    
    ResetEntry --> GetHostInfo
    GetHostInfo --> PlatformCheck
    PlatformCheck -->|"No (x86_64)"| X86Path
    PlatformCheck -->|"Yes (ARM/AArch64)"| ARMExit
    
    style ARMExit fill:#ffcccc
    style X86Path fill:#ccffcc
```

**Platform Detection Flow**: Every reset operation validates platform architecture before proceeding

The `get_host_info()` function from `system_utils` returns a dictionary containing platform information using Python's `platform.machine()` API. Common return values include:
- `"x86_64"` for Intel/AMD 64-bit
- `"aarch64"` for ARM 64-bit
- `"armv7l"` for ARM 32-bit

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:141-142](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:get_host_info]()

---

## Xen HVM Virtualization Support

The reset system provides **full support for Xen HVM (Hardware Virtual Machine) guests** running on paravirtualized hypervisors. This enables Tenstorrent accelerators to be passed through to virtual machines using PCI passthrough while maintaining reset functionality.

### Xen HVM Detection

The system detects Xen HVM mode by reading two sysfs files:

| File Path | Expected Value |
|-----------|----------------|
| `/sys/hypervisor/type` | `"xen"` |
| `/sys/hypervisor/guest_type` | `"HVM"` |

Both conditions must be true for the system to operate in Xen HVM mode. The detection is implemented in the `check_xen_hvm()` function.

```mermaid
graph LR
    CheckXen["check_xen_hvm()"]
    ReadType["Read<br/>/sys/hypervisor/type"]
    ReadGuest["Read<br/>/sys/hypervisor/guest_type"]
    ValidateType{"type == 'xen'?"}
    ValidateGuest{"guest_type == 'HVM'?"}
    ReturnTrue["Return True<br/>(Xen HVM mode)"]
    ReturnFalse["Return False<br/>(Bare metal)"]
    
    CheckXen --> ReadType
    CheckXen --> ReadGuest
    ReadType --> ValidateType
    ReadGuest --> ValidateGuest
    ValidateType -->|Yes| ValidateGuest
    ValidateType -->|No| ReturnFalse
    ValidateGuest -->|Yes| ReturnTrue
    ValidateGuest -->|No| ReturnFalse
    
    style ReturnTrue fill:#ccffcc
    style ReturnFalse fill:#ccccff
```

**Xen HVM Detection Logic**: Two sysfs files must both exist and contain expected values

The function handles `FileNotFoundError` and `OSError` gracefully, returning `False` if either file is missing or inaccessible (indicating bare-metal execution).

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:34-51]()

---

## Xenstore Coordination Protocol

When running in Xen HVM mode, the reset system uses **Xenstore** (Xen's shared configuration/state database) to coordinate PCIe device hot-plug operations with the Dom0 (host) hypervisor.

### Why Xenstore Coordination is Necessary

During a chip reset in a virtual machine:
1. The guest initiates a reset via IOCTL
2. The device undergoes PCIe hot-remove
3. The device reappears on the PCI bus
4. The guest must wait for Dom0 to complete PCI re-enumeration
5. Only after Dom0 updates PCI state can the guest access the device

**Without coordination**, the guest might attempt to access the device before Dom0 has finished PCI rescanning, resulting in I/O errors or device inaccessibility.

### Xenstore File Naming Convention

For each device being reset, a Xenstore path is constructed from the PCI BDF (Bus:Device.Function) address:

```
pci_hard_reset/<bus>_<device>-<function>
```

**Example**: For device at PCI address `0000:81:00.0`, the Xenstore path is:
```
pci_hard_reset/81_00-0
```

The path construction logic splits the BDF string on `:` and `.` separators.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:178-180]()

### Xenstore Protocol State Machine

```mermaid
stateDiagram-v2
    [*] --> GuestWritesOne: Guest starts reset
    GuestWritesOne: Guest writes "1" to xenstore
    GuestWritesOne --> GuestIssuesReset: xenstore-write pci_hard_reset/X_Y-Z 1
    GuestIssuesReset: Guest issues ASIC reset IOCTL
    GuestIssuesReset --> DeviceHotRemove: Device undergoes PCIe hot-remove
    DeviceHotRemove: Device disappears from PCI bus
    DeviceHotRemove --> Dom0Detects: Dom0 detects device removal
    Dom0Detects: Dom0 processes PCI bus change
    Dom0Detects --> Dom0Rescans: Dom0 initiates PCI rescan
    Dom0Rescans: Dom0 re-enumerates PCI bus
    Dom0Rescans --> Dom0Cleanup: Dom0 removes xenstore entry
    Dom0Cleanup: Dom0 deletes pci_hard_reset/X_Y-Z
    Dom0Cleanup --> GuestPolls: Guest polls xenstore
    GuestPolls: Guest checks if xenstore file exists
    GuestPolls --> GuestPolls: File still exists (wait)
    GuestPolls --> DeviceReady: File removed (Dom0 done)
    DeviceReady: Device ready for guest access
    DeviceReady --> [*]: Guest calls POST_RESET IOCTL
```

**Xenstore Protocol State Machine**: Guest and Dom0 coordinate through xenstore file lifecycle

The guest polls the Xenstore path using `xenstore-read` commands until it returns a non-zero exit code (indicating the file no longer exists). This signals that Dom0 has completed PCI re-enumeration.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:214-257]()

### Xenstore Implementation Details

#### Sudo Privileges Requirement

All xenstore operations (`xenstore-write`, `xenstore-read`) require **root/sudo privileges**. The system:
1. Prompts the user for sudo credentials before reset
2. Validates credentials with `sudo -v`
3. Credentials are cached for 5 minutes by sudo
4. Revalidates before polling operations to ensure long-running operations don't timeout

#### Parallel Xenstore Polling

When resetting multiple devices, the system creates **one thread per device** to poll xenstore files in parallel. This prevents a slow Dom0 response for one device from blocking other devices.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Xenstore Polling Threads"
        MainThread["Main Thread"]
        Thread1["Thread 1<br/>wait_for_xenstore_removal<br/>pci_hard_reset/81_00-0"]
        Thread2["Thread 2<br/>wait_for_xenstore_removal<br/>pci_hard_reset/82_00-0"]
        Thread3["Thread 3<br/>wait_for_xenstore_removal<br/>pci_hard_reset/83_00-0"]
    end
    
    MainThread --> Thread1
    MainThread --> Thread2
    MainThread --> Thread3
    
    Thread1 --> Join["Main thread<br/>joins all threads"]
    Thread2 --> Join
    Thread3 --> Join
    
    Join --> Continue["Continue with<br/>POST_RESET operations"]
```

**Parallel Xenstore Polling**: One thread per device polls xenstore independently

Each thread has a **5-minute timeout**. If the xenstore file is not removed within this timeout, the system prints an error and exits.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:228-256]()

#### Error Handling

The xenstore integration handles several error conditions:

| Error Condition | Behavior |
|-----------------|----------|
| `xenstore-write` fails | Print warning, continue with reset (non-fatal) |
| `xenstore-read` timeout (5 min) | Print error, `sys.exit(1)` (fatal) |
| No xenstore filenames stored | Print error, `sys.exit(1)` (fatal) |
| Sudo authentication failure | Subprocess raises exception (fatal) |

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:189-193](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:245-248]()

---

## PCI Hotplug and Device Re-enumeration

After a chip reset, the device **temporarily disappears from the PCI bus** during hot-remove, then **reappears with a potentially different PCI interface ID**. The system must wait for the device to reappear before completing the reset sequence.

### Device Reappearance Detection

The `wait_for_device_to_reappear()` function monitors sysfs for device re-enumeration:

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["wait_for_device_to_reappear(bdf)"]
    SetDeadline["deadline = time.time() + 10s"]
    CheckTime{"time.time() < deadline?"}
    GlobCheck["glob.glob<br/>/sys/bus/pci/devices/{bdf}/tenstorrent/tenstorrent!*"]
    MatchFound{"Matches found?"}
    DevCheck["Check if<br/>/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}<br/>exists"]
    DevExists{"Device node exists?"}
    Return["Return new interface_id"]
    Sleep["time.sleep(0.1)"]
    Timeout["Print error<br/>sys.exit(1)"]
    
    Start --> SetDeadline
    SetDeadline --> CheckTime
    CheckTime -->|Yes| GlobCheck
    CheckTime -->|No| Timeout
    GlobCheck --> MatchFound
    MatchFound -->|Yes| DevCheck
    MatchFound -->|No| Sleep
    DevCheck -->|Yes| Return
    DevCheck -->|No| Sleep
    Sleep --> CheckTime
    
    style Return fill:#ccffcc
    style Timeout fill:#ffcccc
```

**Device Reappearance Detection**: Polls sysfs until device node reappears with 10-second timeout

The function:
1. Uses the **PCI BDF address** (which remains constant) to locate the device in sysfs
2. Extracts the **new interface ID** from the tenstorrent device symlink
3. Verifies the `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}` character device exists
4. Returns the new interface ID (which may differ from the original)

**Why Interface ID Changes**: During PCI hot-remove/hot-add cycles, the kernel driver may assign a different interface ID when the device reappears. The BDF address is stable, but the tt-kmd interface ID is not guaranteed to remain the same.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:87-111]()

### Post-Reset Wait Times

After issuing the reset IOCTL, the system waits for a calculated duration before checking for device reappearance:

| Reset Type | Wait Time |
|------------|-----------|
| ASIC reset (no M3) | `max(2, 0.4 * len(pci_interfaces))` seconds |
| ASIC+DMC reset (M3) | `m3_delay` seconds (default 20) |

The non-M3 reset uses a **per-device scaling factor** (0.4 seconds per device) to account for systems with many devices, where PCI rescanning takes longer.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:259-265]()

---

## Integration with Modern Reset Path

The Xen HVM detection and platform checks integrate into the **delegation pattern** used by chip-specific reset classes.

```mermaid
graph TD
    BHReset["BHChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
    WHReset["WHChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
    VersionCheck{"Driver version<br/>>= 2.4.1?"}
    XenCheck{"check_xen_hvm()<br/>returns True?"}
    UseModern["Use ChipReset<br/>modern implementation"]
    UseLegacy["Use legacy<br/>chip-specific reset"]
    
    BHReset --> VersionCheck
    WHReset --> VersionCheck
    VersionCheck -->|Yes| UseModern
    VersionCheck -->|No| XenCheck
    XenCheck -->|Yes| UseModern
    XenCheck -->|No| UseLegacy
    
    style UseModern fill:#ccffcc
    style UseLegacy fill:#ffeecc
```

**Reset Path Delegation**: Xen HVM detection routes to modern `ChipReset` even if driver < 2.4.1

The **key decision logic** in both `BHChipReset` and `WHChipReset`:

```python
if is_driver_version_at_least(get_driver_version(), "2.4.1") or check_xen_hvm():
    return ChipReset().full_lds_reset(...)
```

This ensures that:
- **Xen HVM guests always use the modern `ChipReset` path**, which includes xenstore coordination
- **Bare-metal systems use legacy paths if driver < 2.4.1**, maintaining backward compatibility
- **Both paths validate platform (reject ARM)** before proceeding

**Important**: The `ChipReset` class still requires driver >= 2.4.1 even in Xen mode. The Xen check bypasses the version check in the chip-specific classes, but `ChipReset.full_lds_reset()` calls `check_driver_version(operation="reset", minimum_required_version_str="2.4.1")`, which will fail if the driver is too old.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:92-99](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:89-90](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:137]()

---

## Driver Version Requirements

Virtualization support requires specific minimum driver versions:

| Feature | Minimum Driver Version |
|---------|----------------------|
| Basic reset operations | 1.26.0 |
| Modern unified reset (ChipReset) | 2.4.1 |
| Xen HVM support | 2.4.1 |
| ASIC_RESET and ASIC_DMC_RESET IOCTLs | 2.4.1 |
| POST_RESET IOCTL | 2.4.1 |

The modern `ChipReset` implementation uses **new IOCTL flags** (`IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_RESET`, `IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_DMC_RESET`, `IoctlResetFlags.POST_RESET`) that were introduced in driver version 2.4.1. These IOCTLs provide better integration with the kernel's PCI hotplug subsystem and are required for Xen HVM coordination.

For details on driver version checking, see [Driver Version Management](#3.1).

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:137](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:25-32]()

---

## Summary Table: Platform and Virtualization Support

| Platform/Environment | Supported | Notes |
|---------------------|-----------|-------|
| x86_64 bare-metal | ✅ Yes | Full support with driver >= 1.26.0 |
| x86_64 + driver >= 2.4.1 | ✅ Yes | Modern unified reset path |
| ARM/AArch64 bare-metal | ❌ No | PCIe rescan issues; requires system reboot |
| Xen HVM (x86_64) | ✅ Yes | Requires driver >= 2.4.1, uses xenstore coordination |
| Xen HVM (ARM) | ❌ No | ARM restriction applies even in virtualization |
| KVM/QEMU | ⚠️ Untested | No explicit support code; may work like bare-metal |
| VMware ESXi | ⚠️ Untested | No explicit support code |
| Windows Hyper-V | ❌ No | Linux-only driver |

The reset system is **explicitly designed and tested** for x86_64 bare-metal and Xen HVM environments. Other virtualization platforms may work but are not officially supported or tested.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:34-51](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:139-148](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:169-257]()
21:T32b5,
# System Utilities

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py)
- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py)

</details>



The System Utilities subsystem provides core infrastructure for managing system-level operations across all tt-tools applications. This module handles driver version validation, host system information collection, hardware detection with real-time status updates, firmware version conversions, and reference clock monitoring. These utilities form the foundation for safe hardware interaction by ensuring compatibility requirements are met before executing operations.

For chip reset operations that utilize these utilities, see [Hardware Reset System](#2). For UI components that display system information, see [User Interface Components](#4).

## Module Architecture

The system utilities are organized into two primary modules that provide complementary functionality for system interaction and hardware management.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "System Utilities Package"
        subgraph "system_utils.py"
            DriverVersion["get_driver_version()<br/>check_driver_version()"]
            HostInfo["get_host_info()<br/>get_host_compatibility_info()"]
            SwVersion["get_sw_ver_info()<br/>get_sw_ver_from_url()"]
        end
        
        subgraph "tools_utils.py"
            ChipDetect["detect_chips_with_callback()"]
            VersionConv["hex_to_semver()<br/>hex_to_semver_eth()<br/>hex_to_semver_m3_fw()<br/>hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw()"]
            RefClk["read_refclk_counter()<br/>refclk_counter_rate()<br/>check_refclk_counter_rate()"]
            DataLoad["init_fw_defines()<br/>get_chip_data()"]
            BoardType["get_board_type()"]
        end
    end
    
    subgraph "External Dependencies"
        PyLuwen["pyluwen.PciChip<br/>pyluwen.detect_chips_fallible"]
        System["psutil<br/>platform<br/>distro"]
        Network["requests"]
    end
    
    subgraph "System Resources"
        KernelDriver["/sys/module/tenstorrent/version"]
        ConfigFile["~/.config/tenstorrent/reset_config.json"]
        DataFiles["data/{chip}/fw_defines.yaml"]
    end
    
    DriverVersion --> KernelDriver
    HostInfo --> System
    SwVersion --> Network
    SwVersion --> ConfigFile
    
    ChipDetect --> PyLuwen
    RefClk --> PyLuwen
    DataLoad --> DataFiles
    
    style DriverVersion fill:#f9f9f9
    style HostInfo fill:#f9f9f9
    style ChipDetect fill:#f9f9f9
    style RefClk fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:1-296](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:1-355]()

## Core Functionality Groups

### Driver Version Management

Driver version management ensures that operations requiring specific kernel driver features validate compatibility before execution. The system reads version information from the kernel module sysfs interface and performs semantic version comparison.

| Function | Purpose | Return Type |
|----------|---------|-------------|
| `get_driver_version()` | Reads driver version from `/sys/module/tenstorrent/version` | `str` or `None` |
| `is_driver_version_at_least()` | Compares semantic versions including pre-release tags | `bool` |
| `check_driver_version()` | Validates version requirement and exits on failure | `None` (exits on error) |

The default minimum version for reset operations is `MINIMUM_DRIVER_VERSION_LDS_RESET = "1.26.0"` [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:17]().

For detailed documentation, see [Driver Version Management](#3.1).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:35-142]()

### Host Information Collection

Host information functions gather system details for compatibility validation and display in user interfaces. The `get_host_info()` function collects basic system information, while `get_host_compatibility_info()` adds validation logic to identify incompatible configurations.

```mermaid
graph LR
    GetHostInfo["get_host_info()"] --> SystemInfo["OS, Distro, Kernel<br/>Hostname, Platform<br/>Python, Memory, Driver"]
    GetHostInfo --> PSUtil["psutil.virtual_memory()"]
    GetHostInfo --> Platform["platform.uname()"]
    GetHostInfo --> Distro["distro.name()"]
    
    SystemInfo --> GetCompatibility["get_host_compatibility_info()"]
    GetCompatibility --> ValidationLogic["OS == Linux<br/>Distro >= Ubuntu 22.04<br/>Memory >= 32GB<br/>Driver >= 1.27"]
    ValidationLogic --> CompatDict["Dict with str or<br/>Tuple[current, expected]"]
```

For detailed documentation, see [Host Information and Compatibility](#3.2).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:145-211]()

### Chip Detection and Communication

The `detect_chips_with_callback()` function provides interactive chip detection with real-time progress feedback. It wraps `pyluwen.detect_chips_fallible()` with a callback mechanism that reports detection status for local PCIe devices and remote Ethernet-connected chips.

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant App as "Application"
    participant Detect as "detect_chips_with_callback()"
    participant Callback as "chip_detect_callback()"
    participant PyLuwen as "pyluwen.detect_chips_fallible()"
    participant Output as "Console Output"
    
    App->>Detect: local_only, ignore_ethernet, print_status
    Detect->>PyLuwen: Start chip detection with callback
    
    loop For each detection event
        PyLuwen->>Callback: status (new_chip, correct_down, status_string)
        Callback->>Callback: Update counters (chip_count, arc_count, dram_count)
        Callback->>Output: Print formatted status with spinner
    end
    
    PyLuwen->>Detect: List of detected devices
    
    loop For each device
        Detect->>Detect: Check device.have_comms()
        Detect->>Detect: device.force_upgrade()
    end
    
    Detect->>App: List[PciChip]
```

For detailed documentation, see [Chip Detection and Communication](#3.3).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:255-354]()

### Version Conversion Utilities

Multiple firmware types use different hexadecimal encoding schemes for version numbers. The utilities provide specialized conversion functions for each firmware type:

| Function | Format | Example |
|----------|--------|---------|
| `hex_to_semver()` | `0xAABBCC00` → `AA.BB.CC` | Standard firmware versions |
| `hex_to_semver_eth()` | `0xAAbCCC` → `AA.b.CCC` | Ethernet firmware (12-bit patch) |
| `hex_to_semver_m3_fw()` | `0xAABBCCDD` → `AA.BB.CC.DD` | M3 firmware (4-part version) |
| `hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw()` | `0xAABBCCDD` → `AA.BB.CC-rcDD` | Zephyr firmware (with RC suffix) |

For detailed documentation, see [Version Conversions and Data Loading](#3.4).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:136-189]()

### Reference Clock Monitoring

Reference clock monitoring validates that the hardware clock counters are incrementing at the expected rate, independent of the ARC clock. This provides a hardware health check mechanism.

```mermaid
graph TD
    ReadRefClk["read_refclk_counter(chip)"] --> ReadHigh["axi_read32(REFCLK_COUNTER_HIGH)"]
    ReadRefClk --> ReadLow["axi_read32(REFCLK_COUNTER_LOW)"]
    ReadHigh --> Check["Check high1 == high2"]
    Check -->|Different| Reread["Re-read low counter"]
    Check -->|Same| Combine["Combine: (high << 32) | low"]
    Reread --> Combine
    
    RefClkRate["refclk_counter_rate(chip, delay)"] --> Before["Read counter and time"]
    Before --> Sleep["time.sleep(delay_interval)"]
    Sleep --> After["Read counter and time"]
    After --> Calculate["(after - before) * 1000 / time_ns"]
    
    CheckRate["check_refclk_counter_rate()"] --> RefClkRate
    CheckRate --> Compare["Compare to expected_refclk"]
    Compare -->|Outside range| Error["Return error message"]
    Compare -->|Within range| Success["Return None"]
```

For detailed documentation, see [Reference Clock Monitoring](#3.5).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:202-253]()

## Data Loading and Board Identification

### Firmware Definitions

The `init_fw_defines()` function loads chip-specific firmware message definitions from YAML files. These definitions map firmware message types and constants for chip communication.

```python
# Example usage
fw_defines = init_fw_defines(chip_name="wormhole", tool_name="tt_smi")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:17-24]()

### Board Type Detection

The `get_board_type()` function extracts board type information from the Unique Part Identifier (UPI) field encoded in the board serial number. The serial number format follows the pattern `AA-BBBBB-C-D-EE-FF-XXX` where `BBBBB` represents the UPI.

```mermaid
graph LR
    SerialNum["Board ID String<br/>AA-BBBBB-C-D-EE-FF-XXX"] --> HexConvert["Convert to hex int"]
    HexConvert --> ExtractUPI["UPI = (serial >> 36) & 0xFFFFF"]
    HexConvert --> ExtractRev["REV = (serial >> 32) & 0xF"]
    
    ExtractUPI --> MapType["UPI Mapping"]
    ExtractRev --> MapType
    
    MapType --> Types["0x1: E300_R2/R3<br/>0x3: e150<br/>0x7: e75<br/>0x8: NEBULA_CB<br/>0xA: e300<br/>0xB: GALAXY<br/>0x14: n300<br/>0x18: n150"]
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:46-91]()

## Software Version Reporting

The system supports optional integration with a remote version tracking service to report software stack versions associated with specific board serial numbers. This feature respects user privacy preferences through configuration flags.

| Configuration Flag | Effect |
|-------------------|--------|
| `disable_sw_version_report` | Returns default "N/A" values for all versions |
| `disable_serial_report` | Queries version service without board serial number |

The configuration is stored in `~/.config/tenstorrent/reset_config.json` [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:217-228]().

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:213-296]()

## Integration with Reset System

System utilities are extensively used by the reset system to validate preconditions before executing hardware operations. The driver version check is mandatory for reset operations, while host compatibility information provides user-facing diagnostics.

```mermaid
graph TB
    ResetOperation["Chip Reset Operation"] --> CheckDriver["check_driver_version('reset', '1.26.0')"]
    
    CheckDriver -->|Pass| DetectChips["detect_chips_with_callback()"]
    CheckDriver -->|Fail| Exit["sys.exit(1) with error message"]
    
    DetectChips --> ValidateComms["Validate device.have_comms()"]
    ValidateComms -->|Fail| Exception["Raise Exception: no comms"]
    ValidateComms -->|Pass| Upgrade["device.force_upgrade()"]
    
    Upgrade --> ResetLogic["Execute Reset Logic"]
```

For complete reset system documentation, see [Hardware Reset System](#2) and [Platform Support and Virtualization](#2.7).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:99-142](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:255-354]()

## Error Handling Patterns

### Version Parsing Errors

The `_parse_version_string()` function handles semantic version strings with pre-release identifiers and build metadata according to SemVer conventions. It strips suffixes before parsing numeric components [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:47-80]().

Examples of supported formats:
- `"1.34.0"` → `(1, 34, 0)`
- `"1.34.1-alpha"` → `(1, 34, 1)`
- `"1.2.3+build456"` → `(1, 2, 3)`
- `"1.4.0-rc1+build42"` → `(1, 4, 0)`

### Communication Validation

The chip detection function validates communication status and raises exceptions for devices without working communication channels. This prevents subsequent operations from failing due to hardware issues:

```python
if not device.have_comms():
    raise Exception(
        f"Do not have communication with {device}, you should reset or "
        "remove this device from your system before continuing."
    )
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:346-349]()

## Usage in Consumer Tools

System utilities are consumed by multiple Tenstorrent tools including tt-smi, tt-flash, and others. Common usage patterns include:

1. **Driver validation at startup**: Call `check_driver_version()` before any hardware operation
2. **System info display**: Use `get_host_info()` or `get_host_compatibility_info()` for UI rendering
3. **Hardware enumeration**: Call `detect_chips_with_callback()` with appropriate progress display
4. **Firmware version display**: Convert hex versions using appropriate `hex_to_semver_*()` variant

For UI integration examples, see [Widget Library Reference](#4.1) and [Building Custom TUI Applications](#4.4).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:1-296](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:1-355]()

# Driver Version Management

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This page documents the driver version management system in tt-tools-common, which provides detection, parsing, and validation of the Tenstorrent kernel driver (tt-kmd) version. The system ensures that operations requiring specific driver capabilities only execute when the installed driver meets minimum version requirements. This prevents runtime failures and provides clear error messages when version requirements are not met.

For information about the overall reset system that depends on driver version validation, see [Hardware Reset System](#2). For details on host information gathering and compatibility checking, see [Host Information and Compatibility](#3.2).

---

## System Overview

The driver version management system consists of four primary components:

1. **Version Detection**: Reading the current driver version from the kernel module
2. **Version Parsing**: Converting version strings into comparable numeric tuples
3. **Version Comparison**: Determining if current version meets minimum requirements
4. **Validation & Enforcement**: Checking requirements and failing gracefully with user guidance

The system supports semantic versioning (SemVer) with extensions for pre-release identifiers and build metadata commonly used in driver versioning schemes.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:1-142]()

---

## Version Detection Architecture

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Client Code"
        ResetOp["Reset Operation<br/>(e.g., ChipReset)"]
        ToolInit["Tool Initialization<br/>(e.g., tt-smi startup)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Public API"
        CheckDriver["check_driver_version()<br/>Validate and exit if insufficient"]
        GetDriver["get_driver_version()<br/>Return version string or None"]
        IsAtLeast["is_driver_version_at_least()<br/>Boolean comparison"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Internal Parsing"
        ParseVersion["_parse_version_string()<br/>SemVer to (major, minor, patch)"]
        TupleCompare["Python tuple comparison<br/>(1,26,0) >= (1,26,0)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Kernel Interface"
        SysFS["/sys/module/tenstorrent/version<br/>Kernel module version file"]
        KernelModule["tt-kmd Driver Module<br/>Loaded in kernel"]
    end
    
    ResetOp --> CheckDriver
    ToolInit --> GetDriver
    
    CheckDriver --> IsAtLeast
    CheckDriver --> GetDriver
    IsAtLeast --> GetDriver
    IsAtLeast --> ParseVersion
    
    ParseVersion --> TupleCompare
    
    GetDriver --> SysFS
    SysFS --> KernelModule
    
    CheckDriver -.->|"Exit on failure"| ErrorMsg["sys.exit(1)<br/>Red error message"]
```

**Version Detection Flow Diagram**

The system follows a layered architecture where high-level operations call validation functions that internally perform version detection and parsing. The kernel interface is accessed through a simple file read from sysfs.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:35-142]()

---

## Version Detection Implementation

### Reading Driver Version from Kernel

The `get_driver_version()` function reads the Tenstorrent driver version directly from the kernel module's sysfs interface:

| Aspect | Details |
|--------|---------|
| **Function** | `get_driver_version()` |
| **Location** | [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:35-45]() |
| **Kernel Path** | `/sys/module/tenstorrent/version` |
| **Return Type** | `Union[str, None]` |
| **Error Handling** | Returns `None` if file doesn't exist or read fails |

The function performs a simple file read operation with exception handling to gracefully handle cases where the driver is not installed or the kernel module is not loaded.

**Typical Version Strings:**
- `"1.26.0"` - Standard release version
- `"1.28-bh"` - Version with extraversion field (Blackhole-specific)
- `"1.34.1-alpha"` - Pre-release version
- `"2.4.1+build456"` - Version with build metadata

Sources: [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:35-45](), [CHANGELOG.md:57-59]()

---

## Semantic Version Parsing

### Version String Format Support

The `_parse_version_string()` function handles multiple version string formats according to semantic versioning conventions:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Input Formats"
        Simple["1.34"]
        Standard["1.34.0"]
        PreRelease["1.34.1-alpha"]
        BuildMeta["1.2.3+build456"]
        Combined["1.4.0-rc1+build42"]
        ExtraVersion["1.28-bh"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Parsing Pipeline"
        StripBuild["Strip Build Metadata<br/>Split on '+'"]
        StripPre["Strip Pre-release<br/>Split on '-'"]
        SplitDots["Split on '.'<br/>Extract numeric parts"]
        DefaultZeros["Default missing parts to 0"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Output"
        Tuple["(major, minor, patch)<br/>e.g., (1, 34, 0)"]
    end
    
    Simple --> StripBuild
    Standard --> StripBuild
    PreRelease --> StripBuild
    BuildMeta --> StripBuild
    Combined --> StripBuild
    ExtraVersion --> StripBuild
    
    StripBuild --> StripPre
    StripPre --> SplitDots
    SplitDots --> DefaultZeros
    DefaultZeros --> Tuple
```

**Semantic Version Parsing Pipeline**

### Parsing Rules

| Rule | Description | Example Input | Extracted Core | Output Tuple |
|------|-------------|---------------|----------------|--------------|
| **Standard** | Three numeric parts | `"1.34.0"` | `"1.34.0"` | `(1, 34, 0)` |
| **Short** | Two or one parts | `"1.34"` | `"1.34"` | `(1, 34, 0)` |
| **Pre-release** | Version with `-identifier` | `"1.34.1-alpha"` | `"1.34.1"` | `(1, 34, 1)` |
| **Build metadata** | Version with `+metadata` | `"1.2.3+build456"` | `"1.2.3"` | `(1, 2, 3)` |
| **Combined** | Both pre-release and build | `"1.4.0-rc1+build42"` | `"1.4.0"` | `(1, 4, 0)` |
| **Extraversion** | Hyphenated extension | `"1.28-bh"` | `"1.28"` | `(1, 28, 0)` |

### Error Handling

The parser raises `ValueError` in the following cases:
- Empty version string
- Empty string after splitting
- Non-integer version components

Sources: [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:47-80]()

---

## Version Comparison Logic

### Comparison Function

The `is_driver_version_at_least()` function performs version comparison using Python's lexicographic tuple comparison:

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["is_driver_version_at_least(<br/>current_version, minimum_version)"]
    
    CheckNull{"current_version<br/>is None?"}
    RaiseError["Raise ValueError:<br/>No driver detected"]
    
    ParseCurrent["Parse current_version<br/>→ current_tuple"]
    ParseMinimum["Parse minimum_version<br/>→ minimum_tuple"]
    
    Compare{"current_tuple >= minimum_tuple<br/>(lexicographic comparison)"}
    
    ReturnTrue["Return True<br/>(version sufficient)"]
    ReturnFalse["Return False<br/>(version insufficient)"]
    
    Start --> CheckNull
    CheckNull -->|Yes| RaiseError
    CheckNull -->|No| ParseCurrent
    ParseCurrent --> ParseMinimum
    ParseMinimum --> Compare
    Compare -->|True| ReturnTrue
    Compare -->|False| ReturnFalse
```

**Version Comparison Decision Flow**

### Comparison Examples

| Current Version | Minimum Required | Current Tuple | Minimum Tuple | Result | Explanation |
|----------------|------------------|---------------|---------------|--------|-------------|
| `"1.34.0"` | `"1.26.0"` | `(1, 34, 0)` | `(1, 26, 0)` | `True` | Current is newer |
| `"1.26.0"` | `"1.26.0"` | `(1, 26, 0)` | `(1, 26, 0)` | `True` | Versions match exactly |
| `"1.25.9"` | `"1.26.0"` | `(1, 25, 9)` | `(1, 26, 0)` | `False` | Current is older (minor) |
| `"2.0.0"` | `"1.35.0"` | `(2, 0, 0)` | `(1, 35, 0)` | `True` | Major version bump |
| `"1.26.0-alpha"` | `"1.26.0"` | `(1, 26, 0)` | `(1, 26, 0)` | `True` | Pre-release stripped |

Python's tuple comparison works lexicographically (left-to-right), which correctly implements semantic version comparison when tuples are ordered as `(major, minor, patch)`.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:82-97]()

---

## Driver Version Validation

### Validation and Enforcement

The `check_driver_version()` function combines detection, parsing, and comparison into a single validation operation with automatic error handling:

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `operation` | `str` | Required | Name of operation requiring driver version check |
| `minimum_required_version_str` | `str` | `"1.26.0"` | Minimum acceptable driver version |

**Behavior:**
1. Calls `get_driver_version()` to detect current version
2. Calls `is_driver_version_at_least()` to compare versions
3. Returns silently if version is sufficient
4. Prints red error messages and calls `sys.exit(1)` if insufficient or parsing fails

### Error Messages

The function provides three categories of error messages:

**1. Parsing Error:**
```
Error parsing driver version. {exception message}
```

**2. Insufficient Version:**
```
Current driver version: {current_version}
Operation '{operation}' requires Tenstorrent driver version {minimum_version} or greater. Your version is too old.
Please update your driver using tt-kmd: https://github.com/tenstorrent/tt-kmd
```

**3. No Driver Detected:**
```
No Tenstorrent driver detected! Please install the driver using tt-kmd: https://github.com/tenstorrent/tt-kmd
```

All error messages use `CMD_LINE_COLOR.RED` for terminal output visibility.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:99-142]()

---

## Integration with Reset System

### Minimum Version Requirements

The reset system defines minimum driver version requirements as module-level constants:

| Constant | Value | Purpose |
|----------|-------|---------|
| `MINIMUM_DRIVER_VERSION_LDS_RESET` | `"1.26.0"` | Required for performing LDS (Link/Device/System) reset operations |

This constant is used as the default parameter value for `check_driver_version()`.

### Reset Integration Points

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Reset Entry Points"
        BHReset["BHChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
        WHReset["WHChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
        ModernReset["ChipReset.full_lds_reset()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Version Validation Layer"
        CheckVersion["check_driver_version(<br/>'reset', '1.26.0')"]
        DriverVersionConstant["MINIMUM_DRIVER_VERSION_LDS_RESET"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Conditional Logic"
        VersionCheck{"Driver >= 2.4.1?"}
        UsesModern["Use ChipReset<br/>(modern path)"]
        UsesLegacy["Use legacy reset<br/>(chip-specific)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Hardware Operations"
        IOCTLReset["IOCTL-based reset"]
        ARCReset["ARC message reset"]
        NOCReset["NOC register reset"]
    end
    
    BHReset --> VersionCheck
    WHReset --> VersionCheck
    
    VersionCheck -->|Yes| ModernReset
    VersionCheck -->|No| UsesLegacy
    
    ModernReset --> CheckVersion
    UsesLegacy --> CheckVersion
    
    CheckVersion --> DriverVersionConstant
    
    CheckVersion -.->|Pass| IOCTLReset
    CheckVersion -.->|Pass| ARCReset
    CheckVersion -.->|Pass| NOCReset
    
    CheckVersion -.->|Fail| Exit["sys.exit(1)"]
```

**Driver Version Check Integration in Reset System**

The reset system performs version checks at multiple levels:
1. **Pre-flight validation**: Before executing any reset operation
2. **Conditional routing**: To determine if modern `ChipReset` implementation can be used (requires driver >= 2.4.1)
3. **Operation gating**: To ensure minimum version 1.26.0 for basic reset functionality

Sources: [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:17](), [CHANGELOG.md:103]()

---

## Usage Patterns

### Pattern 1: Pre-flight Validation

Used at the start of operations that require specific driver versions:

```python
# In reset operation
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import check_driver_version

def perform_reset():
    # Validate driver version, exit if insufficient
    check_driver_version("reset", "1.26.0")
    
    # Continue with reset operations...
```

### Pattern 2: Conditional Feature Enablement

Used to determine which code path to execute based on driver capabilities:

```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import (
    get_driver_version, 
    is_driver_version_at_least
)

driver_version = get_driver_version()
if is_driver_version_at_least(driver_version, "2.4.1"):
    # Use modern ChipReset implementation
    use_modern_reset_path()
else:
    # Fall back to legacy implementation
    use_legacy_reset_path()
```

### Pattern 3: Information Display

Used in diagnostic tools and compatibility menus:

```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import get_driver_version

def show_system_info():
    driver_version = get_driver_version()
    if driver_version:
        print(f"TT-KMD {driver_version}")
    else:
        print("Driver not installed")
```

Sources: [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:99-142]()

---

## Version History and Evolution

### Critical Version Milestones

| Driver Version | Significance |
|----------------|--------------|
| `1.26.0` | Minimum version for LDS reset operations |
| `2.4.1` | Enables modern `ChipReset` unified implementation for Blackhole and Wormhole |

### Bug Fixes and Improvements

| Release | Issue | Fix |
|---------|-------|-----|
| **1.4.7** | Crash when parsing driver versions with extraversion field (e.g., `"1.28-bh"`) | Enhanced `_parse_version_string()` to strip pre-release identifiers before parsing |
| **1.4.0** | Driver version requirement not enforced for reset operations | Added `check_driver_version()` call with minimum version 1.26.0 |

The extraversion field fix in release 1.4.7 was particularly important as it enabled the system to handle Blackhole-specific driver builds that append chip identifiers to version strings.

Sources: [CHANGELOG.md:57-59](), [CHANGELOG.md:103]()

---

## Error Handling and User Guidance

### Error Categories

```mermaid
graph TD
    ErrorEntry["Driver Version Error"]
    
    NoDriver["No Driver Installed<br/>driver_version = None"]
    ParseError["Malformed Version String<br/>ValueError during parsing"]
    InsufficientVersion["Version Too Old<br/>current < minimum"]
    
    NoDriverMsg["Error: No Tenstorrent driver detected!<br/>Install tt-kmd from GitHub"]
    ParseErrorMsg["Error parsing driver version.<br/>exception details"]
    InsufficientMsg["Current driver version: X.Y.Z<br/>Operation requires version A.B.C or greater<br/>Update driver from tt-kmd"]
    
    AllExit["sys.exit(1)<br/>Terminal: Red colored text"]
    
    ErrorEntry --> NoDriver
    ErrorEntry --> ParseError
    ErrorEntry --> InsufficientVersion
    
    NoDriver --> NoDriverMsg
    ParseError --> ParseErrorMsg
    InsufficientVersion --> InsufficientMsg
    
    NoDriverMsg --> AllExit
    ParseErrorMsg --> AllExit
    InsufficientMsg --> AllExit
```

**Error Handling Decision Tree**

### User Guidance Strategy

All error messages direct users to the tt-kmd repository for driver installation or updates: `https://github.com/tenstorrent/tt-kmd`

The error messages use color coding (red) via `CMD_LINE_COLOR.RED` to ensure visibility in terminal output, particularly important when errors occur during automated scripts or CI/CD pipelines.

Sources: [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:86-142]()

# Host Information and Compatibility

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document describes the host information collection and compatibility checking subsystem within tt-tools-common. This subsystem provides functions for gathering system details (OS, distribution, memory, platform architecture), validating compatibility against Tenstorrent requirements, and querying software version information from remote services.

For driver version management and validation, see [Driver Version Management](#3.1). For chip detection and hardware communication, see [Chip Detection and Communication](#3.3). For UI widgets that display this information, see [Widget Library Reference](#4.1).

---

## System Architecture

### Host Information Collection Flow

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Public API Functions"
        GetHostInfo["get_host_info()"]
        GetCompatInfo["get_host_compatibility_info()"]
        GetSwVerInfo["get_sw_ver_info()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "System Libraries"
        Platform["platform.uname()<br/>OS, kernel, hostname"]
        Psutil["psutil.virtual_memory()<br/>Memory info"]
        Distro["distro module<br/>Distribution detection"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Driver Integration"
        GetDriverVer["get_driver_version()<br/>/sys/module/tenstorrent/version"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Remote Services"
        CerealAPI["cereal.tenstorrent.com<br/>Software version query"]
        GetSwVerURL["get_sw_ver_from_url(board_id)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Configuration"
        ResetConfig["~/.config/tenstorrent/reset_config.json"]
        GetSwVerFlags["get_sw_ver_flags()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Return Values"
        HostInfoDict["dict: str -> str<br/>OS, Distro, Kernel, etc."]
        CompatDict["dict: str -> str | tuple<br/>Compatible: str<br/>Incompatible: (current, recommended)"]
        SwVerDict["dict: str -> str<br/>Package versions"]
    end
    
    GetHostInfo --> Platform
    GetHostInfo --> Psutil
    GetHostInfo --> Distro
    GetHostInfo --> GetDriverVer
    GetHostInfo --> HostInfoDict
    
    GetCompatInfo --> GetHostInfo
    GetCompatInfo --> CompatDict
    
    GetSwVerInfo --> GetSwVerFlags
    GetSwVerInfo --> GetSwVerURL
    GetSwVerInfo --> SwVerDict
    
    GetSwVerFlags --> ResetConfig
    GetSwVerURL --> CerealAPI
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:145-211]()

---

## Host Information Collection

### `get_host_info()` Function

The `get_host_info()` function collects comprehensive system information by querying multiple Python standard library modules. It returns a dictionary containing eight key system attributes.

**Data Sources and Collection:**

| Information | Source Module | Collection Method |
|------------|---------------|-------------------|
| OS | `platform.uname()` | `uname.system` |
| Distro | `distro` | `distro.name(pretty=True)` |
| Kernel | `platform.uname()` | `uname.release` |
| Hostname | `platform.uname()` | `uname.node` |
| Platform | `platform.uname()` | `uname.machine` (e.g., "x86_64", "aarch64") |
| Python | `platform` | `platform.python_version()` |
| Memory | `psutil` | `psutil.virtual_memory().total` (formatted via `get_size()`) |
| Driver | Custom | `get_driver_version()` reads `/sys/module/tenstorrent/version` |

**Return Format:**

```python
{
    "OS": str,           # e.g., "Linux"
    "Distro": str,       # e.g., "Ubuntu 22.04.3 LTS"
    "Kernel": str,       # e.g., "5.15.0-89-generic"
    "Hostname": str,     # e.g., "tenstorrent-dev"
    "Platform": str,     # e.g., "x86_64" or "aarch64"
    "Python": str,       # e.g., "3.10.12"
    "Memory": str,       # e.g., "62.68 GB" (human-readable format)
    "Driver": str        # e.g., "TT-KMD 1.27.0" (prefixed with "TT-KMD ")
}
```

**Memory Formatting:**

The `get_size()` helper function [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:20-32]() scales bytes to human-readable format using 1024-based units (KB, MB, GB, TB, PB). For example, `1253656678` bytes becomes `"1.17 GB"`.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:145-168](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:35-45](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:20-32]()

---

## Compatibility Checking

### `get_host_compatibility_info()` Function

This function extends `get_host_info()` by adding compatibility validation against Tenstorrent requirements. The return format uses a special convention to indicate compatibility status.

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Compatibility Checks"
        OSCheck["OS Check<br/>Required: Linux (x86_64)"]
        DistroCheck["Distro Check<br/>Required: Ubuntu 22.04+"]
        MemCheck["Memory Check<br/>Required: 32GB+"]
        DriverCheck["Driver Check<br/>Required: TT-KMD present"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Input Data"
        HostInfo["get_host_info() output"]
        Platform["uname.machine"]
        DistroID["distro.id()"]
        DistroVer["distro.version_parts()"]
        MemTotal["psutil.virtual_memory().total"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Return Value Format"
        Compatible["str value<br/>'Linux (x86_64)'"]
        Incompatible["tuple value<br/>('Linux (aarch64)', 'Linux (x86_64)')"]
    end
    
    HostInfo --> OSCheck
    Platform --> OSCheck
    DistroID --> DistroCheck
    DistroVer --> DistroCheck
    MemTotal --> MemCheck
    HostInfo --> DriverCheck
    
    OSCheck -->|Pass| Compatible
    OSCheck -->|Fail| Incompatible
    DistroCheck -->|Pass| Compatible
    DistroCheck -->|Fail| Incompatible
    MemCheck -->|Pass| Compatible
    MemCheck -->|Fail| Incompatible
    DriverCheck -->|Pass| Compatible
    DriverCheck -->|Fail| Incompatible
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:170-211]()

### Return Value Convention

The function returns `Dict[str, Union[str, Tuple[str, str]]]` where:

- **Compatible items** return a single string: the current value
- **Incompatible items** return a tuple: `(current_value, recommended_value)`

This convention enables UI components to distinguish compatible from incompatible items without additional metadata.

### Compatibility Requirements

| Item | Requirement | Check Logic |
|------|-------------|-------------|
| **OS** | Linux (x86_64) | Compares `uname.system` and `uname.machine`. Non-Linux or ARM platforms return tuple. |
| **Distro** | Ubuntu 22.04 or 24.04 | Checks `distro.id() == "ubuntu"` and version >= 22. Other distros return tuple. |
| **Kernel** | N/A | Always returns string (informational only). |
| **Hostname** | N/A | Always returns string (informational only). |
| **Python** | N/A | Always returns string (informational only). |
| **Memory** | 32GB+ | Checks `psutil.virtual_memory().total >= 32e9`. Less than 32GB returns tuple. |
| **Driver** | TT-KMD present | Returns tuple if driver version is `None`, otherwise returns string. |

**Implementation Details:**

The Ubuntu distro version check [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:188-195]() parses the first two version parts and converts to float:

```python
distro_version = float(".".join(distro.version_parts()[:2]))
if distro_version >= 22:
    checklist["Distro"] = host_info["Distro"]  # Compatible
else:
    checklist["Distro"] = (host_info["Distro"], "22.04 or 24.04")  # Incompatible
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:170-211]()

---

## Software Version Reporting

### Version Query System

The software version reporting system queries a remote service to retrieve recommended software versions for Tenstorrent boards. This system respects privacy flags configured in the reset configuration file.

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Entry Point"
        GetSwVerInfo["get_sw_ver_info(show_sw_ver, board_ids)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Configuration"
        GetFlags["get_sw_ver_flags()"]
        ResetConfig["~/.config/tenstorrent/reset_config.json"]
        DisableSerial["disable_serial_report flag"]
        DisableSwVer["disable_sw_version_report flag"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Remote Query"
        GetSwVerURL["get_sw_ver_from_url(board_id)"]
        CerealAPI["cereal.tenstorrent.com<br/>GET ?SerialNumber=..."]
        JSONParse["JSON response parsing"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Return Data"
        DefaultDict["Default N/A dict"]
        VersionDict["Version dictionary<br/>Firmware, tt-smi, tt-flash, etc."]
    end
    
    GetSwVerInfo --> GetFlags
    GetFlags --> ResetConfig
    ResetConfig --> DisableSerial
    ResetConfig --> DisableSwVer
    
    GetSwVerInfo -->|Enabled| GetSwVerURL
    GetSwVerInfo -->|Disabled| DefaultDict
    
    GetSwVerURL --> CerealAPI
    CerealAPI --> JSONParse
    JSONParse --> VersionDict
    
    DisableSwVer -->|True| DefaultDict
    DisableSerial -->|True| GetSwVerURL
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:213-295]()

### Configuration Flags

The system reads two privacy-related flags from `~/.config/tenstorrent/reset_config.json`:

- **`disable_serial_report`**: If true, queries without board serial numbers (empty string)
- **`disable_sw_version_report`**: If true, returns default N/A values without querying

**Configuration File Format:**

```json
{
  "disable_serial_report": false,
  "disable_sw_version_report": false
}
```

**Flag Parsing:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:213-228]()

### Remote API Integration

**Endpoint:** `https://cereal.tenstorrent.com?SerialNumber=<board_id>`

**Query Process:**

1. Construct URL with board serial number (or empty if `disable_serial_report` is true)
2. Issue HTTP GET request via `requests` library
3. Parse JSON response
4. Transform keys to user-facing names (e.g., "Metallium" → "TT-Metalium")
5. Add hardcoded Buda/Metallium versions

**Response Transformation:**

The function [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:242-251]() performs key renaming:

```python
version["TT-Metalium"] = version["Metallium"]
del version["Metallium"]
version["TT-Buda"] = version["Buda"]
del version["Buda"]
```

**Error Handling:**

| Exception Type | User-Facing Message |
|----------------|---------------------|
| `HTTPError` | "We encountered an HTTP error." |
| `ConnectionError` | "There was an error connecting to the server. Please check your internet connection." |
| `Timeout` | "Timeout error. It seems the server is taking too long to respond." |
| `RequestException` | "Something unexpected happened." |
| `JSONDecodeError` | "No response from server" |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:230-267]()

### Default Return Format

When software version reporting is disabled or fails, the function returns:

```python
{
    "Firmware Bundle": "N/A",
    "tt-smi": "N/A",
    "tt-flash": "N/A",
    "tt-kmd": "N/A",
    "TT-Buda": "N/A",
    "TT-Metalium": "N/A",
}
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:276-288]()

---

## TTHostCompatibilityMenu Widget

### Widget Overview

The `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` is a Textual widget that displays host information with visual compatibility indicators. It integrates with the compatibility checking system to provide real-time feedback on system requirements.

**Widget Features:**

- Displays results from `get_host_compatibility_info()`
- Color-codes compatible (green checkmark) vs incompatible (red X) items
- Shows recommended values for incompatible items
- Auto-updates on system changes
- Integrates with Textual's reactive system

**Changelog Reference:**

Version 1.4.12 [CHANGELOG.md:28-31]() introduced `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` to replace separate "Host Info" and "Compatibility" boxes. Version 1.4.13 [CHANGELOG.md:23-26]() removed hugepages counting from the widget due to allocation complexity.

### Display Format

The widget renders compatibility information in a table-like format:

**Compatible Item Display:**
```
✓ OS: Linux (x86_64)
```

**Incompatible Item Display:**
```
✗ Memory: 16.00 GB (Recommended: 32GB+)
```

### Integration Example

Applications using this widget should:

1. Import the widget class from `tt_tools_common.ui_common.widgets`
2. Call `get_host_compatibility_info()` to retrieve data
3. Pass data to widget constructor or update method
4. Mount widget in Textual application layout

**Sources:** [CHANGELOG.md:28-31]()

---

## Usage Patterns

### Collecting Basic Host Information

```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import get_host_info

host_info = get_host_info()
print(f"Running on {host_info['Distro']} with {host_info['Memory']} memory")
print(f"Driver: {host_info['Driver']}")
```

### Checking Compatibility

```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import get_host_compatibility_info

compat_info = get_host_compatibility_info()

for key, value in compat_info.items():
    if isinstance(value, tuple):
        current, recommended = value
        print(f"✗ {key}: {current} (Recommended: {recommended})")
    else:
        print(f"✓ {key}: {value}")
```

### Querying Software Versions

```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import get_sw_ver_info

# Query with board IDs
board_ids = ["12345ABC", "67890DEF"]
versions = get_sw_ver_info(show_sw_ver=True, board_ids=board_ids)

for package, version in versions.items():
    print(f"{package}: {version}")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:145-295]()

## Constants and Configuration

| Constant | Value | Purpose |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:17-18]()

### Configuration File Location

The reset configuration file that controls software version reporting behavior is located at:

```
~/.config/tenstorrent/reset_config.json
```

This file is created by reset logging functions (see [Reset Configuration and Logging](#2.6)) and read by `get_sw_ver_flags()`.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:217-228]()

---

## Relationship to Other Subsystems

### Driver Version Management

Host information collection includes driver version detection via `get_driver_version()`, but driver version comparison and validation is handled by the Driver Version Management subsystem (see [Driver Version Management](#3.1)). The `get_host_info()` function calls `get_driver_version()` but does not perform version validation.

### Reset Configuration

The software version reporting system reads flags from the reset configuration file generated by the reset logging subsystem (see [Reset Configuration and Logging](#2.6)). These flags control privacy-related behavior for board serial number reporting.

### UI Integration

The `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` widget (see [Widget Library Reference](#4.1)) consumes the data produced by `get_host_compatibility_info()` to provide visual compatibility feedback in Textual-based applications like tt-smi.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:1-296]()

# Chip Detection and Communication

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This page documents the chip detection and communication verification system in tt-tools-common. The system discovers Tenstorrent hardware devices on the host, validates that communication channels are functional, and prepares chips for use by performing firmware upgrades when necessary.

This page focuses on the detection and communication aspects. For chip-specific data loading and version conversions, see [Version Conversions and Data Loading](#3.4). For reference clock monitoring performed after detection, see [Reference Clock Monitoring](#3.5).

## Overview

Chip detection is implemented through the `detect_chips_with_callback()` function, which wraps pyluwen's `detect_chips_fallible()` with a rich callback-based progress reporting system. The detection process:

1. Enumerates PCI devices using pyluwen's hardware abstraction layer
2. Validates communication with each discovered device
3. Reports detailed progress through callback functions
4. Automatically upgrades firmware when needed
5. Returns a list of communicable `PciChip` objects

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:255-354]()

## Detection Architecture

The detection system follows a multi-stage pipeline that progressively validates hardware accessibility:

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["detect_chips_with_callback()"] --> Init["Initialize Counters<br/>chip_count=0<br/>arc_count=0<br/>dram_count=0"]
    Init --> PyLuwen["pyluwen.detect_chips_fallible()"]
    
    PyLuwen --> Callback["chip_detect_callback(status)"]
    
    Callback --> NewChip{"status.new_chip()?"}
    NewChip -->|Yes| IncChip["chip_count++"]
    NewChip -->|No| CheckDown{"status.correct_down()?"}
    CheckDown -->|Yes| DecChip["chip_count--"]
    CheckDown -->|No| ParseStatus
    
    IncChip --> ParseStatus["Parse status_string()"]
    DecChip --> ParseStatus
    
    ParseStatus --> ARC{"Contains 'ARC'?"}
    ParseStatus --> DRAM{"Contains 'DRAM'?"}
    ParseStatus --> ETH{"Contains 'ETH'?"}
    
    ARC -->|Yes| ARCSpinner["arc_count++<br/>Display spinner"]
    DRAM -->|Yes| DRAMSpinner["dram_count++<br/>Display spinner"]
    ETH -->|Yes| ETHSpinner["Parse coordinates<br/>Display spinner"]
    
    ARCSpinner --> Print["Print status to terminal"]
    DRAMSpinner --> Print
    ETHSpinner --> Print
    
    Print --> MoreDevices{"More devices?"}
    MoreDevices -->|Yes| PyLuwen
    MoreDevices -->|No| Validate
    
    Validate --> CommCheck["device.have_comms()"]
    CommCheck -->|False| Error["Raise Exception:<br/>No communication"]
    CommCheck -->|True| Upgrade["device.force_upgrade()"]
    
    Upgrade --> Append["Append to output list"]
    Append --> MoreValidate{"More devices?"}
    MoreValidate -->|Yes| Validate
    MoreValidate -->|No| Return["Return List[PciChip]"]
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:255-354]()

### Detection Parameters

The `detect_chips_with_callback()` function accepts three configuration parameters:

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `local_only` | `bool` | `False` | When `True`, only detects chips directly connected via PCIe. When `False`, also discovers remote chips via Ethernet fabric. |
| `ignore_ethernet` | `bool` | `False` | Passed as `noc_safe` to pyluwen. Skips Ethernet core detection for faster operation. |
| `print_status` | `bool` | `True` | Controls whether detection progress is printed to terminal. Set to `False` for silent operation. |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:255-259]()

## Callback Mechanism

The callback system provides real-time feedback during the detection process. The internal `chip_detect_callback` function is invoked repeatedly by pyluwen as detection progresses.

### Callback State Machine

```mermaid
stateDiagram-v2
    [*] --> Idle
    
    Idle --> ChipDetected: status.new_chip()
    ChipDetected --> UpdateCount: chip_count++
    
    Idle --> ChipRemoved: status.correct_down()
    ChipRemoved --> UpdateCount: chip_count--
    
    UpdateCount --> ClearScreen: block_count > 0
    ClearScreen --> PrintHeader: print_status=True
    
    PrintHeader --> ParseStatus: Parse status_string()
    
    ParseStatus --> ARCDetection: Line contains "ARC"
    ParseStatus --> DRAMDetection: Line contains "DRAM"
    ParseStatus --> ETHDetection: Line contains "ETH"
    ParseStatus --> GenericPrint: Other content
    
    ARCDetection --> DisplaySpinner: arc_count++
    DRAMDetection --> DisplaySpinner: dram_count++
    ETHDetection --> DisplaySpinner: Extract coordinates
    
    DisplaySpinner --> Idle
    GenericPrint --> Idle
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:272-338]()

### Terminal Output Control

The callback implements ANSI escape sequences for dynamic terminal updates:

| Escape Sequence | Purpose | Location |
|----------------|---------|----------|
| `\033[{n}A` | Move cursor up `n` lines | [tools_utils.py:283]() |
| `\033[J` | Clear from cursor to end of screen | [tools_utils.py:284]() |
| `\r` | Return cursor to start of line | [tools_utils.py:288,305,312,329,335]() |

The `block_count` variable tracks how many lines were previously printed, enabling the callback to clear old status and redraw updated information without scrolling.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:282-284]()

### Status String Parsing

The callback parses status strings from pyluwen to provide component-specific feedback:

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    StatusString["status_string()"] --> Filter["Filter empty lines"]
    Filter --> CheckARC{"Contains 'ARC'?"}
    Filter --> CheckDRAM{"Contains 'DRAM'?"}
    Filter --> CheckETH{"Contains 'ETH'?"}
    
    CheckARC -->|Yes| ARCOutput["Print: 'Detecting ARC: ⟳'<br/>Color: BLUE/YELLOW"]
    CheckDRAM -->|Yes| DRAMOutput["Print: 'Detecting DRAM: ⟳'<br/>Color: BLUE/YELLOW"]
    CheckETH -->|Yes| ParseCoords["Regex extract:<br/>Parentheses: (coords)<br/>Brackets: [info]"]
    
    ParseCoords --> ETHOutput["Print: '[coords] ETH: ⟳'<br/>Color: PURPLE/BLUE/YELLOW"]
    
    CheckARC -->|No| CheckDRAM
    CheckDRAM -->|No| CheckETH
    CheckETH -->|No| GenericOutput["Print line as-is"]
```

The spinner characters are selected by cycling through `["\\", "|", "/", "-"]` based on detection counters.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:294-337]()

## Communication Verification

After detection completes, each device undergoes communication verification before being added to the output list.

### have_comms() Check

The `device.have_comms()` method (provided by pyluwen) validates that:
- The device responds to PCIe transactions
- ARC firmware is running and responsive
- Basic register reads/writes succeed

If communication cannot be established, the function raises an exception with a diagnostic message:

```python
if not device.have_comms():
    raise Exception(
        f"Do not have communication with {device}, you should reset or "
        f"remove this device from your system before continuing."
    )
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:346-349]()

### Communication Failure Scenarios

| Scenario | Likely Cause | Recommended Action |
|----------|--------------|-------------------|
| PCIe enumeration succeeds but `have_comms()` fails | ARC firmware hang, hardware fault | Perform chip reset (see [ChipReset](#2.2)) |
| Device not enumerated at all | Power issue, PCIe link failure | Check hardware connections |
| Communication intermittent | PCIe signal integrity, thermal throttling | Check host system compatibility (see [Host Information and Compatibility](#3.2)) |

## Firmware Upgrade Process

After communication is verified, the detection system automatically performs firmware upgrades through the `force_upgrade()` method.

### Upgrade Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Detect as detect_chips_with_callback
    participant Device as PciChip device
    participant PyLuwen as pyluwen firmware layer
    participant ARC as ARC Processor
    
    Detect->>Device: have_comms()
    Device->>ARC: Poll status registers
    ARC-->>Device: Communication OK
    Device-->>Detect: True
    
    Detect->>Device: force_upgrade()
    Device->>PyLuwen: Check firmware version
    
    alt Upgrade needed
        PyLuwen->>ARC: Load new firmware image
        ARC->>ARC: Flash and reboot
        PyLuwen->>ARC: Wait for reboot
        ARC-->>PyLuwen: New firmware running
    else No upgrade needed
        PyLuwen-->>Device: Current version OK
    end
    
    Device-->>Detect: Upgraded PciChip
    Detect->>Detect: Append to output list
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:351-352]()

### When Upgrades Occur

Firmware upgrades happen automatically when:
1. The installed firmware version is older than the version bundled with pyluwen
2. The firmware is corrupted or reports an invalid version
3. The firmware is incompatible with the current driver version

The upgrade process is transparent to the caller and ensures all returned `PciChip` objects have compatible firmware.

### Upgrade Timing Considerations

From CHANGELOG.md, version 1.4.8 notes:
> "Updated reset completion logic to handle the case where the bmfw needs to upgrade itself"

This indicates that firmware upgrades can occur during reset operations as well, not just during detection. The system handles these asynchronous upgrades gracefully.

**Sources:** [CHANGELOG.md:48-50]()

## Integration with PyLuwen

The detection system serves as a high-level wrapper around pyluwen's hardware abstraction layer:

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "tt-tools-common (This Module)"
        DetectFunc["detect_chips_with_callback()"]
        CallbackImpl["chip_detect_callback()"]
        StatusProc["Status String Processing"]
        ColorOutput["CMD_LINE_COLOR formatting"]
    end
    
    subgraph "PyLuwen Hardware Layer"
        DetectFallible["detect_chips_fallible()"]
        StatusObj["Detection Status object"]
        PciChip["PciChip class"]
        HaveComms["have_comms() method"]
        ForceUpgrade["force_upgrade() method"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Kernel Interface"
        IOCTLDev["/dev/tenstorrent/"]
        PCIEnum["PCIe enumeration"]
    end
    
    DetectFunc --> DetectFallible
    DetectFallible --> CallbackImpl
    CallbackImpl --> StatusObj
    StatusObj --> StatusProc
    StatusProc --> ColorOutput
    
    DetectFallible --> PciChip
    PciChip --> HaveComms
    HaveComms --> ForceUpgrade
    
    DetectFallible --> PCIEnum
    PCIEnum --> IOCTLDev
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:1-14,255-354]()

### PyLuwen Function Mapping

| tt-tools-common Function | PyLuwen Function | Purpose |
|--------------------------|------------------|---------|
| `detect_chips_with_callback()` | `detect_chips_fallible()` | Main detection entry point |
| Internal callback | `callback` parameter | Status reporting mechanism |
| Parameter: `local_only` | `local_only` parameter | Scope of detection |
| Parameter: `ignore_ethernet` | `noc_safe` parameter | Skip Ethernet validation |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:340-345]()

## Detection Flags and Behavior

The function's behavior varies based on configuration flags:

### Local-Only Mode

When `local_only=True`:
- Only detects chips directly connected to the host via PCIe
- Skips Ethernet fabric traversal
- Faster detection for systems without multi-chip Ethernet connections
- Callback status strings are minimal

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:256,296,341]()

### Ethernet-Ignored Mode

When `ignore_ethernet=True`:
- Detection still occurs for all chips (local and remote)
- Ethernet core validation is skipped via `noc_safe=True`
- Reduces detection time when Ethernet functionality is not required
- Used when only Tensix/DRAM communication is needed

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:257,344]()

### Silent Mode

When `print_status=False`:
- All terminal output is suppressed
- Callback logic still executes for counter tracking
- Useful for scripting and automated tools
- Added in version 1.4.10 (2024-12-16)

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:258,282,286,296](), [CHANGELOG.md:37-40]()

## Error Handling

The detection system implements fail-fast error handling:

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Detect["detect_chips_with_callback()"] --> Loop["For each detected device"]
    Loop --> CommCheck{"device.have_comms()"}
    
    CommCheck -->|False| BuildError["Build exception message:<br/>'Do not have communication with {device}'"]
    BuildError --> Raise["raise Exception()"]
    Raise --> Abort["Function aborts<br/>Partial results discarded"]
    
    CommCheck -->|True| Upgrade["device.force_upgrade()"]
    Upgrade --> Append["Append to output list"]
    Append --> NextDevice{"More devices?"}
    
    NextDevice -->|Yes| Loop
    NextDevice -->|No| Return["Return complete list"]
```

The system uses `continue_on_failure=False` when calling `detect_chips_fallible()`, meaning detection stops at the first non-communicable device rather than attempting to continue.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:340-349]()

## Return Value and Usage

The function returns `List[PciChip]`, where each `PciChip` object:
- Has verified communication (`have_comms()` returned `True`)
- Has up-to-date firmware (`force_upgrade()` completed)
- Is ready for immediate use in reset operations, telemetry queries, etc.

### Typical Usage Pattern

```python
# Example usage from consumer tools
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import detect_chips_with_callback

# Detect all chips with full feedback
chips = detect_chips_with_callback(
    local_only=False,
    ignore_ethernet=False,
    print_status=True
)

# chips is now a list of communicable PciChip objects
for chip in chips:
    # Perform operations on each chip
    pass
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:255-354]()

## Color Formatting Constants

The detection callback uses color constants from `tt_tools_common.ui_common.themes`:

| Constant | Usage | Line |
|----------|-------|------|
| `CMD_LINE_COLOR.PURPLE` | Chip count header, Ethernet coordinates | [288,329]() |
| `CMD_LINE_COLOR.YELLOW` | Numeric values, spinner characters | [288,306,313,330]() |
| `CMD_LINE_COLOR.BLUE` | Status labels ("Detecting ARC:", etc.) | [305,312,329]() |
| `CMD_LINE_COLOR.ENDC` | Reset color to terminal default | [288,306,313,330]() |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:14,288-330]()

## Summary

The chip detection and communication system provides a robust, user-friendly interface for discovering and validating Tenstorrent hardware. Key features include:

- **Progressive feedback** through callback-based status updates
- **Automatic firmware management** via force_upgrade()
- **Flexible detection modes** for different use cases
- **Fail-fast validation** ensuring all returned chips are communicable
- **Integration with pyluwen** for hardware abstraction

Consumer tools like tt-smi and tt-flash rely on this system as their primary hardware discovery mechanism, typically calling `detect_chips_with_callback()` during initialization to build their device inventory.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:1-354](), [CHANGELOG.md:1-143]()
