# Version Conversions and Data Loading

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [CHANGELOG.md](CHANGELOG.md)
- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This page documents the utility functions for converting firmware version formats, identifying board types from hardware identifiers, and loading chip-specific data files. These utilities support runtime version parsing, hardware identification, and configuration loading throughout the tt-tools-common library.

For driver version checking and semantic version parsing with extraversion fields, see [Driver Version Management](#3.1). For chip detection and hardware communication, see [Chip Detection and Communication](#3.3).

## Version Conversion Architecture

The version conversion system handles multiple firmware types, each with distinct hexadecimal encoding schemes. All conversion functions follow a consistent pattern: they accept a hexadecimal integer and return a semantic version string, handling invalid values (0x0 or 0xFFFFFFFF) appropriately.

### Version Conversion Flow

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Input Sources"
        Telemetry["Chip Telemetry<br/>(hex values)"]
        ARCMsg["ARC Messages<br/>(hex responses)"]
        FWHeader["Firmware Headers<br/>(hex metadata)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Conversion Functions"
        HexToSemver["hex_to_semver()<br/>Standard: 0x0A0F0100 → 10.15.1"]
        HexToSemverEth["hex_to_semver_eth()<br/>Ethernet: 0x061000 → 6.1.0"]
        HexToSemverM3["hex_to_semver_m3_fw()<br/>M3: 0x0A0F0100 → 10.15.1.0"]
        HexToSemverZephyr["hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw()<br/>Zephyr: 0x0A0F0101 → 10.15.1-rc1"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Output Format"
        SemVer["Semantic Version Strings<br/>MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH[.VER][-rcN]"]
        NA["Error Cases<br/>'N/A'"]
    end
    
    Telemetry --> HexToSemver
    ARCMsg --> HexToSemverEth
    FWHeader --> HexToSemverM3
    FWHeader --> HexToSemverZephyr
    
    HexToSemver --> SemVer
    HexToSemverEth --> SemVer
    HexToSemverEth --> NA
    HexToSemverM3 --> SemVer
    HexToSemverM3 --> NA
    HexToSemverZephyr --> SemVer
    HexToSemverZephyr --> NA
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:136-190]()

### Standard Semantic Version Conversion

The `hex_to_semver()` function converts standard firmware versions encoded in 32-bit hexadecimal format. The encoding uses the lower 24 bits for version components.

**Bit Layout:**
| Bits | Field | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| 31-24 | Reserved | Unused (0x00) |
| 23-16 | Major | Major version number |
| 15-8 | Minor | Minor version number |
| 7-0 | Patch | Patch version number |

**Example:**
- Input: `0x0A0F0100` (hex)
- Extraction: Major=10, Minor=15, Patch=1
- Output: `"10.15.1"`

The function raises `ValueError` for invalid inputs (0x0 or 0xFFFFFFFF) rather than returning "N/A", as these represent uninitialized or corrupted firmware metadata.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:136-145]()

### Ethernet Firmware Version Conversion

The `hex_to_semver_eth()` function handles ethernet firmware versions with a non-standard bit layout that allocates more bits to the patch version field.

**Bit Layout:**
| Bits | Field | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| 23-16 | Major | Major version number |
| 15-12 | Minor | Minor version number (4 bits) |
| 11-0 | Patch | Patch version number (12 bits) |

**Example:**
- Input: `0x061000` (hex)
- Extraction: Major=6, Minor=1, Patch=0
- Output: `"6.1.0"`

Invalid values return `"N/A"` instead of raising exceptions, allowing graceful handling of ethernet firmware absence.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:148-157]()

### M3 Firmware Version Conversion

The `hex_to_semver_m3_fw()` function converts M3 firmware versions which include a fourth version component, producing a four-part semantic version string.

**Bit Layout:**
| Bits | Field | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| 31-24 | Major | Major version number |
| 23-16 | Minor | Minor version number |
| 15-8 | Patch | Patch version number |
| 7-0 | Ver | Additional version component |

**Example:**
- Input: `0x0A0F0100` (hex)
- Extraction: Major=10, Minor=15, Patch=1, Ver=0
- Output: `"10.15.1.0"`

The four-component format distinguishes M3 firmware from standard ARC firmware versions.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:160-170]()

### Zephyr Firmware Version Conversion

The `hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw()` function converts Zephyr RTOS firmware versions, which support release candidate suffixes for pre-release builds.

**Bit Layout and RC Handling:**
| Bits | Field | Purpose |
|------|-------|---------|
| 31-24 | Major | Major version number |
| 23-16 | Minor | Minor version number |
| 15-8 | Patch | Patch version number |
| 7-0 | RC | Release candidate number (0=final) |

**RC Encoding:**
- `rc_num = 0`: Final release (no suffix)
- `rc_num > 0`: Release candidate with `-rcN` suffix

**Examples:**
- Input: `0x0A0F0100` → Output: `"10.15.1"` (final release)
- Input: `0x0A0F0101` → Output: `"10.15.1-rc1"` (release candidate 1)
- Input: `0x0A0F0105` → Output: `"10.15.1-rc5"` (release candidate 5)

This format enables pre-release testing while maintaining semantic version compatibility.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:172-189]()

## Date and Time Conversion

The `hex_to_date()` function converts firmware build timestamps from a compact hexadecimal format to human-readable date strings.

**Encoding Format (0xYMDDHHMM):**
| Bits | Field | Range | Purpose |
|------|-------|-------|---------|
| 31-28 | Year offset | 0-15 | Years since 2020 (0x0=2020, 0xF=2035) |
| 27-24 | Month | 1-12 | Calendar month |
| 23-16 | Day | 1-31 | Day of month |
| 15-8 | Hour | 0-23 | Hour in 24h format |
| 7-0 | Minute | 0-59 | Minute |

**Example Conversion:**
- Input: `0x51A0830` (hex)
- Decoding: Year=2025 (5+2020), Month=1, Day=10, Hour=8, Minute=48
- Output: `"2025-01-10 08:48"`

The `include_time` parameter controls whether the time portion is appended. Invalid dates (0x0 or 0xFFFFFFFF) return `"N/A"`.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:93-109]()

## Board Type Identification System

The board type identification system decodes hardware serial numbers to determine board models. Board IDs are 56-bit values encoded as hexadecimal strings.

### Board ID Structure

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Board ID Format: AA-BBBBB-C-D-EE-FF-XXX"
        SerialNum["56-bit Serial Number<br/>Hex String"]
        
        AA["AA<br/>Reserved<br/>Bits 55-48"]
        UPI["BBBBB<br/>Unique Part ID<br/>Bits 47-32<br/>(20 bits)"]
        Rev["C<br/>Revision<br/>Bits 35-32<br/>(4 bits)"]
        D["D<br/>Reserved<br/>Bits 31-28"]
        EE["EE<br/>Reserved<br/>Bits 27-20"]
        FF["FF<br/>Reserved<br/>Bits 19-12"]
        XXX["XXX<br/>Reserved<br/>Bits 11-0"]
    end
    
    SerialNum --> AA
    SerialNum --> UPI
    SerialNum --> Rev
    SerialNum --> D
    SerialNum --> EE
    SerialNum --> FF
    SerialNum --> XXX
    
    UPI --> BoardType["get_board_type()<br/>Maps UPI → Board Name"]
    Rev --> BoardType
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:46-90]()

### UPI to Board Type Mapping

The `get_board_type()` function extracts the Unique Part Identifier (UPI) and revision fields from the board ID, then maps them to specific board types.

**Extraction Logic:**
```python
serial_num = int(f"0x{board_id}", base=16)
upi = (serial_num >> 36) & 0xFFFFF  # Bits 47-32
rev = (serial_num >> 32) & 0xF       # Bits 35-32
```

**UPI Mapping Table:**

| UPI (hex) | Revision | Board Type | Notes |
|-----------|----------|------------|-------|
| 0x1 | 0x2 | E300_R2 | Early E300 revision 2 |
| 0x1 | 0x3, 0x4 | E300_R3 | E300 revision 3/4 |
| 0x3 | Any | e150 | Formerly E300_105 |
| 0x7 | Any | e75 | Entry-level board |
| 0x8 | Any | NEBULA_CB | Nebula carrier board |
| 0xA | Any | e300 | Formerly E300_X2 |
| 0xB | Any | GALAXY | Multi-chip galaxy system |
| 0x14 | Any | n300 | Formerly NEBULA_X2 |
| 0x18 | Any | n150 | Formerly NEBULA_X1 |
| Other | Any | N/A | Unknown/invalid UPI |

The function returns `"N/A"` for unrecognized UPI values or invalid revision combinations (e.g., UPI 0x1 with revision outside 0x2-0x4).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:46-90]()

## Chip Data File Loading

The chip data loading system provides access to chip-specific configuration files, firmware definitions, and other static data assets.

### Data File Organization

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Package Structure"
        ToolsCommon["tt_tools_common/"]
        DataDir["data/"]
        WormholeDir["wormhole/"]
        GrayskullDir["grayskull/"]
        IgnoredDir[".ignored/"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Data Files"
        FWDefines["fw_defines.yaml<br/>ARC message definitions"]
        ConfigFiles["*.yaml<br/>Chip configurations"]
        InternalData["Internal/proprietary data"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Access Functions"
        GetChipData["get_chip_data()<br/>Generic file loader"]
        InitFWDefines["init_fw_defines()<br/>Loads fw_defines.yaml"]
    end
    
    ToolsCommon --> DataDir
    DataDir --> WormholeDir
    DataDir --> GrayskullDir
    ToolsCommon --> IgnoredDir
    
    WormholeDir --> FWDefines
    GrayskullDir --> FWDefines
    WormholeDir --> ConfigFiles
    GrayskullDir --> ConfigFiles
    IgnoredDir --> InternalData
    
    GetChipData --> WormholeDir
    GetChipData --> GrayskullDir
    GetChipData --> IgnoredDir
    InitFWDefines --> GetChipData
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:17-43]()

### Loading Firmware Definitions

The `init_fw_defines()` function loads chip-specific firmware message definitions from YAML files. These definitions include ARC message types, register addresses, and protocol specifications.

**Function Signature:**
```python
def init_fw_defines(chip_name: str = "wormhole", tool_name: str = "tt_smi"):
```

**Parameters:**
- `chip_name`: Chip architecture (`"wormhole"` or `"grayskull"`)
- `tool_name`: Package name for path resolution (default: `"tt_smi"`)

**Usage Pattern:**
1. Resolves package path using `importlib.resources`
2. Constructs path: `data/{chip_name}/fw_defines.yaml`
3. Loads YAML with `safe_load()`
4. Returns dictionary with firmware definitions

**Example:**
```python
fw_defines = init_fw_defines(chip_name="wormhole", tool_name="tt_smi")
# Returns: {'MSG_TYPE_RESET': 0x10, 'MSG_TYPE_...': ...}
```

The returned dictionary is typically used for ARC message protocol encoding/decoding.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:17-24]()

### Generic Data File Access

The `get_chip_data()` function provides generic access to any file in the chip data directories, supporting both public and internal data locations.

**Function Signature:**
```python
def get_chip_data(chip_name, file, internal: bool, tool_name="tt_smi"):
```

**Parameters:**
- `chip_name`: Chip architecture (`"wormhole"` or `"grayskull"`)
- `file`: Filename within the chip directory
- `internal`: If `True`, loads from `.ignored/` directory
- `tool_name`: Package name for path resolution

**Path Resolution Logic:**

| Condition | Path Template |
|-----------|---------------|
| `internal=True` | `.ignored/{chip_name}/{file}` |
| `internal=False` | `data/{chip_name}/{file}` |
| Tool name contains `.data` | `{chip_name}/{file}` (special case) |

**Example Usage:**
```python
# Load public configuration
config = get_chip_data("wormhole", "reset_config.yaml", False)

# Load internal/proprietary data
internal_data = get_chip_data("wormhole", "proprietary.yaml", True)
```

The function returns a file handle opened in read mode, raising an `Exception` if the chip name is not supported (only Wormhole and Grayskull are valid).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:31-43]()

## Utility Functions Reference

### Reverse Conversion Functions

Two utility functions support conversion from semantic version strings back to hexadecimal format:

**`semver_to_hex(semver: str)`**
- Converts semantic version string to hexadecimal
- Input: `"10.15.1"` → Output: `"0a0f0100"`
- Used for firmware upgrade validation and version comparison

**`date_to_hex(date: int)`**
- Converts date string to hexadecimal timestamp
- Input: `"202501100848"` (YYYYMMDDHHMM) → Output: `"051a0830"`
- Used for firmware build date encoding

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:118-133]()

### Integration with Other Systems

Version conversion functions are primarily consumed by:
- **Chip telemetry parsing**: Converting raw hardware registers to human-readable versions
- **Firmware upgrade validation**: Comparing current vs. target firmware versions
- **Reset logging**: Recording firmware versions in `HostResetLog` structures (see [Reset Configuration and Logging](#2.6))
- **Compatibility checking**: Validating firmware version requirements

Board type identification is used by:
- **Hardware detection**: Identifying board models during `detect_chips_with_callback()` (see [Chip Detection and Communication](#3.3))
- **Configuration selection**: Loading board-specific reset configurations
- **Compatibility validation**: Ensuring operations are supported on detected hardware

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:1-355]()

# Reference Clock Monitoring

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

The reference clock monitoring system provides functionality to read and validate the hardware reference clock counter on Tenstorrent chips. This system verifies that the `REFCLK_COUNTER` register pair is incrementing at the expected frequency, independent of the ARC clock (`ARCLK`). The monitoring system is primarily used during chip initialization and reset validation to ensure proper hardware operation.

For information about chip reset procedures that may use these validation functions, see [Hardware Reset System](#2). For general chip detection and communication verification, see [Chip Detection and Communication](#3.3).

## System Architecture

The reference clock monitoring system consists of four primary functions that work together to read, measure, and validate the hardware clock counter:

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Reference Clock Monitoring API"
        ReadCounter["read_refclk_counter(chip)"]
        CalcRate["refclk_counter_rate(chip, delay_interval)"]
        CheckSpeed["check_refclk_counter_read_speed(chip)"]
        CheckRate["check_refclk_counter_rate(chip, expected_refclk, accuracy)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Hardware Registers"
        HighReg["ARC_RESET.REFCLK_COUNTER_HIGH<br/>(upper 32 bits)"]
        LowReg["ARC_RESET.REFCLK_COUNTER_LOW<br/>(lower 32 bits)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "PciChip Interface"
        AXITranslate["chip.axi_translate()"]
        AXIRead["chip.axi_read32()"]
    end
    
    ReadCounter --> AXITranslate
    ReadCounter --> AXIRead
    AXIRead --> HighReg
    AXIRead --> LowReg
    
    CalcRate --> ReadCounter
    CheckSpeed --> ReadCounter
    CheckRate --> CalcRate
    
    style ReadCounter fill:#f9f9f9
    style CalcRate fill:#f9f9f9
    style CheckSpeed fill:#f9f9f9
    style CheckRate fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:198-252]()

## Reference Clock Counter Registers

The reference clock counter is maintained in hardware as a 64-bit value split across two 32-bit registers:

| Register | Address | Bits | Description |
|----------|---------|------|-------------|
| `ARC_RESET.REFCLK_COUNTER_HIGH` | AXI-translated | [63:32] | Upper 32 bits of counter |
| `ARC_RESET.REFCLK_COUNTER_LOW` | AXI-translated | [31:0] | Lower 32 bits of counter |

The counter increments continuously at the reference clock frequency, providing a stable timing reference independent of the ARC processor clock. This separation allows validation of clock behavior without dependency on ARC firmware operation.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:205-206]()

## Counter Reading Mechanism

### `read_refclk_counter(chip)` Function

The counter read operation must handle potential rollover of the lower 32-bit register during the read sequence. The implementation uses a double-read strategy:

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["read_refclk_counter(chip)"] --> CheckGS{"chip.as_gs() ?"}
    CheckGS -->|"Yes"| ReturnNone["return None"]
    CheckGS -->|"No"| Translate["Translate register addresses<br/>via axi_translate()"]
    
    Translate --> Read1["high1 = axi_read32(high_addr)"]
    Read1 --> Read2["low = axi_read32(low_addr)"]
    Read2 --> Read3["high2 = axi_read32(high_addr)"]
    
    Read3 --> Compare{"high1 != high2 ?"}
    Compare -->|"Yes (rollover)"| RereadLow["low = axi_read32(low_addr)"]
    Compare -->|"No"| Combine
    RereadLow --> Combine["Combine: (high2 << 32) | low"]
    
    Combine --> Return["return 64-bit counter"]
    
    style Start fill:#f9f9f9
    style CheckGS fill:#f9f9f9
    style Compare fill:#f9f9f9
```

The algorithm prevents race conditions when the low register rolls over to zero during the read sequence:

1. Read high register (first sample)
2. Read low register
3. Read high register again (second sample)
4. If high values differ, a rollover occurred during the read; re-read the low register
5. Combine `high2` and `low` into a 64-bit value

**Chip Compatibility:** This function returns `None` for Grayskull chips, as they do not implement the `REFCLK_COUNTER` registers.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:202-214]()

## Rate Calculation

### `refclk_counter_rate(chip, delay_interval)` Function

The reference clock frequency is measured by sampling the counter twice with a known time delay:

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `chip` | `PciChip` | - | Target chip instance |
| `delay_interval` | `float` | `0.1` | Delay between samples in seconds |
| **Returns** | `float` | - | Measured frequency in MHz |

**Algorithm:**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Caller
    participant Function as refclk_counter_rate
    participant Counter as read_refclk_counter
    participant Time as time module
    
    Caller->>Function: call with chip, delay_interval
    Function->>Counter: read initial counter value
    Counter-->>Function: before_refclk
    Function->>Time: time.time_ns()
    Time-->>Function: before_ns
    
    Function->>Function: sleep(delay_interval)
    
    Function->>Counter: read final counter value
    Counter-->>Function: after_refclk
    Function->>Time: time.time_ns()
    Time-->>Function: after_ns
    
    Function->>Function: Calculate rate:<br/>(after_refclk - before_refclk) * 1000 / (after_ns - before_ns)
    Function-->>Caller: return rate in MHz
```

**Formula:**

```
Rate (MHz) = (ΔCounter × 1000) / ΔTime(ns)
```

Where:
- `ΔCounter` = `after_refclk - before_refclk` (counter ticks)
- `ΔTime(ns)` = `after_ns - before_ns` (nanoseconds elapsed)
- Factor of 1000 converts from GHz (counter ticks per ns) to MHz

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:218-227]()

## Validation Operations

The monitoring system provides two validation functions to detect hardware issues.

### Read Speed Validation

#### `check_refclk_counter_read_speed(chip)` Function

This function verifies that counter read operations complete within expected time bounds. Slow reads may indicate PCIe bus issues, driver problems, or hardware faults.

**Operation:**

1. Performs 100 consecutive counter reads
2. Measures total elapsed time
3. Calculates average time per read
4. Prints warning if reads exceed 100 microseconds each

```mermaid
graph LR
    Start["check_refclk_counter_read_speed(chip)"] --> Loop["Loop 100 times"]
    Loop --> Read["read_refclk_counter(chip)"]
    Read --> Loop
    Loop --> Calculate["Calculate average time per read"]
    Calculate --> Check{"Average > 100μs?"}
    Check -->|"Yes"| Warn["Print warning with actual time"]
    Check -->|"No"| Return["Return silently"]
    
    style Start fill:#f9f9f9
    style Check fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Expected Performance:** Each read should complete in under 100 microseconds. Exceeding this threshold suggests potential issues with:
- PCIe communication latency
- AXI bus contention
- Driver overhead
- Hardware access bottlenecks

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:230-240]()

### Rate Accuracy Validation

#### `check_refclk_counter_rate(chip, expected_refclk, accuracy)` Function

This function validates that the measured clock rate matches the expected hardware specification within a tolerance threshold.

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `chip` | `PciChip` | Target chip instance |
| `expected_refclk` | `float` | Expected reference clock frequency in MHz |
| `accuracy` | `float` | Acceptable deviation percentage (e.g., `5.0` for ±5%) |
| **Returns** | `str` or `None` | Error message if out of range, `None` if valid |

**Validation Logic:**

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["check_refclk_counter_rate(chip, expected_refclk, accuracy)"] --> Measure["observed_refclk = refclk_counter_rate(chip)"]
    
    Measure --> CalcDeviation["Calculate deviation:<br/>abs(expected - observed) / min(expected, observed)"]
    
    CalcDeviation --> CheckThreshold{"deviation > (accuracy / 100) ?"}
    
    CheckThreshold -->|"Yes (out of range)"| ReturnError["return error string with observed value"]
    CheckThreshold -->|"No (within range)"| ReturnNone["return None"]
    
    style Start fill:#f9f9f9
    style CheckThreshold fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Deviation Formula:**

```
deviation = |expected - observed| / min(expected, observed)
```

The minimum value is used in the denominator to ensure symmetric tolerance bounds regardless of whether the measured value is higher or lower than expected.

**Example:**
- Expected: 100 MHz
- Accuracy: 5.0 (±5%)
- Measured: 94 MHz
- Deviation: |100 - 94| / 94 = 6.38%
- Result: "REFCLK_COUNTER outside of allowed range: 94"

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:243-252]()

## Chip Compatibility and Limitations

### Supported Architectures

| Chip Type | REFCLK_COUNTER Support | Notes |
|-----------|------------------------|-------|
| Blackhole | ✓ Yes | Full support via `ARC_RESET` registers |
| Wormhole | ✓ Yes | Full support via `ARC_RESET` registers |
| Grayskull | ✗ No | `read_refclk_counter()` returns `None` |

The `read_refclk_counter()` function explicitly checks for Grayskull architecture and returns `None` if detected:

```python
if chip.as_gs():
    return None
```

This check prevents attempting to access non-existent registers on Grayskull hardware.

### AXI Translation Requirement

All register accesses use the `chip.axi_translate()` method to convert symbolic register names to physical addresses. This abstraction layer handles chip-specific address mapping and ensures portability across different hardware revisions.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:203-206]()

## Integration with Reset and Validation Workflows

The reference clock monitoring functions are typically invoked during chip initialization and reset validation sequences. While these functions are defined in `tools_utils.py`, they are used by higher-level reset implementations to verify hardware state after reset operations.

**Common usage patterns:**

1. **Post-reset validation:** After executing a chip reset, call `check_refclk_counter_rate()` to verify the reference clock resumed operation at the expected frequency.

2. **Hardware diagnosis:** Use `check_refclk_counter_read_speed()` to detect PCIe communication issues before attempting complex operations.

3. **Clock stability monitoring:** Periodically sample `refclk_counter_rate()` during long-running operations to detect clock drift or instability.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:198-252]()

# User Interface Components

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py](tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py)
- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css](tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css)
- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py](tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py)

</details>



This document covers the reusable UI component library provided by tt-tools-common for building Terminal User Interface (TUI) applications. The library provides custom Textual widgets, modal screens, and a unified CSS theme system that can be integrated into any Tenstorrent command-line tool requiring interactive interfaces.

For detailed API documentation of individual widgets and their methods, see [UI Components API Reference](#7.3). For guidance on building applications using these components, see [Building Custom TUI Applications](#4.4).

## Overview

The UI component library is built on top of the [Textual](https://textual.textualize.io/) framework and provides standardized widgets that implement the Tenstorrent visual design language. All components share a common styling system defined in CSS, enabling consistent appearance across different tools.

The UI system is organized into three primary layers:

| Layer | Purpose | Location |
|-------|---------|----------|
| Widget Classes | Reusable components with built-in behavior | `tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py` |
| CSS Theme | Visual styling and layout rules | `tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css` |
| Integration Examples | Reference implementations | `tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py` |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-365](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:1-226]()

## Component Architecture

The following diagram illustrates the dependency relationships between UI components and the external Textual framework:

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Application Layer"
        TTApp["Consumer Applications<br/>(tt-smi, tt-flash, etc.)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "tt_tools_common.ui_common"
        subgraph "Layout Widgets"
            TTHeader["TTHeader<br/>lines 22-45"]
            TTFooter["TTFooter<br/>lines 48-62"]
            TTDataTable["TTDataTable<br/>lines 65-117"]
        end
        
        subgraph "Display Widgets"
            TTMenu["TTMenu<br/>lines 120-146"]
            TTHostCompatibilityMenu["TTHostCompatibilityMenu<br/>lines 149-210"]
            TTCompatibilityMenu["TTCompatibilityMenu<br/>lines 213-243"]
        end
        
        subgraph "Modal Screens"
            TTConfirmBox["TTConfirmBox<br/>lines 246-271"]
            TTHelperMenuBox["TTHelperMenuBox<br/>lines 274-305"]
            TTSettingsMenu["TTSettingsMenu<br/>lines 308-364"]
        end
        
        CommonCSS["common_style.css<br/>Theme Definitions"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Textual Framework"
        Widget["textual.widget.Widget"]
        Container["textual.containers.Container"]
        ModalScreen["textual.screen.ModalScreen"]
        DataTable["textual.widgets.DataTable"]
        Button["textual.widgets.Button"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Rich Library"
        Panel["rich.panel.Panel"]
        Table["rich.table.Table"]
        Text["rich.text.Text"]
    end
    
    TTApp --> TTHeader
    TTApp --> TTFooter
    TTApp --> TTDataTable
    TTApp --> TTMenu
    TTApp --> TTConfirmBox
    TTApp --> CommonCSS
    
    TTHeader --> Widget
    TTHeader --> Panel
    TTHeader --> Table
    
    TTFooter --> Widget
    TTFooter --> Panel
    TTFooter --> Table
    
    TTDataTable --> Container
    TTDataTable --> DataTable
    
    TTMenu --> Container
    TTMenu --> Text
    TTHostCompatibilityMenu --> Container
    TTHostCompatibilityMenu --> Text
    TTCompatibilityMenu --> Container
    TTCompatibilityMenu --> Text
    
    TTConfirmBox --> ModalScreen
    TTConfirmBox --> Button
    TTHelperMenuBox --> ModalScreen
    TTSettingsMenu --> ModalScreen
    TTSettingsMenu --> Button
    
    CommonCSS -.styles.-> TTHeader
    CommonCSS -.styles.-> TTFooter
    CommonCSS -.styles.-> DataTable
    CommonCSS -.styles.-> TTMenu
    CommonCSS -.styles.-> TTConfirmBox
```

**Widget Inheritance Hierarchy:**

- **Widget-based components** (`TTHeader`, `TTFooter`): Inherit directly from `textual.widget.Widget` and implement custom rendering using Rich library primitives
- **Container-based components** (`TTMenu`, `TTCompatibilityMenu`, `TTHostCompatibilityMenu`, `TTDataTable`): Inherit from Textual container types to compose child widgets
- **Modal screens** (`TTConfirmBox`, `TTHelperMenuBox`, `TTSettingsMenu`): Inherit from `textual.screen.ModalScreen` for overlay dialogs

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-19](), [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:8-19]()

## Component Categories

### Layout Components

Layout components provide structural elements that frame the application interface:

| Component | Purpose | Key Features |
|-----------|---------|--------------|
| `TTHeader` | Top application header | Auto-updating timestamp, app name/version display |
| `TTFooter` | Bottom application footer | Configurable content, flexible justification |
| `TTDataTable` | Scrollable data grid | Wrapped DataTable with styled headers, cell update methods |

**TTHeader** ([widgets.py:22-45]()) renders a three-column panel displaying version information (left), application name (center), and a live timestamp (right). The timestamp updates every second via `set_interval`.

**TTFooter** ([widgets.py:48-62]()) accepts a list of content strings and arranges them in columns with configurable justification.

**TTDataTable** ([widgets.py:65-117]()) wraps the Textual `DataTable` widget in a `ScrollableContainer` and provides:
- Pre-styled headers with centering and underlines
- `update_data()` method for refreshing cell contents without full re-render
- Automatic row expansion when new data exceeds current row count

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:22-117]()

### Display Components

Display components present read-only information in formatted layouts:

| Component | Purpose | Use Case |
|-----------|---------|----------|
| `TTMenu` | Key-value list display | General information panels |
| `TTCompatibilityMenu` | Status list with pass/fail indicators | Feature compatibility checking |
| `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` | Status list with warning notes | Host configuration validation |

All menu components accept an `OrderedDict` or `Dict` to preserve display order. They automatically calculate column widths based on the longest key.

**TTMenu** ([widgets.py:120-146]()) renders each key-value pair with `*` bullet points, yellow bolded keys, and standard text values. Special handling exists for `"Failed to fetch"` keys, which render values in dark orange.

**TTCompatibilityMenu** ([widgets.py:213-243]()) expects values as `(bool, str)` tuples. When the boolean is `False`, the string value renders in dark orange to indicate a warning.

**TTHostCompatibilityMenu** ([widgets.py:149-210]()) accepts values as either strings (fully compatible) or `(str, str)` tuples (current value, recommended value). The border title changes to "Config Warning!" when any tuple values exist, and recommendations display in dark orange with indentation.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:120-243]()

### Modal Screens

Modal screens provide overlay interfaces for user interactions:

| Component | Purpose | Interaction Pattern |
|-----------|---------|---------------------|
| `TTConfirmBox` | Yes/No confirmation dialog | Button callbacks for yes/no actions |
| `TTHelperMenuBox` | Help text display | Markdown content with keyboard dismissal |
| `TTSettingsMenu` | Application settings panel | Switch widgets for boolean options |

**TTConfirmBox** ([widgets.py:246-271]()) displays a question label with Yes/No buttons in a grid layout. It accepts optional `on_yes` and `on_no` callback functions that execute before the screen automatically pops.

**TTHelperMenuBox** ([widgets.py:274-305]()) renders Markdown content in a modal with built-in bindings for `q`, `escape`, and `h` to dismiss the screen.

**TTSettingsMenu** ([widgets.py:308-364]()) provides a settings interface specifically designed for tt-smi, with switches for dark mode and software version checking. It demonstrates the `@on(Switch.Changed)` decorator pattern for handling switch events.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-364]()

## Theming System

The theming system uses CSS to define colors, layouts, and visual styles across all components. The stylesheet is located at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css]().

### Color Palette

The following color variables are defined for consistent branding:

| Variable | Color Value | Usage |
|----------|-------------|-------|
| `$red` | #f04f5e | Error states, attention elements |
| `$green` | #1eb57d | Borders, success states, primary text |
| `$yellow` | #ffd10a | Highlights, key text, cursor |
| `$purple` | #786bb0 | Secondary accents |
| `$orange` | darkorange | Warnings, failed states |
| `$gray` | ansi_bright_black | Disabled elements |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:6-12]()

### Global Styles

Global rules ([common_style.css:14-26]()) apply to all components:
- Default text color: `$yellow`
- Scrollbar colors: `$yellow` foreground, `$green` background
- Border titles: left-aligned, yellow, bold

### Widget-Specific Styles

The stylesheet defines specific rules for each component type:

**Header and Footer** ([common_style.css:28-43]()): Fixed height of 3 lines, bold text, green outline, docked to top/bottom respectively.

**DataTable** ([common_style.css:45-85]()): Green borders and text, centered alignment, yellow cursor with black text, transparent header background, yellow hover states at 60% opacity.

**Menu Widgets** ([common_style.css:87-101]()): 1-unit padding, green borders and text. All three menu variants (`TTMenu`, `TTCompatibilityMenu`, `TTHostCompatibilityMenu`) share these base styles.

**Modal Screens** ([common_style.css:103-187]()): Centered alignment, specific sizing for dialogs, green borders on surface background. Buttons use yellow background with white text, changing to red on hover/focus.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:14-226]()

## Component Integration Flow

The following diagram shows how applications integrate UI components at runtime:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant App as "Textual App"
    participant CSS as "common_style.css"
    participant Widget as "Custom Widget"
    participant Textual as "Textual Framework"
    participant Rich as "Rich Library"
    
    App->>App: Define CSS_PATH
    App->>CSS: Load stylesheet
    CSS->>Textual: Register styles
    
    App->>Widget: compose() yields widgets
    Widget->>Textual: Inherit base classes
    Widget->>Widget: __init__() with parameters
    
    App->>Widget: on_mount() event
    Widget->>Widget: Initialize state
    Widget->>Widget: set_interval() for updates
    
    loop Render Cycle
        Textual->>Widget: render() method call
        Widget->>Rich: Create Panel/Table/Text
        Rich-->>Widget: Styled output
        Widget-->>Textual: RenderResult
        Textual->>CSS: Apply styles
        CSS-->>Textual: Styled widget
        Textual-->>App: Display to terminal
    end
    
    App->>Widget: User interaction event
    Widget->>Widget: Event handler
    Widget->>Widget: Update internal state
    Widget->>Widget: refresh() or update_data()
```

**Key Integration Points:**

1. **CSS Loading**: Applications define `CSS_PATH` as a class attribute pointing to `common_style.css`
2. **Widget Composition**: The `compose()` method yields widget instances configured with application-specific parameters
3. **Event Handlers**: Widgets define methods like `on_mount()` to handle lifecycle events
4. **Rendering**: Each widget implements `render()` returning Rich objects or `compose()` yielding child widgets
5. **State Updates**: Widgets expose methods like `update_data()` for programmatic content updates

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:26-88](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:30-31]()

## Example Application Structure

The test widget app demonstrates proper component integration:

```mermaid
graph TD
    TTApp["TTApp<br/>test_widget_app.py:26-88"]
    
    subgraph "compose() Layout"
        Header["TTHeader<br/>app_name + version"]
        HContainer["Horizontal Container"]
        Footer["Footer<br/>Textual Footer"]
        
        subgraph "Horizontal Layout"
            VContainer["Vertical Container"]
            DataTable["TTDataTable<br/>id='dt_example'"]
            Menu3["TTMenu<br/>id='menu_3'"]
            
            subgraph "Vertical Layout"
                Menu1["TTMenu<br/>id='menu_1'"]
                Menu2["TTMenu<br/>id='menu_2'"]
            end
        end
    end
    
    TTApp --> Header
    TTApp --> HContainer
    TTApp --> Footer
    
    HContainer --> VContainer
    HContainer --> DataTable
    HContainer --> Menu3
    
    VContainer --> Menu1
    VContainer --> Menu2
```

**Application Structure** ([test_widget_app.py:26-88]()):

1. **Class Definition**: `TTApp` inherits from `textual.app.App` with `CSS_PATH` pointing to common_style.css
2. **Initialization**: Constructor accepts `app_name`, `app_version`, and optional `key_bindings`
3. **Composition**: `compose()` method arranges widgets in a layout hierarchy using Horizontal/Vertical containers
4. **Mounting**: `on_mount()` populates the DataTable with initial data (42 rows in the example)
5. **Actions**: Key bindings trigger action methods like `action_toggle_dark()` and `action_test_confirmbox()`

**Widget ID System**: Each widget instance receives an `id` parameter for later retrieval via `get_widget_by_id()`. This enables programmatic updates like calling `update_data()` on a specific `TTDataTable`.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:26-88](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:68-75]()

# Header with app metadata
header = TTHeader(app_name="My Tool", app_version="1.2.3")

# Footer with multiple content sections
footer = TTFooter(content=["Section 1", "Section 2", "Section 3\

## Purpose and Scope

This document provides a complete reference for all custom Textual widgets implemented in tt-tools-common. These widgets extend the [textual](https://github.com/Textualize/textual) TUI framework with Tenstorrent-specific components for building consistent terminal-based interfaces across TT-Tools applications.

This page covers the core widget classes (`TTHeader`, `TTFooter`, `TTDataTable`, `TTMenu`, `TTHostCompatibilityMenu`, `TTCompatibilityMenu`). For modal screen components (`TTConfirmBox`, `TTHelperMenuBox`, `TTSettingsMenu`), see [Modal Screens and Dialogs](#4.2). For styling and theming information, see [Theming and Styling](#4.3). For practical integration examples, see [Building Custom TUI Applications](#4.4).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-365]()

## Widget Library Architecture

The widget library is organized into three functional categories: layout widgets that structure the application frame, data display widgets that present information, and modal screens that handle user interactions.


---

## Layout Widgets

### TTHeader

The `TTHeader` widget provides a standardized application header displaying the application name, version, and a real-time clock. The header automatically refreshes every second to update the timestamp.

**Class Definition:**
```
TTHeader(Widget)
```

**Constructor Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `app_name` | `str` | Application name displayed in center column |
| `app_version` | `str` | Version string displayed in left column with "Version" prefix |

**Implementation Details:**

The widget uses a Rich `Table.grid` with three columns (ratio 0.25:0.5:0.25) for left-justified version, centered app name, and right-justified timestamp. The render method is called automatically every second via `set_interval(1, callback=self.refresh)` configured in `on_mount()`.

**Rendering Layout:**
```
[Version X.Y.Z]     [Application Name]     [MMM DD YYYY HH:MM:SS AM/PM]
```

**CSS Styling:**

The header receives the following default styles from `common_style.css`:
- Height: 3 lines
- Dock position: top
- Outline: solid green border
- Text style: bold

**Code Reference:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:22-45]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:22-45](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:28-43]()

---

### TTFooter

The `TTFooter` widget provides a customizable footer for displaying static or dynamic content across the bottom of the application. Unlike the standard Textual `Footer` which shows keybindings, this widget supports arbitrary content.

**Class Definition:**
```
TTFooter(Widget)
```

**Constructor Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `content` | `List[str]` | required | List of strings to display as columns |
| `justify` | `str` | `"center"` | Text justification: "left", "center", or "right" |

**Implementation Details:**

The widget creates a Rich `Table.grid` with equal-ratio columns based on the length of the `content` list. Each string in the list occupies one column with the specified justification.

**CSS Styling:**

The footer receives the following default styles:
- Height: 3 lines
- Dock position: bottom
- Outline: solid green border
- Text style: bold

**Code Reference:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:48-62]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:48-62](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:28-43]()

---

## Data Display Widgets

### TTDataTable

The `TTDataTable` widget wraps Textual's `DataTable` in a `ScrollableContainer` with standardized styling and data management methods. This widget is the primary component for displaying tabular data in TT-Tools applications.

**Class Definition:**
```
TTDataTable(ScrollableContainer)
```

**Constructor Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `title` | `str` | required | Border title for the table |
| `header` | `List[str]` | `None` | Column header labels (auto-styled with underline) |
| `id` | `str` | `None` | Widget identifier |
| `**kwargs` | | | Additional arguments passed to `DataTable` constructor |

**Key Attributes:**

| Attribute | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `dt` | `DataTable` | Internal DataTable widget instance (ID: `{id}_table`) |
| `border_title` | `str` | Title displayed in container border |

**Key Methods:**

**`update_data(rows: List[str]) -> None`**

Updates table data efficiently. Attempts cell-by-cell updates first; if row count changed, clears and re-populates the entire table. This method enables dynamic data refresh without recreating the table.

**`style_header() -> None`**

Internal method that applies Rich `Text` styling to header cells (centered, underlined). Called automatically during initialization if `header` is provided.

**DataTable Configuration:**

The internal `DataTable` is configured with:
- `zebra_stripes = False`: Disabled for consistent coloring
- `cursor_type = "cell"`: Cell-level selection rather than row
- Border title matches the container title

**Usage Pattern:**

```python
# In compose():
yield TTDataTable(title="Results", header=["ID", "Status", "Value"], id="results_dt")

# In on_mount() or update handler:
tt_dt = self.get_widget_by_id("results_dt")
tt_dt.dt.add_rows([["0", "Pass", "100"], ["1", "Fail", "0"]])

# For dynamic updates:
tt_dt.update_data([["0", "Pass", "150"], ["1", "Pass", "200"]])
```

**CSS Styling:**

DataTable receives specific cursor and hover styles:
- Cursor background: yellow (`$yellow`)
- Cursor text: black
- Hover background: yellow at 60% opacity
- Header: bold, centered, transparent background

**Code Reference:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:65-117]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:65-117](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:45-86]()

---

### TTMenu

The `TTMenu` widget displays a list of key-value pairs with consistent formatting. Keys are bold and yellow-colored, while values use default styling. This widget is suitable for displaying system information or configuration details.

**Class Definition:**
```
TTMenu(Container)
```

**Constructor Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `id` | `str` | Widget identifier |
| `title` | `str` | Border title |
| `data` | `OrderedDict[str, str]` | Ordered dictionary of key-value pairs to display |

**Display Format:**

Each entry is rendered as:
```
* Key         : Value
```

Keys are left-justified based on the longest key length plus 1. The asterisk bullet point is prepended to each line.

**Special Handling:**

If a key equals `"Failed to fetch"`, the value is displayed in dark orange color on a new line without the colon separator, used for error messages.

**Implementation Details:**

The widget calculates `justify_width` as the maximum key length plus 1 to ensure consistent alignment. Rich `Text` objects are composed with styled segments for keys (yellow, bold) and plain text for values.

**Code Reference:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:120-146]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:120-146](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:88-95]()

---

### TTHostCompatibilityMenu

The `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` widget extends `TTMenu` to display host configuration information with compatibility warnings. Values can be simple strings (compatible) or tuples containing the current value and a recommended value (incompatible).

**Class Definition:**
```
TTHostCompatibilityMenu(Container)
```

**Constructor Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `id` | `str` | Widget identifier |
| `title` | `str` | Base border title |
| `data` | `Dict[str, Union[str, Tuple]]` | Dictionary with string values (compatible) or tuple values (current, recommended) |

**Value Type Handling:**

| Value Type | Display Behavior | Example |
|------------|------------------|---------|
| `str` | Single line with key-value pair | `* OS: Ubuntu 22.04` |
| `Tuple[str, str]` | Two lines: current value + recommendation in orange | `* Kernel: 5.15.0`<br/>&nbsp;&nbsp;`* Kernel >= 6.1.0` |

**Border Title Behavior:**

The constructor automatically modifies the border title based on compatibility:
- All values are strings → `"{title} (Fully Compatible)"`
- Any tuple values present → `"{title} (Config Warning!)"` with red border title and subtitle `"* Recommended Config"`

**CSS Styling:**

Border title and subtitle colors are dynamically set via `self.styles.border_title_color` and `self.styles.border_subtitle_color` when warnings are present.

**Code Reference:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:149-210]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:149-210](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:88-95]()

---

### TTCompatibilityMenu

The `TTCompatibilityMenu` widget displays boolean compatibility checks with pass/fail indication. Each item in the data dictionary contains a tuple of `(bool, str)` representing the check result and associated message.

**Class Definition:**
```
TTCompatibilityMenu(Container)
```

**Constructor Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `id` | `str` | Widget identifier |
| `title` | `str` | Border title |
| `data` | `OrderedDict[str, Tuple[bool, str]]` | Ordered dictionary mapping check names to `(result, message)` tuples |

**Display Format:**

Each entry renders as:
```
* Check Name  : Message
```

The message text color depends on the boolean result:
- `True`: Default green color (normal text)
- `False`: Dark orange color (warning)

**Implementation Details:**

The widget is structurally similar to `TTMenu` but expects tuple values where `value[0]` is the boolean check result and `value[1]` is the display message. Keys are justified based on the longest key length.

**Code Reference:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:213-243]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:213-243](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:88-95]()

---

The following diagram illustrates how widgets compose together with Textual's built-in components and the styling system:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Application Composition"
        App["Textual App"]
        ComposeResult["compose()<br/>method"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Widget Instances"
        HeaderInst["TTHeader instance<br/>app_name, app_version"]
        FooterInst["TTFooter instance<br/>content list"]
        DataTableInst["TTDataTable instance<br/>id, title, header"]
        MenuInst["TTMenu instance<br/>id, title, data"]
        HostMenuInst["TTHostCompatibilityMenu<br/>id, title, data"]
        CompatMenuInst["TTCompatibilityMenu<br/>id, title, data"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Internal Components"
        DT["DataTable widget<br/>id={parent_id}_table"]
        RichText["Rich Text objects"]
        RichTable["Rich Table.grid"]
        RichPanel["Rich Panel"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Textual Rendering"
        RenderResult["RenderResult"]
        Screen["Screen display"]
    end
    
    App --> ComposeResult
    ComposeResult --> HeaderInst
    ComposeResult --> FooterInst
    ComposeResult --> DataTableInst
    ComposeResult --> MenuInst
    ComposeResult --> HostMenuInst
    ComposeResult --> CompatMenuInst
    
    HeaderInst -->|render| RichTable
    FooterInst -->|render| RichTable
    RichTable --> RichPanel
    
    DataTableInst -->|compose| DT
    
    MenuInst -->|render| RichText
    HostMenuInst -->|render| RichText
    CompatMenuInst -->|render| RichText
    
    RichPanel --> RenderResult
    RichText --> RenderResult
    DT --> RenderResult
    
    RenderResult --> Screen
```

## Styling Integration

All widgets inherit global styles from `common_style.css` and can be further customized through CSS selectors. The styling system uses CSS variables for consistent color theming.

### Color Variables

| Variable | Value | Usage |
|----------|-------|-------|
| `$red` | `#f04f5e` | Errors, warnings, hover states |
| `$green` | `#1eb57d` | Borders, primary text, success states |
| `$yellow` | `#ffd10a` | Headers, keys, scrollbars, cursors |
| `$purple` | `#786bb0` | (Reserved for future use) |
| `$orange` | `darkorange` | Warning text, incompatibility notes |
| `$gray` | `ansi_bright_black` | Secondary text |

### Global Widget Styles

All widgets (`*` selector) receive:
- Text color: `$yellow`
- Scrollbar colors: `$yellow` (thumb), `$green` (track)
- Border title: left-aligned, yellow, bold

### Widget-Specific Selectors

| CSS Selector | Target Widgets |
|--------------|----------------|
| `TTHeader, TTFooter` | Layout widgets |
| `DataTable` | Internal tables in TTDataTable |
| `TTMenu, TTCompatibilityMenu, TTHostCompatibilityMenu` | All menu-style widgets |
| `TTConfirmBox` | Modal confirmation dialogs |
| `TTHelperMenuBox` | Help screen modals |

For complete styling documentation, see [Theming and Styling](#4.3).

**Code Reference:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:1-226]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:1-226]()

## Usage Example: Test Widget Application

The test application demonstrates how to compose multiple widgets into a functional TUI. This example is used for both manual testing and automated validation.

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "TTApp Application Structure"
        AppClass["TTApp(App)<br/>CSS_PATH: common_style.css"]
        ComposeMethod["compose() method"]
        OnMountMethod["on_mount() method"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Layout Hierarchy"
        Header["TTHeader<br/>app_name, app_version"]
        HContainer["Horizontal container"]
        VContainer["Vertical container"]
        Footer["Textual Footer<br/>keybindings"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Content Widgets"
        Menu1["TTMenu<br/>id='menu_1'<br/>title='Menu 1'"]
        Menu2["TTMenu<br/>id='menu_2'<br/>title='Menu 2'"]
        DT["TTDataTable<br/>id='dt_example'<br/>header=['Board ID', ...]"]
        Menu3["TTMenu<br/>id='menu_3'<br/>title='Right Menu'"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Actions"
        ToggleDark["action_toggle_dark()<br/>Toggle dark mode"]
        TestConfirm["action_test_confirmbox()<br/>Push TTConfirmBox modal"]
    end
    
    AppClass --> ComposeMethod
    AppClass --> OnMountMethod
    ComposeMethod --> Header
    ComposeMethod --> HContainer
    ComposeMethod --> Footer
    
    HContainer --> VContainer
    HContainer --> DT
    HContainer --> Menu3
    
    VContainer --> Menu1
    VContainer --> Menu2
    
    OnMountMethod -->|populate 42 rows| DT
    
    AppClass -->|keybinding 'd'| ToggleDark
    AppClass -->|keybinding 'b'| TestConfirm
```

**Key Implementation Points:**

1. **CSS Loading**: The app specifies `CSS_PATH = "../ui_common/common_style.css"` to load the theme
2. **Widget Composition**: Widgets are yielded in `compose()` using context managers for container hierarchy
3. **Dynamic Data**: Table rows are populated in `on_mount()` after widget tree is mounted
4. **Widget Access**: `self.get_widget_by_id()` retrieves widget instances for manipulation
5. **Modal Integration**: Modal screens are pushed using `self.push_screen(TTConfirmBox(...))`

**Code Reference:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:26-88]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:26-88](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-365]()

---

## Widget Lifecycle and Event Handling

Understanding the Textual widget lifecycle is essential for proper widget usage:

```mermaid
stateDiagram-v2
    [*] --> Constructed: __init__()
    Constructed --> Mounted: on_mount()
    Mounted --> Active: ready for events
    
    Active --> Refreshed: set_interval() or refresh()
    Refreshed --> Active
    
    Active --> Updated: update_data() or other methods
    Updated --> Active
    
    Active --> Removed: remove()
    Removed --> [*]
    
    note right of Mounted
        TTHeader: set_interval(1, refresh)
        TTDataTable: add_rows() available
        Application: get_widget_by_id() works
    end note
    
    note right of Active
        Render methods called automatically
        User input events processed
        Timers fire callbacks
    end note
```

**Lifecycle Methods by Widget:**

| Widget | `__init__` Parameters | `on_mount` Actions | `render` Behavior |
|--------|----------------------|-------------------|-------------------|
| TTHeader | Store app_name, app_version | Set 1-second refresh interval | Build 3-column grid with timestamp |
| TTFooter | Store content list, justify | None | Build N-column grid from content |
| TTDataTable | Initialize DataTable, add header | User populates data | Container renders DataTable |
| TTMenu | Store data dict, calculate justify_width | None | Build styled Text from dict |
| TTHostCompatibilityMenu | Check compatibility, set border styling | None | Build Text with conditional orange styling |
| TTCompatibilityMenu | Store data dict | None | Build Text with pass/fail coloring |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-243]()

---

## API Summary Table

The following table provides a quick reference for all widget constructors and their key methods:

| Widget | Constructor Signature | Key Methods | Return Types |
|--------|----------------------|-------------|--------------|
| `TTHeader` | `(app_name: str, app_version: str)` | `on_mount()`, `render()` | `RenderResult` |
| `TTFooter` | `(content: List[str], justify: str = "center")` | `render()` | `RenderResult` |
| `TTDataTable` | `(title: str, header: List[str] = None, id: str = None, **kwargs)` | `update_data(rows: List[str])`, `compose()` | `ComposeResult` |
| `TTMenu` | `(id: str, title: str, data: OrderedDict[str, str])` | `render()` | `RenderResult` |
| `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` | `(id: str, title: str, data: Dict[str, Union[str, Tuple]])` | `render()` | `RenderResult` |
| `TTCompatibilityMenu` | `(id: str, title: str, data: OrderedDict[str, Tuple[bool, str]])` | `render()` | `RenderResult` |

For modal screen widgets (`TTConfirmBox`, `TTHelperMenuBox`, `TTSettingsMenu`), see [Modal Screens and Dialogs](#4.2).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:22-243]()

## Integration with Consumer Applications

The widget library is consumed by multiple TT-Tools applications. The following diagram shows the typical integration pattern:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Consumer Application (e.g., tt-smi)"
        AppMain["main.py<br/>Application entrypoint"]
        AppClass["TTSMIApp(App)<br/>Custom application class"]
        AppCSS["Custom app.css<br/>Application-specific styles"]
    end
    
    subgraph "tt-tools-common.ui_common"
        Widgets["widgets.py<br/>TTHeader, TTFooter, TTDataTable<br/>TTMenu, etc."]
        CommonCSS["common_style.css<br/>Global theme"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Textual Framework"
        TextualApp["textual.app.App"]
        TextualWidgets["textual.widgets.*"]
    end
    
    AppMain -->|instantiate| AppClass
    AppClass -->|inherit| TextualApp
    AppClass -->|import| Widgets
    AppClass -->|load CSS| CommonCSS
    AppClass -->|load CSS| AppCSS
    
    Widgets -->|extend| TextualWidgets
    Widgets -->|styled by| CommonCSS
    
    AppCSS -.override.-> CommonCSS
```

**Typical Import Pattern:**

```python
from tt_tools_common.ui_common.widgets import (
    TTHeader,
    TTFooter,
    TTDataTable,
    TTMenu,
    TTHostCompatibilityMenu,
    TTCompatibilityMenu,
    TTConfirmBox,
)
```

**CSS Loading:**

Applications specify `CSS_PATH = "path/to/common_style.css"` as a class attribute to load the global theme. Additional application-specific CSS files can be loaded to override or extend the base styles.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:13-35](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-10]()
