# Modal Screens and Dialogs

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css](tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css)
- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py](tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document covers the modal screen components provided by tt-tools-common for building interactive dialogs in Textual-based TUI applications. Modal screens are overlay widgets that block interaction with the underlying application until dismissed. The library provides three pre-built modal components: `TTConfirmBox` for yes/no confirmations, `TTHelperMenuBox` for displaying help documentation, and `TTSettingsMenu` for application settings with toggle switches.

For information about non-modal widgets like headers, footers, and data tables, see [Widget Library Reference](#4.1). For theming and CSS customization of these modals, see [Theming and Styling](#4.3).

---

## Modal Screen Architecture

All modal components in tt-tools-common inherit from Textual's `ModalScreen` base class, which provides the fundamental overlay behavior. Modal screens suspend interaction with the base application until explicitly dismissed via `app.pop_screen()`.

```mermaid
graph TD
    TextualModalScreen["textual.screen.ModalScreen<br/>(Textual Framework)"]
    
    TTConfirmBox["TTConfirmBox<br/>Confirmation Dialog"]
    TTHelperMenuBox["TTHelperMenuBox<br/>Help Documentation"]
    TTSettingsMenu["TTSettingsMenu<br/>Application Settings"]
    
    Grid["textual.containers.Grid<br/>Layout Container"]
    Markdown["textual.widgets.Markdown<br/>Rich Text Display"]
    Label["textual.widgets.Label"]
    Button["textual.widgets.Button"]
    Switch["textual.widgets.Switch"]
    
    TextualModalScreen --> TTConfirmBox
    TextualModalScreen --> TTHelperMenuBox
    TextualModalScreen --> TTSettingsMenu
    
    TTConfirmBox --> Grid
    TTConfirmBox --> Label
    TTConfirmBox --> Button
    
    TTHelperMenuBox --> Markdown
    
    TTSettingsMenu --> Grid
    TTSettingsMenu --> Label
    TTSettingsMenu --> Switch
    
    style TextualModalScreen fill:#f9f9f9
    style TTConfirmBox fill:#e8e8e8
    style TTHelperMenuBox fill:#e8e8e8
    style TTSettingsMenu fill:#e8e8e8
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:10](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-365]()

---

## TTConfirmBox: Confirmation Dialogs

### Overview

`TTConfirmBox` provides a simple yes/no confirmation dialog with customizable text and callback functions. It renders as a centered modal with two buttons and automatically dismisses itself after user selection.

### Class Definition

The class is defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-272]() with the following signature:

```python
class TTConfirmBox(ModalScreen):
    def __init__(
        self, text: str, on_yes: Callable = None, on_no: Callable = None
    ) -> None
```

**Parameters:**
| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `text` | `str` | The question or confirmation message to display |
| `on_yes` | `Callable` (optional) | Callback function executed when "Yes" is pressed |
| `on_no` | `Callable` (optional) | Callback function executed when "No" is pressed |

### Component Structure

The dialog is composed using a `Grid` container with three child widgets:

```mermaid
graph TD
    TTConfirmBox["TTConfirmBox<br/>(ModalScreen)"]
    
    GridContainer["Grid Container<br/>id='dialog'"]
    QuestionLabel["Label<br/>id='question'<br/>Displays confirmation text"]
    YesButton["Button<br/>id='yes'<br/>Text: 'Yes'"]
    NoButton["Button<br/>id='no'<br/>Text: 'No'"]
    
    TTConfirmBox --> GridContainer
    GridContainer --> QuestionLabel
    GridContainer --> YesButton
    GridContainer --> NoButton
    
    YesButton -.on_button_pressed.-> OnYesCallback["Execute on_yes() callback"]
    NoButton -.on_button_pressed.-> OnNoCallback["Execute on_no() callback"]
    
    OnYesCallback --> PopScreen["app.pop_screen()"]
    OnNoCallback --> PopScreen
```

The grid layout is configured at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:259-264]() with a 2-column structure where the label spans both columns.

### Event Handling

The button press handler at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:266-271]() implements the following logic:

1. Check which button was pressed via `event.button.id`
2. If "yes" and `on_yes` callback exists, execute it
3. If "no" and `on_no` callback exists, execute it
4. Always pop the screen to dismiss the dialog

### CSS Styling

The modal styling is defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:105-138]():

| CSS Selector | Properties | Purpose |
|--------------|------------|---------|
| `TTConfirmBox` | `align: center middle` | Centers the dialog on screen |
| `#dialog` | `width: 30%`, `height: 25%`, `border: solid $green` | Dialog container dimensions and border |
| `#question` | `column-span: 2`, `content-align: center middle` | Question label spans full width, centered text |
| `Button` | `background: $yellow`, `color: white` | Default button appearance |
| `Button:hover` / `Button:focus` | `background: $red`, `text-style: bold` | Interactive feedback |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-272](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:105-138]()

---

## TTHelperMenuBox: Help Documentation Modal

### Overview

`TTHelperMenuBox` displays help documentation as a modal screen using Markdown rendering. It supports keyboard navigation and auto-dismisses on multiple key bindings.

### Class Definition

The class is defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:274-306]() with the following structure:

```python
class TTHelperMenuBox(ModalScreen):
    BINDINGS = [
        ("q", "quit", "Quit"),
        ("escape", "esc_screen", "Escape the open screen"),
        ("h", "help", "Quit the help box"),
    ]
    
    def __init__(self, text: str, theme: OrderedDict = {}) -> None
```

**Parameters:**
| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `text` | `str` | Markdown-formatted help content |
| `theme` | `OrderedDict` (optional) | Theme dictionary (currently unused in implementation) |

### Key Bindings

Three key bindings provide identical dismiss functionality:

```mermaid
graph LR
    KeyQ["Key: 'q'<br/>action_quit()"]
    KeyEsc["Key: 'escape'<br/>action_esc_screen()"]
    KeyH["Key: 'h'<br/>action_help()"]
    
    PopScreen["app.pop_screen()<br/>Dismiss Modal"]
    
    KeyQ --> PopScreen
    KeyEsc --> PopScreen
    KeyH --> PopScreen
```

All three actions at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:291-305]() execute `self.app.pop_screen()` to return to the main application. Note that `action_quit` is defined twice (lines 291 and 299), which appears to be a duplicate.

### Markdown Rendering

The help content is rendered using Textual's `Markdown` widget at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:289]():

```python
yield Markdown(self.text, id="help_menu_box")
```

The Markdown widget automatically handles:
- Headers (styled via `MarkdownH1` CSS rules)
- Tables (styled via `MarkdownTableContent` CSS rules)
- Code blocks
- Lists and other standard Markdown syntax

### CSS Styling

Help menu styling is defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:175-206]():

| CSS Selector | Properties | Purpose |
|--------------|------------|---------|
| `TTHelperMenuBox` | `align: center middle` | Centers the modal on screen |
| `#help_menu_box` | `width: 110`, `height: 30`, `border: solid $green` | Fixed dimensions for help content |
| `MarkdownH1` | `background: $accent-darken-2`, `text-style: bold`, `padding: 1` | Styled header with background |
| `MarkdownTableContent>.markdown-table--header` | `text-style: bold` | Bold table headers |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:274-306](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:175-206]()

---

## TTSettingsMenu: Application Settings Dialog

### Overview

`TTSettingsMenu` provides an interactive settings dialog with toggle switches for application configuration. It dynamically reads and updates application state using Switch widgets.

### Class Definition

The class is defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:308-365]():

```python
class TTSettingsMenu(ModalScreen):
    BINDINGS = [
        ("q, Q, s, S", "quit", "Quit"),
        ("escape", "esc_screen", "Escape the open screen"),
    ]
    
    def __init__(self, text: str, theme: OrderedDict = {}) -> None
```

**Parameters:**
| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `text` | `str` | Text parameter (currently unused in implementation) |
| `theme` | `OrderedDict` | Theme dictionary for styling text labels |

### Settings Configuration

The settings menu is specifically designed for tt-smi with two configurable options:

```mermaid
graph TD
    TTSettingsMenu["TTSettingsMenu"]
    
    Grid["Grid Container<br/>id='settings_menu_box'"]
    
    Heading["Label: 'TT-SMI Settings'<br/>id='heading'"]
    Instruction["Label: navigation instructions<br/>id='instruction'"]
    
    DarkLabel["Label: 'o Dark Mode:'<br/>id='dark_label'"]
    DarkSwitch["Switch<br/>id='dark_switch'<br/>Bound to: app.dark"]
    
    SWLabel["Label: 'o Latest SW versions:'<br/>id='sw_label'"]
    SWSwitch["Switch<br/>id='sw_switch'<br/>Bound to: app.get_latest_sw_vers"]
    
    TTSettingsMenu --> Grid
    Grid --> Heading
    Grid --> Instruction
    Grid --> DarkLabel
    Grid --> DarkSwitch
    Grid --> SWLabel
    Grid --> SWSwitch
    
    DarkSwitch -.on change.-> UpdateDark["Update app.dark"]
    SWSwitch -.on change.-> UpdateSW["Update app.get_latest_sw_vers"]
```

The composition at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:321-332]() creates a grid with paired labels and switches for each setting.

### Switch Event Handling

The event handler at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:334-348]() uses Textual's `@on` decorator to handle `Switch.Changed` events:

```python
@on(Switch.Changed)
def select_changed(self, event: Switch.Changed) -> None:
    if event.switch.id == "dark_switch":
        self.app.dark = event.switch.value
    if event.switch.id == "sw_switch":
        self.app.get_latest_sw_vers = event.switch.value
```

**Event Flow:**

1. User toggles a switch via keyboard (Tab/Enter) or mouse click
2. `Switch.Changed` event is emitted
3. Handler checks `event.switch.id` to identify which switch changed
4. Corresponding app property is updated with `event.switch.value` (boolean)
5. Application state persists across screen dismissals

### Initial Switch State

Switches are initialized with current application state at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:328-330]():

```python
Switch(value=self.app.dark, id="dark_switch")
Switch(value=self.app.get_latest_sw_vers, id="sw_switch")
```

This ensures the UI reflects the current configuration when the modal opens.

### Key Bindings

Multiple keys dismiss the settings menu:

| Keys | Action | Description |
|------|--------|-------------|
| `q`, `Q`, `s`, `S` | `action_quit` | Return to main app |
| `escape` | `action_esc_screen` | Escape the modal |

All dismissal actions at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:350-364]() call `self.app.pop_screen()`. Note that settings changes are applied immediately on switch toggle, not on modal dismiss.

### CSS Styling

Switch styling is defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:208-217]():

| CSS Selector | Properties | Purpose |
|--------------|------------|---------|
| `Switch>.switch--slider` | `color: $red`, `background: red 12%` | Off state (red) |
| `Switch.-on>.switch--slider` | `color: $green`, `background: $green 15%` | On state (green) |

The grid layout styling (not explicitly defined) inherits from default Grid container styles.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:308-365](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:208-217]()

---

## Modal Screen Lifecycle and Usage Patterns

### Display and Dismissal Pattern

All modal screens follow a consistent lifecycle managed by the Textual application:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant App as "Textual Application"
    participant Modal as "Modal Screen<br/>(TTConfirmBox/TTHelperMenuBox/TTSettingsMenu)"
    participant User as "User"
    
    App->>Modal: app.push_screen(modal_instance)
    activate Modal
    Note over App: Base app suspended
    
    Modal->>User: Display modal content
    User->>Modal: Interact (button/key press)
    
    alt TTConfirmBox
        Modal->>Modal: Execute on_yes or on_no callback
        Modal->>App: app.pop_screen()
    else TTHelperMenuBox
        Modal->>App: app.pop_screen() on q/escape/h
    else TTSettingsMenu
        Modal->>Modal: Update app properties on switch change
        Modal->>App: app.pop_screen() on q/s/escape
    end
    
    deactivate Modal
    Note over App: Base app resumed
```

### Instantiation Pattern

Typical usage involves creating the modal instance and immediately pushing it to the screen stack:

```python
# From application code (pattern inferred from widget design)

# Confirmation dialog
confirm_box = TTConfirmBox(
    text="Are you sure you want to reset all chips?",
    on_yes=lambda: self.perform_reset(),
    on_no=lambda: self.log_cancel()
)
self.app.push_screen(confirm_box)

# Help menu
help_box = TTHelperMenuBox(
    text=HELP_MARKDOWN_CONTENT,
    theme=self.theme
)
self.app.push_screen(help_box)

# Settings menu
settings = TTSettingsMenu(
    text="",  # Currently unused
    theme=self.theme
)
self.app.push_screen(settings)
```

### Modal Screen Coordination

Modal screens operate independently but can access application state via `self.app`:

```mermaid
graph TD
    BaseApp["Base Textual Application<br/>app.dark<br/>app.get_latest_sw_vers"]
    
    Modal1["TTConfirmBox<br/>Access: self.app"]
    Modal2["TTHelperMenuBox<br/>Access: self.app"]
    Modal3["TTSettingsMenu<br/>Access: self.app"]
    
    Modal1 -.read/write.-> BaseApp
    Modal2 -.read/write.-> BaseApp
    Modal3 -.read/write.-> BaseApp
    
    PopScreen["self.app.pop_screen()<br/>Universal dismiss"]
    
    Modal1 --> PopScreen
    Modal2 --> PopScreen
    Modal3 --> PopScreen
```

This pattern enables modals to read application state (like switch initial values) and write updates (like settings changes) without explicit parameter passing.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-365]()

---

## Design Considerations and Limitations

### Current Implementation Notes

1. **Theme Dictionary Usage**: Both `TTHelperMenuBox` and `TTSettingsMenu` accept a `theme` parameter, but:
   - `TTHelperMenuBox` does not use it [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:283-289]()
   - `TTSettingsMenu` uses it only for label styling [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:325-326]()

2. **Duplicate Method Definitions**: `TTHelperMenuBox.action_quit` is defined twice [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:291-301](), which may indicate a copy-paste artifact.

3. **Hard-Coded Settings**: `TTSettingsMenu` is specifically designed for tt-smi with fixed settings options. To use in other applications, you would need to modify the compose method or create a subclass.

4. **No Border Titles**: `TTConfirmBox` has a TODO comment indicating border titles are not yet implemented [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:256]().

### CSS Customization Points

All modal screens can be styled through CSS by targeting:

- The class name (e.g., `TTConfirmBox`)
- Component IDs (e.g., `#dialog`, `#help_menu_box`, `#settings_menu_box`)
- Child widget selectors (e.g., `Button`, `Switch`, `MarkdownH1`)

For comprehensive styling information, see [Theming and Styling](#4.3).

### Extensibility

To create custom modal dialogs:

1. Inherit from `ModalScreen`
2. Override `compose()` to define layout
3. Implement action methods for key bindings
4. Call `self.app.pop_screen()` to dismiss
5. Access parent app via `self.app` for state management

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-365](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:105-217]()
2a:T57a9,
# Theming and Styling

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css](tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css)
- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py](tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This page documents the CSS-based theming system used by tt-tools-common's Textual UI components. It explains the color variables, global style rules, and widget-specific styling classes defined in the shared stylesheet. For documentation of the actual widget components and their functionality, see [Widget Library Reference](#4.1). For information on modal screen components, see [Modal Screens and Dialogs](#4.2).

The theming system provides a consistent visual identity across all TT-Tools applications through centralized CSS definitions that leverage Textual's CSS engine.

---

## CSS Theming Architecture

The theming system uses a single centralized CSS file that applications load to apply consistent styling across all widgets. The architecture separates presentation (CSS) from widget logic (Python classes).

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Application Layer"
        App["Textual App<br/>e.g., tt-smi"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CSS Loading"
        CSSFile["common_style.css"]
        LoadCSS["App.CSS_PATH or<br/>App.THEME"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Style Components"
        ColorVars["Color Variables<br/>$red, $green, $yellow, etc."]
        GlobalStyles["Global Styles<br/>* selector"]
        WidgetStyles["Widget-Specific Styles<br/>TTHeader, DataTable, etc."]
        IDStyles["ID-Based Styles<br/>#dialog, #question, etc."]
    end
    
    subgraph "Widget Instances"
        TTHeader["TTHeader Widget"]
        TTFooter["TTFooter Widget"]
        DataTable["DataTable Widget"]
        TTMenu["TTMenu Widget"]
        Buttons["Button Widgets"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Runtime Styling"
        TextualEngine["Textual CSS Engine"]
        AppliedStyles["Applied Styles<br/>border, color, padding, etc."]
    end
    
    App --> LoadCSS
    LoadCSS --> CSSFile
    
    CSSFile --> ColorVars
    CSSFile --> GlobalStyles
    CSSFile --> WidgetStyles
    CSSFile --> IDStyles
    
    ColorVars --> TextualEngine
    GlobalStyles --> TextualEngine
    WidgetStyles --> TextualEngine
    IDStyles --> TextualEngine
    
    TextualEngine --> AppliedStyles
    
    AppliedStyles --> TTHeader
    AppliedStyles --> TTFooter
    AppliedStyles --> DataTable
    AppliedStyles --> TTMenu
    AppliedStyles --> Buttons
```

**Diagram: CSS Theming System Architecture**

Applications load the CSS file through Textual's `CSS_PATH` or `THEME` class variables. The CSS engine processes variable definitions, selectors, and rules to apply styles to widget instances at runtime.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:1-226]()

---

## Color Variable Definitions

The theme defines six primary color variables that establish the Tenstorrent visual identity. These variables are referenced throughout the stylesheet using CSS variable syntax.

| Variable | Hex Value | Usage Context |
|----------|-----------|---------------|
| `$red` | `#f04f5e` | Error states, warnings, hover effects |
| `$green` | `#1eb57d` | Primary accent color, borders, success states |
| `$yellow` | `#ffd10a` | Text color, highlights, scrollbars, key labels |
| `$purple` | `#786bb0` | Reserved for specialized use cases |
| `$orange` | `darkorange` | Warning messages, compatibility notes |
| `$gray` | `ansi_bright_black` | Placeholder text, disabled states |

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Color Variables"
        RedVar["$red<br/>#f04f5e"]
        GreenVar["$green<br/>#1eb57d"]
        YellowVar["$yellow<br/>#ffd10a"]
        PurpleVar["$purple<br/>#786bb0"]
        OrangeVar["$orange<br/>darkorange"]
        GrayVar["$gray<br/>ansi_bright_black"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Usage in Styles"
        Borders["border: solid $green"]
        Text["color: $yellow"]
        Scrollbar["scrollbar-color: $yellow"]
        Hover["background: $red"]
        Warning["color: $orange"]
    end
    
    GreenVar --> Borders
    YellowVar --> Text
    YellowVar --> Scrollbar
    RedVar --> Hover
    OrangeVar --> Warning
```

**Diagram: Color Variable System and Usage**

These variables are defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:6-12]() and used throughout the stylesheet for consistent theming.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:6-12]()

---

## Global Style Rules

The universal selector (`*`) defines default properties inherited by all widgets unless explicitly overridden. These establish baseline theming across the entire application.

### Global Properties

```css
* {
  color: $yellow;
  scrollbar-color: $yellow;
  scrollbar-color-active: white;
  scrollbar-color-hover: white;
  scrollbar-background: $green;
  scrollbar-background-active: $green;
  scrollbar-background-hover: $green;
  border-title-align: left;
  border-title-color: $yellow;
  border-title-style: bold;
}
```

| Property | Value | Effect |
|----------|-------|--------|
| `color` | `$yellow` | Default text color for all widgets |
| `scrollbar-color` | `$yellow` | Default scrollbar thumb color |
| `scrollbar-color-active` | `white` | Scrollbar thumb when clicked |
| `scrollbar-color-hover` | `white` | Scrollbar thumb on hover |
| `scrollbar-background` | `$green` | Scrollbar track background |
| `border-title-align` | `left` | Border title positioning |
| `border-title-color` | `$yellow` | Color for all border titles |
| `border-title-style` | `bold` | Bold styling for border titles |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:15-26]()

---

## Header and Footer Styling

The `TTHeader` and `TTFooter` widgets share common styling with slight positioning differences. Both widgets have fixed height and bold text styling with green outlines.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "TTHeader Styling"
        HeaderHeight["height: 3"]
        HeaderDock["dock: top"]
        HeaderOutline["outline: solid $green"]
        HeaderBold["text-style: bold"]
    end
    
    subgraph "TTFooter Styling"
        FooterHeight["height: 3"]
        FooterDock["dock: bottom"]
        FooterOutline["outline: solid $green"]
        FooterBold["text-style: bold"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Widget Rendering"
        TTHeaderWidget["TTHeader<br/>widgets.py:22-45"]
        TTFooterWidget["TTFooter<br/>widgets.py:48-62"]
    end
    
    HeaderHeight --> TTHeaderWidget
    HeaderDock --> TTHeaderWidget
    HeaderOutline --> TTHeaderWidget
    HeaderBold --> TTHeaderWidget
    
    FooterHeight --> TTFooterWidget
    FooterDock --> TTFooterWidget
    FooterOutline --> TTFooterWidget
    FooterBold --> TTFooterWidget
```

**Diagram: Header and Footer Style Application**

### CSS Rules

Both widgets use shared rules defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:30-43]():

```
TTHeader,
TTFooter {
  height: 3;
  text-style: bold;
  outline: solid $green;
}

TTHeader {
  dock: top;
}

TTFooter {
  dock: bottom;
}
```

The `dock` property determines vertical positioning, while `height: 3` allocates three terminal rows for content display.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:28-43](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:22-62]()

## DataTable Styling

The `DataTable` widget receives extensive styling to support interactive cell selection, hover effects, and header presentation.

### DataTable Style Rules

| Selector | Properties | Purpose |
|----------|-----------|---------|
| `DataTable` | `padding: 1 2`<br/>`color: $green`<br/>`border: solid $green`<br/>`text-align: center` | Base table styling with green color scheme |
| `.datatable--header` | `text-style: bold`<br/>`background: white 0%` | Header row with transparent background |
| `.datatable--cursor` | `background: $yellow`<br/>`color: black` | Active cell selection |
| `.datatable--fixed-cursor` | `background: $yellow`<br/>`color: white` | Fixed cursor state |
| `.datatable--header-cursor` | `background: $yellow`<br/>`color: white` | Column header selection |
| `.datatable--hover` | `background: $yellow 60%`<br/>`color: white` | Cell hover effect with transparency |

```mermaid

    HeaderSelector --> Header
    CursorSelector --> Selected
    HoverSelector --> Hovering
```

**Diagram: DataTable Style State Machine**

The style definitions at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:45-85]() create an interactive table with clear visual feedback for user actions. The cursor styles use full `$yellow` background for selected cells, while hover uses `$yellow 60%` for semi-transparency.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:45-85](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:65-117]()

## Menu Widget Styling

Three menu variants (`TTMenu`, `TTCompatibilityMenu`, `TTHostCompatibilityMenu`) share a common base style defined collectively in the CSS.

### Shared Menu Properties

```
TTMenu,
TTCompatibilityMenu,
TTHostCompatibilityMenu {
  padding: 1 1;
  border: solid $green;
  color: $green;
}
```

These widgets display key-value information with consistent padding and border styling. Individual menu widgets apply programmatic styling for specific use cases:

| Widget Class | Programmatic Style Features | Location |
|--------------|---------------------------|----------|
| `TTMenu` | Yellow bold keys (`#ffd10a`), orange for error messages | [widgets.py:129-146]() |
| `TTCompatibilityMenu` | Orange text for incompatible values | [widgets.py:222-243]() |
| `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` | Dynamic border title color (red for warnings), orange recommendations | [widgets.py:178-210]() |

```mermaid

    end
```

The CSS provides base styling, while widgets apply programmatic styling using `rich.style.Style` objects for dynamic color changes based on data values. For example, `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` sets `self.styles.border_title_color = "red"` at [widgets.py:173]() when compatibility warnings are detected.

### TTHelperMenuBox Styling

The help menu modal displays markdown content in a centered box:

```
TTHelperMenuBox {
  align: center middle;
}

#help_menu_box {
  padding: 1 2;
  width: 110;
  height: 30;
  border: solid $green;
  background: $surface;
  color: white;
}
```

Markdown elements within the help box receive specialized styling:

- `MarkdownH1`: Centered header with accent background and border
- `MarkdownTableContent`: Full-width tables with bold headers
- All defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:174-206]()

### TTSettingsMenu Styling

The settings menu uses `Switch` widgets with custom slider styling:

```
Switch>.switch--slider {
  color: $red;
  background: red 12%;
}

Switch.-on>.switch--slider {
  color: $green;
  background: $green 15%;
}
```

The `.switch--slider` element changes color based on the switch state:
- **Off state**: Red color with 12% red background
- **On state** (with `-on` modifier): Green color with 15% green background

This provides clear visual feedback for boolean settings like dark mode toggles.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:208-217](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:308-364]()

## Interactive Element Styling

### Button States

Buttons use a three-state color system:

| State | Background | Text Color | Text Style | Trigger |
|-------|-----------|------------|-----------|---------|
| Default | `$yellow` | `white` | normal | Base state |
| Hover | `$red` | `white` | `bold` | Mouse over |
| Focus | `$red` | `white` | `bold` | Keyboard navigation |

The hover and focus states share styling to provide consistent feedback regardless of input method. Defined at [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:127-138]().

### Footer (Textual Default)

The standard Textual `Footer` widget receives custom styling:

```
Footer {
  background: $green;
  color: white;
  dock: bottom;
  text-style: bold;
  height: 1;
}
```

Footer key bindings use modifier classes:
- `.footer--highlight`: Highlighted elements with `$accent-darken-1` background
- `.footer--highlight-key`: Key labels with `$yellow` background and bold white text
- `.footer--key`: Regular keys with `$accent-darken-2` background

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:140-161]()

### Input Fields

Input placeholder text receives gray styling for low-emphasis hint text:

```
Input>.input--placeholder {
  color: gray;
}
```

This subtle color differentiates placeholder text from user-entered values.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:164-166]()

## Style Application Flow

The following diagram shows how styles are resolved and applied to widget instances at runtime:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Application Startup"
        AppInit["App.__init__"]
        LoadCSS["Load common_style.css"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CSS Processing"
        ParseVars["Parse Color Variables<br/>$red, $green, etc."]
        ParseGlobal["Parse Global Rules<br/>* selector"]
        ParseWidget["Parse Widget Rules<br/>TTHeader, DataTable, etc."]
        ParseID["Parse ID Rules<br/>#dialog, #question, etc."]
    end
    
    subgraph "Widget Creation"
        CreateWidget["Widget Instance Created"]
        ApplyBase["Apply Base Styles<br/>from * selector"]
        ApplyWidget["Apply Widget Type Styles<br/>from widget selector"]
        ApplyID["Apply ID Styles<br/>if widget has id"]
        ApplyProgram["Apply Programmatic Styles<br/>self.styles.property = value"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Runtime Updates"
        StyleRefresh["Style Refresh Triggered"]
        RecalculateStyles["Recalculate Applied Styles"]
        Render["Re-render Widget"]
    end
    
    AppInit --> LoadCSS
    LoadCSS --> ParseVars
    ParseVars --> ParseGlobal
    ParseGlobal --> ParseWidget
    ParseWidget --> ParseID
    
    CreateWidget --> ApplyBase
    ApplyBase --> ApplyWidget
    ApplyWidget --> ApplyID
    ApplyID --> ApplyProgram
    
    ApplyProgram --> Render
    
    StyleRefresh --> RecalculateStyles
    RecalculateStyles --> Render
```

**Diagram: Style Resolution and Application Process**

### Precedence Rules

Styles are applied in order of increasing specificity:

1. **Global styles** (`*` selector) - Base defaults
2. **Widget type styles** (e.g., `TTHeader`, `DataTable`) - Widget-specific rules
3. **ID-based styles** (e.g., `#dialog`, `#question`) - Instance-specific rules
4. **Programmatic styles** (e.g., `self.styles.border_title_color = "red"`) - Runtime overrides

Programmatic styles set via `self.styles` in widget code have highest precedence and override CSS definitions. For example, `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` sets `self.styles.border_title_color = "red"` at [widgets.py:173]() to override the default yellow from the global styles.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:1-226](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-365]()

---

## Customization Guide

### Loading Custom CSS

Applications can extend or override the default theme by loading additional CSS files:

```python
from textual.app import App

class MyApp(App):
    CSS_PATH = [
        "tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css",
        "my_custom_styles.css"
    ]
```

Later files in the `CSS_PATH` list override earlier definitions due to CSS cascade rules.

### Overriding Color Variables

Define new color variable values in a custom CSS file:

```css
/* my_custom_styles.css */
$red: #ff0000;
$green: #00ff00;
```

This redefines the color palette while preserving all existing style rules that reference these variables.

### Widget-Specific Overrides

Target specific widget instances by ID or add new widget type rules:

```css
/* Custom TTHeader styling */
TTHeader {
  height: 5;
  outline: solid $purple;
}

/* Specific widget instance */
#my_custom_table {
  border: solid $red;
  color: $red;
}
```

### Programmatic Style Modification

Widgets can apply dynamic styles in their code:

```python
class MyWidget(Container):
    def on_mount(self):
        if self.some_condition:
            self.styles.border = ("solid", "$red")
            self.border_title = "Error State"
            self.styles.border_title_color = "red"
```

This approach is useful for state-dependent styling, as seen in `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` at [widgets.py:168-176]() where border colors change based on compatibility status.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:168-176]()

---

## Summary Table: All Style Selectors

| Selector | File Location | Primary Properties | Used By |
|----------|--------------|-------------------|---------|

# Building Custom TUI Applications

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py](tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py)
- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css](tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css)
- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py](tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document provides a practical guide to building terminal user interface (TUI) applications using tt-tools-common's widget library and theming system. It covers the application structure, widget composition, layout strategies, event handling, and styling integration needed to create custom TUI tools.

For detailed reference on individual widgets and their APIs, see [Widget Library Reference](#4.1). For information about modal dialogs, see [Modal Screens and Dialogs](#4.2). For styling customization, see [Theming and Styling](#4.3).

---

## Application Architecture

### Textual App Foundation

TUI applications built with tt-tools-common inherit from `textual.app.App` and integrate the common widget library. The basic structure follows Textual's lifecycle model with tt-tools-common extensions.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Application Lifecycle"
        Init["App.__init__()<br/>Initialize app properties"]
        Compose["compose()<br/>Define widget hierarchy"]
        Mount["on_mount()<br/>Post-composition setup"]
        Action["action_* methods<br/>Handle user interactions"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Core Components"
        BINDINGS["BINDINGS class attribute<br/>Key binding definitions"]
        CSS_PATH["CSS_PATH class attribute<br/>Path to common_style.css"]
        AppProps["App properties<br/>app_name, app_version"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Widget Integration"
        TTHeader["TTHeader widget"]
        TTFooter["TTFooter widget"]
        TTMenu["TTMenu widget"]
        TTDataTable["TTDataTable widget"]
        Modals["Modal screens<br/>TTConfirmBox, etc."]
    end
    
    Init --> AppProps
    Init --> BINDINGS
    Init --> CSS_PATH
    
    Compose --> TTHeader
    Compose --> TTMenu
    Compose --> TTDataTable
    Compose --> TTFooter
    
    Mount --> TTDataTable
    Action --> Modals
    
    CSS_PATH --> TTHeader
    CSS_PATH --> TTMenu
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:26-89](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-365]()

---

### Basic Application Template

The minimal application structure consists of:

| Component | Purpose | Required |
|-----------|---------|----------|
| `__init__()` | Initialize app metadata and bindings | Yes |
| `CSS_PATH` | Link to styling system | Yes |
| `BINDINGS` | Define keyboard shortcuts | Optional |
| `compose()` | Create widget hierarchy | Yes |
| `on_mount()` | Initialize widget data | Optional |
| `action_*` methods | Handle user interactions | Optional |

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "TTApp Class Structure"
        ClassDef["class TTApp(App)"]
        
        subgraph "Class Attributes"
            BINDINGS["BINDINGS list"]
            CSS["CSS_PATH string"]
        end
        
        subgraph "Methods"
            Init["__init__(app_name, app_version)"]
            Compose["compose() -> ComposeResult"]
            Mount["on_mount() -> None"]
            Actions["action_toggle_dark()<br/>action_test_confirmbox()"]
        end
    end
    
    ClassDef --> BINDINGS
    ClassDef --> CSS
    ClassDef --> Init
    ClassDef --> Compose
    ClassDef --> Mount
    ClassDef --> Actions
    
    Init --> Compose
    Compose --> Mount
    Actions --> Modals["push_screen() / pop_screen()"]
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:26-50]()

---

## Widget Composition

### Defining the Widget Hierarchy

The `compose()` method yields widgets to build the application layout. tt-tools-common widgets integrate seamlessly with Textual's container system.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "compose() Method Flow"
        Compose["def compose() -> ComposeResult"]
        
        YieldHeader["yield TTHeader(app_name, version)"]
        YieldContainer["with Horizontal()/Vertical()"]
        YieldMenu["yield TTMenu(title, data, id)"]
        YieldTable["yield TTDataTable(title, header, id)"]
        YieldFooter["yield Footer()"]
    end
    
    Compose --> YieldHeader
    YieldHeader --> YieldContainer
    YieldContainer --> YieldMenu
    YieldContainer --> YieldTable
    YieldTable --> YieldFooter
    
    subgraph "Widget Constructor Parameters"
        HeaderParams["app_name: str<br/>app_version: str"]
        MenuParams["title: str<br/>data: OrderedDict<br/>id: str"]
        TableParams["title: str<br/>header: List[str]<br/>id: str"]
    end
    
    YieldHeader -.-> HeaderParams
    YieldMenu -.-> MenuParams
    YieldTable -.-> TableParams
```

**Example from test application:**

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:51-65]()

The test app demonstrates:
1. **TTHeader** at the top with app name and version
2. **Horizontal** container for side-by-side layout
3. **Vertical** container for stacked menus
4. **TTDataTable** for tabular data display
5. **Footer** (standard Textual) for key bindings

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:51-65](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:22-117]()

---

### Layout Strategies

tt-tools-common widgets work with Textual's container system for flexible layouts:

| Container | Use Case | Example |
|-----------|----------|---------|
| `Horizontal()` | Side-by-side placement | Menu + DataTable + Menu |
| `Vertical()` | Stacked placement | Multiple TTMenu widgets |
| `Grid()` | Cell-based layout | Modal dialogs (TTConfirmBox) |
| `ScrollableContainer` | Scrollable content | Built into TTDataTable |

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Layout Example Structure"
        Root["App Root"]
        
        Header["TTHeader<br/>dock: top"]
        
        HContainer["Horizontal Container"]
        
        VContainer["Vertical Container"]
        Menu1["TTMenu id='menu_1'"]
        Menu2["TTMenu id='menu_2'"]
        
        Table["TTDataTable id='dt_example'"]
        
        Menu3["TTMenu id='menu_3'"]
        
        Footer["Footer<br/>dock: bottom"]
    end
    
    Root --> Header
    Root --> HContainer
    Root --> Footer
    
    HContainer --> VContainer
    HContainer --> Table
    HContainer --> Menu3
    
    VContainer --> Menu1
    VContainer --> Menu2
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:55-64](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:28-43]()

## Styling Integration

### Loading the Common Stylesheet

Applications must set the `CSS_PATH` class attribute to load tt-tools-common's styling system:

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:35]()

The path is relative to the application file. The common stylesheet provides:

| Style Feature | CSS Variable | Applied To |
|---------------|--------------|------------|
| Primary color | `$yellow` (#ffd10a) | Text, titles, scrollbar |
| Accent color | `$green` (#1eb57d) | Borders, backgrounds, scrollbar |
| Error color | `$red` (#f04f5e) | Warnings, alerts |
| Secondary colors | `$purple`, `$orange`, `$gray` | Special cases |

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Styling System Flow"
        AppClass["App class<br/>CSS_PATH attribute"]
        CommonCSS["common_style.css"]
        
        subgraph "CSS Variables"
            Colors["$red, $green, $yellow<br/>$purple, $orange, $gray"]
        end
        
        subgraph "Widget Styles"
            HeaderStyle["TTHeader, TTFooter<br/>height, outline"]
            TableStyle["DataTable<br/>padding, border, cursor"]
            MenuStyle["TTMenu, TTCompatibilityMenu<br/>padding, border, color"]
            ButtonStyle["Button<br/>background, hover states"]
        end
    end
    
    AppClass --> CommonCSS
    CommonCSS --> Colors
    Colors --> HeaderStyle
    Colors --> TableStyle
    Colors --> MenuStyle
    Colors --> ButtonStyle
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:35](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:1-226]()

The stylesheet applies styles using widget class names and CSS selectors:

[tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:14-26]() - Global styles

## Data Population and Updates

### Initializing Widget Data

The `on_mount()` method is called after `compose()` completes, providing the opportunity to populate widgets with data.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Data Population Flow"
        Mount["on_mount() event"]
        GetWidget["get_widget_by_id(id)"]
        Widget["TTDataTable instance"]
        DataTable["widget.dt property<br/>Textual DataTable"]
        AddRows["dt.add_rows(rows)"]
    end
    
    Mount --> GetWidget
    GetWidget --> Widget
    Widget --> DataTable
    DataTable --> AddRows
    
    subgraph "Data Structures"
        RowData["List[List[Any]]<br/>Row-major format"]
        CellData["Individual cell values<br/>converted to strings"]
    end
    
    AddRows --> RowData
    RowData --> CellData
```

**Example from test application:**

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:67-80]()

This code:
1. Retrieves the `TTDataTable` widget by ID
2. Accesses the underlying `DataTable` via the `.dt` property
3. Populates 42 rows of test data
4. Formats timestamps using datetime

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:67-80](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:65-117]()

---

### Updating Data Dynamically

TTDataTable provides the `update_data()` method for refreshing existing data without clearing the table:

[tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:98-113]()

The update logic:
1. Iterates through new rows and cells
2. Attempts to update cells at existing coordinates
3. Falls back to `clear()` and `add_rows()` if structure changed

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "update_data() Logic"
        Start["update_data(rows)"]
        IterRows["For each row i, cell j"]
        TryUpdate["update_cell_at(Coordinate(j, i))"]
        CheckError{"CellDoesNotExist?"}
        UpdateCell["Update cell value"]
        ClearTable["dt.clear()"]
        AddRows["dt.add_rows(rows)"]
        End["Complete"]
    end
    
    Start --> IterRows
    IterRows --> TryUpdate
    TryUpdate --> CheckError
    CheckError -->|No| UpdateCell
    CheckError -->|Yes| ClearTable
    UpdateCell --> IterRows
    ClearTable --> AddRows
    AddRows --> End
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:98-113]()

---

## Event Handling and Actions

### Key Bindings

Applications define keyboard shortcuts through the `BINDINGS` class attribute:

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:29-33]()

Each binding is a tuple: `(key, action_name, description)`

| Element | Purpose | Example |
|---------|---------|---------|
| Key | Keyboard key(s) | `"d"`, `"q"`, `"ctrl+c"` |
| Action name | Method name without `action_` prefix | `"toggle_dark"` → `action_toggle_dark()` |
| Description | Footer display text | `"Toggle dark mode"` |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:29-33]()

---

### Action Methods

Action methods handle key binding triggers and other user interactions:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Action Method Pattern"
        KeyPress["User presses key"]
        Textual["Textual framework"]
        ActionMethod["action_<name>() method"]
        
        subgraph "Example Actions"
            ToggleDark["action_toggle_dark()<br/>Toggle app.dark property"]
            Quit["action_quit()<br/>Exit application"]
            TestConfirm["action_test_confirmbox()<br/>push_screen(TTConfirmBox)"]
        end
    end
    
    KeyPress --> Textual
    Textual --> ActionMethod
    ActionMethod --> ToggleDark
    ActionMethod --> Quit
    ActionMethod --> TestConfirm
```

**Example implementations:**

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:82-88]()

The `action_toggle_dark()` method toggles the `self.dark` boolean property, which Textual uses to switch between light and dark themes.

The `action_test_confirmbox()` method pushes a modal screen onto the screen stack using `push_screen()`.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:82-88]()

---

### Widget-Specific Event Handlers

Widgets can define event handlers using the `@on()` decorator or `on_<event>()` method naming:

[tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:334-348]()

This pattern allows widgets to respond to their own events without action methods.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:266-271](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:334-348]()

---

## Modal Screens

### Pushing Modal Screens

Modal screens overlay the main application and capture input focus. The `push_screen()` method adds a modal to the screen stack:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Modal Screen Lifecycle"
        Trigger["User action triggers modal"]
        Create["Instantiate TTConfirmBox(text, callbacks)"]
        Push["app.push_screen(modal)"]
        Display["Modal displayed"]
        UserInteract["User interacts with modal"]
        Pop["app.pop_screen()"]
        Return["Return to main app"]
    end
    
    Trigger --> Create
    Create --> Push
    Push --> Display
    Display --> UserInteract
    UserInteract --> Pop
    Pop --> Return
```

**Example usage:**

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:86-88]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:86-88]()

---

### Implementing Custom Modals

Modal screens inherit from `textual.screen.ModalScreen` and define their own composition and event handling:

[tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-271]()

Key features:
1. **Grid layout** for structured button placement
2. **Callback parameters** (`on_yes`, `on_no`) for custom actions
3. **Button event handling** via `on_button_pressed()`
4. **Screen management** via `app.pop_screen()`

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "TTConfirmBox Structure"
        ModalScreen["ModalScreen base class"]
        
        subgraph "Initialization"
            Init["__init__(text, on_yes, on_no)"]
            Callbacks["Store callback functions"]
        end
        
        subgraph "Composition"
            Compose["compose() -> ComposeResult"]
            Grid["Grid container"]
            Label["Label with question text"]
            YesBtn["Button id='yes'"]
            NoBtn["Button id='no'"]
        end
        
        subgraph "Event Handling"
            ButtonPressed["on_button_pressed(event)"]
            CheckID{"event.button.id?"}
            CallYes["Call on_yes()"]
            CallNo["Call on_no()"]
            Pop["app.pop_screen()"]
        end
    end
    
    ModalScreen --> Init
    Init --> Callbacks
    Callbacks --> Compose
    Compose --> Grid
    Grid --> Label
    Grid --> YesBtn
    Grid --> NoBtn
    
    YesBtn --> ButtonPressed
    NoBtn --> ButtonPressed
    ButtonPressed --> CheckID
    CheckID -->|yes| CallYes
    CheckID -->|no| CallNo
    CallYes --> Pop
    CallNo --> Pop
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-271]()

### Step-by-Step Implementation

#### 1. Import Required Modules

```python
from textual.app import App, ComposeResult
from textual.containers import Container, Horizontal, Vertical
from textual.widgets import Footer

from tt_tools_common.ui_common.widgets import (
    TTHeader,
    TTFooter,
    TTDataTable,
    TTMenu,
    TTConfirmBox,
)
```

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:8-19]()

---

#### 2. Define App Class with Configuration

Create the application class with bindings and CSS:

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:26-35]()

---

#### 3. Initialize with Custom Properties

Allow customization through constructor parameters:

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:37-49]()

This pattern allows:
- Setting app name and version
- Extending key bindings from parent application
- Calling the Textual `App` superclass constructor

---

#### 4. Compose Widget Hierarchy

Build the layout structure:

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:51-65]()

Layout hierarchy:
- **Top level:** TTHeader
- **Middle level:** Horizontal container
  - Left: Vertical container with two menus
  - Center: TTDataTable
  - Right: One menu
- **Bottom level:** Footer

---

#### 5. Populate Widget Data

Initialize data after composition:

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:67-80]()

This demonstrates:
- Widget retrieval by ID
- Accessing the underlying DataTable

- Timestamp formatting

## Best Practices

### Widget ID Management

Always assign unique IDs to widgets that need programmatic access:

| Pattern | Usage |
|---------|-------|
| `id="menu_1"` | Single widget instance |
| `id=f"menu_{i}"` | Multiple similar widgets |
| `id="dt_example"` | Descriptive names for data tables |
| `id=self.id + "_table"` | Child widget IDs based on parent |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:69-83](), [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:57-64]()

---

### Error Handling in Data Updates

TTDataTable's `update_data()` method handles structural changes gracefully:

[tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:105-113]()

This pattern:
1. Attempts efficient cell-by-cell updates
2. Falls back to full table refresh if structure changed
3. Prevents exceptions from propagating

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:98-113]()

---

### Modal Screen Callbacks

Use callback parameters for flexible modal behavior:

[tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:249-255]()

This allows:
- Reusable modal screens
- Decoupled confirmation logic
- Optional callback handling (checks `if self.on_yes`)

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-271]()

---

### Layout Responsiveness

Leverage Textual's layout system for responsive designs:

| Container | Behavior | Use When |
|-----------|----------|----------|
| `Horizontal()` | Side-by-side, fills width | Multiple columns needed |
| `Vertical()` | Top-to-bottom, fills height | Stacking widgets |
| `Grid()` | Cell-based, fixed structure | Forms, dialogs |
| `ScrollableContainer` | Overflow scrolling | Large content areas |

The CSS controls sizing with `height: 1fr` (fill remaining space) and explicit values.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:55-64](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:45-53]()

---

## Testing Applications

### Unit Testing with pytest

The test suite uses pytest with Textual's async testing support:

[tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:91-103]()

Key patterns:
1. **Fixtures** provide app instances
2. **`@pytest.mark.asyncio`** enables async tests
3. **Assertion checks** verify properties

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:91-103]()

---

### Running the Test App

The test widget app can be run directly for visual testing:

```bash
python -m pytest tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py -v
```

Or interactively (if a `run()` method is added):

```python
if __name__ == "__main__":
    app = TTApp()
    app.run()
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:1-105]()

---

## Integration with Consumer Applications

### Importing tt-tools-common Widgets

Consumer applications (like tt-smi or tt-flash) import widgets as a library:

```python
from tt_tools_common.ui_common.widgets import (
    TTHeader,
    TTFooter,
    TTDataTable,
    TTMenu,
    TTHostCompatibilityMenu,
    TTConfirmBox,
)
```

The widgets are designed for reusability across different Tenstorrent tools.

---

### Extending Widget Behavior

Applications can subclass tt-tools-common widgets to add custom behavior:

```python
class CustomDataTable(TTDataTable):
    def on_mount(self) -> None:
        super().on_mount()
        # Custom initialization
        
    def custom_method(self) -> None:
        # Additional functionality
        pass
```

This pattern maintains the base widget's styling and behavior while adding application-specific features.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:65-117]()

---

## Summary

Building TUI applications with tt-tools-common requires:

1. **Inherit from `textual.app.App`** and set `CSS_PATH` to load common styling
2. **Define `compose()`** to yield widget hierarchy using containers and tt-tools-common widgets
3. **Implement `on_mount()`** to populate widgets with initial data
4. **Configure `BINDINGS`** and `action_*` methods for user interactions
5. **Use modal screens** via `push_screen()` and `pop_screen()` for dialogs
6. **Access widgets by ID** using `get_widget_by_id()` for dynamic updates
7. **Follow layout patterns** with Horizontal/Vertical containers for responsive designs

The test widget application [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py]() demonstrates all these patterns in a working example that can serve as a template for new applications.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_widget_app.py:1-105](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-365](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:1-226]()
2c:T3cce,
# Build and Distribution

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [.github/workflows/build-all.yml](.github/workflows/build-all.yml)
- [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml](.github/workflows/build-debian.yml)
- [.github/workflows/release.yml](.github/workflows/release.yml)
- [debian/changelog](debian/changelog)
- [setup.py](setup.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This page provides an overview of the build and distribution infrastructure for tt-tools-common. It explains the dual-format packaging strategy (Debian `.deb` and Python `.whl`), version management approach, and the automated release pipeline that orchestrates building, testing, and publishing to multiple distribution channels.

For detailed information about specific aspects of the build system, see:
- [Debian Package Build System](#5.1) - Multi-distro `.deb` builds, GPG signing, and packaging
- [Python Package Build](#5.2) - Wheel creation and setuptools configuration  
- [Automated Release Workflow](#5.3) - Version bumping, changelog generation, and release orchestration
- [Publishing to PyPI and TestPyPI](#5.4) - Package upload and OIDC trusted publishing

## Distribution Strategy

tt-tools-common provides two distribution formats to support different installation workflows:

| Format | Target Users | Installation Method | Build Output |
|--------|-------------|---------------------|--------------|
| **Debian Package** | System administrators, production deployments | `apt install tt-tools-common` | `.deb` files for Ubuntu 22.04, 24.04, latest |
| **Python Wheel** | Developers, pip users | `pip install tt-tools-common` | `.whl` files for PyPI |

Both formats are built from the same source tree and share a single version number defined in [`pyproject.toml`](pyproject.toml:1-100)(). The package name `tt-tools-common` is used consistently across both distribution channels.

**Distribution Diagram: Package Flow**

```mermaid
graph LR
    SourceCode["Source Repository<br/>(GitHub)"]
    
    subgraph "Build Outputs"
        DebPkg["Debian Packages<br/>.deb files"]
        PyPkg["Python Wheels<br/>.whl files"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Distribution Channels"
        GitHub["GitHub Releases<br/>release-dists"]
        PyPI["PyPI<br/>pypi.org/p/tt-tools-common"]
        TestPyPI["TestPyPI<br/>test.pypi.org/p/tt-tools-common"]
    end
    
    SourceCode --> DebPkg
    SourceCode --> PyPkg
    
    DebPkg --> GitHub
    PyPkg --> GitHub
    PyPkg --> TestPyPI
    TestPyPI --> PyPI
```

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml](/.github/workflows/release.yml:1-453)(), [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml:1-100)()

## Version Management

Version information is centralized in [`pyproject.toml`](pyproject.toml:1-100)() under the `project.version` key. The version follows semantic versioning (MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH) and serves as the single source of truth for both Debian and Python packages.

### Version Extraction Mechanism

The [`setup.py`](setup.py:1-21)() file provides backward compatibility for older Ubuntu packaging tools that cannot parse `pyproject.toml` directly. It uses the `tomli` library to extract the version:

```python
# setup.py approach
with open("pyproject.toml", "rb") as f:
    toml_data = tomli.load(f)
version = toml_data['project']['version']
```

The release workflow uses `toml-cli` to read and `bump2version` to increment version numbers:

```bash
# Extract current version
package_version=$(toml get project.version --toml-path pyproject.toml)

# Bump version (patch/minor/major)
bump2version --current-version ${package_version} patch pyproject.toml
```

Sources: [setup.py](setup.py:1-21)(), [.github/workflows/release.yml:95-121]()

### Changelog Synchronization

The Debian changelog at [`debian/changelog`](debian/changelog:1-236)() is automatically synchronized with git history using `gbp dch` (git-buildpackage debian changelog):

```bash
gbp dch \
  --debian-branch ${branch} \
  -R \
  -N ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH} \
  --spawn-editor=never
```

This ensures version numbers remain consistent between `pyproject.toml` and `debian/changelog`.

Sources: [debian/changelog](debian/changelog:1-236)(), [.github/workflows/release.yml:203-216](), [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:119-127]()

## Build System Architecture

**Build System Component Diagram**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Workflow Entry Points"

    end
    
    subgraph "Release Orchestration"
        ReleaseWorkflow["release.yml<br/>Main Coordinator"]
        TempBranch["create-temp-branch<br/>rc-temp-SHA-TIMESTAMP"]

        BuildAll["build_all_depends job<br/>build-all.yml"]

        GenerateRelease["generate-release job<br/>GitHub Release"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Build Matrix"
        BuildAllYml["build-all.yml"]
        BuildDebian["build-debian.yml<br/>matrix: ubuntu-22.04/24.04/latest"]
        BuildPyPi["build-pypi.yml<br/>Python wheel"]
    end

        DebArtifacts["*.deb files<br/>*.changes files"]

    end

    CallTrigger --> ReleaseWorkflow

    Changelogs --> BuildAll
    BuildAll --> TagRelease

    BuildAllYml --> BuildDebian
    BuildAllYml --> BuildPyPi

    Changelogs --> Changelog

```

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml](/.github/workflows/release.yml:1-453)(), [.github/workflows/build-all.yml](/.github/workflows/build-all.yml:1-53)()

### Temporary Branch Isolation Pattern

The release workflow uses a temporary branch strategy to isolate version modifications before merging to `main`. This prevents race conditions when multiple release steps modify files:

**Temporary Branch Lifecycle**

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant User
    participant create_temp_branch
    participant versionchange
    participant changelogs
    participant build_all
    participant tagrelease
    participant mergeback
    participant main
    
    User->>create_temp_branch: Trigger release workflow
    create_temp_branch->>create_temp_branch: Generate rc-temp-{SHA}-{TIMESTAMP}
    create_temp_branch->>versionchange: Pass temp branch ref
    versionchange->>versionchange: checkout temp branch
    versionchange->>versionchange: bump2version pyproject.toml
    versionchange->>versionchange: git commit & push
    changelogs->>changelogs: checkout temp branch
    changelogs->>changelogs: gbp dch (generate changelog)
    changelogs->>changelogs: git commit & push
    build_all->>build_all: Build from temp branch
    build_all->>tagrelease: Signal completion
    tagrelease->>tagrelease: git tag vX.Y.Z
    tagrelease->>mergeback: Signal completion
    mergeback->>main: git rebase temp branch
    mergeback->>mergeback: Delete temp branch
```

The temporary branch name format is: `rc-temp-{SHORT_SHA}-{YYYY.MM.DD-HH.MM.SS}`

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:41-62]()

## GitHub Actions Workflows

### Core Workflows

| Workflow | File | Purpose | Trigger |
|----------|------|---------|---------|
| **Create Release** | `release.yml` | Orchestrates entire release process | Manual `workflow_dispatch` |
| **Build All** | `build-all.yml` | Parallel trigger for Debian + Python builds | Called by `release.yml` |
| **Build Ubuntu Packages** | `build-debian.yml` | Matrix build for 3 Ubuntu versions | Called by `build-all.yml` |
| **Build Python Package** | `build-pypi.yml` (referenced) | Creates `.whl` for PyPI | Called by `build-all.yml` |

### Workflow Data Flow

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "release.yml Jobs"
        J1["create-temp-branch<br/>outputs: temp_branch_ref"]
        J2["versionchange<br/>outputs: version_*, git_hash"]
        J3["changelogs<br/>outputs: git_hash"]
        J4["build_all_depends"]
        J5["tagrelease"]
        J6["generate-release"]
        J7["mergeback"]
        J8["publish-to-testpypi"]
        J9["publish-to-pypi"]
    end
    
    J1 --> J2
    J2 --> J3
    J3 --> J4
    J4 --> J5
    J5 --> J6
    J6 --> J7
    J4 --> J8
    J8 --> J9
    
    J2 -.version_major/minor/patch.-> J4
    J1 -.temp_branch_ref.-> J2
    J1 -.temp_branch_ref.-> J3
    J1 -.temp_branch_ref.-> J4
    J3 -.git_hash.-> J5
```

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml](/.github/workflows/release.yml:1-453)()

### Build Matrix Strategy

The Debian build workflow uses a matrix strategy with `fail-fast: false` to build packages for multiple Ubuntu versions independently:

```yaml
strategy:
  fail-fast: false
  matrix:
    os:
      - ubuntu-22.04
      - ubuntu-24.04
      - ubuntu-latest
```

This ensures that a build failure on one Ubuntu version does not block builds for other versions. Each matrix job produces a uniquely-named artifact that includes the distro identifier.

Sources: [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:26-34]()

## Build Dependencies

### Debian Build Dependencies

The Debian build process requires the following system packages:

| Package | Purpose |
|---------|---------|
| `build-essential` | C/C++ compiler toolchain |
| `debhelper` | Debian package building helpers |
| `dh-python` | Python-specific Debian helpers |
| `dh-sequence-python3` | Python3 build sequence |
| `git-buildpackage` | `gbp` tools for changelog generation |
| `gnupg` | GPG signing for package authentication |
| `pybuild-plugin-pyproject` | PEP 517/518 build system support |
| `python3-tomli` | TOML parsing for `pyproject.toml` |

These are installed via `apt` at [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:53-66]().

### Python Build Dependencies

Python builds require:
- `setuptools` - Package building (referenced in `pyproject.toml`)
- `tomli` - TOML parsing (for `setup.py` compatibility)
- `bump2version` - Version incrementing
- `toml-cli` - Command-line TOML manipulation

Sources: [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:53-66](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:95-100](), [setup.py:1-21]()

## Artifact Management

### Artifact Naming Conventions

Debian packages use distro-specific naming to prevent collisions:

```bash
# Original: tt-tools-common_1.6.0_all.deb
# Renamed:  tt-tools-common_1.6.0_all-ubuntu-22.04.deb
```

This renaming occurs at [.github/workflows/release.yml:328-344]() before uploading to GitHub Releases.

### Artifact Collection

The release workflow collects artifacts from multiple sources:

```yaml
files: |
  ${{ github.workspace }}/${{ env.project_name }}*/*.deb
  ${{ github.workspace }}/[!artifacts-]*/*.deb
  ${{ github.workspace }}/*/*.whl
```

This pattern captures:
- `.deb` files from all distro-specific artifact directories
- `.whl` files from Python build artifacts
- Associated `.changes` files for Debian package signatures

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:346-357]()

### Artifact Upload Destinations

| Artifact Type | Immediate Destination | Final Destination |
|--------------|----------------------|-------------------|
| `.deb` files | GitHub Actions artifacts | GitHub Releases (tagged) |
| `.whl` files | GitHub Actions artifacts | TestPyPI → PyPI |
| `.changes` files | GitHub Actions artifacts | GitHub Releases |
| `debian/changelog` | GitHub Actions artifacts | Git repository (committed) |

## GPG Signing

Debian packages are signed using GPG keys stored in GitHub Secrets. The `crazy-max/ghaction-import-gpg` action imports the private key at [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:67-71]():

```yaml
- name: Import GPG key
  uses: crazy-max/ghaction-import-gpg@v6
  with:
    gpg_private_key: ${{ secrets.PKG_SIGNING_KEY_DEB }}
```

The key fingerprint is passed to `gbp buildpackage` via the `DEBSIGN_KEYID` environment variable at [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:128-133]().

Sources: [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:67-71](), [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:128-133]()

## Environment Variables and Outputs

### Release Workflow Outputs

The `versionchange` job produces outputs consumed by downstream jobs:

| Output Variable | Purpose | Example Value |
|----------------|---------|---------------|
| `git_hash` | Commit SHA after version bump | `abc123def456...` |
| `package_name` | Project name from pyproject.toml | `tt-tools-common` |
| `package_version_new` | New version after bump | `1.6.0` |
| `version_major` | Major version component | `1` |
| `version_minor` | Minor version component | `6` |
| `version_patch` | Patch version component | `0` |
| `number_of_commits_since_tag` | Commits since last tag | `5` |

These outputs enable data flow between independent jobs without file system sharing.

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:73-84]()

### Environment Variable Propagation

Version components are propagated through nested workflow calls:

```yaml
build_all_depends:
  uses: ./.github/workflows/build-all.yml
  with:
    ref: ${{ needs.create-temp-branch.outputs.temp_branch_ref }}
    MAJOR: ${{ needs.versionchange.outputs.version_major }}
    MINOR: ${{ needs.versionchange.outputs.version_minor }}
    PATCH: ${{ needs.versionchange.outputs.version_patch }}
    NUMBER_OF_COMMITS_SINCE_TAG: ${{ needs.versionchange.outputs.number_of_commits_since_tag }}
```

This pattern propagates from `release.yml` → `build-all.yml` → `build-debian.yml`.

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:241-253](), [.github/workflows/build-all.yml:34-45]()

## Release Creation

GitHub Releases are created by the `generate-release` job using the `softprops/action-gh-release` action. The release includes:

1. **Auto-generated changelog** from git history using `mikepenz/release-changelog-builder-action`
2. **All build artifacts** (`.deb` and `.whl` files)
3. **Git tag** in format `vX.Y.Z`

The changelog builder uses hybrid mode to capture both PRs and direct commits:

```json
{
  "template": "#{{CHANGELOG}}\
\
## Contributors\
#{{CONTRIBUTORS}}",
  "categories": [
    {
      "title": "## 🔄 Changes",
      "labels": []
    }
  ],
  "pr_template": "- #{{TITLE}} (#{{NUMBER}}) by @#{{AUTHOR}}",
  "commit_template": "- #{{TITLE}} (#{{MERGE_SHA}}) by @#{{AUTHOR}}"
}
```

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:288-357]()

## Compatibility Considerations

### Python Version Support

The minimum Python version is 3.10, enforced in:
- [`pyproject.toml`](pyproject.toml:1-100)() via `requires-python = ">=3.10"`
- [`setup.py:19`](setup.py:19)() via `python_requires=">=3.10"`

This requirement was added at version 1.4.31 as noted in [`debian/changelog:60`](debian/changelog:60)().

### Ubuntu Version Support

The matrix build targets three Ubuntu versions:
- **ubuntu-22.04** (Jammy Jellyfish) - LTS, older packaging tools
- **ubuntu-24.04** (Noble Numbat) - LTS, current recommendation
- **ubuntu-latest** - Rolling latest for future compatibility

The `setup.py` compatibility shim exists specifically for Ubuntu 22.04, which ships with older versions of setuptools that cannot parse modern `pyproject.toml` files directly.

Sources: [setup.py:1-21](), [debian/changelog:60](), [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:31-34]()
