# Debian Package Build System

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml](.github/workflows/build-debian.yml)
- [debian/changelog](debian/changelog)
- [debian/control](debian/control)
- [setup.py](setup.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This document explains the Debian packaging infrastructure for tt-tools-common, covering the multi-distribution build matrix, package configuration files, GPG signing, and artifact generation. The system produces `.deb` packages for multiple Ubuntu versions (22.04, 24.04, and latest) with automated changelog generation and version management.

For Python wheel creation and PyPI publishing, see [Python Package Build](#5.2). For the overall release workflow that orchestrates both Debian and Python builds, see [Automated Release Workflow](#5.3).

---

## Build Matrix Architecture

The Debian build system employs a parallel matrix strategy to generate packages for multiple Ubuntu distributions simultaneously. This ensures compatibility across different LTS releases and accommodates varying toolchain requirements.

### Matrix Configuration

```mermaid
graph TB
    Trigger["workflow_dispatch or workflow_call"]
    
    subgraph "Matrix Strategy"
        Matrix["strategy:<br/>fail-fast: false"]
        Ubuntu2204["ubuntu-22.04<br/>Requires setup.py"]
        Ubuntu2404["ubuntu-24.04<br/>Native pyproject.toml"]
        UbuntuLatest["ubuntu-latest<br/>Bleeding edge"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Parallel Execution"
        Runner2204["GitHub Runner<br/>ubuntu-22.04"]
        Runner2404["GitHub Runner<br/>ubuntu-24.04"]
        RunnerLatest["GitHub Runner<br/>ubuntu-latest"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Artifacts"
        Deb2204["*.deb<br/>*_all-ubuntu-22.04.deb"]
        Changes2204["*.changes<br/>*_amd64-ubuntu-22.04.changes"]
        Deb2404["*.deb<br/>*_all-ubuntu-24.04.deb"]
        Changes2404["*.changes<br/>*_amd64-ubuntu-24.04.changes"]
        DebLatest["*.deb<br/>*_all-ubuntu-latest.deb"]
        ChangesLatest["*.changes<br/>*_amd64-ubuntu-latest.changes"]
    end
    
    Trigger --> Matrix
    Matrix --> Ubuntu2204
    Matrix --> Ubuntu2404
    Matrix --> UbuntuLatest
    
    Ubuntu2204 --> Runner2204
    Ubuntu2404 --> Runner2404
    UbuntuLatest --> RunnerLatest
    
    Runner2204 --> Deb2204
    Runner2204 --> Changes2204
    Runner2404 --> Deb2404
    Runner2404 --> Changes2404
    RunnerLatest --> DebLatest
    RunnerLatest --> ChangesLatest
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:28-34]()

The `fail-fast: false` configuration ensures that build failures in one Ubuntu version do not halt the other builds, allowing partial success and easier debugging of distribution-specific issues.

---

## Debian Package Configuration Files

### Package Metadata and Dependencies

The `debian/control` file defines the source and binary package metadata:

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "debian/control Structure"
        Source["Source: tt-tools-common<br/>Section: utils<br/>Priority: optional"]
        Maintainer["Maintainer:<br/>Sam Bansal"]
        BuildDeps["Build-depends:<br/>- debhelper (>= 10)<br/>- dh-python<br/>- pybuild-plugin-pyproject<br/>- python3-setuptools<br/>- python3-wheel<br/>- python3-all<br/>- python3-pip"]
        BinaryPkg["Package:<br/>python3-tt-tools-common<br/>Architecture: all"]
        RuntimeDeps["Depends:<br/>- python3:Depends<br/>- python3-pyluwen"]
    end
    
    Source --> BuildDeps
    Source --> BinaryPkg
    BinaryPkg --> RuntimeDeps
```

**Sources:** [debian/control:1-36]()

| Field | Value | Purpose |
|-------|-------|---------|
| **Source** | `tt-tools-common` | Package source name |
| **Section** | `utils` | Debian archive section classification |
| **Priority** | `optional` | Installation priority level |
| **Architecture** | `all` | Architecture-independent Python package |
| **Build-depends** | `pybuild-plugin-pyproject` | Modern pyproject.toml build support |
| **Runtime depends** | `python3-pyluwen` | Critical hardware abstraction dependency |

The package depends on `python3-pyluwen` as the sole explicit runtime dependency beyond Python standard libraries, as pyluwen provides the hardware communication layer required by the reset system.

### Version History and Changelog

The `debian/changelog` follows Debian changelog format with structured release entries:

```
tt-tools-common (1.6.0) noble; urgency=medium

  * pyproject.toml- updating version to 1.6.0

 -- Tenstorrent Releases <releases@tenstorrent.com>  Tue, 23 Dec 2025 20:59:35 +0000
```

**Sources:** [debian/changelog:1-5]()

Each entry contains:
- **Version number** in parentheses (e.g., `1.6.0`)
- **Distribution target** (e.g., `noble` for Ubuntu 24.04)
- **Urgency level** (typically `medium`)
- **Change description** with contributor attribution
- **Maintainer signature** with RFC 2822 timestamp

---

## Build Workflow Steps

The build process executes through several distinct phases, each handling specific aspects of package creation.

### Workflow Execution Sequence

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Trigger as "workflow_dispatch/call"
    participant Checkout as "actions/checkout@v4"
    participant GPG as "ghaction-import-gpg@v6"
    participant GBP as "git-buildpackage (gbp)"
    participant Artifacts as "actions/upload-artifact@v4"
    
    Trigger->>Checkout: "Clone repository<br/>ref: inputs.ref<br/>fetch-tags: true<br/>fetch-depth: 0"
    
    Note over Checkout: "Extract version from inputs<br/>or damienaicheh/extract-version-from-tag-action"
    
    Checkout->>GPG: "Import PKG_SIGNING_KEY_DEB"
    GPG-->>GPG: "gpg --list-keys<br/>gpg --list-secret-keys"
    
    GPG->>GBP: "gbp dch<br/>--debian-branch ${ref_name}<br/>-R -N ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}<br/>--spawn-editor=never"
    
    Note over GBP: "Generate debian/changelog<br/>from git commit history"
    
    GBP->>GBP: "gbp buildpackage<br/>--git-ignore-new"
    
    Note over GBP: "DEBSIGN_KEYID from GPG import<br/>Signs .deb and .changes files"
    
    GBP->>Artifacts: "Upload *.deb as<br/>${DEB_FILENAME_DISTRO}"
    GBP->>Artifacts: "Upload *.changes as<br/>${DEB_FILENAME_CHANGES_DISTRO}"
    GBP->>Artifacts: "Upload debian/changelog as<br/>debian-changelog-${DISTRO_IDENT}"
    GBP->>Artifacts: "Upload artifacts/ as<br/>artifacts-${DISTRO_IDENT}.zip"
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:37-178]()

### Dependency Installation

The workflow installs Debian build tools before package creation:

```bash
# From .github/workflows/build-debian.yml:54-66
sudo apt install -y \
  build-essential \      # GCC, make, etc.
  debhelper \            # Debian package helpers
  dh-python \            # Python packaging helpers
  dh-sequence-python3 \  # Python 3 build sequence
  git-buildpackage \     # gbp tooling
  gnupg \                # GPG signing
  libpython3-all-dev \   # Python development headers
  pybuild-plugin-pyproject \ # pyproject.toml support
  python3-all \          # Python 3 interpreters
  python3-pip \          # Package installer
  python3-tomli          # TOML parser for setup.py
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:53-66]()

The `pybuild-plugin-pyproject` package enables native pyproject.toml builds on Ubuntu 24.04 and later, while `python3-tomli` supports the compatibility `setup.py` shim required for Ubuntu 22.04.

---

## GPG Signing Infrastructure

All Debian packages and changes files are cryptographically signed using GPG to ensure authenticity and integrity.

### Signing Process Flow

```mermaid
graph TD
    Secret["GitHub Secret:<br/>PKG_SIGNING_KEY_DEB"]
    
    ImportAction["ghaction-import-gpg@v6<br/>crazy-max/ghaction-import-gpg"]
    
    Keyring["Local GPG Keyring<br/>gpg --list-keys<br/>gpg --list-secret-keys"]
    
    Fingerprint["outputs.fingerprint<br/>$steps.gpg_key_import.outputs.fingerprint"]
    
    EnvVar["DEBSIGN_KEYID<br/>Environment Variable"]
    
    GBP["gbp buildpackage<br/>Automatic signing"]
    
    SignedFiles["Signed Artifacts:<br/>*.deb (signed)<br/>*.changes (signed)"]
    
    Secret --> ImportAction
    ImportAction --> Keyring
    ImportAction --> Fingerprint
    Fingerprint --> EnvVar
    EnvVar --> GBP
    Keyring --> GBP
    GBP --> SignedFiles
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:67-73](), [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:132-133]()

The GPG key import step outputs a fingerprint that is passed to `gbp buildpackage` via the `DEBSIGN_KEYID` environment variable. The build tool automatically signs both the `.deb` binary package and the `.changes` metadata file during package creation.

---

## Version Management and Changelog Generation

Version information flows from multiple sources and is synchronized across package metadata files.

### Version Extraction and Propagation

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Input Sources"
        WorkflowInputs["workflow_call inputs:<br/>MAJOR, MINOR, PATCH<br/>NUMBER_OF_COMMITS_SINCE_TAG"]
        GitTags["Git Tags:<br/>damienaicheh/extract-version-from-tag-action"]
        PyProject["pyproject.toml:<br/>project.version"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Environment Variables"
        EnvMAJOR["$MAJOR"]
        EnvMINOR["$MINOR"]
        EnvPATCH["$PATCH"]
        EnvCommits["$NUMBER_OF_COMMITS_SINCE_TAG"]
        EnvRef["$ref_name"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Tools and Files"
        GBPDch["gbp dch<br/>Changelog generator"]
        DebChangelog["debian/changelog<br/>Debian format"]
        SetupPy["setup.py<br/>tomli.load(pyproject.toml)"]
    end
    
    WorkflowInputs --> EnvMAJOR
    WorkflowInputs --> EnvMINOR
    WorkflowInputs --> EnvPATCH
    WorkflowInputs --> EnvCommits
    GitTags --> EnvMAJOR
    GitTags --> EnvMINOR
    GitTags --> EnvPATCH
    
    EnvMAJOR --> GBPDch
    EnvMINOR --> GBPDch
    EnvPATCH --> GBPDch
    EnvRef --> GBPDch
    
    GBPDch --> DebChangelog
    PyProject --> SetupPy
    
    DebChangelog --> GBP["gbp buildpackage"]
    SetupPy --> GBP
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:80-116](), [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:119-127](), [setup.py:10-20]()

### Changelog Generation Command

The `gbp dch` (git-buildpackage debian changelog) command generates changelog entries from git commit history:

```bash
# From .github/workflows/build-debian.yml:120-124
gbp dch \
  --debian-branch ${ref_name} \    # Target branch
  -R \                              # Release mode (not snapshot)
  -N ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH} \  # New version number
  --spawn-editor=never              # Non-interactive
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:120-124]()

The command parses git commit messages between the current version and HEAD, formatting them into Debian changelog entries. The `EMAIL` and `NAME` environment variables control the maintainer attribution line.

---

## Ubuntu 22.04 Compatibility Layer

Ubuntu 22.04 ships with older packaging tools that lack native pyproject.toml support, requiring a compatibility shim.

### Compatibility Setup Script

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "setup.py Components"
        Shebang["#!/usr/bin/env python3"]
        Imports["import setuptools<br/>import tomli"]
        LoadToml["tomli.load('pyproject.toml')"]
        ExtractVersion["toml_data['project']['version']"]
        SetupCall["setuptools.setup(<br/>name='tt-tools-common'<br/>version=extracted_version<br/>packages=find_packages()<br/>python_requires='>=3.10')"]
    end
    
    Shebang --> Imports
    Imports --> LoadToml
    LoadToml --> ExtractVersion
    ExtractVersion --> SetupCall
```

**Sources:** [setup.py:1-21]()

The `setup.py` script serves exclusively as a fallback for Ubuntu 22.04's `dpkg-buildpackage` tool, which invokes `setup.py` when `pybuild-plugin-pyproject` is unavailable. The script:

1. Loads `pyproject.toml` using the `tomli` library
2. Extracts the version from `toml_data['project']['version']`
3. Passes minimal metadata to `setuptools.setup()`

On Ubuntu 24.04 and later, the `pybuild-plugin-pyproject` package enables direct pyproject.toml consumption, making `setup.py` unused.

---

## Artifact Naming and Collection

Build artifacts follow a structured naming convention to distinguish packages built for different Ubuntu distributions.

### Artifact Naming Transformation

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Original Build Outputs"
        OrigDeb["tt-tools-common_1.6.0_all.deb"]
        OrigChanges["tt-tools-common_1.6.0_amd64.changes"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Environment Variable Extraction"
        DistroIdent["DISTRO_IDENT=$matrix.os<br/>e.g., ubuntu-22.04"]
        BaseDeb["DEB_FILENAME=<br/>basename artifacts/*.deb"]
        DistroSuffix["_all → _all-$DISTRO_IDENT<br/>_amd64 → _amd64-$DISTRO_IDENT"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Renamed Artifacts"
        RenamedDeb["tt-tools-common_1.6.0_all-ubuntu-22.04.deb"]
        RenamedChanges["tt-tools-common_1.6.0_amd64-ubuntu-22.04.changes"]
        Changelog["debian-changelog-ubuntu-22.04"]
        ArtifactZip["artifacts-ubuntu-22.04.zip"]
    end
    
    OrigDeb --> DistroIdent
    OrigChanges --> DistroIdent
    DistroIdent --> BaseDeb
    BaseDeb --> DistroSuffix
    DistroSuffix --> RenamedDeb
    DistroSuffix --> RenamedChanges
    DistroIdent --> Changelog
    DistroIdent --> ArtifactZip
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:143-178]()

### Artifact Upload Table

| Artifact Type | Naming Pattern | Example | Purpose |
|--------------|----------------|---------|---------|
| **Debian Package** | `$DEB_FILENAME_DISTRO` | `tt-tools-common_1.6.0_all-ubuntu-22.04.deb` | Installable binary package |
| **Changes File** | `$DEB_FILENAME_CHANGES_DISTRO` | `tt-tools-common_1.6.0_amd64-ubuntu-22.04.changes` | Package metadata and checksums |
| **Changelog** | `debian-changelog-$DISTRO_IDENT` | `debian-changelog-ubuntu-22.04` | Version history documentation |
| **Full Archive** | `artifacts-$DISTRO_IDENT.zip` | `artifacts-ubuntu-22.04.zip` | Complete artifact bundle |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:143-178]()

The distro identifier is extracted from `${{ matrix.os }}` and appended to artifact names, ensuring that packages from parallel matrix builds do not collide when uploaded to GitHub Actions artifacts or GitHub Releases. The `.changes` file contains cryptographic checksums and build metadata required for Debian repository integration.

---

## Build Package Dependencies

The `gbp buildpackage` process requires specific package dependencies to successfully build and sign Debian packages.

### Dependency Categories

| Category | Packages | Purpose |
|----------|----------|---------|
| **Core Build** | `build-essential`, `debhelper` | Fundamental Debian packaging tools |
| **Python Integration** | `dh-python`, `dh-sequence-python3`, `pybuild-plugin-pyproject` | Python-specific packaging helpers |
| **Python Runtime** | `python3-all`, `python3-pip`, `python3-setuptools`, `python3-wheel` | Python interpreter and packaging tools |
| **Security** | `gnupg` | GPG signing for package authentication |
| **Version Control** | `git-buildpackage` | Git integration for Debian packaging |
| **Development Headers** | `libpython3-all-dev` | Python C extension compilation support |
| **Configuration Parsing** | `python3-tomli` | TOML parser for Ubuntu 22.04 setup.py |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:54-66](), [debian/control:5-13]()

The build dependencies in `debian/control` mirror the runtime installation requirements in the workflow, ensuring that the Debian package can be rebuilt on any system meeting the declared build-depends specifications.

# Python Package Build

<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

## Purpose and Scope

This document covers the Python wheel packaging system for `tt-tools-common`, including the configuration in `pyproject.toml`, setuptools integration, version management, and package data inclusion rules. The build process creates standard Python wheels (`.whl` files) that can be installed via `pip` and published to PyPI.

For Debian package creation, see [Debian Package Build System](#5.1). For the automated release workflow that triggers builds, see [Automated Release Workflow](#5.3). For PyPI publication procedures, see [Publishing to PyPI and TestPyPI](#5.4).

---

## Build System Architecture

The Python package build uses a **PEP 517/518 compliant** build system with `setuptools` as the build backend. The configuration is centralized in `pyproject.toml` with a compatibility shim in `setup.py` for Ubuntu 22.04 packaging tools.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Build Configuration"
        PyProject["pyproject.toml<br/>[project] metadata<br/>[tool.setuptools] config"]
        SetupPy["setup.py<br/>Compatibility layer<br/>Reads pyproject.toml"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Build Tools"
        Pip["pip build"]
        SetupTools["setuptools>=43.0.0"]
        Wheel["wheel builder"]
        Tomli["tomli<br/>TOML parser"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Source Files"
        PythonCode["Python modules<br/>reset_common/<br/>utils_common/<br/>ui_common/"]
        DataFiles["Data files<br/>*.css<br/>data/*/*.yaml"]
        Metadata["Metadata<br/>README.md<br/>LICENSE"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Build Outputs"
        WheelFile["tt_tools_common-X.Y.Z-py3-none-any.whl"]
        SDistFile["tt-tools-common-X.Y.Z.tar.gz"]
    end
    
    PyProject -->|"version = '1.6.0'"| SetupTools
    SetupPy -->|"tomli.load()"| PyProject
    
    Pip --> SetupTools
    SetupTools --> Wheel
    SetupPy --> Tomli
    
    PyProject -->|"[tool.setuptools.packages.find]"| PythonCode
    PyProject -->|"[tool.setuptools.package-data]"| DataFiles
    PyProject -->|"readme/license"| Metadata
    
    PythonCode --> WheelFile
    DataFiles --> WheelFile
    Metadata --> WheelFile
    
    PythonCode --> SDistFile
    DataFiles --> SDistFile
    Metadata --> SDistFile
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:1-84](), [setup.py:1-21]()

---

## pyproject.toml Structure

The `pyproject.toml` file contains all package metadata and build configuration. It follows the PEP 621 standard for project metadata.

### Project Metadata

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Project Section [project]"
        Name["name = 'tt-tools-common'"]
        Version["version = '1.6.0'"]
        PythonReq["requires-python = '>=3.10'"]
        Desc["description<br/>readme<br/>license"]
        Authors["authors/maintainers<br/>Sam Bansal"]
        Classifiers["classifiers[]<br/>Beta status<br/>Python 3.10/3.11"]
    end
    
    subgraph "URL References [project.urls]"
        Homepage["Homepage"]
        BugReports["Bug Reports"]
        Source["Source"]
    end
    
    Name --> Version
    Version --> PythonReq
    PythonReq --> Desc
    Desc --> Authors
    Authors --> Classifiers
    Classifiers --> Homepage
```

| Field | Value | Purpose |
|-------|-------|---------|
| `name` | `"tt-tools-common"` | Package name on PyPI |
| `version` | `"1.6.0"` | Single source of truth for version |
| `requires-python` | `">=3.10"` | Minimum Python version requirement |
| `description` | `"Common library for Tenstorrent tooling"` | Short package description |
| `readme` | `"README.md"` | Path to long description |
| `license` | `{file = "LICENSE"}` | Apache 2.0 license file |
| `authors` | Sam Bansal | Primary contact |

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:1-22]()

### Python Version Compatibility

The package requires **Python 3.10 or higher** to leverage modern language features:

- Pattern matching (match/case statements)
- Improved type hints (e.g., `X | Y` union syntax)
- Structural pattern matching in error handling

The classifiers explicitly list supported versions:
- `Programming Language :: Python :: 3.10`
- `Programming Language :: Python :: 3.11`
- `Programming Language :: Python :: 3 :: Only`

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:3,18-21]()

## Package Data Inclusion

The build system uses `setuptools` package discovery with explicit inclusion rules for non-Python files.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Package Discovery [tool.setuptools.packages.find]"
        Where["where = ['.']<br/>Search current directory"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Include Rules [tool.setuptools.package-data]"
        CSS["*.css<br/>Theme files"]
        YAMLLevel1["data/*/*.yaml<br/>Chip definitions"]
        YAMLLevel2["data/*/*/*.yaml<br/>Nested configs"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Exclude Rules [tool.setuptools.exclude-package-data]"
        Build["build/<br/>Build artifacts"]
        Debian["debian/<br/>Packaging files"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Final Wheel Contents"
        ResetCommon["reset_common/"]
        UtilsCommon["utils_common/"]
        UICommon["ui_common/<br/>+ *.css files"]
        Data["data/<br/>+ *.yaml files"]
    end
    
    Where --> ResetCommon
    Where --> UtilsCommon
    Where --> UICommon
    Where --> Data
    
    CSS --> UICommon
    YAMLLevel1 --> Data
    YAMLLevel2 --> Data
    
    Build -.exclude.-> ResetCommon
    Debian -.exclude.-> ResetCommon
```

### Package Discovery Configuration

The `[tool.setuptools.packages.find]` section controls automatic package discovery:

```toml
[tool.setuptools.packages.find]
where = [ ".", ]
```

This searches the current directory for all Python packages (directories with `__init__.py`).

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:71-72]()

### Package Data Configuration

The `[tool.setuptools.package-data]` section includes non-Python files:

```toml
[tool.setuptools.package-data]
"*" = [
  "*.css",
  "data/*/*.yaml",
  "data/*/*/*.yaml",
]
```

This includes:
- **CSS files** for Textual theming (e.g., `ui_common/common_style.css`)
- **YAML files** in `data/` subdirectories (e.g., `data/blackhole/fw_defines.yaml`)
- **Nested YAML files** for chip-specific configurations

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:58-63]()

### Exclusion Rules

The `[tool.setuptools.exclude-package-data]` section prevents build artifacts from being packaged:

```toml
[tool.setuptools.exclude-package-data]
"*" = [
  'build',
  'debian',
]
```

This excludes:
- **`build/`** directory created during wheel generation
- **`debian/`** directory containing Debian packaging files

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:65-69]()

## Version Management

Version management uses a **single source of truth** approach with manual versioning in `pyproject.toml`.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Version Source"
        PyProjectVersion["pyproject.toml<br/>version = '1.6.0'"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Version Consumers"
        SetupPy["setup.py<br/>tomli.load()"]
        BuildMeta["setuptools.build_meta<br/>Reads [project]"]
        WheelFilename["Wheel filename<br/>tt_tools_common-1.6.0-py3-none-any.whl"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Release Process"
        Bump2Version["bump2version<br/>Automated increment"]
        GitTag["Git tag<br/>v1.6.0"]
        GbpDch["gbp dch<br/>Debian changelog"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Runtime Access"
        ModuleImport["import tt_tools_common<br/>__version__ attribute"]
    end
    
    PyProjectVersion --> SetupPy
    PyProjectVersion --> BuildMeta
    BuildMeta --> WheelFilename
    
    Bump2Version -->|"updates"| PyProjectVersion
    PyProjectVersion --> GitTag
    GitTag --> GbpDch
    
    WheelFilename --> ModuleImport
```

### Version Format

The version follows **semantic versioning** (MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH):
- `version = "1.6.0"` in [pyproject.toml:4]()

### Version Extraction in setup.py

The `setup.py` compatibility layer reads the version from `pyproject.toml`:

```python
# setup.py:11-17
with open("pyproject.toml", "rb") as f:
    toml_data = tomli.load(f)

setup(
    name="tt-tools-common",
    version=toml_data['project']['version'],
    ...
)
```

This ensures version consistency when using Ubuntu 22.04 packaging tools that require `setup.py`.

**Sources:** [setup.py:11-17]()

### Version Extraction in CI

The Debian build workflow extracts version components from Git tags using `damienaicheh/extract-version-from-tag-action`:

```yaml
# .github/workflows/build-debian.yml:80-81
- name: Extract version from tag
  uses: damienaicheh/extract-version-from-tag-action@v1.3.0
```

This populates environment variables:
- `$MAJOR` - Major version number
- `$MINOR` - Minor version number
- `$PATCH` - Patch version number
- `$NUMBER_OF_COMMITS_SINCE_TAG` - Distance from last tag

These are used by `gbp dch` to generate Debian changelogs with proper versioning.

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:80-107]()

The build system uses the standard `setuptools.build_meta` backend with PEP 517/518 compliance.

```mermaid

    subgraph "Build System Declaration [build-system]"

    SetuptoolsBuildMeta --> WheelBuilder
    
    WheelBuilder --> Wheel
    WheelBuilder --> SDist
```

### Build Requirements

The `[build-system]` section declares build-time dependencies:

```toml
[build-system]
requires = [
  "setuptools>=43.0.0",
  "wheel"
]
build-backend = "setuptools.build_meta"
```

- **`setuptools>=43.0.0`** - Minimum version for PEP 517/518 support
- **`wheel`** - Required for wheel file generation
- **`setuptools.build_meta`** - PEP 517 compliant build backend

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:74-81]()

### Build Commands

To build the package locally:

```bash
# Install build dependencies
pip install build

# Create wheel and source distribution
python -m build

# Output files in dist/:
# - tt_tools_common-1.6.0-py3-none-any.whl
# - tt-tools-common-1.6.0.tar.gz
```

The wheel is a **universal wheel** (`py3-none-any`) indicating:
- **py3** - Python 3 compatible
- **none** - No ABI requirements
- **any** - Platform-independent

## Compatibility Layer: setup.py

The `setup.py` file exists solely for compatibility with Ubuntu 22.04 Debian packaging tools that don't fully support PEP 517.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Legacy Packaging Tools"
        GbpBuildpackage["gbp buildpackage<br/>Ubuntu 22.04"]
        Debhelper["debhelper<br/>dh_python3"]
    end
    
    subgraph "setup.py Shim"
        SetupPyEntry["setup.py<br/>Entry point"]
        TomliImport["import tomli"]
        LoadToml["with open('pyproject.toml', 'rb')"]
        ExtractData["toml_data['project']['version']"]
        SetupCall["setup(name=..., version=...)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Modern Build"
        PyProjectOnly["pyproject.toml only<br/>PEP 517 compliant"]
    end
    
    GbpBuildpackage --> SetupPyEntry
    Debhelper --> SetupPyEntry
    
    SetupPyEntry --> TomliImport
    TomliImport --> LoadToml
    LoadToml --> ExtractData
    ExtractData --> SetupCall
    
    SetupCall -.fallback.-> PyProjectOnly
```

### Implementation Details

The `setup.py` file is minimal and delegates to `pyproject.toml`:

```python
# setup.py:1-21
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Compatibility setup.py for Ubuntu 22.04 packaging tools.
Uses setuptools_scm for dynamic versioning from git tags.
"""
from setuptools import setup, find_packages
import tomli

if __name__ == "__main__":
    with open("pyproject.toml", "rb") as f:
        toml_data = tomli.load(f)

    setup(
        name="tt-tools-common",
        version=toml_data['project']['version'],
        packages=find_packages(),
        python_requires=">=3.10",
    )
```

**Key points:**
- **Reads version from `pyproject.toml`** to maintain single source of truth
- **Uses `tomli`** for TOML parsing (Python <3.11 compatibility)
- **Minimal configuration** - only what's required for legacy tools
- **Delegates package discovery** to `find_packages()`

**When this is used:**
- Debian package builds on Ubuntu 22.04 via `gbp buildpackage`
- Systems with older packaging tools that don't support PEP 517

**When this is NOT used:**
- Modern `pip install` operations (uses `pyproject.toml` directly)
- GitHub Actions Python package builds (uses `setuptools.build_meta`)
- Manual `python -m build` commands (PEP 517 compliant)

**Sources:** [setup.py:1-21]()

---

## Pytest Configuration

The `pyproject.toml` also contains pytest configuration for test discovery and markers:

```toml
[tool.pytest.ini_options]
markers = [
  "requires_hardware: marks tests as requiring Tenstorrent hardware"
]
```

This defines the `@pytest.mark.requires_hardware` decorator used to skip hardware-dependent tests in CI environments without physical devices.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:50-53]()

---

## Build Artifacts

The Python build process creates two types of distribution artifacts:

| Artifact Type | Filename Pattern | Contents | Use Case |
|---------------|------------------|----------|----------|
| **Wheel** | `tt_tools_common-1.6.0-py3-none-any.whl` | Pre-built package with all files | Fast installation via `pip install` |
| **Source Distribution** | `tt-tools-common-1.6.0.tar.gz` | Raw source code + metadata | Building from source, auditing |

### Wheel Structure

The wheel contains:
```
tt_tools_common-1.6.0.dist-info/
  - METADATA (package metadata)
  - WHEEL (wheel format metadata)
  - RECORD (file checksums)
  - LICENSE
  - top_level.txt

reset_common/
  - __init__.py
  - *.py files

utils_common/
  - __init__.py
  - *.py files

ui_common/
  - __init__.py
  - *.py files
  - common_style.css

data/
  - blackhole/fw_defines.yaml
  - wormhole/fw_defines.yaml
  - grayskull/*.yaml
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:55-72]()

---

## Summary

The Python package build system for `tt-tools-common` uses:

1. **`pyproject.toml`** as the single configuration source (PEP 621 compliant)
2. **`setup.py`** as a compatibility shim for Ubuntu 22.04 tools
3. **`setuptools.build_meta`** as the PEP 517 build backend
4. **Manual version management** in `pyproject.toml` (`version = "1.6.0"`)
5. **Explicit package data rules** to include CSS and YAML files
6. **Python 3.10+ requirement** for modern language features
7. **Universal wheel format** (`py3-none-any`) for platform independence

The build outputs are consumed by:
- **PyPI** for pip installation
- **GitHub Releases** for artifact storage
- **TestPyPI** for pre-release validation

For release automation, see [Automated Release Workflow](#5.3). For Debian packaging, see [Debian Package Build System](#5.1).

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:1-84](), [setup.py:1-21]()

# Automated Release Workflow

## Purpose and Scope

This document explains the automated release workflow that manages version bumping, changelog generation, artifact building, and publication to multiple distribution channels (GitHub Releases, PyPI, TestPyPI, and Debian repositories). The workflow implements a temporary branch isolation pattern to safely modify version files and generate changelogs before merging back to the main branch.

For information about building Debian packages specifically, see [Debian Package Build System](#5.1). For Python package building details, see [Python Package Build](#5.2). For PyPI publication mechanics, see [Publishing to PyPI and TestPyPI](#5.4).

## Workflow Overview

The release workflow is defined in [.github/workflows/release.yml:1-453]() and can be triggered manually via `workflow_dispatch` with a required input parameter specifying the version bump type (patch, minor, or major). The workflow orchestrates seven sequential jobs that collectively handle all aspects of creating and publishing a new release.

| Job Name | Primary Responsibility | Key Dependencies |
|----------|----------------------|------------------|
| `create-temp-branch` | Creates isolation branch `rc-temp-<sha>-<timestamp>` | None |
| `versionchange` | Bumps version in `pyproject.toml` using `bump2version` | `create-temp-branch` |
| `changelogs` | Generates `debian/changelog` using `gbp dch` | `versionchange` |
| `build_all_depends` | Orchestrates Debian and Python builds | `changelogs` |
| `tagrelease` | Creates Git tag `v<version>` | `build_all_depends` |
| `generate-release` | Creates GitHub Release with artifacts | `tagrelease` |
| `mergeback` | Merges temp branch to main and deletes temp branch | `generate-release` |

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:1-453]()

## Workflow Trigger and Inputs

The workflow can be triggered manually through the GitHub Actions UI or programmatically via workflow calls. The version bump type determines which semantic version component gets incremented.

```yaml
workflow_dispatch:
  inputs:
    version_bump_type:
      description: 'Version bump type'
      required: true
      default: 'patch'
      type: choice
      options:
        - patch
        - minor
        - major
```

The `version_bump_type` parameter is passed to the `bump2version` command in [.github/workflows/release.yml:116-121](), which modifies [pyproject.toml]() according to semantic versioning rules:

- **patch**: Increments the patch version (1.4.32 → 1.4.33)
- **minor**: Increments the minor version, resets patch (1.4.32 → 1.5.0)
- **major**: Increments the major version, resets minor and patch (1.4.32 → 2.0.0)

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:4-16]()

## Temporary Branch Isolation Pattern

The workflow implements a temporary branch strategy to isolate version changes and changelog generation before merging to main. This prevents conflicts and ensures atomic commits.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Main["main branch<br/>(original state)"]
    TempCreate["create-temp-branch job<br/>Creates rc-temp-{sha}-{timestamp}"]
    TempBranch["rc-temp branch<br/>(isolated workspace)"]
    VersionCommit["Version bump commit<br/>pyproject.toml update"]
    ChangelogCommit["Changelog commit<br/>debian/changelog update"]
    BuildArtifacts["Build artifacts<br/>(debs and whls)"]
    TagRelease["Git tag creation<br/>v{version}"]
    MergeBack["Rebase and merge<br/>back to main"]
    DeleteTemp["Delete temp branch"]
    
    Main --> TempCreate
    TempCreate --> TempBranch
    TempBranch --> VersionCommit
    VersionCommit --> ChangelogCommit
    ChangelogCommit --> BuildArtifacts
    BuildArtifacts --> TagRelease
    TagRelease --> MergeBack
    MergeBack --> DeleteTemp
    DeleteTemp --> Main
```

The temporary branch name is generated using the current Git SHA and timestamp in [.github/workflows/release.yml:54-58]():

```bash
rc-temp-$( git rev-parse --short HEAD )-$( date +%Y.%m.%d-%H.%M.%S )
```

This naming convention ensures uniqueness and provides context about when and from which commit the release was initiated.

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:41-62]()

## Version Management System

Version management centralizes on `pyproject.toml` as the single source of truth. The workflow extracts the current version, bumps it, and propagates the new version to all subsequent jobs.

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    ExtractCurrent["Extract current version<br/>toml-cli reads pyproject.toml"]
    BumpVersion["bump2version<br/>Modifies pyproject.toml"]
    ExtractNew["Extract new version<br/>toml-cli reads updated file"]
    ParseSemver["Parse components<br/>release-kit/semver@v2"]
    OutputVars["Output variables:<br/>package_version_new<br/>version_major<br/>version_minor<br/>version_patch"]
    
    ExtractCurrent --> BumpVersion
    BumpVersion --> ExtractNew
    ExtractNew --> ParseSemver
    ParseSemver --> OutputVars
```

The version extraction uses `toml-cli` in [.github/workflows/release.yml:102-107]():

```bash
package_version="$( toml get project.version --toml-path pyproject.toml )"
```

The `bump2version` tool modifies the version in place in [.github/workflows/release.yml:115-121](). After bumping, the workflow commits the change with a standardized message format in [.github/workflows/release.yml:145-149]():

```bash
git commit pyproject.toml -m "pyproject.toml- updating version to ${package_version_new}"
```

The workflow also calculates the number of commits since the last tag in [.github/workflows/release.yml:138-142](), which is used for Debian package versioning.

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:64-160]()

## Changelog Generation

The changelog generation job uses `gbp dch` (Git-Buildpackage Debian Changelog) to automatically generate `debian/changelog` entries from Git commit history.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    CheckoutTemp["Checkout temp branch<br/>fetch-tags: true<br/>fetch-depth: 0"]
    InstallGbp["Install git-buildpackage<br/>apt install"]
    RunGbp["Execute gbp dch<br/>--debian-branch {temp_branch}<br/>-R (release)<br/>-N {version}<br/>--spawn-editor=never"]
    CommitChangelog["Commit debian/changelog<br/>push to temp branch"]
    
    CheckoutTemp --> InstallGbp
    InstallGbp --> RunGbp
    RunGbp --> CommitChangelog
```

The `gbp dch` command in [.github/workflows/release.yml:209-213]() uses several key flags:

- `--debian-branch`: Specifies the temporary branch to work from
- `-R`: Marks this as a release (not a snapshot)
- `-N ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH}`: Sets the version number explicitly
- `--spawn-editor=never`: Runs non-interactively

The generated changelog follows Debian conventions as shown in [debian/changelog:1-236](). Each entry includes:
- Version number with distribution target (`noble`)
- Commit messages grouped by author
- Timestamp in RFC 2822 format
- Maintainer information from environment variables

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:165-237]()

## Build Orchestration

After version and changelog updates, the workflow triggers the `build-all.yml` workflow to create artifacts for all distribution targets.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    TriggerBuild["build_all_depends job<br/>workflow_call to build-all.yml"]
    PassInputs["Pass inputs:<br/>ref: temp_branch_ref<br/>MAJOR, MINOR, PATCH<br/>NUMBER_OF_COMMITS_SINCE_TAG"]
    BuildAllOrch["build-all.yml orchestration<br/>Parallel build triggers"]
    
    subgraph "Parallel Builds"
        BuildDebian["builddebian job<br/>→ build-debian.yml<br/>Ubuntu 22.04/24.04/latest"]
        BuildPyPI["buildpypi job<br/>→ build-pypi.yml<br/>Python wheels"]
    end
    
    ArtifactsDebian["Debian artifacts:<br/>.deb files<br/>.changes files"]
    ArtifactsWheel["Python artifacts:<br/>.whl files<br/>Source distribution"]
    
    TriggerBuild --> PassInputs
    PassInputs --> BuildAllOrch
    BuildAllOrch --> BuildDebian
    BuildAllOrch --> BuildPyPI
    BuildDebian --> ArtifactsDebian
    BuildPyPI --> ArtifactsWheel
```

The workflow call in [.github/workflows/release.yml:241-253]() passes the temporary branch reference and version components to [.github/workflows/build-all.yml:1-53](), which then dispatches to:

1. **build-debian.yml** - Creates Debian packages for multiple Ubuntu versions with matrix builds
2. **build-pypi.yml** - Builds Python wheel packages

Both build workflows upload their artifacts using GitHub Actions artifact storage, making them available for the release creation job.

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:241-253](), [.github/workflows/build-all.yml:1-53]()

## Git Tag Creation

After successful builds, the `tagrelease` job creates an annotated Git tag pointing to the changelog commit.

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    CheckoutSha["Checkout changelog commit<br/>ref: changelogs.outputs.git_hash"]
    CreateTag["Create Git tag<br/>git tag v{package_version_new}"]
    PushTag["Push tags<br/>git push --tags"]
    
    CheckoutSha --> CreateTag
    CreateTag --> PushTag
```

The tag creation in [.github/workflows/release.yml:279-283]() follows semantic versioning with a `v` prefix:

```bash
git tag v${{ needs.versionchange.outputs.package_version_new }}
git push --tags
```

This tag becomes the permanent reference point for the release and is used by subsequent jobs to identify the release version.

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:257-283]()

## GitHub Release Creation

The `generate-release` job downloads all build artifacts, generates a changelog from Git history, and creates a GitHub Release with attached files.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    DownloadArtifacts["actions/download-artifact@v4<br/>Downloads all artifacts"]
    BuildChangelog["mikepenz/release-changelog-builder-action@v5<br/>Generates changelog from commits/PRs"]
    RenameDebs["Rename .deb files<br/>Add distribution prefix to filenames"]
    FindFiles["Locate all .deb and .whl files<br/>Multiple artifact directories"]
    CreateRelease["softprops/action-gh-release@v1<br/>tag_name: v{version}<br/>Upload files"]
    
    DownloadArtifacts --> BuildChangelog
    BuildChangelog --> RenameDebs
    RenameDebs --> FindFiles
    FindFiles --> CreateRelease
```

The changelog builder in [.github/workflows/release.yml:305-321]() uses a hybrid mode that includes both pull requests and direct commits. The template formats entries with author attribution:

```json
{
  "template": "#{{CHANGELOG}}\
\
## Contributors\
#{{CONTRIBUTORS}}",
  "pr_template": "- #{{TITLE}} (#{{NUMBER}}) by @#{{AUTHOR}}",
  "commit_template": "- #{{TITLE}} (#{{MERGE_SHA}}) by @#{{AUTHOR}}"
}
```

The .deb file renaming logic in [.github/workflows/release.yml:328-344]() prepends the distribution name to prevent filename collisions when multiple Ubuntu versions are built.

The release creation in [.github/workflows/release.yml:346-357]() uploads files matching these patterns:

- `${{ github.workspace }}/${{ env.project_name }}*/*.deb`
- `${{ github.workspace }}/[!artifacts-]*/*.deb`
- `${{ github.workspace }}/*/*.whl`

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:288-357]()

## PyPI Publication Strategy

The workflow implements a staged publication strategy that validates packages on TestPyPI before publishing to production PyPI.

```mermaid
flowchart LR
    BuildComplete["Build artifacts available<br/>release-dists artifact"]
    DownloadTest["Download to dist/ directory<br/>publish-to-testpypi job"]
    PublishTest["pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish@release/v1<br/>repository-url: test.pypi.org<br/>OIDC trusted publishing"]
    ValidateTest["Manual validation<br/>(test installation)"]
    DownloadProd["Download to dist/ directory<br/>publish-to-pypi job"]
    PublishProd["pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish@release/v1<br/>repository-url: pypi.org<br/>OIDC trusted publishing"]
    
    BuildComplete --> DownloadTest
    DownloadTest --> PublishTest
    PublishTest --> ValidateTest
    ValidateTest --> DownloadProd
    DownloadProd --> PublishProd
```

Both publication jobs use OIDC trusted publishing, which requires specific permissions in [.github/workflows/release.yml:404-405]() and [.github/workflows/release.yml:439]():

```yaml
permissions:
  id-token: write  # IMPORTANT: mandatory for trusted publishing
```

The TestPyPI publication job in [.github/workflows/release.yml:391-419]() publishes to the test environment, allowing verification before production deployment. The production PyPI publication in [.github/workflows/release.yml:424-452]() depends on successful TestPyPI publication.

Both jobs download artifacts using the pattern `${{ env.project_name }}*.whl` to collect all built wheel files.

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:391-452]()

## Merge Back Strategy

The final job merges the temporary branch back to main using rebase to maintain a linear history, then deletes the temporary branch.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    CheckoutMain["Checkout main branch<br/>fetch-tags: true<br/>fetch-depth: 0"]
    RebaseTemp["git rebase origin/{temp_branch}"]
    PullRebase["git pull --rebase"]
    PushMain["git push to main"]
    DeleteTemp["git push origin --delete {temp_branch}"]
    
    CheckoutMain --> RebaseTemp
    RebaseTemp --> PullRebase
    PullRebase --> PushMain
    PushMain --> DeleteTemp
```

The merge back sequence in [.github/workflows/release.yml:380-386]() uses rebase instead of merge to avoid merge commits:

```bash
git rebase origin/${{ needs.create-temp-branch.outputs.temp_branch_ref }}
git pull --rebase
git push
git push origin --delete ${{ needs.create-temp-branch.outputs.temp_branch_ref }}
```

This ensures the version bump and changelog commits appear as direct commits on main, maintaining a clean linear history.

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:362-386]()

## Complete Release Flow

The following diagram shows the complete release workflow with all jobs, their dependencies, and key artifacts produced.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["Manual trigger<br/>workflow_dispatch<br/>version_bump_type input"]
    
    TempBranch["create-temp-branch<br/>Creates rc-temp-{sha}-{timestamp}<br/>Output: temp_branch_ref"]
    
    VersionChange["versionchange<br/>bump2version on pyproject.toml<br/>Outputs: package_version_new<br/>version_major/minor/patch<br/>git_hash"]
    
    Changelog["changelogs<br/>gbp dch generates debian/changelog<br/>Commit and push<br/>Output: git_hash"]
    
    BuildAll["build_all_depends<br/>Calls build-all.yml workflow<br/>Passes: ref, version components"]
    
    subgraph "Parallel Build Jobs (in build-all.yml)"
        BuildDebian["builddebian<br/>→ build-debian.yml<br/>Matrix: Ubuntu 22.04/24.04/latest"]
        BuildPyPI["buildpypi<br/>→ build-pypi.yml<br/>Python wheels"]
    end
    
    TagRelease["tagrelease<br/>git tag v{version}<br/>git push --tags"]
    
    GenRelease["generate-release<br/>Download artifacts<br/>Build changelog from git history<br/>Create GitHub Release<br/>Upload .deb and .whl files"]
    
    TestPyPI["publish-to-testpypi<br/>pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish<br/>repository-url: test.pypi.org<br/>Environment: testpypi<br/>OIDC authentication"]
    
    PyPI["publish-to-pypi<br/>pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish<br/>repository-url: pypi.org<br/>Environment: pypi<br/>OIDC authentication"]
    
    MergeBack["mergeback<br/>git rebase temp branch to main<br/>Delete temp branch"]
    
    Start --> TempBranch
    TempBranch --> VersionChange
    VersionChange --> Changelog
    Changelog --> BuildAll
    BuildAll --> BuildDebian
    BuildAll --> BuildPyPI
    BuildDebian --> TagRelease
    BuildPyPI --> TagRelease
    TagRelease --> GenRelease
    GenRelease --> TestPyPI
    GenRelease --> PyPI
    TestPyPI --> PyPI
    PyPI --> MergeBack
```

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:1-453]()

## Workflow Environment Variables

The workflow uses a centralized environment variable for the project name in [.github/workflows/release.yml:18-19]():

```yaml
env:
  project_name: tt-tools-common
```

This variable is referenced throughout the workflow for:
- Artifact path construction
- File pattern matching
- PyPI project URL generation
- GitHub Release file uploads

Job-specific environments set Git configuration:
- `EMAIL: releases@tenstorrent.com`
- `NAME: Tenstorrent Releases`

These credentials are used for automated commits during version bumping and changelog generation.

Sources: [.github/workflows/release.yml:18-19](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:158-160](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:214-216](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:228-230]()

# Publishing to PyPI and TestPyPI

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [.github/workflows/build-all.yml](.github/workflows/build-all.yml)
- [.github/workflows/release.yml](.github/workflows/release.yml)
- [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml)

</details>



This document describes the automated publishing process for distributing `tt-tools-common` Python packages to PyPI (Python Package Index) and TestPyPI (PyPI's testing instance). The system uses GitHub Actions with OIDC-based trusted publishing to securely upload wheel distributions without requiring manual credential management.

For information about building Python wheel packages, see [Python Package Build](#5.2). For the overall release workflow orchestration, see [Automated Release Workflow](#5.3). For Debian package distribution, see [Debian Package Build System](#5.1).

## Publishing Architecture

The publishing system implements a two-stage validation pattern where packages are first published to TestPyPI for validation, then promoted to production PyPI only after successful staging deployment.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    BuildJob["build_all_depends job<br/>(build-all.yml)"]
    ReleaseJob["generate-release job<br/>(release.yml)"]
    
    BuildJob --> WhlArtifacts["Wheel Artifacts<br/>tt-tools-common*.whl"]
    ReleaseJob --> ReadyForPublish["GitHub Release Created"]
    
    WhlArtifacts --> DownloadTest["Download Artifacts<br/>actions/download-artifact@v4"]
    ReadyForPublish --> DownloadTest
    
    DownloadTest --> TestPyPIJob["publish-to-testpypi<br/>Environment: testpypi"]
    
    TestPyPIJob --> OIDCTest["OIDC Token Exchange<br/>id-token: write"]
    OIDCTest --> PublishTest["pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish<br/>repository-url: test.pypi.org"]
    
    PublishTest --> ValidationGate["Validation Gate<br/>Manual/Automated Check"]
    
    ValidationGate --> DownloadProd["Download Artifacts<br/>actions/download-artifact@v4"]
    DownloadProd --> PyPIJob["publish-to-pypi<br/>Environment: pypi"]
    
    PyPIJob --> OIDCProd["OIDC Token Exchange<br/>id-token: write"]
    OIDCProd --> PublishProd["pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish<br/>Default PyPI URL"]
    
    PublishProd --> LivePackage["Live on PyPI<br/>pip install tt-tools-common"]
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:391-453]()

## Trusted Publishing with OIDC

The publishing process uses PyPI's trusted publishing mechanism, which leverages OpenID Connect (OIDC) tokens to authenticate GitHub Actions workflows without requiring stored API tokens or passwords.

### Authentication Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant GHA as "GitHub Actions Workflow"
    participant GHOIDC as "GitHub OIDC Provider"
    participant PyPI as "PyPI/TestPyPI"
    participant Package as "Package Repository"
    
    GHA->>GHA: "Job starts with<br/>id-token: write permission"
    GHA->>GHOIDC: "Request OIDC token"
    GHOIDC->>GHA: "Issue JWT token<br/>(org, repo, workflow claims)"
    
    GHA->>PyPI: "Upload package<br/>+ OIDC token"
    PyPI->>PyPI: "Verify token signature<br/>Validate claims"
    PyPI->>PyPI: "Match to configured publisher<br/>(owner/repo/workflow)"
    
    alt Valid Token
        PyPI->>Package: "Store package"
        Package->>PyPI: "Success"
        PyPI->>GHA: "Upload successful"
    else Invalid Token
        PyPI->>GHA: "Authentication failed"
    end
```

**Key Configuration Requirements:**

| Requirement | Configuration | Location |
|-------------|---------------|----------|
| **Permission** | `id-token: write` | Job-level permissions |
| **Environment** | `testpypi` or `pypi` | Job environment name |
| **Publisher Config** | Repository name, workflow file, environment | PyPI project settings |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:404-405](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:438-439]()

## TestPyPI Publishing Job

The `publish-to-testpypi` job validates package integrity by publishing to PyPI's staging instance before production release.

### Job Configuration

```yaml
Job: publish-to-testpypi
Depends On: build_all_depends, generate-release
Runner: ubuntu-latest
Environment: testpypi
URL: https://test.pypi.org/p/tt-tools-common
```

### Implementation Details

The job executes three key steps:

1. **Artifact Download**: Retrieves wheel files built by the `buildpypi` workflow using pattern matching for `tt-tools-common*.whl` artifacts stored under the `release-dists` artifact name.

2. **Distribution Organization**: Places downloaded `.whl` files into a `dist/` directory, which is the default location expected by the PyPI publishing action.

3. **Upload Execution**: Invokes `pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish@release/v1` with TestPyPI repository URL and verbose logging enabled.

**Artifact Download Pattern:**
```
Pattern: tt-tools-common*.whl
Name: release-dists
Path: dist/
```

**Repository URL Configuration:**
```
repository-url: https://test.pypi.org/legacy/
verbose: true
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:391-420]()

## PyPI Production Publishing Job

The `publish-to-pypi` job performs the production release after successful TestPyPI validation.

### Job Configuration

```yaml
Job: publish-to-pypi
Depends On: build_all_depends, generate-release, publish-to-testpypi
Runner: ubuntu-latest
Environment: pypi
URL: https://pypi.org/p/tt-tools-common
```

### Dependency Chain

```mermaid
graph LR
    BuildAll["build_all_depends"]
    GenRelease["generate-release"]
    TestPyPI["publish-to-testpypi"]
    PyPI["publish-to-pypi"]
    
    BuildAll --> TestPyPI
    GenRelease --> TestPyPI
    TestPyPI --> PyPI
    BuildAll --> PyPI
    GenRelease --> PyPI
```

The production job includes `publish-to-testpypi` in its dependency list, ensuring TestPyPI validation completes before production deployment. This creates a staged deployment pipeline where failures on TestPyPI prevent production publication.

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:424-453]()

## Package Metadata and Build Configuration

The package metadata defined in `pyproject.toml` controls what information appears on PyPI and how the package is built.

### PyPI Project Metadata

| Field | Value | PyPI Display |
|-------|-------|--------------|
| `name` | `tt-tools-common` | Project name and pip install name |
| `version` | `1.6.0` | Current release version |
| `description` | "Common library for Tenstorrent tooling" | Short description |
| `readme` | `README.md` | Long description on project page |
| `requires-python` | `>=3.10` | Python version badge |
| `license` | Apache License 2.0 | License classifier |

### Classifier Configuration

The package includes PyPI classifiers that control search filtering and compatibility display:

```python
classifiers = [
  "Development Status :: 4 - Beta",
  "Environment :: Console :: Curses",
  "License :: OSI Approved :: Apache Software License",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: 3",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: 3.10",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: 3.11",
  "Programming Language :: Python :: 3 :: Only",
]
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:1-22]()

### Package Data Inclusion

The build system includes non-Python assets in the wheel distribution:

```yaml
Package Data Pattern: "*.css"
                      "data/*/*.yaml"
                      "data/*/*/*.yaml"

Excluded Directories: build/
                     debian/
```

This configuration ensures CSS themes and firmware definition YAML files are bundled in the published wheel, making them accessible to consuming applications at runtime.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:55-69]()

## Publishing Workflow Integration

The publishing jobs integrate into the broader release workflow with specific timing and dependencies.

### Workflow Execution Order

```mermaid
graph TD
    TempBranch["create-temp-branch"]
    VersionBump["versionchange"]
    Changelog["changelogs"]
    BuildAll["build_all_depends"]
    TagRelease["tagrelease"]
    GenRelease["generate-release"]
    TestPyPI["publish-to-testpypi"]
    PyPI["publish-to-pypi"]
    Mergeback["mergeback"]
    
    TempBranch --> VersionBump
    VersionBump --> Changelog
    Changelog --> BuildAll
    BuildAll --> TagRelease
    TagRelease --> GenRelease
    GenRelease --> TestPyPI
    TestPyPI --> PyPI
    GenRelease --> Mergeback
```

### Job Coordination Table

| Job | Dependencies | Outputs Produced | Consumers |
|-----|-------------|------------------|-----------|
| `build_all_depends` | `changelogs` | Wheel artifacts (`release-dists`) | `publish-to-testpypi`, `publish-to-pypi` |
| `generate-release` | `tagrelease`, `build_all_depends` | GitHub Release entry | `publish-to-testpypi`, `publish-to-pypi` |
| `publish-to-testpypi` | `build_all_depends`, `generate-release` | TestPyPI package entry | `publish-to-pypi` (implicit validation) |
| `publish-to-pypi` | `publish-to-testpypi`, `build_all_depends`, `generate-release` | PyPI package entry | End users via `pip install` |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:241-253](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:391-453]()

## Artifact Management

Both publishing jobs retrieve the same wheel artifacts built during the `buildpypi` workflow invocation.

### Artifact Retrieval Configuration

```mermaid
graph LR
    BuildPyPI["buildpypi workflow<br/>Produces .whl files"]
    UploadArtifact["Upload as 'release-dists'<br/>with pattern tt-tools-common*.whl"]
    GitHubStorage["GitHub Artifacts Storage"]
    
    DownloadTest["Download in<br/>publish-to-testpypi"]
    DownloadProd["Download in<br/>publish-to-pypi"]
    
    BuildPyPI --> UploadArtifact
    UploadArtifact --> GitHubStorage
    GitHubStorage --> DownloadTest
    GitHubStorage --> DownloadProd
    
    DownloadTest --> DirTest["dist/ directory<br/>(TestPyPI)"]
    DownloadProd --> DirProd["dist/ directory<br/>(PyPI)"]
```

**Download Action Parameters:**

```yaml
uses: actions/download-artifact@v4
with:
  pattern: tt-tools-common*.whl
  name: release-dists
  path: dist/
```

The `pattern` parameter ensures only wheel files are downloaded (excluding source distributions), the `name` matches the artifact uploaded by the build workflow, and `path` places files in the location expected by the PyPI publishing action.

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:408-413](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:442-447]()

## Environment Protection Rules

GitHub Actions environments provide deployment protection and required reviewers for sensitive operations.

### Environment Configuration Requirements

| Environment | Purpose | Typical Protections |
|-------------|---------|---------------------|
| `testpypi` | Staging validation | Optional: Required reviewers for first-time validation |
| `pypi` | Production release | Recommended: Required reviewers, deployment delay |

**Environment URL Mapping:**

- **TestPyPI Environment**: Points to `https://test.pypi.org/p/tt-tools-common` for immediate validation access
- **PyPI Environment**: Points to `https://pypi.org/p/tt-tools-common` for end-user package access

These URLs appear in the GitHub Actions UI as deployment links, allowing quick navigation to published packages for verification.

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:400-402](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:434-436]()

## Publishing Action Configuration

The `pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish` action handles the actual package upload to PyPI services.

### Action Parameters

```mermaid
graph TD
    Action["pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish@release/v1"]
    
    Input1["repository-url<br/>(TestPyPI only)"]
    Input2["verbose: true<br/>(Both environments)"]
    Input3["dist/ directory<br/>(implicit)"]
    Input4["OIDC token<br/>(automatic)"]
    
    Action --> Input1
    Action --> Input2
    Action --> Input3
    Action --> Input4
    
    Output1["Upload to target repository"]
    Output2["Detailed logs in workflow"]
    
    Action --> Output1
    Action --> Output2
```

### Configuration Differences

**TestPyPI-Specific Configuration:**
```yaml
with:
  repository-url: https://test.pypi.org/legacy/
  verbose: true
```

**PyPI Production Configuration:**
```yaml
with:
  verbose: true
  # repository-url omitted - uses default PyPI
```

The `repository-url` parameter is only specified for TestPyPI publishing. When omitted, the action defaults to the production PyPI server at `https://upload.pypi.org/legacy/`.

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:416-419](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:450-452]()

## Version Synchronization

The version published to PyPI comes from the `pyproject.toml` version field, which is automatically bumped during the release workflow.

### Version Flow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant VB as "versionchange job"
    participant PT as "pyproject.toml"
    participant BP as "buildpypi workflow"
    participant WHL as ".whl filename"
    participant PyPI as "PyPI metadata"
    
    VB->>PT: "bump2version updates<br/>project.version"
    PT->>PT: "version = '1.6.0' → '1.7.0'"
    
    BP->>PT: "setuptools reads<br/>project.version"
    BP->>WHL: "Generate filename<br/>tt-tools-common-1.7.0-py3-none-any.whl"
    
    WHL->>PyPI: "Upload package"
    PyPI->>PyPI: "Extract metadata from wheel<br/>Display version 1.7.0"
```

The version is the single source of truth in `pyproject.toml` at line 4. The `versionchange` job modifies this value using `bump2version`, and the Python build process reads it during wheel creation. This ensures version consistency across the wheel filename, package metadata, and PyPI listing.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:4](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:115-121]()

## Testing Published Packages

After publishing to TestPyPI, the package can be validated before production release.

### TestPyPI Installation Command

```bash
pip install --index-url https://test.pypi.org/simple/ \
            --extra-index-url https://pypi.org/simple/ \
            tt-tools-common
```

The `--extra-index-url` parameter is required because `tt-tools-common` has dependencies (pyluwen, textual, etc.) that are not available on TestPyPI. This command checks TestPyPI first for `tt-tools-common`, then falls back to production PyPI for dependencies.

### Validation Checklist

After TestPyPI publication, verify:

1. **Package Installation**: `pip install` completes without errors
2. **Import Verification**: `import tt_tools_common` succeeds
3. **Module Structure**: Key modules (`reset_common`, `utils_common`, `ui_common`) are accessible
4. **Asset Availability**: CSS files and YAML data are bundled (check with `pkg_resources` or `importlib.resources`)
5. **Version Correctness**: `tt_tools_common.__version__` matches expected release version

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:23-34]()

## Troubleshooting Common Issues

### OIDC Authentication Failures

**Symptom**: Job fails with "403 Forbidden" or "OIDC token validation failed"

**Resolution**:
1. Verify `id-token: write` permission is set at job level
2. Check PyPI project settings for trusted publisher configuration
3. Ensure environment name matches PyPI configuration exactly
4. Confirm repository owner, repository name, and workflow filename are correct

### Artifact Not Found Errors

**Symptom**: Download step reports "Artifact 'release-dists' not found"

**Resolution**:
1. Check `build_all_depends` job completed successfully
2. Verify `buildpypi` workflow uploaded artifacts with correct name
3. Confirm artifact pattern `tt-tools-common*.whl` matches actual filenames
4. Ensure workflow has permission to access artifacts from previous jobs

### Package Already Exists

**Symptom**: Upload fails with "File already exists" error

**Resolution**:
1. Version numbers on PyPI cannot be reused - bump version and retry
2. For TestPyPI, consider deleting the test release (only available for project maintainers)
3. Verify `versionchange` job successfully incremented version in `pyproject.toml`

### Missing Package Data

**Symptom**: CSS or YAML files not accessible after installation

**Resolution**:
1. Check `[tool.setuptools.package-data]` includes required patterns
2. Verify `include-package-data = true` is set in `pyproject.toml`
3. Ensure files are tracked in git (setuptools only includes committed files)
4. Confirm files are not listed in `exclude-package-data`

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:404-405](), [pyproject.toml:55-69]()

## Purpose and Scope

This guide covers the development workflow, testing practices, code quality standards, and continuous integration/deployment processes for contributing to tt-tools-common. It provides an overview of the development toolchain and common tasks developers encounter when modifying or extending the library.

For detailed information on specific topics:
- Test suite structure and execution: see [Testing Guide](#6.1)
- Code formatting and linting setup: see [Code Style and Quality Tools](#6.2)

For build and release processes: see [Build and Distribution](#5)

## Development Toolchain Overview

The tt-tools-common development environment uses modern Python tooling with strict quality controls. The toolchain separates runtime dependencies from development-time tools to minimize production package size while providing comprehensive development support.

### Development Dependencies

The project defines development dependencies in the `[project.optional-dependencies]` section of `pyproject.toml`:

| Dependency | Version | Purpose |
|------------|---------|---------|
| `black` | >=23.11.0 | Code formatting |
| `pre-commit` | >=3.5.0 | Git hook automation |
| `pyluwen` | ~=0.8.0 | Hardware abstraction for testing |
| `pytest` | >=7.0.0 | Test framework |
| `pytest-asyncio` | >=0.21.0 | Async test support |

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:36-43]()

### Python Version Requirements

The project supports Python 3.10, 3.11, and 3.12, with 3.10 as the minimum required version [pyproject.toml:3](). All CI workflows test against this matrix to ensure compatibility.

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Python Support Matrix"
        Python310["Python 3.10<br/>(minimum)"]
        Python311["Python 3.11"]
        Python312["Python 3.12"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CI Testing"
        TestWorkflow[".github/workflows/test.yml"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Package Configuration"
        PyProject["pyproject.toml<br/>requires-python: >=3.10"]
        Classifiers["classifiers:<br/>- Python :: 3.10<br/>- Python :: 3.11"]
    end
    
    Python310 --> TestWorkflow
    Python311 --> TestWorkflow
    Python312 --> TestWorkflow
    
    PyProject --> Python310
    PyProject --> Python311
    PyProject --> Python312
```

**Diagram:** Python version compatibility matrix and CI enforcement

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:3](), [pyproject.toml:19-21](), [.github/workflows/test.yml:20]()

## Development Workflow

The standard development workflow follows a feature-branch pattern with automated testing and quality checks at each stage.

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Setup["1. Environment Setup<br/>pip install -e .[dev]"]
    Branch["2. Create Feature Branch<br/>git checkout -b feature/name"]
    Code["3. Write Code<br/>Edit files in tt_tools_common/"]
    PreCommit["4. Pre-commit Hooks<br/>black formatting check"]
    LocalTest["5. Local Testing<br/>pytest -m 'not requires_hardware'"]
    HWTest["6. Hardware Testing (optional)<br/>pytest -m requires_hardware"]
    Push["7. Push Branch<br/>git push origin feature/name"]
    PR["8. Create Pull Request"]
    CITest["9. CI Validation<br/>.github/workflows/test.yml"]
    Review["10. Code Review"]
    Merge["11. Merge to main"]
    
    Setup --> Branch
    Branch --> Code
    Code --> PreCommit
    PreCommit -->|Pass| LocalTest
    PreCommit -->|Fail| Code
    LocalTest -->|Pass| HWTest
    LocalTest -->|Fail| Code
    HWTest -->|Pass or Skip| Push
    HWTest -->|Fail| Code
    Push --> PR
    PR --> CITest
    CITest -->|Pass| Review
    CITest -->|Fail| Code
    Review -->|Approved| Merge
    Review -->|Changes Requested| Code
```

**Diagram:** Standard development workflow from setup to merge

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:36-43](), [.github/workflows/test.yml:4-11]()

### Key Workflow Steps

1. **Environment Setup**: Install the package in editable mode with dev dependencies using `pip install -e ".[dev]"` [.github/workflows/test.yml:34]()
2. **Pre-commit Hooks**: Automated formatting checks run before each commit (configured via `pre-commit` package)
3. **Local Testing**: Run tests without hardware requirements using `pytest -m "not requires_hardware"` [.github/workflows/test.yml:38]()
4. **CI Validation**: All pull requests trigger automated testing across Python 3.10, 3.11, and 3.12
5. **Hardware Testing**: Optional but recommended for reset-related changes, runs on specialized runners

---

## Testing Architecture

The test suite uses pytest with custom markers to differentiate between tests that require physical Tenstorrent hardware and those that can run in any environment.

### Test Organization

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Test Directory Structure"
        TestsDir["tt_tools_common/tests/"]
        Conftest["conftest.py<br/>Fixtures: devices()"]
        TestFiles["test_*.py files"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Test Categories"
        Software["Software Tests<br/>(no marker)"]
        Hardware["Hardware Tests<br/>@pytest.mark.requires_hardware"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Test Execution Paths"
        LocalCI["Local/Standard CI<br/>pytest -m 'not requires_hardware'"]
        HardwareCI["Hardware CI<br/>pytest -m requires_hardware"]
    end
    
    subgraph "CI Runners"
        StandardRunner["ubuntu-latest"]
        HWRunner1["tt-ubuntu-2204-n150-stable"]
        HWRunner2["tt-ubuntu-2204-p150b-stable"]
    end
    
    TestsDir --> Conftest
    TestsDir --> TestFiles
    
    TestFiles --> Software
    TestFiles --> Hardware
    
    Software --> LocalCI
    Hardware --> HardwareCI
    
    LocalCI --> StandardRunner
    HardwareCI --> HWRunner1
    HardwareCI --> HWRunner2
```

**Diagram:** Test suite organization and execution paths

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:50-53](), [tt_tools_common/tests/conftest.py:8-11](), [.github/workflows/test.yml:36-66]()

### pytest Markers

The project defines a custom marker in `pyproject.toml`:

```ini
[tool.pytest.ini_options]
markers = [
  "requires_hardware: marks tests as requiring Tenstorrent hardware"
]
```

This marker enables selective test execution:
- **Without hardware**: `pytest -m "not requires_hardware"` runs in standard CI
- **With hardware**: `pytest -m requires_hardware` runs on specialized runners with Tenstorrent chips

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:50-53]()

### Test Fixtures

The `conftest.py` file defines shared fixtures available to all tests:

| Fixture | Type | Purpose |
|---------|------|---------|
| `devices` | function | Returns list of detected Tenstorrent chips via `pyluwen.detect_chips()` |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/conftest.py:8-11]()

---

## Continuous Integration Matrix

The CI pipeline runs two types of test jobs with different runner configurations.

### Test Matrix Configuration

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "test Job (Software Tests)"
        Matrix1["matrix.python-version:<br/>- '3.10'<br/>- '3.11'<br/>- '3.12'"]
        Runner1["runs-on: ubuntu-latest"]
        Test1["pytest -m 'not requires_hardware'"]
    end
    
    subgraph "test-hardware Job (Hardware Tests)"
        Matrix2["matrix.runner:<br/>- tt-ubuntu-2204-n150-stable<br/>- tt-ubuntu-2204-p150b-stable"]
        Python2["python-version: '3.10' (fixed)"]
        Test2["pytest -m requires_hardware"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Triggers"
        Push["push: main"]
        PR["pull_request: main"]
        Manual["workflow_dispatch"]
    end
    
    Push --> Matrix1
    PR --> Matrix1
    Manual --> Matrix1
    
    Push --> Matrix2
    PR --> Matrix2
    Manual --> Matrix2
```

**Diagram:** CI test matrix showing parallel execution strategies

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/test.yml:14-66]()

### Job Definitions

**Software Tests** [.github/workflows/test.yml:14-38]():
- Runs on `ubuntu-latest`
- Tests Python 3.10, 3.11, 3.12 in parallel
- Uses `fail-fast: false` to complete all version tests even if one fails
- Excludes hardware-dependent tests

**Hardware Tests** [.github/workflows/test.yml:40-66]():
- Runs on specialized self-hosted runners with Tenstorrent hardware
- Fixed to Python 3.10
- Two runner types for different chip architectures (N150, P150B)
- Includes only tests marked with `requires_hardware`

## Common Development Commands

### Installation and Setup

| Command | Purpose |
|---------|---------|
| `pip install -e .` | Install package in editable mode (runtime only) |
| `pip install -e ".[dev]"` | Install with development dependencies |
| `pre-commit install` | Set up git commit hooks |

### Testing

| Command | Purpose |
|---------|---------|
| `pytest tt_tools_common/tests/` | Run all tests |
| `pytest -v` | Run with verbose output |
| `pytest -m "not requires_hardware"` | Run software tests only |
| `pytest -m requires_hardware` | Run hardware tests only |
| `pytest -k test_name` | Run tests matching name pattern |

### Code Quality

| Command | Purpose |
|---------|---------|
| `black .` | Format all Python files |
| `black --check .` | Check formatting without modifying |
| `pre-commit run --all-files` | Run all pre-commit hooks |

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:36-43](), [.github/workflows/test.yml:32-38]()

## Package Installation Modes

The project supports multiple installation modes depending on the development context.

### Installation Mode Comparison

| Mode | Command | Use Case | Dependencies Installed |
|------|---------|----------|------------------------|
| **Production** | `pip install tt-tools-common` | End users, consuming tools | Runtime only |
| **Editable** | `pip install -e .` | Development without testing | Runtime only |
| **Development** | `pip install -e ".[dev]"` | Full development workflow | Runtime + dev tools |

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Installation Modes"
        Prod["Production Install<br/>pip install tt-tools-common"]
        Edit["Editable Install<br/>pip install -e ."]
        Dev["Development Install<br/>pip install -e .[dev]"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Dependency Groups"
        Runtime["Runtime Dependencies<br/>pyproject.toml [project.dependencies]"]
        DevDeps["Dev Dependencies<br/>pyproject.toml [project.optional-dependencies.dev]"]
    end
    
    Prod --> Runtime
    Edit --> Runtime
    Dev --> Runtime
    Dev --> DevDeps
    
    Runtime -->|Includes| Packages1["textual, rich, pyyaml,<br/>pydantic, psutil, etc."]
    DevDeps -->|Includes| Packages2["black, pre-commit,<br/>pytest, pytest-asyncio,<br/>pyluwen"]
```

**Diagram:** Package installation modes and dependency relationships

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:23-43]()

### Editable Installation Benefits

Editable mode (`-e` flag) creates a symlink to the source directory, allowing:
- Code changes to take effect immediately without reinstallation
- Direct file editing in the repository
- Simplified debugging with IDE integration

This is the recommended mode for all development work.

While not strictly required, certain environment variables can enhance the development experience:

| Variable | Purpose | Example |
|----------|---------|---------|
| `PYTHONPATH` | Add uninstalled modules to path | `export PYTHONPATH=/path/to/tt-tools-common` |
| `PYTEST_ADDOPTS` | Default pytest options | `export PYTEST_ADDOPTS="-v --tb=short"` |

## Purpose and Scope

This document explains the test infrastructure for tt-tools-common, including the pytest-based test suite, hardware vs. software test separation, test fixtures, local test execution, and continuous integration testing. It provides guidance for both running existing tests and writing new tests.

For information about setting up a development environment before running tests, see [Development Environment Setup](#6.4). For details on the CI/CD pipeline that executes these tests, see [CI/CD Pipeline Overview](#6.3).

---

## Test Suite Architecture

The test suite is organized into a single directory with modular test files, a shared fixture configuration, and pytest markers to separate hardware-dependent tests from software-only tests.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Test Directory Structure"
        TestDir["tt_tools_common/tests/"]
        Conftest["conftest.py<br/>Shared fixtures"]
        TestReset["test_reset.py<br/>Chip reset tests"]
        TestDetect["test_detect_fallible.py<br/>Chip detection tests"]
        TestConfig["test_reset_config.py<br/>Config parsing tests"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Test Categories"
        HWTests["Hardware Tests<br/>requires_hardware marker"]
        SWTests["Software Tests<br/>No marker"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Fixtures"
        DevicesFix["devices fixture<br/>detect_chips() result"]
        PCIFix["pci_indices fixture<br/>Local chip indices"]
    end
    
    TestDir --> Conftest
    TestDir --> TestReset
    TestDir --> TestDetect
    TestDir --> TestConfig
    
    TestReset --> HWTests
    TestDetect --> HWTests
    TestConfig --> HWTests
    TestConfig --> SWTests
    
    Conftest --> DevicesFix
    TestDetect --> PCIFix
    
    HWTests --> DevicesFix
    HWTests --> PCIFix
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/conftest.py:1-12](), [tt_tools_common/tests/test_reset.py:1-15](), [tt_tools_common/tests/test_detect_fallible.py:1-40](), [tt_tools_common/tests/test_reset_config.py:1-50]()

### Test File Organization

| Test File | Purpose | Hardware Required |
|-----------|---------|-------------------|
| `test_reset.py` | Tests `ChipReset.full_lds_reset()` functionality | Yes |
| `test_detect_fallible.py` | Tests `detect_chips_with_callback()` before and after reset | Yes |
| `test_reset_config.py` | Tests reset configuration parsing and log generation | Mixed (some tests) |

All test files are located in `tt_tools_common/tests/`. The `conftest.py` file provides shared fixtures available to all tests.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/test_reset.py:1-15](), [tt_tools_common/tests/test_detect_fallible.py:1-40](), [tt_tools_common/tests/test_reset_config.py:1-50]()

---

## Test Markers

The test suite uses pytest markers to categorize tests based on hardware requirements. This enables selective test execution in environments with or without Tenstorrent hardware.

### `requires_hardware` Marker

Tests that interact with physical Tenstorrent chips must be marked with `@pytest.mark.requires_hardware`. This marker is used to:

1. **Skip tests in CI environments without hardware** - The standard test job runs with `-m "not requires_hardware"`
2. **Select hardware tests for execution on dedicated hardware runners** - Hardware test jobs run with `-m requires_hardware`

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Test Execution Paths"
        AllTests["All Tests"]
        SoftwareOnly["Software Tests<br/>-m 'not requires_hardware'"]
        HardwareOnly["Hardware Tests<br/>-m requires_hardware"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Test Marking"
        Marked["@pytest.mark.requires_hardware"]
        Unmarked["No marker"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Execution Environments"
        StandardCI["Standard CI<br/>ubuntu-latest"]
        HardwareCI["Hardware Runners<br/>tt-ubuntu-2204-*-stable"]
    end
    
    AllTests --> Marked
    AllTests --> Unmarked
    
    Marked --> HardwareOnly
    Unmarked --> SoftwareOnly
    
    SoftwareOnly --> StandardCI
    HardwareOnly --> HardwareCI
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/test.yml:36-38](), [.github/workflows/test.yml:64-66]()

### Example Usage

Hardware-dependent test example from [tt_tools_common/tests/test_reset.py:10-14]():

```python
@pytest.mark.requires_hardware
def test_full_lds_reset(devices):
    """Test full LDS reset on all detected chips."""
    pci_interfaces = list(range(len(devices)))
    ChipReset().full_lds_reset(pci_interfaces=pci_interfaces)
```

Software-only test example from [tt_tools_common/tests/test_reset_config.py:16-20]():

```python
def test_parse_reset_input_pci_indices():
    """Test parsing comma-separated PCI indices."""
    result = parse_reset_input(["0,1,2,3\
33:T3aef,
# Code Style and Quality Tools

## Purpose and Scope

This document covers code style enforcement, formatting tools, and quality control mechanisms used in tt-tools-common development. It explains the Black code formatter configuration, pre-commit hook setup, development dependencies, and integration with the CI/CD pipeline. For information about running tests, see [Testing Guide](#6.1). For CI/CD pipeline workflows, see [CI/CD Pipeline Overview](#6.3).
