## Development Dependencies Overview

The tt-tools-common project defines development dependencies separate from runtime dependencies to keep the production package lightweight while providing comprehensive tooling for contributors.

### Dependency Categories

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Development Dependencies"
        Black["black>=23.11.0<br/>Code formatter"]
        PreCommit["pre-commit>=3.5.0<br/>Git hook framework"]
        PyLuwen["pyluwen~=0.8.0<br/>Hardware testing"]
        Pytest["pytest>=7.0.0<br/>Test framework"]
        PytestAsync["pytest-asyncio>=0.21.0<br/>Async test support"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Runtime Dependencies"
        Distro["distro>=1.8.0"]
        ES["elasticsearch>=8.11.0"]
        Psutil["psutil>=5.9.6"]
        PyYAML["pyyaml>=6.0.1"]
        Rich["rich>=13.7.0"]
        Textual["textual>=0.59.0"]
        Requests["requests>=2.32.3"]
        TQDM["tqdm>=4.66.3"]
        Pydantic["pydantic>=1.2"]
        Tomli["tomli"]
    end
    
    Black -.->|"formats"| SourceCode["Python Source Files"]
    PreCommit -.->|"triggers"| Black
    Pytest -.->|"tests"| SourceCode
    PyLuwen -.->|"enables"| Pytest
    PytestAsync -.->|"extends"| Pytest
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:36-43]()

### Installing Development Dependencies

Development dependencies are installed as an optional dependency group:

```bash
# Install with development tools
pip install -e ".[dev]"

# Or install separately
pip install black>=23.11.0 pre-commit>=3.5.0 pytest>=7.0.0 pytest-asyncio>=0.21.0
```

The `-e` flag installs the package in editable mode, allowing changes to the source code to be immediately reflected without reinstallation. This is the recommended approach for active development.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:36-43]()

---

## Code Formatting with Black

Black is the opinionated code formatter used for all Python source files in tt-tools-common. It enforces consistent style across the codebase, eliminating debates about formatting preferences.

### Black Configuration

The project uses Black version 23.11.0 or higher with default settings. Black's configuration is intentionally minimal to leverage its opinionated defaults:

| Configuration Aspect | Value | Rationale |
|---------------------|-------|-----------|
| **Line Length** | 88 characters (default) | Black's optimized default |
| **String Quotes** | Double quotes (default) | Consistent string formatting |
| **Target Versions** | Python 3.10+ | Matches project requirement |
| **Skip String Normalization** | No | Enforces quote consistency |
| **Magic Trailing Comma** | Yes | Preserves intentional formatting |

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:38]()

### Running Black

```bash
# Format all Python files in the project
black .

# Check formatting without making changes
black --check .

# Format specific files or directories
black tt_tools_common/ tests/

# Show diff without applying changes
black --diff .
```

Black automatically discovers all `.py` files and applies consistent formatting. The `--check` flag is used in CI to verify formatting without modifying files.

### Black Integration Points

```mermaid
graph LR
    Developer["Developer<br/>Modifies Code"]
    PreCommit["pre-commit Hook<br/>Triggers on git commit"]
    Black["black<br/>Formats staged files"]
    Git["Git Staging Area"]
    CI["GitHub Actions<br/>Test Workflow"]
    BlackCheck["black --check<br/>Validation"]
    
    Developer --> Git
    Git -->|"git commit"| PreCommit
    PreCommit --> Black
    Black -->|"formatted"| Git
    Git -->|"push"| CI
    CI --> BlackCheck
    BlackCheck -->|"fail if unformatted"| CI
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:38-39]()

---

## Pre-commit Hook Framework

The pre-commit framework automates code quality checks before commits reach the repository. It ensures that code meets style and quality standards before entering version control.

### Pre-commit Configuration

While the specific `.pre-commit-config.yaml` file is not provided in the source files, the project includes pre-commit as a development dependency, indicating its use for automated quality checks.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:39]()

### Installing Pre-commit Hooks

```bash
# Install pre-commit in the repository
pre-commit install

# Install hooks for all supported git hooks
pre-commit install --install-hooks

# Uninstall hooks (if needed)
pre-commit uninstall
```

After installation, pre-commit runs automatically on `git commit`. The hooks execute only on staged files, making the checks fast and relevant to the current change.

### Running Pre-commit Manually

```bash
# Run all hooks on staged files
pre-commit run

# Run all hooks on all files in the repository
pre-commit run --all-files

# Run a specific hook
pre-commit run black

# Update hook repositories to latest versions
pre-commit autoupdate
```

Manual execution is useful for:
- Formatting code before staging changes
- Checking all files after updating hook configurations
- Testing hook behavior without committing

### Pre-commit Hook Workflow

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant Dev as Developer
    participant Git as Git
    participant PreCommit as pre-commit
    participant Black as black
    participant Tests as pytest
    
    Dev->>Git: git commit
    Git->>PreCommit: Trigger hooks
    PreCommit->>Black: Run formatter
    alt Formatting needed
        Black->>PreCommit: Files modified
        PreCommit->>Git: Commit failed
        PreCommit->>Dev: Review changes & re-commit
    else Already formatted
        Black->>PreCommit: No changes
        PreCommit->>Tests: Run tests (if configured)
        Tests->>PreCommit: Tests pass
        PreCommit->>Git: Commit succeeds
    end
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:39]()

---

## Development Dependency Details

### Black (Code Formatter)

- **Version:** `>=23.11.0`
- **Purpose:** Enforces consistent Python code formatting
- **Usage:** Automatic via pre-commit; manual via `black .`
- **Configuration:** Uses Black defaults (88 char line length)

### Pre-commit (Hook Framework)

- **Version:** `>=3.5.0`
- **Purpose:** Manages git hooks for quality checks
- **Usage:** Install once with `pre-commit install`, runs on every commit
- **Hooks:** Typically includes Black, trailing whitespace removal, YAML/JSON validation

### PyLuwen (Hardware Abstraction)

- **Version:** `~=0.8.0`
- **Purpose:** Required for hardware tests marked with `@pytest.mark.requires_hardware`
- **Usage:** Import in tests that interact with Tenstorrent chips
- **Note:** Not required for software-only tests

### Pytest (Test Framework)

- **Version:** `>=7.0.0`
- **Purpose:** Runs unit and integration tests
- **Configuration:** Test markers defined in `[tool.pytest.ini_options]`
- **Usage:** See [Testing Guide](#6.1) for detailed information

### Pytest-Asyncio (Async Test Support)

- **Version:** `>=0.21.0`
- **Purpose:** Enables testing of async functions in Textual widgets
- **Usage:** Applied automatically to async test functions
- **Integration:** Works with Textual's App.run_test() for TUI testing

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:36-43](), [pyproject.toml:50-53]()

---

## Python Version Compatibility

The project supports Python 3.10 and higher, with CI testing across multiple versions.

### Version Requirements

```mermaid
graph TD
    subgraph "Python Version Support"
        Py310["Python 3.10<br/>Minimum required"]
        Py311["Python 3.11<br/>Tested in CI"]
        Py312["Python 3.12<br/>Tested in CI"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Version-Dependent Features"
        TypeHints["Modern Type Hints<br/>PEP 604 (X | Y syntax)"]
        MatchStmt["Pattern Matching<br/>PEP 634"]
        TomliBackport["tomli<br/>TOML parsing (built-in in 3.11+)"]
    end
    
    Py310 -.->|"enables"| TypeHints
    Py310 -.->|"enables"| MatchStmt
    Py310 -.->|"requires"| TomliBackport
    Py311 -.->|"native"| TomliBackport
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:3](), [pyproject.toml:19-21]()

### Version-Specific Considerations

| Python Version | Status | Notes |
|---------------|--------|-------|
| **3.10** | Minimum required | All features supported; requires `tomli` for TOML parsing |
| **3.11** | Recommended | Better performance; `tomllib` built-in |
| **3.12** | Supported | Latest features; fully tested in CI |
| **3.9 or lower** | Not supported | Missing type hint features (PEP 604) |

The `requires-python = ">=3.10"` constraint in pyproject.toml prevents installation on incompatible Python versions. This ensures that modern syntax features can be used throughout the codebase without compatibility checks.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:3](), [pyproject.toml:18-21]()

---

## Code Quality in CI/CD

Code quality checks are integrated into the GitHub Actions CI pipeline to ensure all commits meet project standards.

### CI Quality Check Workflow

```mermaid
graph TB
    Push["git push to main/PR"]
    
    subgraph "GitHub Actions: Test Workflow"
        Checkout["actions/checkout<br/>Clone repository"]
        SetupPy["actions/setup-python<br/>Install Python 3.10/3.11/3.12"]
        InstallDeps["pip install -e .[dev]<br/>Install with dev dependencies"]
        BlackCheck["black --check .<br/>Verify formatting"]
        Pytest["pytest<br/>Run test suite"]
    end
    
    Success["✓ All checks pass"]
    Failure["✗ Formatting or tests fail"]
    
    Push --> Checkout
    Checkout --> SetupPy
    SetupPy --> InstallDeps
    InstallDeps --> BlackCheck
    BlackCheck -->|"formatted"| Pytest
    BlackCheck -->|"unformatted"| Failure
    Pytest -->|"pass"| Success
    Pytest -->|"fail"| Failure
```

### Local vs CI Validation

| Check | Local (Pre-commit) | CI (GitHub Actions) |
|-------|-------------------|---------------------|
| **Black Formatting** | Automatic on commit | `black --check .` |
| **File Cleanup** | Trailing whitespace, EOF | Implicit via Black |
| **Test Execution** | Optional (developer choice) | Required for all PRs |
| **Hardware Tests** | Skipped (unless hardware available) | Skipped (`@pytest.mark.requires_hardware`) |

The local pre-commit hooks provide immediate feedback, while CI serves as the authoritative quality gate. Developers should run `pre-commit run --all-files` before pushing to catch issues early.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:38-43]()

---

## Package Data and Exclusions

The project includes specific package data while excluding build artifacts from distribution.

### Included Package Data

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Package Inclusions"
        CSS["*.css<br/>UI stylesheets"]
        YAMLData["data/*/*.yaml<br/>Chip definitions"]
        YAMLNested["data/*/*/*.yaml<br/>Nested configs"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Package Exclusions"
        Build["build/<br/>Build artifacts"]
        Debian["debian/<br/>Packaging files"]
    end
    
    CSS --> Package["tt-tools-common.whl"]
    YAMLData --> Package
    YAMLNested --> Package
    
    Build -.->|"excluded"| Package
    Debian -.->|"excluded"| Package
```

The `include-package-data = true` setting combined with specific patterns ensures that CSS themes and YAML configuration files are included in the wheel distribution, while build artifacts and Debian packaging files are excluded.

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:55-69]()

### Gitignore Patterns

The `.gitignore` file excludes common Python development artifacts:

| Pattern | Purpose |
|---------|---------|
| `__pycache__/` | Bytecode cache directories |
| `*.egg-info` | Package metadata |
| `.eggs/` | Setuptools egg cache |
| `build/` | Build output directory |
| `.venv/`, `venv/`, `.env/` | Virtual environment directories |
| `.pybuild/` | Python build directory |
| `debian/.debhelper`, `debian/files` | Debian build artifacts |
| `.vscode/` | VS Code configuration |

These patterns prevent committing transient build artifacts and developer-specific configurations to version control.

**Sources:** [.gitignore:1-17]()

## Best Practices for Contributors

### Development Workflow

1. **Initial Setup**
   ```bash
   # Clone repository
   git clone https://github.com/tenstorrent/tt-tools-common.git
   cd tt-tools-common
   
   # Create virtual environment
   python3.10 -m venv .venv
   source .venv/bin/activate
   
   # Install with dev dependencies
   pip install -e ".[dev]"
   
   # Install pre-commit hooks
   pre-commit install
   ```

2. **Making Changes**
   ```bash
   # Create feature branch
   git checkout -b feature/my-improvement
   
   # Make code changes
   vim tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py
   
   # Format code (optional, pre-commit will do this)
   black .
   
   # Run tests locally
   pytest -v
   
   # Commit (pre-commit runs automatically)
   git add .
   git commit -m "feat: improve reset logging"
   ```

3. **Before Pushing**
   ```bash
   # Run all pre-commit hooks on all files
   pre-commit run --all-files
   
   # Run full test suite
   pytest -v
   
   # Push to remote
   git push origin feature/my-improvement
   ```

### Code Quality Checklist

- [ ] All code is Black-formatted
- [ ] No trailing whitespace or incorrect line endings
- [ ] Type hints are used for function signatures
- [ ] Docstrings follow project conventions
- [ ] Tests pass locally (software tests minimum)
- [ ] No new imports without updating dependencies
- [ ] Changes are documented if API-facing
- [ ] Pre-commit hooks pass on all files

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:36-43]()

---

## Troubleshooting

### Black Formatting Conflicts

**Issue:** Pre-commit hook fails with Black formatting errors.

**Solution:**
```bash
# Let Black fix the formatting
black .

# Stage the formatted files
git add .

# Commit again
git commit
```

### Pre-commit Hook Not Running

**Issue:** Commits succeed without running hooks.

**Solution:**
```bash
# Reinstall hooks
pre-commit uninstall
pre-commit install

# Verify installation
pre-commit run --all-files
```

### Development Dependencies Not Found

**Issue:** `ModuleNotFoundError` for `black`, `pytest`, etc.

**Solution:**
```bash
# Ensure dev dependencies are installed
pip install -e ".[dev]"

# Verify installation
pip list | grep -E "black|pre-commit|pytest"
```

### Python Version Mismatch

**Issue:** Package installation fails with Python version error.

**Solution:**
```bash
# Check Python version
python --version

# Must be 3.10 or higher
# Use pyenv or system package manager to install correct version
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:3](), [pyproject.toml:36-43]()

# CI/CD Pipeline Overview

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [.github/workflows/build-all.yml](.github/workflows/build-all.yml)
- [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml](.github/workflows/build-debian.yml)

## Purpose and Scope

This document provides a comprehensive overview of the GitHub Actions-based CI/CD pipeline for tt-tools-common. It covers all automated workflows including test execution, release orchestration, multi-target package building, and distribution publishing. For detailed information about the build system configuration and version management, see [Build and Distribution](#5). For testing methodology and pytest configuration, see [Testing Guide](#6.1).

---

## Pipeline Architecture

The CI/CD pipeline consists of five primary workflows that automate the entire development, testing, build, and release lifecycle. Each workflow is implemented as a separate GitHub Actions YAML file in `.github/workflows/`.

### Workflow Overview Diagram

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Trigger Events"
        Push["Push to main"]
        PR["Pull Request"]
        Manual["workflow_dispatch"]
        IssueOpen["Issue/PR opened"]
    end
    
    subgraph "test.yml"
        TestJob["test job<br/>Matrix: Python 3.10, 3.11, 3.12"]
        TestHW["test-hardware job<br/>tt-ubuntu-2204-n150-stable<br/>tt-ubuntu-2204-p150b-stable"]
    end
    
    subgraph "release.yml - Main Release Orchestrator"
        CreateBranch["create-temp-branch<br/>Creates rc-temp-* branch"]
        VersionChange["versionchange<br/>bump2version + toml-cli"]
        Changelogs["changelogs<br/>gbp dch for debian/changelog"]
        BuildAll["build_all_depends<br/>Calls build-all.yml"]
        TagRelease["tagrelease<br/>Creates v*.*.* tag"]
        GenRelease["generate-release<br/>Creates GitHub Release"]
        MergeBack["mergeback<br/>Rebases to main"]
        PubTest["publish-to-testpypi"]
        PubProd["publish-to-pypi"]
    end
    
    subgraph "build-all.yml"
        BuildDeb["builddebian<br/>Calls build-debian.yml"]
        BuildPyPI["buildpypi<br/>Calls build-pypi.yml"]
    end
    
    subgraph "build-debian.yml"
        DebMatrix["build-deb job<br/>Matrix: ubuntu-22.04<br/>ubuntu-24.04<br/>ubuntu-latest"]
        DebArtifacts["Upload .deb + .changes<br/>+ changelog artifacts"]
    end
    
    subgraph "community-issue-tagging.yml"
        CommunityLabel["community-labeling<br/>Auto-tags external issues"]
    end
    
    Push --> TestJob
    PR --> TestJob
    TestJob --> TestHW
    
    Manual --> CreateBranch
    CreateBranch --> VersionChange
    VersionChange --> Changelogs
    Changelogs --> BuildAll
    BuildAll --> BuildDeb
    BuildAll --> BuildPyPI
    BuildAll --> TagRelease
    TagRelease --> GenRelease
    GenRelease --> MergeBack
    GenRelease --> PubTest
    PubTest --> PubProd
    
    BuildDeb --> DebMatrix
    DebMatrix --> DebArtifacts
    
    IssueOpen --> CommunityLabel
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/test.yml:1-67](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:1-453](), [.github/workflows/build-all.yml:1-53](), [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:1-179](), [.github/workflows/community-issue-tagging.yml:1-19]()

### Workflow Trigger Matrix

| Workflow | Triggers | Purpose |
|----------|----------|---------|
| `test.yml` | `push` to main, `pull_request` to main, `workflow_dispatch` | Continuous integration testing across Python versions |
| `release.yml` | `workflow_dispatch` (manual only) | Complete release orchestration with version bumping and publishing |
| `build-debian.yml` | `workflow_call`, `workflow_dispatch` | Multi-distro Debian package generation |
| `build-all.yml` | `workflow_call`, `workflow_dispatch` | Orchestrates parallel Debian and Python builds |
| `community-issue-tagging.yml` | `issues: opened`, `pull_request: opened` | Automatically labels external contributions |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/test.yml:4-11](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:4-16](), [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:3-23](), [.github/workflows/build-all.yml:3-22](), [.github/workflows/community-issue-tagging.yml:3-8]()

---

## Test Automation Workflow

The `test.yml` workflow implements continuous integration testing with hardware and software test separation using pytest markers.

### Test Execution Flow

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["Trigger: push/PR to main"]
    
    subgraph "test job - Software Tests"
        CheckoutCode["actions/checkout@v4"]
        SetupPy["actions/setup-python@v5<br/>Matrix: 3.10, 3.11, 3.12"]
        InstallDeps["pip install -e .[dev]"]
        RunTests["pytest -m 'not requires_hardware'"]
    end
    
    subgraph "test-hardware job - Hardware Tests"
        CheckoutHW["actions/checkout@v4"]
        SetupPyHW["actions/setup-python@v5<br/>Python 3.10 only"]
        InstallDepsHW["pip install -e .[dev]"]
        RunHWTests["pytest -m requires_hardware"]
    end
    
    Start --> CheckoutCode
    CheckoutCode --> SetupPy
    SetupPy --> InstallDeps
    InstallDeps --> RunTests
    
    Start --> CheckoutHW
    CheckoutHW --> SetupPyHW
    SetupPyHW --> InstallDepsHW
    InstallDepsHW --> RunHWTests
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/test.yml:13-67]()

### Test Job Configuration

The `test` job runs in parallel across three Python versions with `fail-fast: false` to ensure all versions are tested even if one fails:

```yaml
strategy:
  fail-fast: false
  matrix:
    python-version: ["3.10", "3.11", "3.12"]
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/test.yml:17-20]()

The `test-hardware` job runs on self-hosted runners with actual Tenstorrent hardware:

| Runner | Hardware Configuration |
|--------|----------------------|
| `tt-ubuntu-2204-n150-stable` | N150 card configuration |
| `tt-ubuntu-2204-p150b-stable` | P150B card configuration |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/test.yml:40-48]()

### Test Marker Strategy

Tests are separated by the `requires_hardware` marker:
- Software tests: `pytest -m "not requires_hardware"` - Run on standard GitHub runners
- Hardware tests: `pytest -m requires_hardware` - Run on self-hosted runners with Tenstorrent chips

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/test.yml:36-38](), [.github/workflows/test.yml:64-66]()

---

## Release Workflow

The `release.yml` workflow orchestrates the complete release process through a series of dependent jobs that modify version files, generate changelogs, build artifacts, and publish to multiple targets.

### Release Job Dependency Chain

```mermaid
graph TD
    Manual["workflow_dispatch<br/>Input: version_bump_type<br/>patch/minor/major"]
    
    CreateTemp["create-temp-branch<br/>Creates rc-temp-SHA-TIMESTAMP"]
    VersionJob["versionchange<br/>bump2version pyproject.toml<br/>Extracts MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH"]
    ChangelogJob["changelogs<br/>gbp dch for debian/changelog<br/>Commits to temp branch"]
    BuildJob["build_all_depends<br/>Calls build-all.yml workflow"]
    TagJob["tagrelease<br/>git tag v*.*.* and push"]
    ReleaseJob["generate-release<br/>Creates GitHub Release<br/>Attaches .deb + .whl"]
    TestPyPI["publish-to-testpypi<br/>Validates on test.pypi.org"]
    PyPI["publish-to-pypi<br/>Publishes to pypi.org"]
    Merge["mergeback<br/>git rebase to main<br/>Delete temp branch"]
    
    Manual --> CreateTemp
    CreateTemp --> VersionJob
    VersionJob --> ChangelogJob
    ChangelogJob --> BuildJob
    BuildJob --> TagJob
    TagJob --> ReleaseJob
    ReleaseJob --> TestPyPI
    TestPyPI --> PyPI
    ReleaseJob --> Merge
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:21-453]()

### Temporary Branch Isolation Pattern

The release workflow uses a temporary branch strategy to isolate version modifications before merging back to main. This prevents merge conflicts and ensures atomic version updates:

1. **Branch Creation**: Job `create-temp-branch` generates a unique branch name: `rc-temp-{SHORT_SHA}-{TIMESTAMP}`
2. **Version Modifications**: Jobs `versionchange` and `changelogs` commit to this temporary branch
3. **Build Isolation**: All build workflows use this branch via `inputs.ref`
4. **Merge Back**: Job `mergeback` rebases changes to main and deletes the temporary branch

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:41-62](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:362-386]()

### Version Management Jobs

#### versionchange Job

The `versionchange` job modifies `pyproject.toml` using `bump2version` and extracts version components:

| Tool | Purpose | Configuration |
|------|---------|---------------|
| `toml-cli` | Extract current version from `pyproject.toml` | `toml get project.version` |
| `bump2version` | Increment version based on input | `--current-version` + `patch/minor/major` argument |
| `release-kit/semver@v2` | Parse version into MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH components | Used for downstream jobs |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:64-160]()

The job outputs 8 key values used by downstream jobs:
- `git_hash`: Commit SHA after version update
- `package_name`: Extracted from `project.name` in pyproject.toml
- `package_version_new`: New version after bumping
- `version_major`, `version_minor`, `version_patch`: Semantic version components
- `number_of_commits_since_tag`: Commit count since last tag

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:74-84]()

#### changelogs Job

Generates Debian changelog using `git-buildpackage` (gbp):

```bash
gbp dch \
  --debian-branch ${TEMP_BRANCH_REF} \
  -R \
  -N ${MAJOR}.${MINOR}.${PATCH} \
  --spawn-editor=never
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:203-213]()

### Release Publication Jobs

#### generate-release Job

Creates GitHub Release with automated changelog generation:

1. **Download Artifacts**: Retrieves all `.deb` and `.whl` files from build jobs
2. **Generate Changelog**: Uses `mikepenz/release-changelog-builder-action@v5` in HYBRID mode to include both PRs and direct commits
3. **Rename Artifacts**: Deduplicates `.deb` files by embedding distro name in filename
4. **Create Release**: Uses `softprops/action-gh-release@v1` to attach all artifacts

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:288-357]()

Changelog template configuration:

```json
{
  "template": "#{{CHANGELOG}}\
\
## Contributors\
#{{CONTRIBUTORS}}",
  "categories": [
    {
      "title": "## 🔄 Changes",
      "labels": []
    }
  ],
  "pr_template": "- #{{TITLE}} (#{{NUMBER}}) by @#{{AUTHOR}}",
  "commit_template": "- #{{TITLE}} (#{{MERGE_SHA}}) by @#{{AUTHOR}}"
}
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:305-321]()

---

## Build Workflows

### build-all.yml Orchestrator

The `build-all.yml` workflow serves as a coordination point that triggers both Debian and Python builds in parallel using `workflow_call`:

```mermaid
graph LR
    BuildAll["build-all.yml<br/>Input: ref, version components"]
    DebBuild["build-debian.yml<br/>Matrix build"]
    PyBuild["build-pypi.yml<br/>Wheel generation"]
    
    BuildAll -->|"workflow_call"| DebBuild
    BuildAll -->|"workflow_call"| PyBuild
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-all.yml:24-53]()

The workflow passes version components as inputs:
- `ref`: Git reference to build from (typically the temp branch)
- `MAJOR`, `MINOR`, `PATCH`: Version components from `versionchange`
- `NUMBER_OF_COMMITS_SINCE_TAG`: For development builds

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-all.yml:6-22]()

### build-debian.yml Matrix Build

The Debian build workflow generates packages for three Ubuntu distributions in parallel.

#### Build Matrix Configuration

```yaml
strategy:
  fail-fast: false
  matrix:
    os:
      - ubuntu-22.04
      - ubuntu-24.04
      - ubuntu-latest
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:26-34]()

#### Debian Build Pipeline

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["build-deb job<br/>Matrix: 3 Ubuntu versions"]
    
    InstallDeps["Install build-essential<br/>debhelper, dh-python<br/>git-buildpackage, pybuild-plugin-pyproject"]
    ImportGPG["Import GPG key<br/>crazy-max/ghaction-import-gpg@v6"]
    Checkout["actions/checkout@v4<br/>fetch-tags: true<br/>fetch-depth: 0"]
    ExtractVer["Extract version from inputs<br/>MAJOR, MINOR, PATCH"]
    GenChangelog["gbp dch for changelog<br/>-N MAJOR.MINOR.PATCH"]
    BuildPkg["gbp buildpackage<br/>--git-ignore-new<br/>DEBSIGN_KEYID from GPG"]
    MoveDeb["Move .deb to artifacts/"]
    SetDistro["Set DISTRO_IDENT<br/>from /etc/os-release"]
    RenameFiles["Embed distro in filename<br/>*_all.deb → *_all-ubuntu-22.04.deb"]
    UploadDeb["Upload .deb artifact"]
    UploadChangelog["Upload debian/changelog"]
    UploadChanges["Upload .changes file"]
    
    Start --> InstallDeps
    InstallDeps --> ImportGPG
    ImportGPG --> Checkout
    Checkout --> ExtractVer
    ExtractVer --> GenChangelog
    GenChangelog --> BuildPkg
    BuildPkg --> MoveDeb
    MoveDeb --> SetDistro
    SetDistro --> RenameFiles
    RenameFiles --> UploadDeb
    RenameFiles --> UploadChangelog
    RenameFiles --> UploadChanges
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:36-178]()

#### GPG Signing

Packages are signed using a GPG key stored in GitHub Secrets:

```yaml
- name: Import GPG key
  id: gpg_key_import
  uses: crazy-max/ghaction-import-gpg@v6
  with:
    gpg_private_key: ${{ secrets.PKG_SIGNING_KEY_DEB }}
```

The fingerprint is passed to `gbp buildpackage` via `DEBSIGN_KEYID` environment variable.

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:67-133]()

#### Artifact Naming Strategy

Artifacts are renamed to embed distro identification to prevent filename collisions:

| Original Filename | Renamed Filename |
|------------------|------------------|
| `tt-tools-common_1.0.0_all.deb` | `tt-tools-common_1.0.0_all-ubuntu-22.04.deb` |
| `tt-tools-common_1.0.0_amd64.changes` | `tt-tools-common_1.0.0_amd64-ubuntu-22.04.changes` |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:143-158]()

### Build Dependencies

The Debian build requires specific packages for Python packaging and Debian tooling:

```bash
sudo apt install -y \
  build-essential \
  debhelper \
  dh-python \
  dh-sequence-python3 \
  git-buildpackage \
  gnupg \
  libpython3-all-dev \
  pybuild-plugin-pyproject \
  python3-all \
  python3-pip \
  python3-tomli
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:53-66]()

## Publishing Workflows

### TestPyPI Staging

The `publish-to-testpypi` job validates packages on the TestPyPI staging server before production publication. This job uses trusted publishing via OIDC tokens, eliminating the need for API keys.

#### TestPyPI Configuration

```yaml
environment:
  name: testpypi
  url: https://test.pypi.org/p/tt-tools-common

permissions:
  id-token: write  # IMPORTANT: mandatory for trusted publishing
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:391-405]()

The job downloads wheel artifacts and publishes using `pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish@release/v1`:

```yaml
- name: Download Python distributions
  uses: actions/download-artifact@v4
  with:
    pattern: tt-tools-common*.whl
    name: release-dists
    path: dist/
    
- name: Publish distribution 📦 to TestPyPI
  uses: pypa/gh-action-pypi-publish@release/v1
  with:
    repository-url: https://test.pypi.org/legacy/
    verbose: true
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:408-419]()

### Production PyPI Publication

The `publish-to-pypi` job runs only after TestPyPI validation succeeds. It uses identical configuration except for the target URL:

```yaml
needs:
  - build_all_depends
  - generate-release
  - publish-to-testpypi  # Ensures TestPyPI succeeded first
```

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:424-432]()

### Trusted Publishing with OIDC

Both PyPI publishing jobs use GitHub's OIDC provider for authentication instead of long-lived API tokens. This requires:

1. **GitHub Environment Configuration**: Environments named `testpypi` and `pypi` must be configured in repository settings
2. **PyPI Trusted Publisher Setup**: PyPI projects must register the GitHub repository as a trusted publisher
3. **Token Permissions**: Job must have `id-token: write` permission

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:404-405](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:438-439]()

## Supporting Workflows

### Community Issue Tagging

The `community-issue-tagging.yml` workflow automatically labels issues and PRs opened by external contributors using a reusable workflow from `tenstorrent/tt-github-actions`:

```yaml
jobs:
  community-labeling:
    uses: tenstorrent/tt-github-actions/.github/workflows/issues-community-autotag.yml@main
    secrets:
      AUTOLABEL_COMMUNITY_ISSUES: ${{ secrets.AUTOLABEL_COMMUNITY_ISSUES }}
```

**Triggers:**
- `issues: opened`
- `pull_request: opened`

**Permissions:**
- `contents: read`
- `issues: write`
- `pull-requests: write`

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/community-issue-tagging.yml:1-19]()

---

## Version Extraction for Packaging

The `setup.py` file provides backward compatibility for Ubuntu 22.04 packaging tools that don't fully support PEP 621 `pyproject.toml`. It dynamically extracts the version from `pyproject.toml` using `tomli`:

```python
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Compatibility setup.py for Ubuntu 22.04 packaging tools.
Uses setuptools_scm for dynamic versioning from git tags.
"""
from setuptools import setup, find_packages

import tomli

if __name__ == "__main__":
    with open("pyproject.toml", "rb") as f:
        toml_data = tomli.load(f)

    setup(
        name="tt-tools-common",
        version=toml_data['project']['version'],
        packages=find_packages(),
        python_requires=">=3.10",
    )
```

**Sources:** [setup.py:1-21]()

This approach ensures:
- Single source of truth: Version only exists in `pyproject.toml`
- Debian compatibility: `pybuild` can parse version information
- Build reproducibility: Same version used for both `.deb` and `.whl` artifacts

---

## Workflow Execution Summary

### Complete Release Pipeline Flow

The following table summarizes the complete execution order during a release:

| Step | Job Name | Workflow | Key Actions | Artifacts |
|------|----------|----------|-------------|-----------|
| 1 | `create-temp-branch` | release.yml | Creates `rc-temp-*` branch | Branch reference |
| 2 | `versionchange` | release.yml | Runs `bump2version`, extracts version components | Version outputs |
| 3 | `changelogs` | release.yml | Generates `debian/changelog` with `gbp dch` | Changelog commit |
| 4 | `build_all_depends` | build-all.yml | Triggers parallel builds | None (orchestrator) |
| 5a | `build-deb` | build-debian.yml | Matrix build for 3 Ubuntu versions | `.deb`, `.changes`, `changelog` |
| 5b | `buildpypi` | build-pypi.yml | Generates Python wheel | `.whl` |
| 6 | `tagrelease` | release.yml | Creates and pushes `v*.*.*` git tag | Git tag |
| 7 | `generate-release` | release.yml | Creates GitHub Release, attaches artifacts | GitHub Release |
| 8 | `publish-to-testpypi` | release.yml | Uploads to test.pypi.org | PyPI package |
| 9 | `publish-to-pypi` | release.yml | Uploads to pypi.org | PyPI package |
| 10 | `mergeback` | release.yml | Rebases to main, deletes temp branch | Merged commits |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:21-453]()

---

## Environment Variables and Secrets

### Required Secrets

| Secret Name | Used By | Purpose |
|------------|---------|---------|
| `PKG_SIGNING_KEY_DEB` | build-debian.yml | GPG private key for signing `.deb` packages |
| `AUTOLABEL_COMMUNITY_ISSUES` | community-issue-tagging.yml | Token for labeling external contributions |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:71](), [.github/workflows/community-issue-tagging.yml:18]()

### Environment Variables

Key environment variables used across workflows:

| Variable | Source | Purpose |
|----------|--------|---------|
| `EMAIL` | Hardcoded to `releases@tenstorrent.com` | Git commit author email |
| `NAME` | Hardcoded to `Tenstorrent Releases` | Git commit author name |
| `DEBSIGN_KEYID` | Output from `gpg_key_import` step | GPG key fingerprint for package signing |
| `MAJOR`, `MINOR`, `PATCH` | Output from `versionchange` job | Version components passed between jobs |
| `NUMBER_OF_COMMITS_SINCE_TAG` | Calculated from `git rev-list` | Development build identifier |

**Sources:** [.github/workflows/release.yml:158-160](), [.github/workflows/build-debian.yml:125-127](), [.github/workflows/release.yml:177-180]()

# Development Environment Setup

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [pyproject.toml](pyproject.toml)
- [tt_tools_common/tests/conftest.py](tt_tools_common/tests/conftest.py)

## Purpose and Scope

This document provides a comprehensive guide for setting up a local development environment for tt-tools-common. It covers installing the package in editable mode, managing development dependencies, and configuring the environment for both software-only and hardware-based testing.

For information about running tests after setup, see [Testing Guide](#6.1). For code quality tools configuration, see [Code Style and Quality Tools](#6.2). For understanding the automated testing infrastructure, see [CI/CD Pipeline Overview](#6.3).

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:1-84]()

---

## Prerequisites

### System Requirements

| Requirement | Specification | Notes |
|------------|--------------|-------|
| Python Version | ≥ 3.10 | 3.10, 3.11, and 3.12 officially supported |
| Operating System | Linux (Ubuntu 22.04/24.04 recommended) | ARM platforms have restrictions for some operations |
| Kernel Driver | tt-kmd ≥ 1.26.0 | Required only for hardware testing |
| Hardware | Tenstorrent chips (optional) | BH/WH/GS supported for hardware tests |

### Development Workflow Overview

```mermaid

    Activate["Activate Environment<br/>source venv/bin/activate"]
    
    InstallEditable["Install Editable Package<br/>pip install -e ."]
    InstallDev["Install Dev Dependencies<br/>pip install -e '.[dev]'"]
    
    subgraph "Optional Hardware Setup"
        InstallDriver["Install tt-kmd Driver<br/>≥1.26.0"]
        ConfigPyluwen["Verify pyluwen<br/>import pyluwen"]
        TestHW["Run Hardware Tests<br/>pytest -m requires_hardware"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Software-Only Development"
        ConfigPreCommit["Configure pre-commit<br/>pre-commit install"]
        RunTests["Run Software Tests<br/>pytest -m 'not requires_hardware'"]
        CodeFormat["Format Code<br/>black ."]
    end
    
    Clone --> VirtEnv
    VirtEnv --> Activate
    Activate --> InstallEditable
    InstallEditable --> InstallDev
    
    InstallDev --> ConfigPreCommit
    InstallDev --> InstallDriver

    ConfigPyluwen --> TestHW

## Installation for Development

### Step 1: Clone and Create Virtual Environment

```bash
# Clone the repository
git clone https://github.com/tenstorrent/tt-tools-common.git
cd tt-tools-common

# Create and activate virtual environment
python3 -m venv venv
source venv/bin/activate  # On Linux/macOS
# venv\Scripts\activate   # On Windows (if supported)
```

### Step 2: Install Package in Editable Mode

The editable installation allows code changes to be immediately reflected without reinstalling:

```bash
# Install with core dependencies only
pip install -e .

# Install with development dependencies (recommended)
pip install -e '.[dev]'
```

The `'.[dev]'` syntax installs the optional development dependencies defined in [pyproject.toml:36-43]().

### Step 3: Verify Installation

```bash
# Check package is installed
pip list | grep tt-tools-common

# Verify imports work
python3 -c "from tt_tools_common import reset_common, system_utils, ui_common"

# Check development tools (if installed with [dev])
black --version
pytest --version
```

### Editable Installation Details

| Installation Method | Command | Use Case |
|-------------------|---------|----------|
| Core only | `pip install -e .` | Consuming tt-tools-common in other projects |
| Full development | `pip install -e '.[dev]'` | Contributing to tt-tools-common |
| From PyPI (production) | `pip install tt-tools-common` | End-user installation |

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:1-43]()

---

## pyluwen Configuration for Hardware Testing

### pyluwen Installation and Role

`pyluwen` is the hardware abstraction layer that provides the `PciChip` interface for communicating with Tenstorrent devices. It is installed as part of the `[dev]` optional dependency group.

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Test Environment"
        PytestTests["pytest Tests"]
        Conftest["conftest.py<br/>fixtures"]
    end
    
    subgraph "tt-tools-common Hardware Interface"
        ResetCommon["reset_common/*<br/>ChipReset classes"]
        SystemUtils["system_utils.py<br/>Driver checks"]
        ToolsUtils["tools_utils.py<br/>detect_chips_with_callback"]
    end
    
    subgraph "pyluwen Library"
        DetectChips["pyluwen.detect_chips"]
        PciChip["pyluwen.PciChip"]
        Exceptions["pyluwen.PciError"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Kernel Space"
        TTKMD["tt-kmd Driver<br/>/dev/tenstorrent/*"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Hardware"
        Chips["BH/WH/GS Chips"]
    end
    
    PytestTests --> Conftest
    Conftest --> DetectChips
    
    ResetCommon --> PciChip
    SystemUtils --> PciChip
    ToolsUtils --> DetectChips
    ToolsUtils --> PciChip
    
    DetectChips --> TTKMD
    PciChip --> TTKMD
    
    TTKMD --> Chips
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:40](), [tt_tools_common/tests/conftest.py:1-12]()

### Hardware Testing Prerequisites

Before running hardware tests, ensure:

1. **Driver Installation**: The tt-kmd kernel driver must be installed and loaded:
   ```bash
   # Check driver version
   modinfo tenstorrent | grep version
   
   # Verify driver is loaded
   lsmod | grep tenstorrent
   
   # Check device nodes exist
   ls -la /dev/tenstorrent/
   ```

2. **Hardware Detection**: Verify pyluwen can detect devices:
   ```bash
   python3 -c "from pyluwen import detect_chips; print(detect_chips())"
   ```

3. **Permissions**: Ensure user has access to device nodes:
   ```bash
   # Add user to tenstorrent group (if it exists)
   sudo usermod -a -G tenstorrent $USER
   
   # Or check device permissions
   ls -l /dev/tenstorrent/*
   ```

### Test Fixture Configuration

The `conftest.py` file provides a `devices` fixture that wraps `pyluwen.detect_chips()`:

```python
# From tt_tools_common/tests/conftest.py
@pytest.fixture()
def devices():
    """Return devices detected on the system."""
    return detect_chips()
```

Tests requiring hardware use this fixture and the `requires_hardware` marker:

```python
@pytest.mark.requires_hardware
def test_chip_reset(devices):
    assert len(devices) > 0, "No hardware detected"
    # Test implementation...
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/tests/conftest.py:8-11](), [pyproject.toml:51-53]()

The package includes non-Python assets that are bundled during installation:

| Asset Type | Pattern | Purpose |

| Chip Data | `data/*/*.yaml` | Firmware definitions and chip configurations |
| Nested Configs | `data/*/*/*.yaml` | Additional configuration files |

These files are configured in [pyproject.toml:58-63]() and are accessible via `importlib.resources` or package-relative paths at runtime.

## Development Environment Validation

### Verification Checklist

After completing the setup, verify each component:

```bash
# 1. Check Python version
python3 --version  # Should be >=3.10

# 2. Verify package installation
python3 -c "import tt_tools_common; print(tt_tools_common.__file__)"

# 3. Check core dependencies
python3 -c "import textual, pydantic, pyyaml; print('Core deps OK')"

# 4. Verify dev dependencies (if installed with [dev])
black --version
pytest --version
pre-commit --version

# 5. Test pyluwen (if hardware available)
python3 -c "from pyluwen import detect_chips; print(f'Found {len(detect_chips())} devices')"

# 6. Run software tests
pytest -m "not requires_hardware" -v

# 7. Run hardware tests (if hardware available)
pytest -m requires_hardware -v
```

### Environment Configuration Check

```mermaid

    CheckDriver["Check tt-kmd<br/>modinfo tenstorrent"]

    RunSoftwareTests -->|No HW| Complete
```

## Common Setup Issues and Troubleshooting

### Issue: pyluwen Import Fails

**Symptom:**
```
ImportError: No module named 'pyluwen'
```

**Solution:**
```bash
# Ensure dev dependencies are installed
pip install -e '.[dev]'

# Or install pyluwen specifically
pip install 'pyluwen~=0.8.0'
```

### Issue: Hardware Tests Skip or Fail

**Symptom:**
```
ERROR: No hardware detected
```

**Solutions:**
1. Check driver is loaded: `lsmod | grep tenstorrent`
2. Verify driver version: `modinfo tenstorrent | grep version` (should be ≥1.26.0)
3. Check device nodes: `ls /dev/tenstorrent/`
4. Test pyluwen directly: `python3 -c "from pyluwen import detect_chips; print(detect_chips())"`

### Issue: Package Data Files Not Found

**Symptom:**
```
FileNotFoundError: data/chip_data/fw_defines.yaml not found
```

**Solution:**
Ensure package was installed with `-e` flag for editable mode, which preserves data file paths:
```bash
pip uninstall tt-tools-common
pip install -e .
```

### Issue: Pre-commit Hooks Fail

**Symptom:**
```
black...................................................................Failed
```

**Solution:**
```bash
# Install or reinstall pre-commit hooks
pre-commit install

# Run hooks manually to fix issues
pre-commit run --all-files

# Or format code directly
black .
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:36-43](), [pyproject.toml:51-53]()

---

## IDE and Editor Configuration

### VS Code Settings (Recommended)

Create `.vscode/settings.json` in the repository root:

```json
{
    "python.defaultInterpreterPath": "${workspaceFolder}/venv/bin/python",
    "python.formatting.provider": "black",
    "python.linting.enabled": true,
    "python.testing.pytestEnabled": true,
    "python.testing.pytestArgs": [
        "tt_tools_common/tests",
        "-v"
    ]
}
```

### pytest Configuration

The pytest configuration is defined in [pyproject.toml:50-53]() with custom markers:

| Marker | Purpose | Usage |
|--------|---------|-------|
| `requires_hardware` | Tests needing physical devices | `@pytest.mark.requires_hardware` |

To run only software tests (no hardware):
```bash
pytest -m "not requires_hardware"
```

To run only hardware tests:
```bash
pytest -m requires_hardware
```

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:50-53]()

---

## Development Workflow Summary

### Complete Setup Command Sequence

```bash
# 1. Initial setup
git clone https://github.com/tenstorrent/tt-tools-common.git
cd tt-tools-common
python3 -m venv venv
source venv/bin/activate

# 2. Install package and dependencies
pip install -e '.[dev]'

# 3. Configure pre-commit (for code quality)
pre-commit install

# 4. Verify installation
python3 -c "import tt_tools_common; print('✓ Package installed')"
pytest --version

# 5. Run tests
pytest -m "not requires_hardware" -v  # Software tests
pytest -m requires_hardware -v        # Hardware tests (if available)

# 6. Format code before committing
black .
pre-commit run --all-files
```

### Next Steps After Setup

After completing environment setup:

1. **Read the Testing Guide** ([#6.1](#6.1)) to understand test structure and markers
2. **Configure code quality tools** ([#6.2](#6.2)) for black formatting and linting
3. **Review CI/CD workflows** ([#6.3](#6.3)) to understand automated testing
4. **Explore API references** ([#7](#7)) for detailed module documentation

**Sources:** [pyproject.toml:1-84](), [tt_tools_common/tests/conftest.py:1-12]()

- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css](tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css)
- [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py](tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py)
- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py)
- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py)

</details>



This page provides a comprehensive overview of the public API exposed by `tt-tools-common`. The library organizes its functionality into four major subsystems: **Reset Operations**, **System Utilities**, **UI Components**, and **Data Models**. Each subsystem is detailed in its respective sub-page (see sections [7.1](#7.1) through [7.4](#7.4)).

This page focuses on module organization, import paths, and high-level API categories. For detailed documentation of individual classes, functions, and parameters, refer to the specialized sub-pages listed in the sections below.

---

## Module Organization

The `tt-tools-common` package is organized into three primary top-level modules, each containing specialized submodules:

| Module | Submodules | Purpose |
|--------|------------|---------|
| `reset_common` | `chip_reset`, `bh_reset`, `wh_reset`, `gs_reset`, `reset_utils`, `host_reset_log` | Chip reset operations and logging |
| `utils_common` | `system_utils`, `tools_utils` | System utilities and hardware detection |
| `ui_common` | `widgets`, `themes`, `common_style.css` | Textual UI components and styling |

**Diagram: Package Structure and Import Paths**

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "tt_tools_common Package"
        subgraph "reset_common"
            ChipReset["chip_reset.py<br/>ChipReset<br/>check_xen_hvm<br/>IoctlResetFlags"]
            BHReset["bh_reset.py<br/>BHChipReset"]
            WHReset["wh_reset.py<br/>WHChipReset"]
            GSReset["gs_reset.py<br/>GSTensixReset"]
            ResetUtils["reset_utils.py<br/>parse_reset_input<br/>generate_reset_logs<br/>ResetType"]
            HostLog["host_reset_log.py<br/>HostResetLog<br/>PciResetDeviceInfo<br/>MoboReset"]
        end
        
        subgraph "utils_common"
            SystemUtils["system_utils.py<br/>get_driver_version<br/>check_driver_version<br/>get_host_info<br/>get_host_compatibility_info"]
            ToolsUtils["tools_utils.py<br/>detect_chips_with_callback<br/>hex_to_semver*<br/>get_board_type<br/>init_fw_defines<br/>refclk_counter_rate"]
        end
        
        subgraph "ui_common"
            Widgets["widgets.py<br/>TTHeader, TTFooter<br/>TTDataTable, TTMenu<br/>TTConfirmBox<br/>TTSettingsMenu"]
            Themes["themes.py<br/>CMD_LINE_COLOR"]
            CSS["common_style.css<br/>Color Variables<br/>Widget Styles"]
        end

            ChipData["wormhole/fw_defines.yaml<br/>grayskull/fw_defines.yaml"]
        end
    end
    
    ChipReset -.depends.-> SystemUtils
    BHReset -.depends.-> ChipReset
    WHReset -.depends.-> ChipReset
    ResetUtils -.depends.-> HostLog
    ToolsUtils -.uses.-> ChipData
    Widgets -.uses.-> CSS
```

## Import Patterns

All public APIs are designed to be imported directly from their containing modules. The recommended import patterns are:

### Reset Operations
```python
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.chip_reset import ChipReset, check_xen_hvm, IoctlResetFlags
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.bh_reset import BHChipReset
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.wh_reset import WHChipReset
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.gs_reset import GSTensixReset
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.reset_utils import parse_reset_input, generate_reset_logs, ResetType
```

### System Utilities
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import (
    get_driver_version,
    check_driver_version,
    get_host_info,
    get_host_compatibility_info,
    is_driver_version_at_least
)
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import (
    detect_chips_with_callback,
    hex_to_semver,
    hex_to_semver_eth,
    hex_to_semver_m3_fw,
    hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw,
    get_board_type,
    refclk_counter_rate
)
```

### UI Components
```python
from tt_tools_common.ui_common.widgets import (
    TTHeader,
    TTFooter,
    TTDataTable,
    TTMenu,
    TTHostCompatibilityMenu,
    TTCompatibilityMenu,
    TTConfirmBox,
    TTHelperMenuBox,
    TTSettingsMenu
)
from tt_tools_common.ui_common.themes import CMD_LINE_COLOR
```

### Data Models
```python
from tt_tools_common.reset_common.host_reset_log import (
    HostResetLog,
    PciResetDeviceInfo,
    MoboReset,
    ElasticModel
)
```

Sources: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:1-24](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:1-16](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-19]()

### 1. Reset API (Detailed in [7.1](#7.1))

The reset subsystem provides chip-level reset functionality for Blackhole, Wormhole, and Grayskull architectures. Key entry points include:

| Function/Class | Module | Purpose |
|----------------|--------|---------|
| `ChipReset.full_lds_reset()` | `chip_reset` | Modern unified reset for BH/WH (driver >= 2.4.1) |
| `BHChipReset.full_lds_reset()` | `bh_reset` | Blackhole-specific reset with legacy fallback |
| `WHChipReset.full_lds_reset()` | `wh_reset` | Wormhole-specific reset with legacy fallback |
| `GSTensixReset.tensix_reset()` | `gs_reset` | Grayskull Tensix core reset |
| `parse_reset_input()` | `reset_utils` | Parse reset arguments (ALL/ID_LIST/CONFIG_JSON) |
| `generate_reset_logs()` | `reset_utils` | Generate HostResetLog JSON configuration |

**Common Pattern:**
```python
# Parse user input
reset_input = parse_reset_input(["0", "1", "2\
37:T67c8,
# Reset API Reference

<details>

- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py)

</details>



This page provides complete API documentation for all reset-related classes, functions, and data models in tt-tools-common. The reset system provides both modern unified reset implementations and chip-specific legacy implementations for Blackhole, Wormhole, and Grayskull devices.

For architectural information about how these components interact and the migration strategy from legacy to modern implementations, see [Reset Architecture and Design Patterns](#2.1). For detailed implementation guides for specific chip types, see [Blackhole Reset Implementation](#2.3), [Wormhole Reset Implementation](#2.4), and [Grayskull Tensix Reset](#2.5).

## Reset API Usage Flow

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["Application code needs to reset chips"]
    
    ParseInput["parse_reset_input(value)<br/>Returns ResetInput"]
    
    DetermineChip{"Chip type?"}
    
    BH["BHChipReset().full_lds_reset()"]
    WH["WHChipReset().full_lds_reset()"]
    GS["GSTensixReset(device).tensix_reset()"]
    
    CheckDriver{"Driver version<br/>>= 2.4.1?"}
    CheckXen{"Xen HVM<br/>detected?"}
    
    Modern["ChipReset().full_lds_reset()<br/>Modern unified implementation"]
    Legacy["Legacy chip-specific<br/>implementation"]
    
    IOCTL["reset_device_ioctl()<br/>IOCTL communication"]
    ARC["ARC message<br/>communication"]
    NOC["NOC read/write<br/>operations"]
    
    Logging["generate_reset_logs()<br/>Create HostResetLog"]
    
    Result["Returns List[PciChip]"]
    
    Start --> ParseInput
    ParseInput --> DetermineChip
    
    DetermineChip -->|Blackhole| BH
    DetermineChip -->|Wormhole| WH
    DetermineChip -->|Grayskull| GS
    
    BH --> CheckDriver
    WH --> CheckDriver
    
    CheckDriver -->|Yes| Modern
    CheckDriver -->|No| CheckXen
    CheckXen -->|Yes| Modern
    CheckXen -->|No| Legacy
    
    Modern --> IOCTL
    Legacy --> IOCTL
    Legacy --> ARC
    
    GS --> NOC
    
    IOCTL --> Result
    ARC --> Result
    NOC --> Logging
    
    Logging --> Result
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:33-87](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:68-99](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:68-90](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-133]()

## ChipReset Class

Modern unified reset implementation for Blackhole and Wormhole devices. Requires driver version >= 2.4.1.

**Class Definition:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:53-54]()

### Class Attributes

| Attribute | Type | Value | Description |
|-----------|------|-------|-------------|
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC` | `int` | `0xFA` | IOCTL magic number for Tenstorrent devices |
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_RESET_DEVICE` | `int` | `0xFA06` | IOCTL command code for device reset |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:56-58]()

### IoctlResetFlags Enum

```python
class IoctlResetFlags(IntEnum):
    RESTORE_STATE = 0        # Restore device state after reset
    RESET_PCIE_LINK = 1      # Perform secondary bus reset
    CONFIG_WRITE = 2         # Configuration space write
    USER_RESET = 3           # User-initiated reset
    ASIC_RESET = 4           # ASIC-only reset
    ASIC_DMC_RESET = 5       # ASIC + DMC/M3 reset
    POST_RESET = 6           # Post-reset cleanup actions
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:25-32]()

### Methods

#### full_lds_reset()

Performs a full LDS (Link Down State) reset of a list of chips using the modern unified reset sequence.

**Signature:**
```python
def full_lds_reset(
    self,
    pci_interfaces: List[int],
    reset_m3: bool = False,
    silent: bool = False,
    m3_delay: int = 20,
    secondary_bus_reset: bool = True,
) -> List[PciChip]
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `pci_interfaces` | `List[int]` | Required | List of PCI interface IDs to reset |
| `reset_m3` | `bool` | `False` | Whether M3/DMC should be reset (full board reset) |
| `silent` | `bool` | `False` | Whether to suppress console output |
| `m3_delay` | `int` | `20` | Time in seconds to wait after M3 reset |
| `secondary_bus_reset` | `bool` | `True` | Whether to perform secondary bus reset before ASIC reset |

**Returns:** `List[PciChip]` - List of `PciChip` objects for the reset devices.

**Raises:**
- `SystemExit` - If driver version < 2.4.1, platform is ARM, or reset operations fail
- `FileNotFoundError` - If device file `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}` doesn't exist

**Implementation Details:**

1. Validates driver version >= 2.4.1 and platform is not ARM [chip_reset.py:137-148]()
2. Collects BDF (Bus:Device.Function) for all devices [chip_reset.py:159-165]()
3. If Xen HVM detected, writes to xenstore to coordinate with host [chip_reset.py:169-193]()
4. Performs optional secondary bus reset using `RESET_PCIE_LINK` flag [chip_reset.py:196-203]()
5. Issues ASIC reset or ASIC+DMC reset based on `reset_m3` parameter [chip_reset.py:206-212]()
6. Waits for xenstore files to be removed by host if in Xen HVM mode [chip_reset.py:214-256]()
7. Waits for devices to reappear on PCI bus [chip_reset.py:267-268]()
8. Executes post-reset cleanup using `POST_RESET` flag [chip_reset.py:270-278]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:114-288]()

#### reset_device_ioctl()

Low-level method to issue IOCTL commands to the kernel driver for device reset operations.

**Signature:**
```python
def reset_device_ioctl(self, interface_id: int, flags: int) -> bool
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `interface_id` | `int` | PCI interface ID of the device |
| `flags` | `int` | Reset operation flags (use `IoctlResetFlags` enum) |

**Returns:** `bool` - `True` if operation succeeded, `False` otherwise.

**Implementation:** Opens `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}`, packs reset request struct with output size and flags, executes `fcntl.ioctl()`, and unpacks result.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:60-85]()

#### wait_for_device_to_reappear()

Waits for a device to reappear on the PCI bus after reset, typically after PCIe hot-plug removal/insertion.

**Signature:**
```python
def wait_for_device_to_reappear(self, bdf: str, timeout: int = 10) -> int
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `bdf` | `str` | Required | PCI Bus:Device.Function string (e.g., "0000:01:00.0") |
| `timeout` | `int` | `10` | Maximum wait time in seconds |

**Returns:** `int` - New PCI interface ID for the device.

**Raises:** `SystemExit` - If device doesn't reappear within timeout.

**Implementation:** Polls `/sys/bus/pci/devices/{bdf}/tenstorrent/tenstorrent!*` and `/dev/tenstorrent/{interface_id}` until both exist or timeout expires.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:87-111]()

---

## BHChipReset Class

Blackhole-specific reset implementation with automatic delegation to `ChipReset` when conditions are met.

**Class Definition:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:27-28]()

### Class Attributes

| Attribute | Type | Value | Description |
|-----------|------|-------|-------------|
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC` | `int` | `0xFA` | IOCTL magic number |
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_RESET_DEVICE` | `int` | `0xFA06` | IOCTL reset command |
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESTORE_STATE` | `int` | `0` | Restore state flag |
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESET_PCIE_LINK` | `int` | `1` | PCIe link reset flag |
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_CONFIG_WRITE` | `int` | `2` | Config write flag |
| `A3_STATE_PROP_TIME` | `float` | `0.03` | A3 state propagation time in seconds |
| `POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME` | `int` | `2` | Post-reset wait time in seconds |
| `MSG_TRIGGER_SPI_COPY_LtoR` | `int` | `0x50` | ARC message: trigger SPI copy |
| `MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3` | `int` | `0xA3` | ARC message: enter A3 state |
| `MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET` | `int` | `0x56` | ARC message: trigger reset |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:30-40]()

### Methods

#### full_lds_reset()

Performs full LDS reset for Blackhole devices. Automatically delegates to modern `ChipReset` implementation when driver version >= 2.4.1 or running under Xen HVM.

**Signature:**
```python
def full_lds_reset(
    self,
    pci_interfaces: List[int],
    reset_m3: bool = False,
    silent: bool = False,
    m3_delay: int = 20,
    secondary_bus_reset: bool = True,
) -> List[PciChip]
```

**Parameters:** Same as `ChipReset.full_lds_reset()` (see above).

**Returns:** `List[PciChip]` - List of reset devices.

**Delegation Logic:**
1. Checks driver version using `is_driver_version_at_least(get_driver_version(), "2.4.1")` [bh_reset.py:92]()
2. Checks for Xen HVM using `check_xen_hvm()` [bh_reset.py:92]()
3. If either condition is true, delegates to `ChipReset().full_lds_reset()` [bh_reset.py:93-99]()
4. Otherwise, executes legacy implementation [bh_reset.py:101-223]()

**Legacy Implementation Flow:**
1. Validates platform is not ARM [bh_reset.py:111-118]()
2. Collects PCI BDF for all devices [bh_reset.py:127-136]()
3. Issues reset IOCTLs or ARC messages based on `reset_m3` [bh_reset.py:137-144]()
4. Polls config space reset bit until completion [bh_reset.py:150-192]()
5. Restores device state [bh_reset.py:207-210]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:68-223]()

#### reset_device_ioctl()

Identical to `ChipReset.reset_device_ioctl()`. See ChipReset documentation above.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:42-66]()

---

## WHChipReset Class

Wormhole-specific reset implementation with automatic delegation to `ChipReset` when conditions are met.

**Class Definition:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:28-29]()

### Class Attributes

| Attribute | Type | Value | Description |
|-----------|------|-------|-------------|
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_MAGIC` | `int` | `0xFA` | IOCTL magic number |
| `TENSTORRENT_IOCTL_RESET_DEVICE` | `int` | `0xFA06` | IOCTL reset command |
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESTORE_STATE` | `int` | `0` | Restore state flag |
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESET_PCIE_LINK` | `int` | `1` | PCIe link reset flag |
| `A3_STATE_PROP_TIME` | `float` | `0.03` | A3 state propagation time |
| `POST_RESET_MSG_WAIT_TIME` | `int` | `2` | Post-reset wait time |
| `MSG_TRIGGER_SPI_COPY_LtoR` | `int` | `0x50` | ARC message: trigger SPI copy |
| `MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3` | `int` | `0xA3` | ARC message: enter A3 safe state |
| `MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET` | `int` | `0x56` | ARC message: trigger reset |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:31-40]()

### Methods

#### full_lds_reset()

Performs full LDS reset for Wormhole devices. Automatically delegates to modern `ChipReset` implementation when driver version >= 2.4.1 or running under Xen HVM.

**Signature:**
```python
def full_lds_reset(
    self,
    pci_interfaces: List[int],
    reset_m3: bool = False,
    silent: bool = False,
    secondary_bus_reset: bool = True,
) -> List[PciChip]
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `pci_interfaces` | `List[int]` | Required | List of PCI interface IDs to reset |
| `reset_m3` | `bool` | `False` | Whether M3 should be reset |
| `silent` | `bool` | `False` | Whether to suppress output |
| `secondary_bus_reset` | `bool` | `True` | Whether to perform secondary bus reset |

**Note:** Unlike BH reset, WH does not expose `m3_delay` parameter.

**Returns:** `List[PciChip]` - List of reset devices.

**Delegation Logic:**
1. Checks driver version >= 2.4.1 or Xen HVM [wh_reset.py:89]()
2. If true, delegates to `ChipReset().full_lds_reset()` [wh_reset.py:90]()
3. Otherwise, executes legacy implementation [wh_reset.py:92-180]()

**Legacy Implementation Flow:**
1. Validates driver version >= 1.26.0 and platform is not ARM [wh_reset.py:101-112]()
2. Issues PCIe link reset IOCTL for all devices [wh_reset.py:121-124]()
3. Reads reference clock counters before reset [wh_reset.py:126-141]()
4. Sends ARC message to enter A3 safe state [wh_reset.py:143-144]()
5. Triggers ASIC or M3 reset via ARC message [wh_reset.py:146-149]()
6. Validates reset by comparing reference clock counters [wh_reset.py:153-164]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:68-180]()

#### reset_device_ioctl()

Identical to `ChipReset.reset_device_ioctl()`. See ChipReset documentation above.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:42-66]()

---

## GSTensixReset Class

Grayskull-specific Tensix core reset implementation using NOC operations.

**Class Definition:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:17-20]()

### Class Attributes

| Attribute | Type | Value | Description |
|-----------|------|-------|-------------|
| `NIU_CFG_0` | `int` | `0x100` | NIU config register 0 (bit 0: CG enable, bit 12: tile clock disable) |
| `ROUTER_CFG_0` | `int` | `0x104` | Router config register 0 (bit 0: CG enable) |
| `ROUTER_CFG_1` | `int` | `0x108` | Router config register 1 (broadcast disable) |
| `ROUTER_CFG_3` | `int` | `0x110` | Router config register 3 (row broadcast disable) |
| `GRID_SIZE_X` | `int` | `13` | Grid width |
| `GRID_SIZE_Y` | `int` | `12` | Grid height |
| `NUM_TENSIX_X` | `int` | `12` | Number of Tensix columns |
| `NUM_TENSIX_Y` | `int` | `10` | Number of Tensix rows |
| `NOC_MAX_BACKOFF_EXP` | `int` | `0xF` | Maximum exponential backoff for NOC |
| `PHYS_Y_TO_NOC_0_Y` | `List[int]` | `[0,11,1,10,2,9,3,8,4,7,5,6]` | Physical Y to NOC0 Y mapping |
| `DRAM_LOCATIONS` | `List[Tuple]` | (see code) | DRAM core coordinates |
| `ARC_LOCATIONS` | `List[Tuple]` | `[(0, 2)]` | ARC core coordinates |
| `PCI_LOCATIONS` | `List[Tuple]` | `[(0, 4)]` | PCI core coordinates |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:23-45]()

### Constructor

```python
def __init__(self, device: PciChip)
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `device` | `PciChip` | Grayskull PciChip object to reset |

**Initialization:**
1. Builds routing-to-physical coordinate lookup table [gs_tensix_reset.py:51-56]()
2. Initializes AXI register interface [gs_tensix_reset.py:58]()
3. Loads firmware defines for Grayskull [gs_tensix_reset.py:59]()
4. Detects harvested rows from efuses [gs_tensix_reset.py:60]()
5. Builds list of active (non-harvested) cores [gs_tensix_reset.py:61]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:47-61]()

### Methods

#### tensix_reset()

Resets all Tensix cores on the Grayskull chip, leaving un-harvested RISCs in soft reset.

**Signature:**
```python
def tensix_reset(self, silent: bool = False) -> None
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `silent` | `bool` | `False` | Whether to suppress console output |

**Returns:** `None`

**Implementation Flow:**
1. Lowers clocks to safe values [gs_tensix_reset.py:376]()
2. Asserts hard reset on all RISCs [gs_tensix_reset.py:384]()
3. Toggles reset on all Tensix cores [gs_tensix_reset.py:385]()
4. Configures NOC routers with broadcast disables [gs_tensix_reset.py:386]()
5. Asserts soft reset on un-harvested RISCs via NOC broadcast [gs_tensix_reset.py:387]()
6. Deasserts hard reset on un-harvested RISCs only [gs_tensix_reset.py:388]()
7. Restores clocks to original values [gs_tensix_reset.py:402]()

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:366-402]()

#### get_harvested_rows()

Reads harvesting fuses to determine which Tensix rows are disabled.

**Signature:**
```python
def get_harvested_rows(self) -> frozenset[int]
```

**Returns:** `frozenset[int]` - Set of NOC0 Y coordinates for harvested rows.

**Implementation:** Reads harvesting fuses via ARC message `MSG_TYPE_ARC_GET_HARVESTING` or from environment variable `T6PY_HARVESTING_OVERRIDE`.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:71-97]()

#### get_core_list()

Builds a dictionary of active (non-harvested) Tensix cores.

**Signature:**
```python
def get_core_list(self) -> Dict[Tuple[int, int], None]
```

**Returns:** `Dict[Tuple[int, int], None]` - Dictionary with NOC coordinates as keys for deterministic ordering.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:99-115]()

#### setup_noc()

Configures all NOC nodes with appropriate broadcast disables, clock gating, and backoff settings.

**Signature:**
```python
def setup_noc(self) -> None
```

**Implementation:** Iterates through all NOC coordinates and writes configuration registers based on node type (DRAM, ARC, PCI, or Tensix). For Tensix cores, also sets tile clock disable bit for harvested cores.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:188-318]()

#### set_safe_clks()

Sends ARC message to enter or exit safe clock mode.

**Signature:**
```python
def set_safe_clks(self, enter_safe_clks: bool) -> None
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `enter_safe_clks` | `bool` | `True` to lower clocks, `False` to restore |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/gs_tensix_reset.py:143-162]()

---

## Helper Functions

### parse_reset_input()

Parses command-line arguments into structured reset input.

**Signature:**
```python
def parse_reset_input(value: list) -> ResetInput
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `value` | `list` | List of string arguments from command line |

**Returns:** `ResetInput` - Dataclass containing:
- `type`: One of `ResetType.ALL`, `ResetType.CONFIG_JSON`, or `ResetType.ID_LIST`
- `value`: `None` for ALL, `Dict` for CONFIG_JSON, `List[int]` for ID_LIST

**Parsing Rules:**
1. Empty list or `["all"]` → `ResetType.ALL` with `value=None`
2. Single argument that is valid file path → `ResetType.CONFIG_JSON` with parsed JSON dict
3. Single argument with commas (e.g., "0,1,2") → `ResetType.ID_LIST` with list of ints
4. Multiple arguments → `ResetType.ID_LIST` with list of ints

**Raises:** `SystemExit` if input cannot be parsed.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:33-87]()

### generate_reset_logs()

Generates and saves reset configuration logs in Elasticsearch-compatible JSON format.

**Signature:**
```python
def generate_reset_logs(devices, result_filename: str = None) -> str
```

**Parameters:**

| Parameter | Type | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|---------|-------------|
| `devices` | `List[PciChip]` | Required | List of detected devices |
| `result_filename` | `str` | `None` | Output file path (default: `~/.config/tenstorrent/reset_config.json`) |

**Returns:** `str` - Path to the generated log file.

**Generated Structure:**
- Separates Wormhole and Grayskull devices
- Creates `HostResetLog` with sample mobo reset configurations
- Includes device lists for `gs_tensix_reset` and `wh_link_reset`
- Sets timestamps and hostname

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:89-134]()

### check_xen_hvm()

Detects if the system is running as a Xen HVM guest.

**Signature:**
```python
def check_xen_hvm() -> bool
```

**Returns:** `bool` - `True` if running under Xen HVM, `False` otherwise.

**Implementation:** Reads `/sys/hypervisor/type` and `/sys/hypervisor/guest_type`, returns `True` only if both read "xen" and "HVM" respectively.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:34-51]()

---

Saves the model as formatted JSON to a file.

## API Constants

### IOCTL Reset Device Flags

The following constants are used as flags for the `reset_device_ioctl()` method:

| Constant | Value | Usage |
|----------|-------|-------|
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESTORE_STATE` | `0` | Restore device configuration state (BH/WH legacy) |
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_RESET_PCIE_LINK` | `1` | Perform PCIe secondary bus reset (BH/WH legacy) |
| `TENSTORRENT_RESET_DEVICE_CONFIG_WRITE` | `2` | Perform config space reset (BH legacy) |
| `IoctlResetFlags.USER_RESET` | `3` | User-initiated reset (ChipReset modern) |
| `IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_RESET` | `4` | ASIC-only reset (ChipReset modern) |
| `IoctlResetFlags.ASIC_DMC_RESET` | `5` | ASIC + DMC/M3 reset (ChipReset modern) |
| `IoctlResetFlags.POST_RESET` | `6` | Post-reset cleanup (ChipReset modern) |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/chip_reset.py:25-32](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:33-35](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:34-35]()

### ARC Message Types

ARC firmware messages used in reset operations:

| Constant | Value | Description |
|----------|-------|-------------|
| `MSG_TRIGGER_SPI_COPY_LtoR` | `0x50` | Trigger SPI copy from left to right |
| `MSG_TYPE_ARC_STATE3` | `0xA3` | Enter A3 safe state (no pending regulator requests) |
| `MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET` | `0x56` | Trigger device reset |

**Usage:**
- `arg0=3` with `MSG_TYPE_TRIGGER_RESET` triggers full M3/DMC reset
- `arg0` omitted or other values trigger ASIC-only reset

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/reset_common/bh_reset.py:38-40](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/wh_reset.py:38-40]()
