# System Utilities API Reference

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py)
- [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py](tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py)

</details>



## Purpose and Scope

This page provides complete API documentation for the system utilities modules in tt-tools-common. These modules provide foundational functionality for driver management, host information collection, hardware detection, and version conversions used across all Tenstorrent tools.

The system utilities are organized into two modules:
- **`system_utils`**: Driver version checking, host information gathering, and software version reporting
- **`tools_utils`**: Chip detection, firmware data loading, version conversions, and reference clock monitoring

For documentation of the hardware reset system that uses these utilities, see [Reset API Reference](#7.1). For UI components that display system information, see [UI Components API Reference](#7.3).

---

## Module Organization

The system utilities provide distinct but complementary capabilities:

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "system_utils Module"
        DriverAPI["Driver Version API<br/>get_driver_version()<br/>check_driver_version()<br/>is_driver_version_at_least()"]
        HostAPI["Host Information API<br/>get_host_info()<br/>get_host_compatibility_info()"]
        SoftwareAPI["Software Version API<br/>get_sw_ver_info()<br/>get_sw_ver_from_url()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "tools_utils Module"
        ChipDataAPI["Chip Data API<br/>init_fw_defines()<br/>get_chip_data()"]
        BoardAPI["Board Identification API<br/>get_board_type()"]
        VersionAPI["Version Conversion API<br/>hex_to_semver_*()<br/>hex_to_date()"]
        RefclkAPI["Reference Clock API<br/>read_refclk_counter()<br/>refclk_counter_rate()"]
        DetectAPI["Chip Detection API<br/>detect_chips_with_callback()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "External Dependencies"
        PyLuwen["pyluwen.PciChip"]
        Psutil["psutil"]
        Distro["distro"]
        Requests["requests"]
    end
    
    DriverAPI -->|"reads from"| SysFS["/sys/module/tenstorrent/version"]
    HostAPI --> Psutil
    HostAPI --> Distro
    SoftwareAPI --> Requests
    
    ChipDataAPI -->|"loads"| YAMLFiles["data/*/fw_defines.yaml"]
    BoardAPI -->|"parses"| SerialNumber["Board ID format"]
    DetectAPI --> PyLuwen
    RefclkAPI --> PyLuwen
    
    style DriverAPI fill:#f9f9f9
    style HostAPI fill:#f9f9f9
    style ChipDataAPI fill:#f9f9f9
    style DetectAPI fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:1-296](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:1-355]()

---

## system_utils Module API

The `system_utils` module provides system-level utilities for driver management, host information collection, and compatibility checking.

### Driver Version Management

#### `get_driver_version() -> Union[str, None]`

Returns the version string of the currently installed Tenstorrent kernel driver.

**Returns:**
- `str`: Version string (e.g., "1.26.0", "2.4.1-rc1")
- `None`: If no driver is detected

**Implementation Details:**
- Reads from `/sys/module/tenstorrent/version`
- Returns `None` on any exception (file not found, permission denied, etc.)

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import get_driver_version

version = get_driver_version()
if version:
    print(f"Driver version: {version}")
else:
    print("No Tenstorrent driver detected")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:35-45]()

---

#### `is_driver_version_at_least(current_version: str, minimum_version: str) -> bool`

Compares two semantic version strings to determine if the current version meets or exceeds the minimum required version.

**Parameters:**
- `current_version` (str): Current driver version to check
- `minimum_version` (str): Minimum required version

**Returns:**
- `bool`: `True` if current version >= minimum version, `False` otherwise

**Raises:**
- `ValueError`: If `current_version` is `None` or if version strings are malformed

**Supported Version Formats:**
- Standard SemVer: `"1.34.0"`
- Short version: `"1.34"` (patch defaults to 0)
- Pre-release: `"1.34.0-alpha"` (pre-release suffix stripped)
- Build metadata: `"1.2.3+build456"` (build suffix stripped)
- Combined: `"1.4.0-rc1+build42"`

**Version Comparison Logic:**
Version tuples are compared lexicographically: `(major, minor, patch)`
- `(1, 34, 0) >= (1, 26, 0)` → `True`
- `(1, 26, 0) >= (1, 26, 0)` → `True`
- `(2, 0, 0) >= (1, 35, 0)` → `True`
- `(1, 25, 0) >= (1, 26, 0)` → `False`

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:47-97]()

---

#### `check_driver_version(operation: str, minimum_required_version_str: str = "1.26.0")`

Validates that the installed driver version is sufficient for the specified operation. Exits the program with status code 1 if validation fails.

**Parameters:**
- `operation` (str): Description of the operation requiring the driver (e.g., "chip reset", "firmware update")
- `minimum_required_version_str` (str, optional): Minimum required version. Defaults to `"1.26.0"` (`MINIMUM_DRIVER_VERSION_LDS_RESET`)

**Exit Conditions:**
The function calls `sys.exit(1)` if:
- No driver is detected (`current_version` is `None`)
- Version strings are malformed
- Current driver version < minimum required version

**Output:**
Prints colored error messages to stdout indicating:
- Current driver version
- Required minimum version for the operation
- Instructions to update driver via tt-kmd

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import check_driver_version

# Will exit if driver version < 1.26.0
check_driver_version("chip reset")

# Check for custom minimum version
check_driver_version("advanced feature", "2.4.1")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:99-142]()

---

### Host Information Collection

#### `get_host_info() -> dict`

Collects comprehensive host system information including OS, distribution, kernel, hardware platform, and driver version.

**Returns:**
Dictionary with the following keys:
| Key | Type | Description | Example |
|-----|------|-------------|---------|
| `"OS"` | str | Operating system name | `"Linux"` |
| `"Distro"` | str | Distribution name (pretty format) | `"Ubuntu 22.04.3 LTS"` |
| `"Kernel"` | str | Kernel release version | `"5.15.0-91-generic"` |
| `"Hostname"` | str | System hostname | `"tt-server-01"` |
| `"Platform"` | str | Hardware architecture | `"x86_64"`, `"aarch64"` |
| `"Python"` | str | Python interpreter version | `"3.10.12"` |
| `"Memory"` | str | Total system memory (human-readable) | `"64.00 GB"` |
| `"Driver"` | str | Tenstorrent driver version with prefix | `"TT-KMD 1.26.0"` |

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import get_host_info

info = get_host_info()
for key, value in info.items():
    print(f"{key}: {value}")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:145-168]()

---

#### `get_host_compatibility_info() -> Dict[str, Union[str, Tuple]]`

Returns host information with compatibility validation against Tenstorrent system requirements.

**Returns:**
Dictionary where:
- **Compatible items**: Value is a `str` with the current state
- **Incompatible items**: Value is a `Tuple[str, str]` where:
  - First element: Current state
  - Second element: Required/recommended state

**Compatibility Rules:**
| Item | Compatible Condition | Required Value |
|------|---------------------|----------------|
| OS | `"Linux"` | `"Linux (x86_64)"` |
| Distro | Ubuntu >= 22.04 | `"22.04 or 24.04"` |
| Memory | >= 32 GB | `"32GB+"` |
| Driver | Driver detected | `"TT-KMD v1.27+"` |
| Kernel | Always compatible | N/A |
| Hostname | Always compatible | N/A |
| Python | Always compatible | N/A |

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import get_host_compatibility_info

checklist = get_host_compatibility_info()
for key, value in checklist.items():
    if isinstance(value, tuple):
        print(f"⚠️  {key}: {value[0]} (requires {value[1]})")
    else:
        print(f"✓ {key}: {value}")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:170-211]()

---

### Software Version Reporting

#### `get_sw_ver_info(show_sw_ver: bool, board_ids: str) -> dict`

Retrieves software version information for Tenstorrent tools and frameworks, optionally querying a remote server based on board serial numbers.

**Parameters:**
- `show_sw_ver` (bool): Whether to fetch version information. If `False`, returns default "N/A" values
- `board_ids` (str): List of board serial numbers to query

**Returns:**
Dictionary with keys for various software components:
| Key | Description |
|-----|-------------|
| `"Firmware Bundle"` | Firmware bundle version |
| `"tt-smi"` | tt-smi tool version |
| `"tt-flash"` | tt-flash tool version |
| `"tt-kmd"` | Kernel driver version |
| `"TT-Buda"` | TT-Buda framework version |
| `"TT-Metalium"` | TT-Metalium framework version |

**Behavior:**
1. Checks for `~/.config/tenstorrent/reset_config.json` for reporting flags
2. If `disable_sw_version_report` flag is set, returns default values
3. If `disable_serial_report` flag is set, queries server with empty board ID
4. Otherwise, queries server with provided board IDs

**Remote Query:**
- Endpoint: `https://cereal.tenstorrent.com?SerialNumber={board_id}`
- Handles HTTP errors, connection errors, timeouts gracefully
- Returns error messages in `"Failed to fetch"` key on failure

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:269-295](), [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:230-267]()

---

#### `get_sw_ver_from_url(board_id: str) -> dict`

Internal function that performs the HTTP request to fetch software versions for a specific board.

**Parameters:**
- `board_id` (str): Board serial number in hex format

**Returns:**
Dictionary with software component versions or error messages

**Error Handling:**
| Exception | Error Message |
|-----------|--------------|
| `HTTPError` | `"We encountered an HTTP error."` |
| `ConnectionError` | `"There was an error connecting to the server. Please check your internet connection."` |
| `Timeout` | `"Timeout error. It seems the server is taking too long to respond."` |
| `RequestException` | `"Something unexpected happened."` |
| JSON decode error | `"No response from server"` |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:230-267]()

---

### Utility Functions

#### `get_size(size_bytes: int, suffix: str = "B") -> str`

Converts byte count to human-readable format with appropriate unit scaling.

**Parameters:**
- `size_bytes` (int): Size in bytes
- `suffix` (str, optional): Unit suffix. Defaults to `"B"`

**Returns:**
- `str`: Formatted size string (e.g., `"1.20 MB"`, `"1.17 GB"`)

**Scaling:**
Uses 1024-based units: `B`, `KB`, `MB`, `GB`, `TB`, `PB`

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import get_size

print(get_size(1253656))      # "1.20 MB"
print(get_size(1253656678))   # "1.17 GB"
print(get_size(32 * 1024**3)) # "32.00 GB"
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:20-32]()

---

## tools_utils Module API

The `tools_utils` module provides tool-specific utilities for chip detection, firmware data loading, version conversions, and hardware monitoring.

### Chip Data and Firmware Definitions

#### `init_fw_defines(chip_name: str = "wormhole", tool_name: str = "tt_smi") -> dict`

Loads firmware message definitions from the chip's data directory.

**Parameters:**
- `chip_name` (str, optional): Chip architecture name. Defaults to `"wormhole"`. Valid values: `"wormhole"`, `"grayskull"`
- `tool_name` (str, optional): Tool name for path resolution. Defaults to `"tt_smi"`

**Returns:**
- `dict`: Parsed YAML content from `fw_defines.yaml`

**File Loading:**
Loads from: `data/{chip_name}/fw_defines.yaml`

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import init_fw_defines

wh_defines = init_fw_defines("wormhole")
gs_defines = init_fw_defines("grayskull")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:17-24]()

---

#### `get_chip_data(chip_name: str, file: str, internal: bool, tool_name: str = "tt_smi")`

Loads arbitrary data files from the chip's data directory.

**Parameters:**
- `chip_name` (str): Chip architecture name (`"wormhole"` or `"grayskull"`)
- `file` (str): Filename to load
- `internal` (bool): If `True`, loads from `.ignored/{chip_name}/`, otherwise `data/{chip_name}/`
- `tool_name` (str, optional): Tool name for path resolution. Defaults to `"tt_smi"`

**Returns:**
- File object opened in read mode

**Raises:**
- `Exception`: If chip_name is not `"wormhole"` or `"grayskull"`

**Path Resolution:**
- External files: `data/{chip_name}/{file}`
- Internal files: `.ignored/{chip_name}/{file}`

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:31-43]()

---

### Board Type Identification

#### `get_board_type(board_id: str) -> str`

Extracts board type from a board ID serial number string.

**Parameters:**
- `board_id` (str): Board ID in hex format (e.g., `"01000012345678"`)

**Returns:**
- `str`: Board type identifier or `"N/A"` if unknown

**Board ID Format:**
```
AA-BBBBB-C-D-EE-FF-XXX
│   │    │ │  │  │  └─ XXX: Additional info
│   │    │ │  │  └──── FF: Manufacturer
│   │    │ │  └─────── EE: Region
│   │    │ └────────── D: Reserved
│   │    └──────────── C: Revision
│   └───────────────── BBBBB: Unique Part Identifier (UPI)
└────────────────────── AA: Reserved
```

**UPI to Board Type Mapping:**
| UPI (hex) | Revision | Board Type |
|-----------|----------|------------|
| 0x1 | 0x2 | `"E300_R2"` |
| 0x1 | 0x3, 0x4 | `"E300_R3"` |
| 0x3 | Any | `"e150"` |
| 0x7 | Any | `"e75"` |
| 0x8 | Any | `"NEBULA_CB"` |
| 0xA | Any | `"e300"` |
| 0xB | Any | `"GALAXY"` |
| 0x14 | Any | `"n300"` |
| 0x18 | Any | `"n150"` |
| Other | Any | `"N/A"` |

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import get_board_type

board_type = get_board_type("0A00001234567890")
print(f"Board type: {board_type}")  # "e300"
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:46-90]()

---

### Version Conversion Functions

The module provides multiple version conversion functions for different firmware components with varying encoding schemes.

```mermaid
graph LR
    subgraph "Hex Encodings"
        Standard["Standard<br/>0x0A0F0100<br/>(4 bytes)"]
        ETH["Ethernet<br/>0x061000<br/>(3 bytes)"]
        M3["M3 Firmware<br/>0x0A0F0164<br/>(4 bytes + ver)"]
        Zephyr["Zephyr<br/>0x0A0F0101<br/>(4 bytes + rc)"]
        Date["Date<br/>0x4B181430<br/>(YMDDHHMM)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Conversion Functions"
        HexToSemver["hex_to_semver()"]
        HexToSemverETH["hex_to_semver_eth()"]
        HexToSemverM3["hex_to_semver_m3_fw()"]
        HexToSemverZephyr["hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw()"]
        HexToDate["hex_to_date()"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Output Formats"
        SemVerStd["10.15.1"]
        SemVerETH["6.1.0"]
        SemVerM3["10.15.1.100"]
        SemVerZephyr["10.15.1-rc1"]
        DateStr["2024-11-24 20:48"]
    end
    
    Standard --> HexToSemver --> SemVerStd
    ETH --> HexToSemverETH --> SemVerETH
    M3 --> HexToSemverM3 --> SemVerM3
    Zephyr --> HexToSemverZephyr --> SemVerZephyr
    Date --> HexToDate --> DateStr
    
    style HexToSemver fill:#f9f9f9
    style HexToSemverETH fill:#f9f9f9
    style HexToSemverM3 fill:#f9f9f9
    style HexToSemverZephyr fill:#f9f9f9
    style HexToDate fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:93-189]()

---

#### `hex_to_semver(hexsemver: int) -> str`

Converts standard firmware version from hex to semantic version string.

**Encoding:** `0xZZMMNNPP` where:
- Byte 3 (0xZZ): Reserved/unused
- Byte 2 (0xMM): Major version
- Byte 1 (0xNN): Minor version
- Byte 0 (0xPP): Patch version

**Parameters:**
- `hexsemver` (int): Hex-encoded version

**Returns:**
- `str`: Version string in format `"major.minor.patch"`

**Raises:**
- `ValueError`: If `hexsemver` is `0` or `0xFFFFFFFF` (invalid values)

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import hex_to_semver

version = hex_to_semver(0x0A0F0100)  # Returns "10.15.1"
version = hex_to_semver(0x01020003)  # Returns "1.2.3"
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:136-145]()

---

#### `hex_to_semver_eth(hexsemver: int) -> str`

Converts Ethernet firmware version from hex to semantic version string.

**Encoding:** `0x00MMMPPP` where:
- Bits 23-16 (0xMM): Major version
- Bits 15-12 (0xN): Minor version (4 bits)
- Bits 11-0 (0xPPP): Patch version (12 bits)

**Parameters:**
- `hexsemver` (int): Hex-encoded version

**Returns:**
- `str`: Version string in format `"major.minor.patch"` or `"N/A"` if invalid

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import hex_to_semver_eth

version = hex_to_semver_eth(0x061000)  # Returns "6.1.0"
version = hex_to_semver_eth(0x000000)  # Returns "N/A"
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:148-157]()

---

#### `hex_to_semver_m3_fw(hexsemver: int) -> str`

Converts M3 firmware version from hex to semantic version string with 4-part version.

**Encoding:** `0xMMNNPPVV` where:
- Byte 3 (0xMM): Major version
- Byte 2 (0xNN): Minor version
- Byte 1 (0xPP): Patch version
- Byte 0 (0xVV): Version/build number

**Parameters:**
- `hexsemver` (int): Hex-encoded version

**Returns:**
- `str`: Version string in format `"major.minor.patch.ver"` or `"N/A"` if invalid

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import hex_to_semver_m3_fw

version = hex_to_semver_m3_fw(0x0A0F0164)  # Returns "10.15.1.100"
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:160-170]()

---

#### `hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw(hexsemver: int) -> str`

Converts Zephyr firmware version from hex to semantic version string with optional release candidate suffix.

**Encoding:** `0xMMNNPPRR` where:
- Byte 3 (0xMM): Major version
- Byte 2 (0xNN): Minor version
- Byte 1 (0xPP): Patch version
- Byte 0 (0xRR): Release candidate number (0 = final release)

**Parameters:**
- `hexsemver` (int): Hex-encoded version

**Returns:**
- `str`: Version string in format `"major.minor.patch"` or `"major.minor.patch-rcN"` or `"N/A"` if invalid

**RC Number Handling:**
- `rc_num == 0`: Final release, no suffix → `"10.15.1"`
- `rc_num > 0`: Release candidate → `"10.15.1-rc1"`

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw

version = hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw(0x0A0F0100)  # Returns "10.15.1"
version = hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw(0x0A0F0101)  # Returns "10.15.1-rc1"
version = hex_to_semver_zephyr_fw(0x0A0F0102)  # Returns "10.15.1-rc2"
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:172-189]()

---

#### `hex_to_date(hexdate: int, include_time: bool = True) -> str`

Converts hex-encoded date to human-readable string.

**Encoding:** `0xYMDDHHMM` where:
- Bits 31-28 (Y): Year offset from 2020
- Bits 27-24 (M): Month (1-12)
- Bits 23-16 (DD): Day of month
- Bits 15-8 (HH): Hour
- Bits 7-0 (MM): Minute

**Parameters:**
- `hexdate` (int): Hex-encoded date
- `include_time` (bool, optional): Whether to include time in output. Defaults to `True`

**Returns:**
- `str`: Date string in format `"YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM"` or `"YYYY-MM-DD"` or `"N/A"` if invalid

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import hex_to_date

date = hex_to_date(0x4B181430)           # Returns "2024-11-24 20:48"
date = hex_to_date(0x4B181430, False)    # Returns "2024-11-24"
date = hex_to_date(0x00000000)           # Returns "N/A"
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:93-109]()

---

### Reference Clock Monitoring

These functions monitor the reference clock counter hardware register to validate clock operation.

```mermaid
graph TB
    subgraph "Reference Clock Counter Hardware"
        HighReg["ARC_RESET.REFCLK_COUNTER_HIGH<br/>(Upper 32 bits)"]
        LowReg["ARC_RESET.REFCLK_COUNTER_LOW<br/>(Lower 32 bits)"]
    end
    
    subgraph "API Functions"
        Read["read_refclk_counter(chip)<br/>Returns 64-bit counter value"]
        Rate["refclk_counter_rate(chip, delay)<br/>Returns rate in MHz"]
        CheckSpeed["check_refclk_counter_read_speed(chip)<br/>Validates read latency"]
        CheckRate["check_refclk_counter_rate(chip, expected, accuracy)<br/>Validates frequency"]
    end
    
    subgraph "Validation Logic"
        SpeedCheck["Read latency < 100us?"]
        RateCheck["Within accuracy% of expected?"]
    end
    
    Read -->|"axi_read32()"| HighReg
    Read -->|"axi_read32()"| LowReg
    Rate -->|"calls"| Read
    CheckSpeed -->|"100 iterations"| Read
    CheckRate -->|"calls"| Rate
    
    CheckSpeed --> SpeedCheck
    CheckRate --> RateCheck
    
    style Read fill:#f9f9f9
    style Rate fill:#f9f9f9
    style CheckSpeed fill:#f9f9f9
    style CheckRate fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:198-253]()

---

#### `read_refclk_counter(chip) -> int`

Reads the 64-bit reference clock counter from hardware registers.

**Parameters:**
- `chip`: PciChip object with AXI access capabilities

**Returns:**
- `int`: 64-bit counter value
- `None`: For Grayskull chips (not supported)

**Implementation:**
1. Reads `ARC_RESET.REFCLK_COUNTER_HIGH` (first read)
2. Reads `ARC_RESET.REFCLK_COUNTER_LOW`
3. Reads `ARC_RESET.REFCLK_COUNTER_HIGH` (second read)
4. If high values differ, re-reads low register to handle overflow
5. Returns `(high2 << 32) | low`

**Overflow Handling:**
The double-read of the high register detects overflow that occurs between reading low and high registers, ensuring atomic 64-bit reads.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:202-214]()

---

#### `refclk_counter_rate(chip, delay_interval: float = 0.1) -> float`

Calculates the reference clock counter rate by measuring counter increments over time.

**Parameters:**
- `chip`: PciChip object
- `delay_interval` (float, optional): Measurement interval in seconds. Defaults to `0.1`

**Returns:**
- `float`: Counter rate in MHz

**Calculation:**
```
rate_MHz = (counter_after - counter_before) * 1000 / (time_ns_after - time_ns_before)
```

**Accuracy:**
Longer delay intervals provide more accurate measurements but take more time. Default 0.1s provides good balance.

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import refclk_counter_rate

rate = refclk_counter_rate(chip, delay_interval=0.5)
print(f"Reference clock rate: {rate:.2f} MHz")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:217-227]()

---

#### `check_refclk_counter_read_speed(chip)`

Validates that reference clock counter reads complete within expected latency.

**Parameters:**
- `chip`: PciChip object

**Behavior:**
- Performs 100 reads of the reference clock counter
- Calculates average read time
- Prints warning if average read time > 100 microseconds

**Output:**
Prints to stdout if reads are slow:
```
REFCLK_COUNTER reads are unusually slow (150us).
```

**Purpose:**
Detects communication issues or driver problems that cause slow hardware access.

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:230-240]()

---

#### `check_refclk_counter_rate(chip, expected_refclk: float, accuracy: float)`

Validates that the reference clock counter is incrementing at the expected frequency.

**Parameters:**
- `chip`: PciChip object
- `expected_refclk` (float): Expected clock rate in MHz
- `accuracy` (float): Allowed deviation percentage (e.g., 1.0 for ±1%)

**Returns:**
- `str`: Error message if rate is outside tolerance
- `None`: If rate is within tolerance

**Validation:**
Checks if: `|expected - observed| / min(expected, observed) <= accuracy / 100`

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import check_refclk_counter_rate

error = check_refclk_counter_rate(chip, expected_refclk=100.0, accuracy=1.0)
if error:
    print(f"Clock error: {error}")
else:
    print("Clock rate is within tolerance")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:243-252]()

---

### Chip Detection

#### `detect_chips_with_callback(local_only: bool = False, ignore_ethernet: bool = False, print_status: bool = True) -> List[PciChip]`

Detects all Tenstorrent chips in the system with real-time status updates via callback mechanism.

**Parameters:**
- `local_only` (bool, optional): If `True`, only detect local PCIe chips. Defaults to `False`
- `ignore_ethernet` (bool, optional): If `True`, skip Ethernet neighbor detection. Defaults to `False`
- `print_status` (bool, optional): If `True`, print detection progress. Defaults to `True`

**Returns:**
- `List[PciChip]`: List of detected chips with verified communication

**Raises:**
- `Exception`: If any detected chip fails communication verification

**Detection Process:**

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["detect_chips_with_callback()"] --> PyLuwen["pyluwen.detect_chips_fallible()"]
    
    PyLuwen -->|"callback events"| EventHandler["chip_detect_callback()"]
    
    EventHandler --> NewChip{"new_chip()?"}
    EventHandler --> CorrectDown{"correct_down()?"}
    
    NewChip -->|"yes"| IncCount["chip_count++"]
    NewChip -->|"no"| GetStatus
    
    CorrectDown -->|"yes"| DecCount["chip_count--"]
    CorrectDown -->|"no"| GetStatus
    
    IncCount --> UpdateDisplay
    DecCount --> UpdateDisplay
    
    GetStatus["status.status_string()"] --> ParseStatus{"Parse status type"}
    
    ParseStatus -->|"ARC"| ShowARC["Show ARC spinner"]
    ParseStatus -->|"DRAM"| ShowDRAM["Show DRAM spinner"]
    ParseStatus -->|"ETH"| ShowETH["Show ETH detection"]
    ParseStatus -->|"other"| ShowOther["Show raw line"]
    
    ShowARC --> UpdateDisplay
    ShowDRAM --> UpdateDisplay
    ShowETH --> UpdateDisplay
    ShowOther --> UpdateDisplay
    
    UpdateDisplay["Update terminal display"] --> NextEvent
    
    PyLuwen --> CheckComms{"have_comms()?"}
    CheckComms -->|"no"| RaiseError["Raise Exception"]
    CheckComms -->|"yes"| Upgrade["force_upgrade()"]
    
    Upgrade --> AppendList["Append to output list"]
    AppendList --> NextEvent{"More chips?"}
    
    NextEvent -->|"yes"| PyLuwen
    NextEvent -->|"no"| Return["Return chip list"]
    
    style EventHandler fill:#f9f9f9
    style CheckComms fill:#f9f9f9
```

**Callback Events:**
The internal `chip_detect_callback` function handles these event types:
1. **`new_chip()`**: New chip detected, increment counter
2. **`correct_down()`**: Previously detected chip removed, decrement counter
3. **`status_string()`**: Provides detailed detection progress messages

**Status Display:**
When `print_status=True`, shows:
- **Chip count**: Total detected chips (purple text)
- **ARC detection**: Rotating spinner (blue text)
- **DRAM detection**: Rotating spinner (blue text)
- **Ethernet detection**: Per-chip progress (purple/blue text)

**Communication Verification:**
After detection, each chip is checked with `have_comms()`. If communication fails, raises:
```
Exception: Do not have communication with {device}, you should reset or remove this device from your system before continuing.
```

**Firmware Upgrade:**
Successfully detected chips are upgraded via `force_upgrade()` to ensure latest firmware capabilities.

**Example:**
```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import detect_chips_with_callback

# Detect all chips with status display
chips = detect_chips_with_callback()

# Detect only local chips silently
local_chips = detect_chips_with_callback(local_only=True, print_status=False)

# Detect without Ethernet neighbors
pcie_only = detect_chips_with_callback(ignore_ethernet=True)
```

**Terminal Output Example:**
```
 Detected Chips: 4
 Detecting ARC: |
 Detecting DRAM: /
 [0] ETH detection: -
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:255-354]()

## Version String Parsing Details

### Internal Version Parser

The `_parse_version_string()` function implements robust semantic version parsing used by driver version checking.

**Syntax Support:**
| Format | Example | Parsed As |
|--------|---------|-----------|
| Major.Minor.Patch | `"1.26.0"` | `(1, 26, 0)` |
| Major.Minor | `"1.26"` | `(1, 26, 0)` |
| Major only | `"2"` | `(2, 0, 0)` |
| Pre-release | `"1.26.0-alpha"` | `(1, 26, 0)` |
| Build metadata | `"1.26.0+build123"` | `(1, 26, 0)` |
| Combined | `"1.26.0-rc1+build42"` | `(1, 26, 0)` |

**Parsing Algorithm:**
1. Strip build metadata (text after `+`)
2. Strip pre-release identifier (text after `-`)
3. Split remaining string on `.`
4. Parse as integers with defaults: `(major, minor or 0, patch or 0)`

**Error Cases:**
- Empty string → `ValueError`
- Non-numeric parts → `ValueError`
- Invalid format → `ValueError`

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/system_utils.py:47-80]()

## Integration Examples

### Example: Pre-flight Validation

Complete validation before chip reset operation:

```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.system_utils import (
    check_driver_version,
    get_host_compatibility_info
)
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import detect_chips_with_callback

# Validate driver version
check_driver_version("chip reset", "1.26.0")

# Check host compatibility
compat_info = get_host_compatibility_info()
for key, value in compat_info.items():
    if isinstance(value, tuple):
        print(f"Warning: {key} is {value[0]}, recommended: {value[1]}")

# Detect chips
chips = detect_chips_with_callback(local_only=False, print_status=True)
print(f"Detected {len(chips)} chips")
```

---

### Example: Firmware Version Display

Display firmware versions with proper formatting:

```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import (
    hex_to_semver,
    hex_to_semver_eth,
    hex_to_semver_m3_fw,
    hex_to_date
)

# Assume chip provides these values from registers
arc_fw_version = 0x010A0300  # ARC firmware
eth_fw_version = 0x061000    # Ethernet firmware
m3_fw_version = 0x01020364   # M3 firmware
build_date = 0x4B181430      # Build date

print(f"ARC Firmware: {hex_to_semver(arc_fw_version)}")
print(f"ETH Firmware: {hex_to_semver_eth(eth_fw_version)}")
print(f"M3 Firmware: {hex_to_semver_m3_fw(m3_fw_version)}")
print(f"Build Date: {hex_to_date(build_date)}")
```

---

### Example: Reference Clock Health Check

Monitor reference clock operation:

```python
from tt_tools_common.utils_common.tools_utils import (
    check_refclk_counter_rate,
    check_refclk_counter_read_speed
)

# Validate read performance
check_refclk_counter_read_speed(chip)

# Check clock is running at expected 100MHz ±1%
error = check_refclk_counter_rate(chip, expected_refclk=100.0, accuracy=1.0)
if error:
    print(f"Clock validation failed: {error}")
else:
    print("Reference clock validated successfully")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/utils_common/tools_utils.py:202-252]()

## Purpose and Scope

This page provides comprehensive API reference documentation for all Textual widget classes, modal screens, and styling components in the `tt_tools_common/ui_common` module. Each widget class is documented with its constructor parameters, public methods, properties, CSS selectors, and usage patterns.

For higher-level guidance on using these widgets to build TUI applications, see [Widget Library Reference](#4.1). For theming and styling concepts, see [Theming and Styling](#4.3). For complete application examples, see [Building Custom TUI Applications](#4.4).

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:4-11](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:22-364]()

## Core Display Widgets

### TTHeader

**Class Definition:** `TTHeader(Widget)`

A time-updating header widget that displays application name, version, and current timestamp.

#### Constructor Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required | Description |
|-----------|------|----------|-------------|
| `app_name` | `str` | Yes | Application name displayed in center column |
| `app_version` | `str` | Yes | Version string displayed in left column (prefixed with "Version ") |

#### Methods

| Method | Return Type | Description |
|--------|-------------|-------------|
| `on_mount()` | `None` | Sets 1-second interval timer for automatic refresh |
| `render()` | `RenderResult` | Renders 3-column Rich Panel with version, app name, and timestamp |

#### Layout Structure

The header uses a Rich `Table.grid` with three columns:
- **Left (25%):** Version string with "Version " prefix
- **Center (50%):** Application name
- **Right (25%):** Current date/time in format "MMM DD YYYY HH:MM:SS AM/PM"

#### CSS Selectors

- `TTHeader` - Main widget selector
- Inherits global `*` styles

#### Example Usage

```python
header = TTHeader(app_name="TT-SMI", app_version="1.2.3")
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:22-45](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:30-39]()

---

### TTFooter

**Class Definition:** `TTFooter(Widget)`

A customizable footer widget for displaying multi-column content in a panel.

#### Constructor Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|----------|---------|-------------|
| `content` | `List[str]` | Yes | - | List of strings, one per column |
| `justify` | `str` | No | `"center"` | Text justification: "left", "center", or "right" |

#### Methods

| Method | Return Type | Description |
|--------|-------------|-------------|
| `render()` | `RenderResult` | Renders Rich Panel with collapsible grid of content columns |

#### Layout Structure

Creates a Rich `Table.grid` with:
- Number of columns equal to length of `content` list
- Each column has equal ratio (1)
- `collapse_padding=False` to maintain spacing

#### CSS Selectors

- `TTFooter` - Main widget selector

#### Example Usage

```python
footer = TTFooter(
    content=["Status: Ready", "Chips: 4", "Mode: Monitor"],
    justify="center"
)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:48-62](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:30-43]()

---

### TTDataTable

**Class Definition:** `TTDataTable(ScrollableContainer)`

A scrollable container wrapping a Textual `DataTable` with additional configuration and update capabilities.

#### Constructor Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|----------|---------|-------------|
| `title` | `str` | Yes | - | Border title for both container and inner DataTable |
| `header` | `List[str]` | No | `None` | Column headers (auto-styled with underline and center justification) |
| `id` | `str` | No | `None` | Widget ID (inner DataTable gets `id + "_table"`) |
| `**kwargs` | `Any` | No | - | Additional kwargs passed to DataTable constructor |

#### Properties

| Property | Type | Description |
|----------|------|-------------|
| `dt` | `DataTable` | Reference to inner DataTable widget |
| `header` | `List[str]` | Column headers (converted to Rich Text objects when styled) |
| `border_title` | `str` | Container border title |
| `_title` | `str` | Private copy of title for DataTable configuration |

#### Methods

| Method | Parameters | Return Type | Description |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------------|
| `style_header()` | None | `None` | Converts header strings to Rich Text with center justification and underline style |
| `config_dt(**kwargs)` | `**kwargs` | `DataTable` | Creates and configures inner DataTable with zebra_stripes=False, cursor_type="cell" |
| `update_data(rows)` | `rows: List[str]` | `None` | Updates DataTable cells individually; clears and re-adds rows if dimensions changed |
| `compose()` | None | `ComposeResult` | Yields nested ScrollableContainer with inner DataTable |

#### DataTable Configuration

The inner DataTable is configured with:
- `zebra_stripes = False`
- `cursor_type = "cell"`
- `border_title` set to title parameter
- `id` set to `{container_id}_table`

#### Update Behavior

The `update_data()` method attempts cell-by-cell updates using `update_cell_at()`. If `CellDoesNotExist` is raised (row count increased), it falls back to `clear()` followed by `add_rows()`.

#### CSS Selectors

- `TTDataTable` - Container selector (inherits from ScrollableContainer)
- `DataTable` - Inner DataTable styling
- `.datatable--header` - Header row styling
- `.datatable--cursor` - Cell cursor styling
- `.datatable--hover` - Hover state styling

#### Example Usage

```python
table = TTDataTable(
    title="Device Information",
    header=["PCI ID", "Architecture", "Status"],
    id="device_table"
)
table.update_data([
    ["0000:01:00.0", "Wormhole", "Active"],
    ["0000:02:00.0", "Blackhole", "Active"]
])
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:65-117](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:45-85]()

---

## Menu Display Widgets

### TTMenu

**Class Definition:** `TTMenu(Container)`

A key-value list widget that displays data in a formatted menu style with bullet points.

#### Constructor Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required | Description |
|-----------|------|----------|-------------|
| `id` | `str` | Yes | Widget identifier |
| `title` | `str` | Yes | Border title for the container |
| `data` | `OrderedDict[str, str]` | Yes | Key-value pairs to display |

#### Properties

| Property | Type | Description |
|----------|------|-------------|
| `data` | `OrderedDict[str, str]` | Key-value data to render |
| `justify_width` | `int` | Width for key column alignment (max key length + 1) |
| `border_title` | `str` | Container border title |

#### Methods

| Method | Return Type | Description |
|--------|-------------|-------------|
| `render()` | `RenderResult` | Renders Rich Text with formatted key-value pairs |

#### Rendering Format

Each key-value pair is rendered as:
```
* <key (left-justified to justify_width)>: <value>
```

**Special Handling:** If key is `"Failed to fetch"`, the value is displayed on a new line in dark orange without the colon separator.

#### Styling

- Keys: `#ffd10a` (yellow), bold
- Values: Default color
- Failed fetch values: `dark_orange`
- Bullet points: `* ` prefix for normal entries

#### CSS Selectors

- `TTMenu` - Main widget selector

#### Example Usage

```python
from collections import OrderedDict

menu = TTMenu(
    id="info_menu",
    title="System Information",
    data=OrderedDict([
        ("Hostname", "tt-server-01"),
        ("OS", "Ubuntu 22.04"),
        ("Kernel", "5.15.0-91-generic")
    ])
)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:120-146](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:88-95]()

---

### TTHostCompatibilityMenu

**Class Definition:** `TTHostCompatibilityMenu(Container)`

A menu widget for displaying host information with compatibility warnings. Used primarily in tt-smi to show system configuration issues.

#### Constructor Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required | Description |
|-----------|------|----------|-------------|
| `id` | `str` | Yes | Widget identifier |
| `title` | `str` | Yes | Base border title (appended with compatibility status) |
| `data` | `Dict[str, Union[str, Tuple]]` | Yes | Key-value pairs or key-(value, recommendation) tuples |

#### Data Format

The `data` dictionary accepts two value types:

1. **String value:** Simple key-value pair (indicates compatible configuration)
2. **Tuple value:** `(current_value, recommendation_note)` (indicates configuration warning)

#### Title and Styling Behavior

| Condition | Border Title | Border Color | Subtitle |
|-----------|--------------|--------------|----------|
| All values are strings | `{title} (Fully Compatible)` | Default (yellow) | None |
| Any value is tuple | `{title} (Config Warning!)` | Red | `"* Recommended Config"` (red) |

#### Properties

| Property | Type | Description |
|----------|------|-------------|
| `data` | `Dict[str, Union[str, Tuple]]` | Key-value data with optional recommendations |
| `justify_width` | `int` | Width for key column alignment (max key length + 1) |
| `border_title` | `str` | Container border title with compatibility status |
| `border_subtitle` | `str` | Set to "* Recommended Config" if warnings exist |

#### Methods

| Method | Return Type | Description |
|--------|-------------|-------------|
| `render()` | `RenderResult` | Renders Rich Text with formatted entries and warnings |

#### Rendering Format

**For string values:**
```
* <key>: <value>
```

**For tuple values:**
```
* <key>: <current_value>
         * <recommendation>
```

#### Styling

- Keys: `#ffd10a` (yellow), bold
- String values: Default color
- Tuple values (current): Default color
- Recommendations: `dark_orange` with indentation
- Border title: Red if warnings present

#### CSS Selectors

- `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` - Main widget selector

#### Example Usage

```python
menu = TTHostCompatibilityMenu(
    id="host_compat",
    title="Host Configuration",
    data={
        "OS": "Ubuntu 22.04",
        "Kernel": ("5.10.0-generic", "5.15.0+ recommended"),
        "Driver": ("1.25.0", "1.26.0+ required"),
        "Memory": "64 GB"
    }
)
# Border title: "Host Configuration (Config Warning!)"
# Border title and subtitle color: red
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:149-210](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:89-95]()

### TTCompatibilityMenu

**Class Definition:** `TTCompatibilityMenu(Container)`

A menu widget for displaying compatibility status with boolean indicators and colored status messages.

#### Constructor Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required | Description |
|-----------|------|----------|-------------|
| `id` | `str` | Yes | Widget identifier |
| `title` | `str` | Yes | Border title for the container |
| `data` | `OrderedDict` | Yes | Key to (boolean, message) tuple mapping |

#### Data Format

Each entry in `data` must be: `key: (status_bool, status_message)`

- `status_bool`: `True` for compatible, `False` for incompatible
- `status_message`: Description or status text

#### Properties

| Property | Type | Description |
|----------|------|-------------|
| `data` | `OrderedDict` | Key to (bool, str) tuple mapping |
| `justify_width` | `int` | Width for key column alignment (max key length + 1) |
| `border_title` | `str` | Container border title |

#### Methods

| Method | Return Type | Description |
|--------|-------------|-------------|
| `render()` | `RenderResult` | Renders Rich Text with formatted status entries |

#### Rendering Format

```
* <key>: <message>
```

#### Styling

- Keys: `#ffd10a` (yellow), bold
- Messages (status_bool=True): Default color
- Messages (status_bool=False): `dark_orange`

#### CSS Selectors

- `TTCompatibilityMenu` - Main widget selector

#### Example Usage

```python
from collections import OrderedDict

menu = TTCompatibilityMenu(
    id="compat_check",
    title="System Compatibility",
    data=OrderedDict([
        ("Driver Version", (True, "1.26.0 (Compatible)")),
        ("Platform", (False, "ARM (Not Supported)")),
        ("Virtualization", (True, "Xen HVM (Supported)"))
    ])
)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:213-243](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:89-95]()

## Modal Screen Widgets

The following diagram shows the modal screen architecture and callback flow:

```mermaid
graph TB
    App["Textual App<br/>(app.push_screen/pop_screen)"]
    
    TTConfirmBox["TTConfirmBox<br/>(ModalScreen)"]
    TTHelperMenuBox["TTHelperMenuBox<br/>(ModalScreen)"]
    TTSettingsMenu["TTSettingsMenu<br/>(ModalScreen)"]
    
    YesButton["Button id='yes'"]
    NoButton["Button id='no'"]
    OnYesCallback["on_yes: Callable"]
    OnNoCallback["on_no: Callable"]
    
    Markdown["Markdown widget<br/>id='help_menu_box'"]
    HelpBindings["BINDINGS:<br/>q, escape, h"]
    
    DarkSwitch["Switch id='dark_switch'"]
    SwSwitch["Switch id='sw_switch'"]
    AppDarkProp["app.dark property"]
    AppSwVersProp["app.get_latest_sw_vers property"]
    
    App -->|"push_screen(modal)"| TTConfirmBox
    App -->|"push_screen(modal)"| TTHelperMenuBox
    App -->|"push_screen(modal)"| TTSettingsMenu
    
    TTConfirmBox --> YesButton
    TTConfirmBox --> NoButton
    YesButton -->|"on_button_pressed"| OnYesCallback
    NoButton -->|"on_button_pressed"| OnNoCallback
    OnYesCallback -->|"app.pop_screen()"| App
    OnNoCallback -->|"app.pop_screen()"| App
    
    TTHelperMenuBox --> Markdown
    TTHelperMenuBox --> HelpBindings
    HelpBindings -->|"action_quit/esc_screen/help"| App
    
    TTSettingsMenu --> DarkSwitch
    TTSettingsMenu --> SwSwitch
    DarkSwitch -->|"Switch.Changed"| AppDarkProp
    SwSwitch -->|"Switch.Changed"| AppSwVersProp
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-364]()

---

### TTConfirmBox

**Class Definition:** `TTConfirmBox(ModalScreen)`

A modal confirmation dialog with "Yes" and "No" buttons and optional callbacks.

#### Constructor Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|----------|---------|-------------|
| `text` | `str` | Yes | - | Question or confirmation message |
| `on_yes` | `Callable` | No | `None` | Callback executed when "Yes" is pressed |
| `on_no` | `Callable` | No | `None` | Callback executed when "No" is pressed |

#### Methods

| Method | Parameters | Return Type | Description |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------------|
| `compose()` | None | `ComposeResult` | Yields Grid container with Label and two Buttons |
| `on_button_pressed(event)` | `event: Button.Pressed` | `None` | Handles button clicks and executes callbacks |

#### Composition Structure

```
Grid (id="dialog")
├── Label (id="question") - Displays confirmation text
├── Button (id="yes") - "Yes" button
└── Button (id="no") - "No" button
```

#### Behavior

1. When "Yes" button is pressed:
   - Executes `on_yes()` callback if provided
   - Calls `app.pop_screen()` to close modal

2. When "No" button is pressed:
   - Executes `on_no()` callback if provided
   - Calls `app.pop_screen()` to close modal

#### CSS Selectors

- `TTConfirmBox` - Modal screen selector (aligned center middle)
- `#dialog` - Grid container
- `#question` - Label with confirmation text
- `Button` - Both Yes/No buttons
- `Button:hover`, `Button:focus` - Interactive states

#### Example Usage

```python
def confirm_reset():
    def on_yes_callback():
        # Perform reset
        perform_chip_reset()
    
    def on_no_callback():
        # Cancel action
        log_cancel()
    
    confirm = TTConfirmBox(
        text="Are you sure you want to reset all chips?",
        on_yes=on_yes_callback,
        on_no=on_no_callback
    )
    app.push_screen(confirm)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:246-271](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:105-138]()

---

### TTHelperMenuBox

**Class Definition:** `TTHelperMenuBox(ModalScreen)`

A modal screen displaying help text in Markdown format with key bindings for dismissal.

#### Constructor Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|----------|---------|-------------|
| `text` | `str` | Yes | - | Markdown-formatted help content |
| `theme` | `OrderedDict` | No | `{}` | Theme dictionary (currently unused in implementation) |

#### Key Bindings

| Key | Action | Description |
|-----|--------|-------------|
| `q` | `quit` | Close help screen and return to app |
| `escape` | `esc_screen` | Close help screen and return to app |
| `h` | `help` | Close help screen and return to app |

#### Methods

| Method | Return Type | Description |
|--------|-------------|-------------|
| `compose()` | `ComposeResult` | Yields Markdown widget with help content |
| `action_quit()` | `None` | Pops screen to return to app (duplicate definition at lines 291, 299) |
| `action_esc_screen()` | `None` | Pops screen to return to app |
| `action_help()` | `None` | Pops screen to return to app |

#### Composition Structure

```
Markdown (id="help_menu_box")
└── Rendered help text
```

#### CSS Selectors

- `TTHelperMenuBox` - Modal screen selector (aligned center middle)
- `#help_menu_box` - Markdown container (110 width, 30 height, green border)
- `MarkdownH1` - H1 heading styling
- `MarkdownTableContent` - Table content styling

#### Example Usage

```python
help_text = """
# TT-SMI Help

## Key Bindings
| Key | Action |
|-----|--------|
| q   | Quit   |
| r   | Reset  |

## Status Indicators
- Green: Active
- Red: Error
"""

help_screen = TTHelperMenuBox(text=help_text)
app.push_screen(help_screen)
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:274-305](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:175-206]()

---

### TTSettingsMenu

**Class Definition:** `TTSettingsMenu(ModalScreen)`

A modal settings screen with switch controls for dark mode and software version checking.

#### Constructor Parameters

| Parameter | Type | Required | Default | Description |
|-----------|------|----------|---------|-------------|
| `text` | `str` | Yes | - | Settings text (currently unused) |
| `theme` | `OrderedDict` | No | `{}` | Theme dictionary for text styling |

#### Key Bindings

| Key | Action | Description |
|-----|--------|-------------|
| `q, Q, s, S` | `quit` | Close settings screen |
| `escape` | `esc_screen` | Close settings screen |

#### Methods

| Method | Parameters | Return Type | Description |
|--------|------------|-------------|-------------|
| `compose()` | None | `ComposeResult` | Yields Grid with heading, switches, and labels |
| `select_changed(event)` | `event: Switch.Changed` | `None` | Handles switch toggle events |
| `action_setting()` | None | `None` | Pops screen to return to app |
| `action_esc_screen()` | None | `None` | Pops screen to return to app |
| `action_quit()` | None | `None` | Pops screen to return to app (duplicate definitions) |
| `action_help()` | None | `None` | Pops screen to return to app |

#### Composition Structure

```
Grid (id="settings_menu_box")
├── Label (id="heading") - "TT-SMI Settings"
├── Label (id="instruction") - Navigation instructions
├── Label (id="dark_label") - "o Dark Mode:"
├── Switch (id="dark_switch") - Dark mode toggle
├── Label (id="sw_label") - "o Latest SW versions:"
└── Switch (id="sw_switch") - Software version checking toggle
```

#### Switch Behavior

**Dark Mode Switch (id="dark_switch"):**
- Reads initial value from `app.dark`
- Updates `app.dark` property on change
- Controls application dark mode state

**Software Version Switch (id="sw_switch"):**
- Reads initial value from `app.get_latest_sw_vers`
- Updates `app.get_latest_sw_vers` property on change
- Controls whether app fetches latest software versions

#### Switch Change Handler

The `@on(Switch.Changed)` decorator handles switch toggle events:
- Event source identified by `event.switch.id`
- Switch value read from `event.switch.value` (boolean)
- Corresponding app property updated based on switch state

#### CSS Selectors

- `TTSettingsMenu` - Modal screen selector
- `#settings_menu_box` - Grid container
- `#heading`, `#instruction` - Label selectors
- `#dark_label`, `#sw_label` - Switch label selectors
- `#dark_switch`, `#sw_switch` - Switch selectors
- `Switch>.switch--slider` - Switch slider styling
- `Switch.-on>.switch--slider` - Active switch styling

#### Example Usage

```python
from collections import OrderedDict

theme = OrderedDict([
    ("light_green_bold", Style(color="#1eb57d", bold=True)),
    ("attention", Style(color="#ffd10a"))
])

settings = TTSettingsMenu(
    text="",  # Currently unused
    theme=theme
)
app.push_screen(settings)

# App must have these properties:
# - app.dark (bool): Current dark mode state
# - app.get_latest_sw_vers (bool): Software version checking state
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:308-364](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:208-217]()

## CSS Theming System

### Color Variables

The following color variables are defined globally in `common_style.css`:

| Variable | Value | Usage |
|----------|-------|-------|
| `$red` | `#f04f5e` | Error states, warnings, attention |
| `$green` | `#1eb57d` | Primary color, borders, success states |
| `$yellow` | `#ffd10a` | Secondary color, text highlights, keys |
| `$purple` | `#786bb0` | (Defined but not actively used) |
| `$orange` | `darkorange` | Warnings, recommendations |
| `$gray` | `ansi_bright_black` | Muted content |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:6-12]()

---

### Global Widget Styling

The following table maps CSS selectors to their primary styling rules:

| Selector | Key Properties | Description |
|----------|----------------|-------------|
| `*` | `color: $yellow`<br/>`scrollbar-color: $yellow`<br/>`border-title-color: $yellow` | Universal widget defaults |
| `TTHeader`, `TTFooter` | `height: 3`<br/>`outline: solid $green`<br/>`text-style: bold` | Header/footer appearance |
| `DataTable` | `border: solid $green`<br/>`color: $green`<br/>`padding: 1 2` | DataTable container |
| `.datatable--cursor` | `background: $yellow`<br/>`color: black` | Active cell cursor |
| `.datatable--hover` | `background: $yellow 60%`<br/>`color: white` | Hover state with transparency |
| `TTMenu`, `TTCompatibilityMenu`, `TTHostCompatibilityMenu` | `border: solid $green`<br/>`color: $green`<br/>`padding: 1 1` | Menu containers |
| `Button` | `background: $yellow`<br/>`color: white` | Default button state |
| `Button:hover`, `Button:focus` | `background: $red`<br/>`color: white`<br/>`text-style: bold` | Interactive button states |
| `Switch>.switch--slider` | `color: $red`<br/>`background: red 12%` | Inactive switch (off state) |
| `Switch.-on>.switch--slider` | `color: $green`<br/>`background: $green 15%` | Active switch (on state) |

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:14-225]()

## Widget Composition Patterns

### Standard Application Layout

Most tt-tools applications follow this composition pattern:

```mermaid
graph TB
    App["Textual App"]
    
    Header["TTHeader<br/>(docked top)"]
    Footer["TTFooter<br/>(docked bottom)"]
    Content["Content Area"]
    
    DataTable["TTDataTable"]
    Menu["TTMenu variants"]
    
    Modal["Modal Screens<br/>(pushed on demand)"]
    Confirm["TTConfirmBox"]
    Help["TTHelperMenuBox"]
    Settings["TTSettingsMenu"]
    
    App --> Header
    App --> Content
    App --> Footer
    
    Content --> DataTable
    Content --> Menu
    
    App -.push_screen.-> Modal
    Modal --> Confirm
    Modal --> Help
    Modal --> Settings
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-365]()

---

### Typical Compose Method Structure

A standard compose pattern for applications using these widgets:

```python
def compose(self) -> ComposeResult:
    """Compose application layout."""
    yield TTHeader(app_name="My App", app_version="1.0.0")
    
    # Main content area
    yield TTDataTable(
        title="Data View",
        header=["Column 1", "Column 2"],
        id="main_table"
    )
    
    yield TTMenu(
        id="info_menu",
        title="Information",
        data=OrderedDict([...])
    )
    
    yield TTFooter(
        content=["Status", "Info", "More"],
        justify="center"
    )
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:22-117]()

---

## Import Paths

All widgets are importable from `tt_tools_common.ui_common.widgets`:

```python
from tt_tools_common.ui_common.widgets import (
    TTHeader,
    TTFooter,
    TTDataTable,
    TTMenu,
    TTCompatibilityMenu,
    TTHostCompatibilityMenu,
    TTConfirmBox,
    TTHelperMenuBox,
    TTSettingsMenu,
)
```

The CSS stylesheet is automatically loaded when widgets are used in a Textual application. To explicitly reference it:

```python
from pathlib import Path

CSS_PATH = Path(__file__).parent / "tt_tools_common" / "ui_common" / "common_style.css"
```

**Sources:** [tt_tools_common/ui_common/widgets.py:1-20](), [tt_tools_common/ui_common/common_style.css:1-5]()

3a:T412f,
# Data Models and Configuration

<details>
<summary>Relevant source files</summary>

The following files were used as context for generating this wiki page:

- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py)
- [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py](tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py)

</details>



This page documents the Pydantic data models and configuration file formats used throughout tt-tools-common. These models provide structured data validation, Elasticsearch integration, and JSON serialization for reset operations and system logging.

For information about using these models in reset operations, see [Reset Configuration and Logging](#2.6). For API usage examples, see [Reset API Reference](#7.1).

## Overview

The configuration system provides three primary capabilities:

1. **Structured Data Validation**: Pydantic models ensure type safety and required field validation
2. **Elasticsearch Integration**: Models automatically map to Elasticsearch field types for centralized logging
3. **JSON Configuration**: Human-readable and machine-parseable configuration files for complex reset operations

## Pydantic Model Architecture

The model hierarchy is built on `ElasticModel`, which extends Pydantic's `BaseModel` with Elasticsearch mapping capabilities.

```mermaid
graph TD
    BaseModel["pydantic.BaseModel<br/>(v1 or v2)"]
    ElasticModel["ElasticModel<br/>get_mapping()"]
    HostResetLog["HostResetLog<br/>Top-level log model"]
    PciResetDeviceInfo["PciResetDeviceInfo<br/>PCIe device list"]
    MoboReset["MoboReset<br/>Motherboard config"]
    
    BaseModel --> ElasticModel
    ElasticModel --> HostResetLog
    ElasticModel --> PciResetDeviceInfo
    ElasticModel --> MoboReset
    
    HostResetLog --> |"contains"| PciResetDeviceInfo
    HostResetLog --> |"contains List[MoboReset]"| MoboReset
    
    OptionalDecorator["@optional decorator<br/>Makes fields optional"]
    OptionalDecorator -.-> HostResetLog
    OptionalDecorator -.-> PciResetDeviceInfo
    OptionalDecorator -.-> MoboReset
```

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:1-185]()

### ElasticModel Base Class

`ElasticModel` provides the foundation for all data models with Elasticsearch integration:

| Method | Return Type | Description |
|--------|-------------|-------------|
| `get_mapping()` | `dict` | Generates Elasticsearch field mappings from Pydantic field types |
| `save_as_json()` | `None` | Serializes model to JSON file with proper formatting |

The class implements automatic type mapping through helper functions:

- `type_to_mapping()`: Converts Python types to Elasticsearch types
- `field_to_mapping()`: Converts Pydantic fields to ES mappings
- Supports custom types: `Long`, `Keyword`, `Text`, `Date`, `Nested[T]`

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:127-146]()

### Type Mapping System

The following table shows how Python types map to Elasticsearch types:

| Python Type | Elasticsearch Type | Notes |
|-------------|-------------------|-------|
| `int` | `integer` | Standard integer |
| `Long` | `long` | 64-bit integer |
| `float` | `float` | Floating point |
| `bool` | `boolean` | Boolean |
| `str` | `text` + `keyword` | Text with keyword subfield |
| `Keyword` | `keyword` | Exact match only |
| `Text` | `text` | Full-text search |
| `bytes` | `binary` | Base64 encoded |
| `datetime.datetime` | `date` | ISO 8601 format |
| `Date` | `date` | Custom format support |
| `ElasticModel` | `object` | Nested object |
| `Nested[T]` | `nested` | Elasticsearch nested type |

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:68-116]()

## Reset Log Models

### HostResetLog

The top-level model for reset operation logs, capturing all information about a reset event:

```mermaid
classDiagram
    class HostResetLog {
        +datetime.datetime time
        +str host_name
        +PciResetDeviceInfo gs_tensix_reset
        +PciResetDeviceInfo wh_link_reset
        +bool re_init_devices
        +List[MoboReset] wh_mobo_reset
        +bool disable_serial_report
        +bool disable_sw_version_report
        +save_as_json(fname)
    }
    
    class PciResetDeviceInfo {
        +List[int] pci_index
    }
    
    class MoboReset {
        +Union[List[int], None] nb_host_pci_idx
        +str mobo
        +List[str] credo
        +List[str] disabled_ports
    }
    
    HostResetLog "1" --> "1" PciResetDeviceInfo : gs_tensix_reset
    HostResetLog "1" --> "1" PciResetDeviceInfo : wh_link_reset
    HostResetLog "1" --> "0..*" MoboReset : wh_mobo_reset
```

**Field Descriptions**:

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `time` | `datetime.datetime` | Timestamp of reset operation |
| `host_name` | `str` | Hostname from `get_host_info()` |
| `gs_tensix_reset` | `PciResetDeviceInfo` | Grayskull devices to reset |
| `wh_link_reset` | `PciResetDeviceInfo` | Wormhole devices to reset |
| `re_init_devices` | `bool` | Whether to reinitialize devices post-reset |
| `wh_mobo_reset` | `List[MoboReset]` | Motherboard-level reset configurations |
| `disable_serial_report` | `bool` | Skip serial number reporting |
| `disable_sw_version_report` | `bool` | Skip software version reporting |

All fields are decorated with `@optional`, making them optional in the Pydantic schema.

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:167-185]()

### PciResetDeviceInfo

Represents a list of PCIe devices to be reset, identified by their PCI interface indices:

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `pci_index` | `List[int]` | List of PCI interface IDs (e.g., `[0, 1, 2]`) |

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:149-154]()

### MoboReset

Configuration for motherboard-level reset operations, typically used in multi-chip systems with custom PCIe switching:

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `nb_host_pci_idx` | `Union[List[int], None]` | Northbridge host PCIe indices |
| `mobo` | `str` | Motherboard identifier string |
| `credo` | `List[str]` | Credo retimer identifiers (format: `"group_id:credo_id"`) |
| `disabled_ports` | `List[str]` | Ports to keep disabled (format: `"group_id:credo_id"`) |

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:156-165]()

## Configuration Input System

The input system parses various reset specification formats into a unified `ResetInput` structure.

```mermaid
graph LR
    CLI["CLI Arguments<br/>or API call"]
    parse_reset_input["parse_reset_input()<br/>tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py"]
    
    ResetInput["ResetInput<br/>dataclass"]
    ResetType["ResetType enum<br/>ALL | CONFIG_JSON | ID_LIST"]
    
    ALL["ResetType.ALL<br/>value=None"]
    CONFIG_JSON["ResetType.CONFIG_JSON<br/>value=Dict"]
    ID_LIST["ResetType.ID_LIST<br/>value=List[int]"]
    
    CLI --> parse_reset_input
    parse_reset_input --> ResetInput
    ResetInput --> ResetType
    
    ResetType --> ALL
    ResetType --> CONFIG_JSON
    ResetType --> ID_LIST
    
    parse_reset_input -."|[] or ['all']|".-> ALL
    parse_reset_input -."|['config.json']|".-> CONFIG_JSON
    parse_reset_input -."|[0,1,2] or ['0,1,2']|".-> ID_LIST
```

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:23-87]()

### ResetType Enum

Defines three modes of specifying which devices to reset:

```python
class ResetType(Enum):
    ALL = 1           # Reset all detected devices
    CONFIG_JSON = 2   # Use JSON configuration file
    ID_LIST = 3       # List of PCI indices
```

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:23-26]()

### ResetInput Dataclass

Container for parsed reset specifications:

| Field | Type | Description |
|-------|------|-------------|
| `type` | `ResetType` | The reset mode |
| `value` | `Union[Dict, int, None]` | Parsed value based on type |

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:28-31]()

### parse_reset_input Function

Parses various input formats into `ResetInput`:

**Input Formats**:

| Format | Example | Result |
|--------|---------|--------|
| Empty or "all" | `[]` or `["all"]` | `ResetInput(ALL, None)` |
| JSON file | `["config.json"]` | `ResetInput(CONFIG_JSON, {...})` |
| Comma-separated | `["0,1,2"]` | `ResetInput(ID_LIST, [0,1,2])` |
| Space-separated | `["0", "1", "2"]` | `ResetInput(ID_LIST, [0,1,2])` |

**Parsing Logic Flow**:

```mermaid
flowchart TD
    Start["Input: List[str]"]
    CheckEmpty{"Empty or<br/>['all']?"}
    ReturnAll["Return ALL"]
    
    CheckLen{"len == 1?"}
    TryJSON["Try open as JSON"]
    JSONSuccess{"JSON valid?"}
    ReturnJSON["Return CONFIG_JSON"]
    
    TryComma["Try split(',') as ints"]
    CommaSuccess{"Valid ints?"}
    ReturnList1["Return ID_LIST"]
    
    Error1["Print error & exit"]
    
    TrySpaced["Try parse as int list"]
    SpaceSuccess{"Valid ints?"}
    ReturnList2["Return ID_LIST"]
    Error2["Print error & exit"]
    
    Start --> CheckEmpty
    CheckEmpty -->|Yes| ReturnAll
    CheckEmpty -->|No| CheckLen
    
    CheckLen -->|Yes| TryJSON
    TryJSON --> JSONSuccess
    JSONSuccess -->|Yes| ReturnJSON
    JSONSuccess -->|No| TryComma
    TryComma --> CommaSuccess
    CommaSuccess -->|Yes| ReturnList1
    CommaSuccess -->|No| Error1
    
    CheckLen -->|No| TrySpaced
    TrySpaced --> SpaceSuccess
    SpaceSuccess -->|Yes| ReturnList2
    SpaceSuccess -->|No| Error2
```

The function automatically:
- Filters duplicate indices with `sorted(set(...))`
- Validates JSON structure with `json.load()`
- Provides helpful error messages with suggestions

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:33-87]()

## Configuration Generation

### generate_reset_logs Function

Creates a sample reset configuration file with placeholders for motherboard resets:

**Function Signature**:
```python
def generate_reset_logs(devices, result_filename: str = None) -> str
```

**Parameters**:

| Parameter | Type | Description |
|-----------|------|-------------|
| `devices` | `List[PciChip]` | List of pyluwen device objects |
| `result_filename` | `str` | Optional custom output path |

**Returns**: Path to generated JSON file (default: `~/.config/tenstorrent/reset_config.json`)

**Generation Logic**:

```mermaid
graph TD
    Start["generate_reset_logs(devices)"]
    GetTime["Get current datetime"]
    FilterGS["Filter Grayskull PCIe indices"]
    FilterWH["Filter Wormhole PCIe indices<br/>(non-remote only)"]
    
    CreateLog["Create HostResetLog"]
    PopulateFields["Populate fields:<br/>- time<br/>- host_name<br/>- gs_tensix_reset<br/>- wh_link_reset"]
    
    AddMoboTemplate["Add MoboReset templates<br/>with placeholders"]
    
    DetermineOutput{"result_filename<br/>provided?"}
    CustomPath["Use custom path"]
    DefaultPath["Use ~/.config/tenstorrent/<br/>reset_config.json"]
    
    EnsureDir["Create directory if needed"]
    SaveJSON["Call reset_log.save_as_json()"]
    Return["Return filename"]
    
    Start --> GetTime
    GetTime --> FilterGS
    FilterGS --> FilterWH
    FilterWH --> CreateLog
    CreateLog --> PopulateFields
    PopulateFields --> AddMoboTemplate
    AddMoboTemplate --> DetermineOutput
    DetermineOutput -->|Yes| CustomPath
    DetermineOutput -->|No| DefaultPath
    CustomPath --> EnsureDir
    DefaultPath --> EnsureDir
    EnsureDir --> SaveJSON
    SaveJSON --> Return
```

**Generated Template Structure**:

The function creates a `HostResetLog` with:
- Current timestamp
- Host information from `get_host_info()`
- Detected device indices for Grayskull and Wormhole
- Two template `MoboReset` entries with placeholder strings:
  - `"<MOBO NAME>"` for motherboard identifier
  - `"<group id>:<credo id>"` for Credo retimer specifications

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:89-134]()

## JSON Configuration Format

### Complete Example

A fully configured reset log JSON file:

```json
{
    "time": "2024-01-15T10:30:00.123456",
    "host_name": "tt-host-01",
    "gs_tensix_reset": {
        "pci_index": []
    },
    "wh_link_reset": {
        "pci_index": [0, 1, 2, 3]
    },
    "re_init_devices": true,
    "disable_serial_report": false,
    "disable_sw_version_report": false,
    "wh_mobo_reset": [
        {
            "nb_host_pci_idx": [0, 1],
            "mobo": "custom_galaxy_board",
            "credo": ["0:0", "0:1", "1:0", "1:1"],
            "disabled_ports": ["2:0", "2:1"]
        },
        {
            "nb_host_pci_idx": [2, 3],
            "mobo": "custom_galaxy_board",
            "credo": ["0:2", "0:3", "1:2", "1:3"],
            "disabled_ports": []
        }
    ]
}
```

### Field Reference

**Top-Level Fields**:

| Field | Required | Type | Example |
|-------|----------|------|---------|
| `time` | Yes | ISO 8601 datetime | `"2024-01-15T10:30:00"` |
| `host_name` | Yes | String | `"tt-host-01"` |
| `gs_tensix_reset` | Yes | Object | `{"pci_index": []}` |
| `wh_link_reset` | Yes | Object | `{"pci_index": [0,1,2]}` |
| `re_init_devices` | Yes | Boolean | `true` |
| `wh_mobo_reset` | Yes | Array | `[{...}, {...}]` |
| `disable_serial_report` | Yes | Boolean | `false` |
| `disable_sw_version_report` | Yes | Boolean | `false` |

**PciResetDeviceInfo Structure**:

```json
{
    "pci_index": [0, 1, 2]
}
```

**MoboReset Structure**:

```json
{
    "nb_host_pci_idx": [0, 1],
    "mobo": "board_identifier",
    "credo": ["group_id:credo_id", ...],
    "disabled_ports": ["group_id:port_id", ...]
}
```

**Credo Identifier Format**: `"<group_id>:<credo_id>"` where both IDs are integers encoded as strings

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:89-134](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:167-185]()

## Validation and Serialization

### Pydantic Compatibility

The models support both Pydantic v1 and v2 through conditional imports:

```python
try:
    # Pydantic v2 compatibility
    from pydantic.v1 import BaseModel
    from pydantic.v1.fields import Field
except:
    # Pydantic v1 fallback
    from pydantic import BaseModel
    from pydantic.fields import Field
```

This ensures compatibility across different Python environments and dependency versions.

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:15-22]()

### Optional Fields Decorator

The `@optional` decorator makes all fields in a model optional:

**Usage**:
```python
@optional
class MyModel(ElasticModel):
    field1: str
    field2: int
```

**Result**: All fields become `Optional[T]` with `default=None`

The decorator can also target specific fields:
```python
@optional("field1", "field2")
class MyModel(ElasticModel):
    field1: str  # Optional
    field2: int  # Optional
    field3: str  # Required
```

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:47-65]()

### JSON Serialization

The `save_as_json()` method provides formatted JSON output:

**Behavior**:
- Excludes `None` values with `exclude_none=False`
- Pretty-prints with 4-space indentation
- Maintains field order from model definition
- Writes to specified file path (creates directories if needed)

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:180-185]()

## Integration with Reset System

The models integrate with the reset system through this flow:

```mermaid
sequenceDiagram
    participant User
    participant parse_reset_input
    participant ResetClass as "BHChipReset/<br/>WHChipReset"
    participant generate_reset_logs
    participant HostResetLog
    participant Filesystem
    
    User->>parse_reset_input: Provide input
    parse_reset_input->>parse_reset_input: Determine ResetType
    parse_reset_input-->>User: Return ResetInput
    
    alt CONFIG_JSON type
        User->>Filesystem: Read JSON file
        Filesystem-->>User: JSON data
        User->>HostResetLog: Validate with Pydantic
    end
    
    User->>ResetClass: Perform reset
    ResetClass->>ResetClass: Execute reset logic
    
    opt Generate config
        User->>generate_reset_logs: Pass detected devices
        generate_reset_logs->>HostResetLog: Create model
        HostResetLog->>Filesystem: save_as_json()
        Filesystem-->>User: Config file path
    end
```

**Key Integration Points**:

1. **Input Parsing**: `parse_reset_input()` converts various formats to `ResetInput`
2. **Configuration Loading**: JSON files are loaded and validated against `HostResetLog` schema
3. **Reset Execution**: Reset classes consume validated configuration data
4. **Configuration Generation**: `generate_reset_logs()` creates templates for future use

**Sources**: [tt_tools_common/reset_common/reset_utils.py:1-135](), [tt_tools_common/reset_common/host_reset_log.py:1-185]()
